(3) `build_fd_construct_result` (codegen) replaced its fixed `Other(-1)` Err packing with a `select` chain decoding the stable code into the matching variant tag, payload = the code sign-extended (meaningful for `Other`, unread for the fieldless variants), falling back to the caller's default variant (`Other` for TCP, `Protocol` for TLS) for any unclassified code ŌĆö and degrading to "always default" for any future enum lacking the named variants. **Pre-existing gap fixed in passing:** `TcpError` was never in `PRELUDE_TYPES` (only `TlsError` was, from the line-24 work; the read/write surface only ever used `Err(_)`, so naming `TcpError.<variant>` in a `match` was never exercised) ŌĆö added to scope-0 so its variants are nameable without import. **Pre-existing gap tracked (not fixed):** binding a payload from an enum nested inside `Result.Err` ŌĆö `match r { Result.Err(TcpError.Other(c)) => ŌĆ” }` ŌĆö drops the inner binding in codegen (`Undefined variable 'c'`), reproducible with a plain user enum; the line-74 named causes are fieldless so they're unaffected, and the gap is a general match-codegen issue tracked in [`phase-7-codegen.md`](phase-7-codegen.md) (nested enum-payload bind). Tests: runtime units (`net_construct_error_code_maps_io_error_kinds`, `net_construct_error_codes_surface_from_real_syscalls` ŌĆö closed-port connect ŌåÆ -3, in-use rebind ŌåÆ -2), codegen IR-grep (`test_ir_fd_construct_result_classifies_named_causes`), E2E (`test_tcp_stream_connect_err_is_connection_refused`, `test_tcp_bind_err_is_addr_in_use`). Full gate green (fmt, clippy `--all-targets --features llvm`, full non-llvm + runtime suites, codegen / tcp_stream / tcp_listener / tls_codegen / http_server under llvm, memory_sanitizer ASAN). Closes the consumer arc with the `supervised_echo` kata (kara-katas).
    - **Compose-with-TLS audit.** `Server.serve` and `Server.serve_tls` are parallel; confirm a handler written against one works unchanged against the other (the `Request` / `Response` ABI is transport-independent, but verify no implicit assumption sneaked in).
    - **Public-surface freeze list. [x] DRAFTED 2026-05-30 ŌĆö reviewer ratification pending.** Every exported item in `runtime/stdlib/http.kara` with a one-line v1 stability commitment. Outcome: the whole surface is **stable v1 except `Server.serve_static`** (the lone `#[unstable]`); no item is dropped to private. **Two pre-lock refinements applied while freezing** (see the Response and serve_static rows): the `Response.text()` alias of `body()` was *removed* (one-name-per-concept), and `status() -> i64` was *locked* (typed `StatusCode` ruled out). The surface is well-formed ŌĆö the API-walk-vs-three-references pass (above) concluded "mostly keep", and this freeze confirms it.

        | Item | Commitment | Note |
        |---|---|---|
        | `struct Client` / `.new()` | stable v1 | no-arg constructor, matches Go `&http.Client{}` / reqwest `Client::new()` |
        | `Client.get(url)` / `.post(url, body) -> Result[Response, HttpError]` | stable v1 | eager convenience, matches Go `client.Get/Post` |
        | `Client.request(method, url) -> RequestBuilder` | stable v1 | builder entrypoint, matches reqwest |
        | `struct RequestBuilder` / `.header` / `.body` / `.timeout` / `.send` | stable v1 | owned-self chain; `.send() -> Result[Response, HttpError]` |
        | `struct Response` / `.status` / `.body` / `.bytes` / `.header` / `.headers` | stable v1 | **read surface = `body()` + `bytes()`** ŌĆö the `text()` alias of `body()` was dropped 2026-05-30 (one name per concept; `body()` matches the `body` field server handlers construct, and `text()` implied a charset decode v1 doesn't do). **`status() -> i64` is locked** ŌĆö the return type can't change non-breakingly, and a bare int matches Go/Node (the imperative-first baseline); a typed `StatusCode` is **off the table** (it would fight the friction-zero positioning), but `is_success()`-style **predicates** are a non-breaking v1.x-additive option |
        | `struct HttpError` / `.message() -> String` | stable v1 | message-only; `.kind()` discrimination is a v1.x-additive candidate, not a freeze blocker |
        | `struct Server` (opaque marker) | stable v1 | |
        | `Server.serve(addr, handler) -> Result[Unit, HttpError]` | stable v1 | matches Go `ListenAndServe` |
        | `Server.serve_tls(addr, cert_pem, key_pem, handler) -> Result[Unit, HttpError]` | stable v1 | PEM-contents (not file paths like Go) ŌĆö documented divergence |
        | `Server.serve_static(addr, body) -> Result[Unit, HttpError]` | **`#[unstable]`** (decided keep, not remove, 2026-05-30) | strict subset of `serve(handler)`, matches no reference API. Removal was considered (zero real consumers) but **reversed**: it is now load-bearing as the **sole `#[unstable]` baked-stdlib method**, so it is the test specimen for the line-96 `#[unstable]`-baked-method enforcement (3 E2E tests: warn / `#[allow]`-suppress / `#[deny]`-promote). Removing it would delete that coverage or force a synthetic stdlib test fixture ŌĆö more wart than the mild "two ways to serve a fixed response" cost. Stays `#[unstable]`; revisit at v1 lock only if a real `#[unstable]` consumer appears to take over the canary role |
        | `struct Request` / `.path` / `.method` / `.body` / `.header` / `.headers` / `.query` | stable v1 | matches the request-read surface across all three references |
        | `effect resource Network` | stable v1 | unifies sends + receives per the stdlib `Stdin`/`Stdout`/`FileSystem` shape |

        **`#[unstable]` applied** to `Server.serve_static` in `runtime/stdlib/http.kara` (with a `note` pointing callers to `serve(handler)`). **The tag now enforces** at the call site as of 2026-05-30 ŌĆö the method / assoc-fn use-site lint gap (the dedicated `[x]` entry below) is closed, so `Server.serve_static(...)` call sites emit an `unstable_api` warning carrying the note, suppressible with `#[allow(unstable_api)]` / `[lints].allow_unstable_api = true` and promotable with `#[deny(unstable_api)]`. The `http_server` smoke suite (21 tests) and the `serve_static` smoke test still pass with the tag applied.

        **Scope note:** this freeze covers `http.kara` (the line-64 audit's subject). The `tcp.kara` / `tls.kara` / `ws.kara` public surfaces are now `Result`-uniform after the construction-method migration (their detailed freeze belongs to the TLS P0 entry, line ~96, when that surface locks).
    - [x] **`#[unstable]` / `#[deprecated]` use-site lint at method / assoc-fn call sites ŌĆö shipped 2026-05-30.** Surfaced by the `serve_static` `#[unstable]` tagging in the freeze list above. The name-based use-site lint (`check_unstable_use_at` / `check_deprecated_use_at`) fires only from `expr_ops.rs::infer_identifier` (free-fn-name + constant), `fields.rs` (struct/union-literal), and `lowering.rs::lower_path_type` (type-position) ŌĆö never from a method or associated call, so `#[unstable]` / `#[deprecated]` on a method (including `Server.serve_static`) was inert. Now closed, **unblocking enforcement of the entire `#[unstable]`-tagged-method surface** (lines 58/59/60/61 `std.http` / `std.tls` candidates, the line-62 stdlib audit's per-method tags, and the freeze-list `serve_static` tag). **Investigation correction to the original fix sketch.** The sketch ("thread `method_callee_types` into a check that looks up the method symbol's unstable/deprecation sidecar") was only half-right: it works for *user-authored* impl methods (their attributes land in the symbol-table `unstables`/`deprecations` sidecars via `collect_impl` ŌåÆ `record_unstable_if_present`), but **baked-stdlib methods never reach `collect_impl`** ŌĆö they live in `STDLIB_PROGRAMS`, walked by the typechecker directly (`register_baked_stdlib` ŌåÆ `env_add_impl`), and `env.impls`' `ImplInfo.methods` stores only `FunctionSig`, which drops the attributes. So `serve_static`'s tag was nowhere in any sidecar. **Implementation (two payload sources, one emitter).** (a) New `prelude::STDLIB_METHOD_STABILITY: LazyLock<HashMap<"Type.method", (Option<Unstable>, Option<Deprecation>)>>` ŌĆö the baked-stdlib mirror of the symbol-table sidecars, built once from the parsed stdlib AST's impl blocks (any future stdlib stability tag is picked up with no further wiring). (b) New `TypeChecker::check_method_stability(type_name, method, span)` consults the user-method sidecar (`SymbolTable::lookup_method` ŌåÆ `unstable_for` / `deprecation_for`) first, then the baked-stdlib side-table; both routes funnel through the refactored `emit_unstable_warning` / `emit_deprecated_warning` helpers (factored out of the name-based checks so message + cascade are identical). (c) Two call sites: `expr_method_call.rs` for instance methods (`recv.method()` ŌĆö at the central `method_callee_type_name` resolution point, so the hardcoded HTTP/TCP/TLS/WS arms are covered too) and `expr_ops.rs::resolve_path_type`'s assoc-fn-from-impl arm for static calls (`Type.method()`, which never touches `method_callee_types`). Note the original sketch's `method_callee_types` threading proved unnecessary ŌĆö `check_method_stability` keys directly off the resolved `(type_name, method)` at each call site, avoiding the chained-call span-collision hazard entirely. Tests: 8 in `tests/typechecker.rs` ŌĆö baked-stdlib `serve_static` (warn + note, `#[allow]` suppress, `#[deny]` promote), stable stdlib `Server.serve` no-fire, user instance-method `#[unstable]`, user assoc-fn `#[unstable]`, user instance-method `#[deprecated]`, stable user method no-fire. Full gate green (fmt, clippy `--all-targets --features llvm`, full non-llvm suite, codegen + http_server + http_client_codegen + tcp_listener + tls_codegen under llvm). **Known cosmetic gap (not this slice):** `karac check` does not print lint warnings to stderr at all (only errors) ŌĆö the new warnings live in `TypeCheckResult.warnings` and surface under `karac build` / `test` cascades and the test harness, exactly like every other lint; a `check`-prints-warnings change is a separate diagnostics-surface follow-up, untracked until a consumer wants it.

- [x] **`karac query effects` runs effect-check without typecheck ŌĆö under-reports instance-method effects. Fixed 2026-05-30.** Split out of the line 70 effect-annotation audit. `cmd_query`'s `QueryKind::Effects` arm called `pipeline.effectcheck()` directly after `resolve()`, skipping `pipeline.typecheck()`. Because `effectcheck()` sources its `method_callee_types` table from `self.typed` (None when typecheck didn't run), the effect-inference walker's `MethodCall` arm couldn't resolve instance-method callees to their precise `Type.method` key ŌĆö so `query effects` reported an empty/under-approximated effect set for any function whose effects come through an instance method (`c.get(...)` showed no `Network`, even though the same code under `karac build` / `karac test` correctly propagates it, because those pipelines typecheck before effect-checking). Not a miscompile ŌĆö codegen is driven by the typechecked pipeline, which is correct ŌĆö purely a diagnostic-tool accuracy gap. **Fix:** the Effects query now runs `pipeline.typecheck()` + `pipeline.lower()` before `effectcheck()`. **Correction to the original sketch ŌĆö the `Concurrency` query arm had the *same* defect, not the clean reference the sketch assumed.** The sketch said to mirror "the `Ownership` / `Concurrency` arms that already typecheck first"; on inspection only `Ownership` (and `CostSummary` / `Queries` / `Monomorphization`) typecheck first ŌĆö `Concurrency` ran `effectcheck()` ŌåÆ `concurrencycheck()` with no typecheck/lower, so concurrency analysis consumed the same under-reported effect set. Both arms are fixed in this slice (typecheck + lower before effectcheck). Reproduced before + after with a `c.get(...)` program: effects went from `inferred_effects:[]` to the `sends`+`receives(Network)` pair; `File.open` (qualified-path, already correct) unchanged. Regression test `tests/cli.rs::test_query_effects_resolves_instance_method_network_effect` runs the real binary end-to-end. Full gate green (fmt, clippy `--all-targets --features llvm`, full non-llvm suite incl. cli + effectchecker).
- [x] **P0 ŌĆö TLS ŌĆö vendored rustls + `ring` crypto provider (v1). CLOSED 2026-06-01.** `std.tls` API: cross-platform server + client surface; modern-TLS-only (no SSLv3, no insecure ciphers). `ring` shipped at v1 ŌĆö see the dedicated ┬¦ entry below for the aws-lc-rs reconciliation. rustls-provider plug points private at v1 (no public crypto-provider extension API, revisited at v2 if FIPS / post-quantum forces an aws-lc-rs swap). Audit posture: rustls + `ring` already audited upstream, but the FFI binding layer + `std.tls` API + verification callbacks + certificate-chain handling + error-mode coverage are new code and need their own audit pass before v1 ship. **CLOSED 2026-06-01:** all five implementation sub-slices (lines 103ŌĆō107) shipped; the pre-lock new-code audit (line 108) ratified clean by the owner security-reviewer pass; and both carved follow-ups are shipped ŌĆö the line-124 serve-loop slowloris hardening (`9f7f03da`) and the line-125 raw-`accept` blocking-handshake doc-note (`033d2e18`). No remaining TLS compiler / runtime / audit work blocks v1. (The v2-trigger crypto-provider swap to aws-lc-rs stays tracked in `deferred.md`, gated on FIPS / post-quantum needs.)
  - [x] **Server-side TLS transport ŌĆö `TlsListener` / `TlsStream` + rustls FFI.** Shipped under [Phase-6 line 236](phase-6-runtime.md) (all 5 sub-slices, 2026-05-27): 7 `karac_runtime_tls_*` externs in `runtime/src/tls.rs` (config-new from PEM, bind, accept+synchronous handshake, read/write/close), `runtime/stdlib/tls.kara` types (`TlsConfig` / `TlsListener.bind_tls` / `TlsListener.accept` / `TlsStream.read`/`write`/`write_all` + `Drop`), codegen lowerings in `src/codegen/tls.rs` + externs in `src/codegen.rs`, `WebSocket.accept_tls` (WS-over-TLS), and 9 runtime unit tests. Crypto provider is rustls 0.23 + `ring`. Server-side only ŌĆö no client auth, no custom roots. Verified E2E by the Demo 1 `wss://` round-trip.
  - [x] **Client-side TLS transport ŌĆö `TlsStream.connect` + handshake.** Shipped as a static method on the existing `TlsStream` (no new `TlsClientStream` type ŌĆö mirrors the `TcpStream` convention where the same stream type carries both directions). `TlsStream.connect(addr, server_name, roots_pem) -> TlsStream`: TCP connect + sync rustls handshake against `server_name` (SNI + cert verification) trusting only the certs in `roots_pem`. No fallback to webpki / system roots at v1 ŌĆö minimal explicit-PEM posture matching `TlsListener.bind_tls`. Runtime: new `karac_runtime_tls_client_connect` extern; `TlsSession.conn` widened from `ServerConnection` to the `rustls::Connection` enum so the shared per-fd `SESSIONS` map carries both directions and the existing `karac_runtime_tls_read` / `_write` / `_close` paths reuse unchanged (`drive_read` / `drive_write` and `TlsConnIo` in `event_loop.rs` now operate on `rustls::Connection`; both inner variants delegate the called methods). Codegen: extern decl in `Codegen::new`; `lower_tls_stream_connect` in `src/codegen/tls.rs` + dispatch arm in `assoc_call.rs`. Tests: 3 runtime units (`round_trip_via_client_connect_ffi` proves end-to-end handshake + read/write through the new FFI; `client_connect_with_bad_addr_returns_minus_one` and `_with_garbage_roots_returns_minus_one` pin failure modes) + an IR-grep codegen test (`test_ir_tls_stream_connect_dispatches_to_runtime_ffi`). Public-CA trust (webpki-roots default) is left for a follow-on once `Client.get("https://...")` lands ŌĆö at that point the trust-root question is resolved by the HTTP client's surface, not here. **Effect propagation (2026-05-30):** the TLS network methods (`TlsListener.accept`, `TlsStream.{connect,read,write,write_all}`) declare `with sends(Network) receives(Network)` in `tls.kara`, but baked-stdlib declarations aren't consumed for caller propagation ŌĆö they were seeded in `seed_builtin_effects` alongside the http/tcp/ws surface under the line-70 effect-annotation audit so callers actually inherit the network effect (regression: `tests/effectchecker.rs::tcp_tls_ws_network_effects_propagate_to_callers`).
  - [x] **HTTPS for `std.http` `Server.serve` ŌĆö std.http ├Ś TLS bridge.** Shipped via parallel `Server.serve_tls(addr, cert_pem, key_pem, handler)`. Runtime: `karac_runtime_serve_https` mirrors `karac_runtime_serve_http` but each accepted TCP stream is wrapped in `tokio_rustls::TlsAcceptor` before feeding hyper; PEM parsing reuses `tls::build_server_config` (now `pub(crate)`) ŌĆö rustls 0.23 + `ring` provider, modern TLS only. Per-connection handshake failures are swallowed so one bad client cannot break the accept loop. The handler shim (`Request` / `Response` ABI) is transport-independent, so codegen reuses `emit_http_handler_shim` and replicates the `Server.serve` rc ŌåÆ `Result[Unit, HttpError]` translation. Same `BOUND_PORT=<n>` stdout convention as plain `serve`. New runtime dep: `tokio-rustls = "0.26"` (features mirror `rustls`'s `ring` setup). Test: `tests/http_server.rs::test_server_serve_tls_https_smoke` reads the `tests/fixtures/tls/{cert,key}.pem` fixtures, embeds them in a K─üra source calling `Server.serve_tls`, performs an HTTPS GET via a hand-rolled sync-rustls client, and asserts the handler ran through the TLS layer (chain validation is disabled in the test client because the fixture has `CA:TRUE`; the smoke proves karac's serve_tls wiring, not rustls verification).
  - [x] **`TlsError` enum + error-mode coverage.** Shipped: `enum TlsError { Interrupted, Other(i32), Protocol(i32) }` in `runtime/stdlib/tls.kara`. `TlsStream.read` / `.write` / `.write_all` now return `Result[i64, TlsError]` (replaces `Result[i64, TcpError]`). Codegen: `wrap_tls_io_result` mirrors `wrap_tcp_io_result` but classifies the runtime's `n == -1` sentinel as `Protocol(-1)` instead of `Other(1)`; `lower_tls_stream_write_all`'s err_exit block applies the same classification before the `Result.Err` build. The enum is layout-seeded next to `TcpError` and added to `PRELUDE_TYPES` for scope-0 visibility. **Honest v1 framing:** rustls 0.23 does NOT distinguish handshake failure / cert-verify failure / renegotiation attempts at the API surface ŌĆö `Connection::complete_io` and `process_new_packets` collapse them into opaque errors ŌĆö so v1 ships ONE `Protocol(code)` variant rather than the originally-proposed four dead variants. The carried i32 is currently always `-1` and reserved for finer-grained classification if rustls grows a richer error API. Known v1 quirk: `n == -1` from `io_err_to_neg` with EPERM (errno=1) mis-classifies as `Protocol(-1)` rather than `Other(1)` ŌĆö EPERM during a TLS socket read/write is exceedingly rare; a runtime sentinel rework that disambiguates lands if a real workload surfaces it. Tests: `test_ir_tls_stream_read_wraps_with_tls_io_result` + `test_ir_tls_stream_write_all_classifies_protocol_in_err_exit` pin the codegen routing.
  - [x] **Crypto provider ŌĆö `ring` at v1, aws-lc-rs deferred to v2+.** Resolved by choosing `ring` (over the originally-named aws-lc-rs) and amending the line-20 parent wording to match shipped reality. Rationale: `ring` ships in pure-Rust + asm with no nasm build dependency (`runtime/Cargo.toml` strips `aws_lc_rs` for exactly this); both providers are upstream-audited and rustls treats them as interchangeable behind `CryptoProvider`. Same `ring` provider is installed explicitly at every `ServerConfig::builder_with_provider` / `ClientConfig::builder_with_provider` site (`runtime/src/tls.rs::build_server_config` / `build_client_config`), so there's no process-global `install_default` state to migrate later. **v2 trigger** stays as documented on the parent: FIPS-certified deployments or post-quantum cipher requirements would force aws-lc-rs; the provider plug-points stay private at v1 so the migration is an internal swap rather than an API break. Tracked separately in `deferred.md` if the trigger fires.
  - [x] **Pre-lock new-code audit. RATIFIED 2026-06-01** (owner security-reviewer pass ŌĆö items 1ŌĆō4 & 6 confirmed clean against current source, item 5's finding already carved to line 124, plus one new doc-note carved below). Prerequisites now met ŌĆö server transport (line 21), client transport (line 22), HTTPS for `Server.serve` (line 23), `TlsError` (line 24), and crypto-provider reconciliation (line 25) are all `[x]`, so the audit sees the real v1 shape. rustls + `ring` are upstream-audited; what needs an in-house pass is the new-code surface that wraps them. **Concrete review checklist** (split this entry as findings land):
    - **FFI safety contracts** ŌĆö every `#[no_mangle] unsafe extern "C" fn karac_runtime_tls_*` in `runtime/src/tls.rs` + `karac_runtime_serve_https` in `runtime/src/lib.rs`: documented `# Safety` clause matches the caller-side codegen invariants; null-pointer / negative-length / invalid-utf-8 paths all reject with the documented sentinel; no use-after-free across the `SESSIONS` map's `register` / `lookup` / `close` lifecycle.
    - **`std.tls` public API shape** ŌĆö `TlsListener` / `TlsStream` / `TlsConfig` field opacity (no field-access escape hatch); `bind_tls` / `accept` / `connect` / `read` / `write` / `write_all` signatures match TCP siblings for predictability; `Drop` for `TlsListener` frees the config + closes fd, `Drop` for `TlsStream` closes fd (no double-free, no leaked sessions).
    - **Verification callbacks + cert-chain handling** ŌĆö `build_server_config` accepts only valid PEM via `rustls-pemfile`; private-key formats (PKCS#8 / RSA / SEC1) all parse correctly; `build_client_config` builds a root store from supplied PEM only (no implicit webpki / system roots); rustls's `with_safe_default_protocol_versions` is the only `ProtocolVersions` setter (no SSLv3 / TLS1.0 / TLS1.1 surface).
    - **`TlsError` coverage** ŌĆö the three variants (`Interrupted` / `Other` / `Protocol`) are exhaustive for the runtime's negative-return scheme; no information leakage in the `Protocol(code)` payload (the `-1` carried today is generic); EPERM-vs-Protocol ambiguity (line 24 known quirk) is documented and acceptable for v1 or warrants the runtime sentinel rework.
    - **HTTPS-via-tokio-rustls integration** ŌĆö per-connection handshake failures (`acceptor.accept(tcp_stream).await` Err arm in `karac_runtime_serve_https`) drop the connection silently without leaking session state or opening a DoS through repeated bad handshakes; tokio-rustls's `TlsAcceptor` carries the same `Arc<ServerConfig>` the existing `tls.rs` builds (no provider/version drift between the WS-over-TLS and HTTPS-server paths); the runtime's `BOUND_PORT=<n>` stdout leak (tests-only convention) is documented as such.
    - **Test-cert fixture posture** ŌĆö `tests/fixtures/tls/{cert,key}.pem` are clearly marked self-signed CN=localhost test-only material (README + script); the `NoVerify` rustls `ServerCertVerifier` lives only in test code (`tests/http_server.rs`), not in any runtime path.

    **New-code audit walk (2026-05-31): all six checklist items executed; five close clean (one with a doc-drift fix), one split a real finding into its own `[ ]` entry. Down to security-reviewer ratification.** **RATIFIED 2026-06-01** ŌĆö owner security-reviewer pass re-verified every clean verdict against current source (not just the walk's prose). Items 2/3/4 confirmed by reading the actual `tls.rs` config builders + accept paths; item 1 deepened past the walk's name-narrow grep (see its margin note); item 6 unchanged. Two dispositions recorded: line 124 severity confirmed (pre-public-v1, not Demo-1-blocking), and one new doc-note finding carved out of item 5's re-read (raw-`accept` blocking handshake ŌĆö the `[ ]` below line 124).
    1. *FFI safety contracts* ŌĆö **clean.** Every `karac_runtime_tls_*` + `karac_runtime_serve_https` carries a `# Safety` clause matching its codegen invariants; null / non-positive-length / invalid-UTF-8 inputs all reject with the documented sentinel (`null` config / `-1` fd / `0`-byte I/O return ŌĆö verified at `config_new` / `tls_accept` / `tls_client_connect` / `tls_read` / `tls_write`); `config_free` is null-idempotent (double-free is documented UB, resolved by codegen's single-`Drop` guarantee); the `SESSIONS` register/lookup/close lifecycle has no use-after-free in the documented one-I/O-op-per-connection-at-a-time posture (the inner per-fd `Mutex` serialises read/write; the read/write paths use the borrow-the-fd `from_raw_fd` + `into_raw_fd` pattern so no spurious `close(2)` fires). **Documented v1 limitation (not a bug):** `tls_close` removes the session + closes the fd *without* taking the inner `Mutex`, so a `close` racing an in-flight I/O on the same fd would be a fd-reuse hazard ŌĆö unreachable from the parking primitive's per-connection serial dispatch, called out in the `tls.rs` module doc. **Ratification note (2026-06-01):** the in-house re-check deepened this past the walk's original name-narrow grep (which only matched the `NoVerify` *type name*) ŌĆö confirmed zero `dangerous()` / `with_custom_certificate_verifier` / `set_certificate_verifier` / `DangerousClientConfig` / `ServerCertVerifier` anywhere in `runtime/`, and zero bare `ClientConfig::builder()` / `ServerConfig::builder()` sites (every config uses `builder_with_provider`, so no `install_default` global-provider reliance). Verdict holds; the original *method* was too narrow to use as precedent for future verifier-absence checks.
    2. *`std.tls` API shape* ŌĆö **clean after a doc-drift fix** (`[x]` below). Field opacity holds (`TlsConfig` empty, `TlsListener {fd, config}`, `TlsStream {fd}` are codegen-only structs with no user field-access path); `bind_tls`/`accept`/`connect`/`read`/`write`/`write_all` mirror the TCP siblings; `Drop` for `TlsListener` frees config + closes fd and `Drop` for `TlsStream` closes fd (single-free ŌĆö the i32 handle is zeroed on move, no double-free, the session entry is removed on close).
    3. *Verification callbacks + cert-chain* ŌĆö **clean, fails-secure.** `build_server_config` accepts only `rustls-pemfile`-valid PEM and `private_key()` covers PKCS#8 / RSA / SEC1; `build_client_config` builds the root store from the supplied PEM **only**, with NO implicit webpki / system-root fallback, and an empty / unparseable roots set fails *closed* (`NoCertsFound` ŌåÆ `-1`, never the "trust-nothing degrades to trust-all" footgun); `with_safe_default_protocol_versions` is the sole protocol setter at all four config sites (`tls.rs` ├Ś3 + `lib.rs` http-client agent), so there is no SSLv3 / TLS1.0 / TLS1.1 surface; no insecure verifier exists in any runtime path (`NoVerify` is confined to `tests/http_server.rs` + `tests/coro_e2e.rs`, grep-confirmed).
    4. *`TlsError` coverage* ŌĆö **clean.** `Interrupted` / `Other(errno)` / `Protocol(code)` (+ the line-74 construction causes) are exhaustive for the negative-return scheme; no information leakage in `Protocol(code)` (the carried `-1` is generic); the EPERM-vs-`Protocol` ambiguity (line 24 known quirk) is documented and acceptable for v1.
    5. *HTTPS-via-tokio-rustls* ŌĆö **partially clean.** Per-connection handshake failures (`acceptor.accept(tcp_stream).await` Err) drop the connection with no session-state leak Ō£ō; `acceptor.clone()` shares the one `Arc<ServerConfig>` the existing `tls.rs` builds, so there is no provider/version drift between the WS-over-TLS and HTTPS-server paths Ō£ō; the `BOUND_PORT=<n>` stdout leak is documented tests-only Ō£ō. **BUT** the "no DoS through repeated bad handshakes" sub-claim does **NOT** hold ŌĆö carved as its own `[ ]` P0 below.

    - [x] **`std.tls` API-doc drift ŌĆö stale `fd: -1` sentinel language. Fixed 2026-05-31 (surfaced by item 2 of this walk).** After the line-71 `Result` migration, `runtime/stdlib/tls.kara`'s docstrings still described `TlsListener.accept` / `TlsStream.connect` / `TlsListener.bind_tls` as returning a `TlsStream { fd: -1 }` / `TlsListener { fd: -1, config: 0 }` sentinel in four spots (file-header summary + each of the three method docstrings) ŌĆö directly contradicting the migrated `Result[T, TlsError]` signatures a few lines below in the same docstring. Corrected to describe the `Ok(...)` / `Err(TlsError.*)` shape (with the `connect` path noting the line-74 branchable TCP-connect causes). Comment-only change to a `.kara` stdlib file ŌĆö no codegen / behaviour change, Rust + codegen test surface unaffected; `cargo fmt --all -- --check` clean.
    - [x] **P0 ŌĆö server accept-loop resource bounds (handshake/header timeout + bounded connection concurrency). Shipped 2026-06-01 (`9f7f03da`).** Surfaced by item 5 of this audit walk. All three `karac_runtime_serve_*` accept loops (`serve_http` `lib.rs` ~4292, `serve_https` ~4407, `serve_http_static` ~4503) do an **unbounded `tokio::spawn` per accepted connection with no timeout on the handshake / first-request-header read and no cap on concurrent in-flight connections.** A slowloris-style client that opens many TCP connections and either (HTTPS) never completes the TLS `ClientHello` ŌĆö leaving each spawned task awaiting `acceptor.accept(tcp_stream).await` indefinitely ŌĆö or (plain HTTP) dribbles request headers, exhausts tokio tasks / socket fds / memory. **Not TLS-specific:** the unbounded-spawn pattern is shared across all three serve paths and hyper's http1 builder ships no default header-read timeout, so the plain-HTTP path carries the symmetric exposure ŌĆö a TLS-only patch would be a workaround (no-workarounds policy). **v1 framing:** severity is deployment-dependent (loopback Demo 1 is unaffected; an internet-facing backend is exposed), but the friction-zero-backend positioning means it must be hardened before a public-facing v1 (it does NOT block Demo 1). **Fix shape:** wrap the handshake / first-header read in a `tokio::time::timeout`, and gate each `tokio::spawn` behind a `tokio::sync::Semaphore`-bounded connection permit (configurable, sane default), applied uniformly to all three serve loops; add a slowloris-style regression test (open N stalled connections, assert a healthy connection still completes + bounded task/fd growth). Cross-ref: the plain HTTP server surface (line 15 routing / line 16a keep-alive). **Severity ratified 2026-06-01 (owner):** pre-public-v1 hardening, does **NOT** block Demo 1 ŌĆö Demo 1 is 1M *completed-handshake* idle connections over loopback/controlled clients, which never exercises the incomplete-handshake threat. The connection-cap half of the fix carries a mild Demo-1 robustness angle (fd/task backpressure at 1M conns with no cap), but that's tuning, not the DoS, and doesn't change the non-blocking call. **Shipped as `ServeLimits` (read once per serve call), applied uniformly to all three loops.** `header_timeout`: **on by default** (10 s; `KARAC_HTTP_HEADER_TIMEOUT_MS` overrides, `0` disables) ŌĆö plain HTTP via hyper's `TokioTimer`-backed `header_read_timeout`, HTTPS additionally wraps `acceptor.accept()` in `tokio::time::timeout` (the primary HTTPS vector). `conn_permits`: **off by default** (unbounded; `KARAC_HTTP_MAX_CONNS=<n>` bounds it), permit acquired *before* `accept` so reaching the cap applies backpressure at the OS accept backlog rather than spawning unbounded. The on/off default posture was the owner's call (timeout on, cap off ŌĆö never silently breaks the 1M-idle workload). Parse logic split into pure `ServeLimits::from_raw` for env-free unit testing; `tokio` gains the `time` + `sync` features. **9 runtime unit tests:** `from_raw` parse matrix (default / explicit / `0`-disables / garbage-falls-back / whitespace-trim, cap on/off), semaphore backpressure (cap=1 blocks until released; no-cap never blocks), and two behavioral tests driving real hyper connections ŌĆö a slow-header connection is reaped by the timeout, a healthy request still succeeds under it. Gate green: fmt, clippy `--all --all-targets` ┬▒`llvm`, full non-llvm suite, `http_server` (21 E2E), `http_client`/`tcp`/`ws` codegen. (One pre-existing unrelated failure on `main`: `tls_codegen::test_ir_websocket_accept_tls_parks_then_calls_runtime_ffi` ŌĆö confirmed failing without this change too, not in scope.)
    - [x] **Doc-note ŌĆö `TlsListener.accept` blocking handshake (carved from the 2026-06-01 audit ratification, item-5 re-read). Shipped 2026-06-01 (`033d2e18`).** The raw `std.tls` server path's `karac_runtime_tls_accept` (`runtime/src/tls.rs:325`) runs the rustls handshake **synchronously** via `conn.complete_io(&mut sock)` on the calling thread. This is correct, by-design semantics for a low-level blocking-socket primitive (mirrors Go's `tls.Conn.Handshake()`), but it means a user-authored accept loop built on `TlsListener.accept()` lets one stalled/malicious client block the **entire** accept loop ŌĆö a strictly worse shape than the line-124 managed-serve-loop slowloris, which only parks one tokio task. **Deliberately NOT folded into line 124:** these are different layers. The three `karac_runtime_serve_*` loops are karac's loops (karac owns the accept policy ŌåÆ karac hardens them), whereas `TlsListener.accept` is the raw you-own-the-loop primitive ŌĆö injecting a forced timeout/semaphore there would bake accept policy into a primitive whose contract is that the caller sets policy. **Fix = doc-only:** a one-line `runtime/stdlib/tls.kara` docstring on `TlsListener.accept` stating the handshake is blocking and that user-built accept loops must spawn-per-connection and/or apply their own handshake timeout. No codegen / behaviour change. **Shipped:** added an *Availability note ŌĆö you own the accept loop* paragraph to `TlsListener.accept`'s docstring conveying exactly the above (synchronous handshake ŌćÆ a stalled/malicious peer blocks the whole user-built accept loop; by-design, mirrors Go's `tls.Conn.Handshake()`; cross-refs the managed `Server.serve`/`serve_tls` line-124 hardening). Comment-only; stdlib parse + typecheck verified.
