- [x] **P0 ŌĆö WebSocket ŌĆö RFC 6455. CLOSED 2026-06-01.** Server-side framing (continuation, ping/pong, close), handshake, message/binary distinction, fragmentation, masking. Built on `std.http` upgrade handshake. The canonical idle-keep-alive workload ŌĆö Demo 1 (1M+ idle connections) is shaped around this surface. **CLOSED:** all RFC 6455 framing/handshake sub-slices (9e.1ŌĆō9e.4 + WS-over-TLS) shipped and verified; the compliance audit walk + three-lens reviewer ratification ran clean; both v1-blocking handshake gaps (┬¦4.2.1 validation + the residual dribble-slowloris) are fixed, and the only remaining carves (close-frame conformance sub-P1, subprotocol negotiation, `recv_text` UTF-8 validation) are genuinely-additive post-v1 items that do not gate v1. No remaining WS compiler/runtime work blocks v1. Effects: same `sends(Network)` / `receives(Network)` as `std.http` ŌĆö and as of 2026-05-30 the WebSocket network methods (`accept` / `accept_tls` / `recv_text` / `send_text` / `recv_binary` / `send_binary` / `send_text_masked` / `send_binary_masked`) actually *propagate* that effect to callers, via the `seed_builtin_effects` extension recorded under the line-70 effect-annotation audit (the stdlib `with` clauses alone were decorative ŌĆö baked-stdlib declarations aren't consumed for propagation).

    **RFC 6455 compliance audit walk (2026-06-01).** The framing + handshake surface shipped incrementally across Phase-6 slices 9e.1ŌĆō9e.4 (text/binary frames, FIN/opcode/payload-length encoding, masked send, continuation-frame fragmentation reassembly, ping/pong/close control frames, the SHA-1 + base64 `Sec-WebSocket-Accept` handshake, and WS-over-TLS via `accept_tls`); the runtime FFI lives in `runtime/src/event_loop.rs` (`karac_runtime_ws_*`) with codegen lowerings in `src/codegen/tcp.rs` + `src/codegen/tls.rs`. The audit walked the implemented surface against the RFC and confirmed the framing/fragmentation/masking layers are wire-correct, with the control layer correct on the data-bearing path but carrying a close-frame conformance gap surfaced at ratification (see the `[ ]` close-frame entry) (38 runtime unit tests in `event_loop.rs` + 18 codegen IR-grep tests in `tests/ws_framing.rs`). It surfaced **two genuine v1-blocking gaps in the *handshake* path** (both fixed this slice, see the `[x]` sub-entries) plus two genuinely-post-v1-additive gaps (carved `[ ]` below), and added the **first end-to-end compiled-binary round-trip coverage** for the plain-TCP path (previously only WS-over-TLS had an E2E test; the plain path was IR-grep-only per the `tests/ws_framing.rs` header note).

    **Reviewer ratification (2026-06-01) ŌĆö RATIFIED with two carve-outs.** A three-lens reviewer pass (correctness / security-DoS / RFC-6455-conformance) re-verified the walk's verdicts against current source rather than the prose. Net: the change is a correct improvement ŌĆö RFC ┬¦4.2.1 validation is wire-conformant, the handshake-timeout clear-on-success path is exactly right (established idle connections never inherit the deadline, so Demo 1 is structurally safe), no fd / TLS-session leak on any reject path, no info disclosure (the runtime-side request `preview` is `eprintln`-to-stderr, env-gated, never sent to the client), and there are **zero hard MUST-violations on the normal client-masked server-role path**. Two findings were carved (both consistent with the line-124/125 dispositioning ŌĆö neither blocks Demo 1): (1) the handshake read-timeout is a *per-read* `SO_RCVTIMEO`, not a whole-request wall-clock bound, so a **dribble-slowloris** survives it (bounded only by the 8 KiB request cap; the TLS handshake pool's unbounded work-queue amplifies the blast radius) ŌĆö carved as a pre-public-v1 P0 below, and the overstated "bounds the handshake" wording corrected here and in the runtime comments; (2) **close-frame handling** does not echo the peer's close status code, does not validate the inbound close body, and TCP-drops on protocol error instead of sending Close 1002 (┬¦5.5.1 / ┬¦7.4.1) ŌĆö carved as a sub-P1 below. The minor ┬¦5.2 64-bit-length MSB-zero check is absent but harmless (the `out_max_len` bounds check rejects any oversize length first); folded into the close-frame entry's scope. **Parent closed `[x]` 2026-06-01** once the carved residual-slowloris P0 shipped (the `[x]` entry below) ŌĆö mirroring how the TLS P0 (line 102) closed after its carved line-124/125 follow-ons landed; the additive deferrals (subprotocol, UTF-8, close-frame) do not gate v1 on their own and remain `[ ]` as post-v1 work.
    - [x] **Handshake hardening ŌĆö RFC ┬¦4.2.1 header validation + slowloris read-timeout (this slice).** Both server handshake paths (`karac_runtime_ws_accept` plain TCP, and `ws_handshake_conn_tls` ŌåÆ `ws_drive_upgrade_handshake` for WS-over-TLS) previously accepted **any** request carrying a `Sec-WebSocket-Key`, ignoring the other RFC ┬¦4.2.1-mandated request headers (`Upgrade: websocket`, `Connection: Upgrade`, `Sec-WebSocket-Version: 13`) ŌĆö a real RFC-6455-conformance gap for a P0 labelled "RFC 6455", and a slowloris exposure symmetric to the line-124 managed-serve-loop hardening (the blocking handshake read had no timeout, so a peer that completed the TCP connect but stalled/dribbled the upgrade request could pin the accept indefinitely). **Fix (`runtime/src/event_loop.rs`):** new pure `ws_validate_handshake(request) -> Result[&key, WsHandshakeReject]` checks Upgrade/Connection (token-in-comma-list, so `Connection: keep-alive, Upgrade` matches) then `Sec-WebSocket-Version` (token-in-list offering `13`) then key-presence, in RFC order; a non-conforming request is answered with `400 Bad Request` (missing Upgrade/Connection/Key) or `426 Upgrade Required` + `Sec-WebSocket-Version: 13` (unsupported version, per RFC ┬¦4.4) **rather than upgrading anyway**. The two handshake paths were de-duplicated ŌĆö `karac_runtime_ws_accept` now drives the same generic `ws_drive_upgrade_handshake<S: Read + Write>` the TLS path uses (its cfg gate relaxed from `feature = "tls"` to plain `unix`, since it carries no TLS types), so both transports get identical validation + rejection-status behaviour. A `set_read_timeout` is applied to the socket for the **pre-`101` phase only** and cleared the instant the upgrade completes (so post-upgrade framed I/O, which parks through the event loop, never inherits the deadline) ŌĆö configurable via `KARAC_WS_HANDSHAKE_TIMEOUT_MS` (**on by default, 10 s**; `0` disables). The default-on posture is safe for Demo 1: it governs only the handshake, never an established idle connection, so the 1M-idle-connection workload is structurally unaffected (unlike the line-124 connection-*cap*, which stayed off-by-default for exactly that reason). **Ratification correction:** this is a *per-read* inactivity deadline (`SO_RCVTIMEO`), which reaps a silently-stalled peer but not a byte-per-interval *dribbler* ŌĆö it does **not** bound total handshake duration; the whole-request wall-clock deadline is the carved residual-slowloris P0 below. The deliberately-unenforced request-line / `Host` checks are documented as a non-gap (every real client sends them; rejecting buys no protocol safety). **Tests:** 12 new runtime unit tests (validation accept + each rejection class, token-in-list for Connection + Version, case-insensitive header names, the 400/426 response-status shapes, the timeout parse matrix `default`/`explicit`/`0`-disables/`whitespace`/`garbage`-falls-back, a behavioral `ws_read_http_request`-reaps-stalled-peer timeout test, and a full `karac_runtime_ws_accept` round-trip asserting a real `426` for a bad version). The stale "v1 limitation" comment block in `event_loop.rs` was rewritten to describe the now-enforced validation + timeout knob.
    - [x] **End-to-end compiled-binary round-trip tests for the plain-TCP path (this slice).** `tests/ws_framing.rs` was IR-grep-only for the plain path (its header documented that the historical blocker ŌĆö stdlib `stream.fd` field access returning const 0 ŌĆö was lifted by the `WebSocket.accept(listener)` builder, which the WS-over-TLS coro E2E already exploits). Added two real link-and-run tests to `tests/coro_e2e.rs` (reusing its `compile_link_coro` / `BOUND_PORT` harness, gated on `--features llvm` + the runtime archive): `e2e_plain_websocket_text_echo_roundtrip` compiles a kara `WebSocket.accept` ŌåÆ `recv_text`/`send_text` echo server, drives a hand-rolled masked-frame client against the real binary, and asserts the payload echoes back (proving the runtime framing FFI + codegen wiring round-trips, not just the IR shape); `e2e_plain_websocket_handshake_rejects_bad_request` drives the line-128 handshake validation through a real binary ŌĆö an unsupported `Sec-WebSocket-Version` gets `426`, a request missing `Upgrade`/`Connection` gets `400`, never a spurious `101`. Existing WS-over-TLS coro E2E (`coroutine_ws_over_tls_handler_executes` + the concurrent-handlers regression) re-verified green under the handshake changes.
    - [x] **P0 ŌĆö residual handshake slowloris (per-read vs whole-request deadline + unbounded TLS handshake-pool queue). Carved + SHIPPED 2026-06-01.** The line-131 handshake read-timeout is `SO_RCVTIMEO`, a *per-read* inactivity deadline that re-arms on every successful `read(2)` ŌĆö so it reaps a silently-stalled peer but **not** a peer that dribbles one byte per `(timeout ŌłÆ ╬Ą)` interval, which keeps the clock reset indefinitely. Such a connection is bounded only by `ws_read_http_request`'s 8 KiB `MAX_REQUEST_SIZE` cap (Ōēł 8192 ├Ś timeout worst case ŌåÆ ~22 h at the 10 s default). **Blast radius is transport-dependent:** the plain path (`karac_runtime_ws_accept`) runs one dribbler per codegen-parked accept task (no per-connection concurrency cap, the line-124 `conn_permits` analog is absent here), but the **TLS path is worse** ŌĆö `ws_handshake_pool_for` runs a *fixed* worker pool (`max(32, 2├Ścpus)`) draining an **unbounded `VecDeque<i32>` work queue**, so ~32 dribblers saturate every worker and the queue then grows without bound, stalling the whole WS-over-TLS accept pipeline (the line-125 "one stalled peer blocks the loop" shape, amplified to N peers blocking the pool). **Severity: pre-public-v1 hardening, does NOT block Demo 1** (which is completed-handshake idle connections over loopback/controlled clients ŌĆö the dribble vector needs adversarial clients and never fires there) ŌĆö same disposition as line-124/125. **Fix shape:** capture `Instant::now()` at handshake entry and enforce a whole-request wall-clock deadline inside both `ws_read_http_request`'s read loop and the TLS `complete_io` phase (so per-read inactivity *and* total duration are bounded), plus a per-listener in-flight-handshake cap on the TLS pool's work queue (reject/backpressure beyond N pending, mirroring line-124's `conn_permits`); add a dribble-slowloris regression test (the existing `test_ws_read_http_request_times_out_on_stalled_peer` only covers the silent-stall case). Reuse the `KARAC_WS_HANDSHAKE_TIMEOUT_MS` knob for the wall-clock bound; a new `KARAC_WS_MAX_PENDING_HANDSHAKES` for the pool cap. **Shipped (`runtime/src/event_loop.rs`):** (a) **whole-request wall-clock deadline** ŌĆö `ws_read_http_request` gained a `deadline: Option<Instant>` checked before every read; both accept paths derive it from the handshake timeout (`now + t`) so the per-read `SO_RCVTIMEO` (reaps a silent stall) and the deadline (reaps a dribbler) together bound total handshake-read time to Ōēł `2t`. The TLS `complete_io` (dribbled-`ClientHello`) phase is bounded by a new `DeadlineStream<S>` `Read`/`Write` adapter that fails reads with `TimedOut` past the deadline; the upgrade phase is bounded by the same deadline inside `ws_read_http_request`. On by default (the timeout is), cleared on success, so Demo 1's established idle connections are untouched. (b) **TLS handshake-pool in-flight cap** ŌĆö `WsHandshakePool` gained a `max_pending: Option<usize>` from `KARAC_WS_MAX_PENDING_HANDSHAKES` (**off by default**, mirroring the line-124 connection-cap disposition); the `karac_runtime_ws_accept_tls` accept-drain checks it *before* each `accept(2)` and stops draining at the cap, leaving excess connections in the OS accept backlog (true backpressure, nothing dropped). With the deadline reaping dribblers in Ōēł `2t`, workers free promptly even with the cap off; the cap is defense-in-depth against a fresh-connection flood. **Tests:** `test_ws_read_http_request_deadline_reaps_dribbler` (a 50 ms/byte dribbler past a 300 ms deadline is reaped < 900 ms, not held to the 8 KiB cap), `test_ws_max_pending_from_raw_parse_matrix` (off/ŌĆŗ`0`-off/ŌĆŗpositive/ŌĆŗgarbage/ŌĆŗnegative), plus the existing silent-stall + WS-over-TLS concurrent E2E re-verified green. Gate: fmt, clippy `--all-targets` ┬▒`tls`, runtime WS units (tls 40 / no-tls 38), llvm `coro_e2e` WS (plain + TLS).
    - [ ] **Close-frame conformance ŌĆö status-code echo + inbound close-body validation + protocol-error Close 1002 (┬¦5.5.1 / ┬¦7.4.1). Carved at 2026-06-01 ratification.** On receiving a client Close (0x8), `ws_recv_data_frame_inner` replies with an **empty** Close frame and returns 0 ŌĆö it does not echo the peer's 2-byte status code (┬¦5.5.1 SHOULD), does not parse/validate the inbound close body (a 1-byte close body is malformed per ┬¦5.5.1; reserved codes 1005/1006/1015 in the body are invalid), and every decoder protocol-violation TCP-drops (returns `-1`) rather than sending a Close frame with code **1002** (┬¦7.4.1 SHOULD). These are SHOULD-level gaps (no hard MUST-violation on the data path), but the audit's "wire-correct control layer" wording overclaimed them, so they are tracked here. **Also folded in (minor):** the ┬¦5.2 64-bit extended-length MSB-must-be-zero check is absent ŌĆö harmless because the `out_max_len` bounds check rejects any oversize length first, but it's a literal ┬¦5.2 conformance miss. Build alongside an Autobahn-style conformance pass if/when WS conformance becomes a v1 marketing claim; until then these are low-real-world-impact niceties.
    - [ ] **Subprotocol / extension negotiation (`Sec-WebSocket-Protocol` / `Sec-WebSocket-Extensions`).** The `101` response never echoes a negotiated subprotocol or extension. RFC 6455 permits a server to ignore these (a client that *requires* one will fail its own check), so this is post-v1-additive, not a v1 blocker. Build when a real consumer needs subprotocol routing (e.g. a kata that multiplexes `graphql-ws` vs a custom protocol on one endpoint) ŌĆö the handshake response builder in `ws_drive_upgrade_handshake` is the single insertion point.
    - [ ] **`recv_text` UTF-8 validation (RFC ┬¦8.1 / ┬¦8.2).** A text frame's payload is currently passed through verbatim without validating it is well-formed UTF-8 (the runtime returns raw bytes; `recv_binary` deliberately passes through, and the two share the frame-decode path). RFC ┬¦8.1 requires text frames carry valid UTF-8 and ┬¦8.2 mandates failing the connection with close code 1007 on a violation. Deferred as a strictness nicety ŌĆö it risks rejecting existing callers that (ab)use `recv_text` as a byte channel, and the conformance value is low for a server that hands payloads to user code. Revisit if Autobahn-style conformance becomes a v1 marketing claim.
- [ ] **P0 ŌĆö `karac new <name>` default project template ŌĆö backend HTTP server skeleton.** Default scaffolding: `std.http` + `std.tracing` + `/health` endpoint + `/ws` WebSocket route. `--lib` for libraries, `--cli` for CLI tools, `--data` for data-pipeline scaffolding (Kafka consumer + processor + sink shape). Default-being-backend reinforces the positioning at the friction-zero entry point.
  - [x] **`karac new <name>` command + `--backend` (default) / `--lib` / `--cli` flags + backend HTTP skeleton + `/health` endpoint.** Shipped 2026-05-29. `karac new my_api` creates `./my_api/` with `src/main.kara` carrying `Server.serve("127.0.0.1:8080", handle)`, manual `req.path()` dispatch per the v1 routing answer (phase-8 line 15), and a `/health` endpoint returning `200 OK / ok`. Effect declarations (`sends(Network) receives(Network)`) propagated through `main` so the generated source effectchecks cleanly. `karac init --backend` joins the existing `karac init` template menu so the bare-cwd init form gets the same skeleton. `--cli` maps to the existing `Template::Bin` (the hello-world scaffold; renaming the enum would have broken every existing test). 9 new tests: 4 scaffold unit tests in `src/scaffold.rs::tests` (anchors in the body, placeholder test shape, scaffold-writes-files, opposite-entry-collision); 4 integration tests in `tests/scaffold.rs` (writes-expected-files, parses-resolves-typechecks-effectchecks, test-file-parses) + 1 codegen E2E (compiles + links to a real executable, gated on `--features llvm` and the runtime archive). Full v1 flow verified manually: `karac new my_api && cd my_api && karac build` produces a working backend binary on first try.
  - [ ] **`--data` Kafka pipeline scaffold.** Reserved in the `karac new` parser with a structured `"deferred"` diagnostic. Blocked on a Kafka client surface that doesn't exist yet ŌĆö the entry implies a `kafka-rs` (or equivalent) dep + `std.process` integration for the pipeline-stage harness. Implementation shape per the parent line: consumer + processor + sink scaffold with topic-configuration scaffolding, dead-letter routing primitive, and an Arrow IPC handoff between processor and sink. Lands once a data-engineering consumer signals demand; until then `karac new --data` rejects loudly so users get a "planned, not yet" signal instead of "unknown flag".
  - [ ] **`/ws` WebSocket route on the HTTP server ŌĆö the original "one new arm" plan was infeasible against the shipped surface; re-scoped 2026-06-01.** The WebSocket RFC 6455 surface shipped (line 128, CLOSED 2026-06-01), but it does **not** compose with `Server.serve`'s request handler the way this entry originally assumed. The shipped WS entry points are `WebSocket.accept(listener: TcpListener)` / `accept_tls(listener: TlsListener)` ŌĆö a **separate accept loop** (see `examples/ws_idle_holder`, the Demo-1 flagship, which runs exactly this standalone loop and never touches `Server.serve`). `Server.serve(addr, handler)` is a hyper request/response loop: the handler receives an **opaque `Request`** (`path`/`method`/`body`/`header`/`headers`/`query` only ŌĆö no socket access) and returns a `Response`, with no upgrade hook (line 15 ratifies this one-handler-dispatch model). So there is no `WebSocket.accept(req)` and no way to add a `/ws` arm inside the `Server.serve` handler ŌĆö the original "no scaffold reshape, just one new arm" claim was wrong. **Two genuinely-separate things were conflated:** (a) a real `Server.serve` WebSocket-upgrade integration (carved as its own `[ ]` below ŌĆö the actual gate for a `/ws`-on-the-same-HTTP-server route), and (b) merely demonstrating the *standalone* WS idiom in the scaffold. (b) is deliberately NOT done: `Server.serve` blocks the calling thread, so a standalone `WebSocket.accept` loop cannot coexist with it in one `main()` without spawning the server into a task ŌĆö an advanced shape wrong for a default `karac new` skeleton, and the standalone idiom is already demonstrated properly in `examples/ws_idle_holder`. The backend scaffold stays HTTP-only (`Server.serve` + `/health`) until the upgrade hook below lands.
    - [ ] **`Server.serve` WebSocket-upgrade integration ŌĆö the real gate for a `/ws` route on the HTTP server.** For `/ws` to be a route on the same server as `/health` (the canonical backend shape: axum, Go `net/http` + gorilla/websocket, express + ws), `Server.serve` needs an in-place upgrade path: hyper's HTTP/1.1 `Upgrade` handling detaches the raw upgraded TCP (or TLS) stream, which is then fed to the existing WebSocket framing FFI (`karac_runtime_ws_*` in `runtime/src/event_loop.rs`). **Open design question ŌĆö handler signaling:** the handler is `Fn(Request) -> Response` today; upgrading needs a way for a handler arm to say "upgrade this connection and run this frame loop" rather than return a `Response`. Candidate shapes: a `req.upgrade() -> Result[WebSocket, _]` accessor that detaches the connection (mirrors hyper's `on_upgrade`), a sum return type (`Response | Upgrade`), or a distinct `Server.serve_with_ws(http_handler, ws_handler)` callback pair. This is a real runtime + surface-design slice in its own right (comparable in weight to the line-17 body-streaming or line-144 HTTP/2 work), NOT a scaffold edit. v1 has structurally treated HTTP-serve and WebSocket as two separate surfaces ŌĆö Demo 1 uses the standalone loop ŌĆö so this is post-Demo-1 work; build it when a real consumer needs HTTP and WS multiplexed on one port. Once it lands, the scaffold's manual `req.path()` dispatch gains a genuine `/ws` arm and entry (a) above closes.
  - [x] **`std.tracing` integration in the backend skeleton. Shipped 2026-06-02.** Was blocked on a user-visible tracing *emission* surface (the `1d172e9` data shapes were interpreter-only); that surface ŌĆö `StdoutExporter` + full `std.tracing` codegen ŌĆö landed in the P1 `std.tracing` entry below. The scaffold's `backend_main_body` now emits the "Listening on ŌĆ”" announcement through the tracing idiom (`let tracer = StdoutExporter {}; tracer.export_event(LogEvent.info("Listening on http://127.0.0.1:8080"))`) instead of a bare `println`, so a fresh `karac new` project shows the structured-logging surface from day one. `K─üra` has no `span!()`/`event!()` macros ŌĆö the idiom is the builder + exporter (matching the rest of the surface), so "structured span+event" is realized as the `LogEvent.info(...)` build + `export_event` call. Verified end-to-end: `backend_main_kara_codegens_to_executable` compiles + links the new body to a real binary (it previously failed once the tracing call was added ŌĆö that gap is exactly what the codegen slice closed); the per-handler span idea (emit inside `handle` without threading an exporter) waits on the ambient/registered exporter, tracked separately under the `std.tracing` P1.
- [x] **P1 ŌĆö HTTP/2 ŌĆö multiplexed streams + flow control. Shipped 2026-06-03.** HPACK header compression, stream prioritization, server push (default-off), `Server-Sent Events` interop. Required for gRPC (which is post-v1; see [`deferred.md ┬¦ gRPC`](../deferred.md#grpc-streaming-reflection-server--client)). Sequenced after HTTP/1.1 in implementation order; ships at v1 launch. **Shipped:** the three `karac_runtime_serve_*` loops (`runtime/src/lib.rs`) no longer hardcode `hyper::server::conn::http1::Builder` ŌĆö they construct hyper-util's protocol-negotiating `hyper_util::server::conn::auto::Builder` over a `TokioExecutor`, which detects the protocol **per-connection**: an HTTP/2 connection preface drives the h2 path (sent by an h2c-prior-knowledge client over plain TCP, or by an ALPN-`h2` client over TLS), and anything else falls through to HTTP/1.1 (no regression). **The headline deliverables ŌĆö multiplexed streams, HPACK, flow control, stream prioritization ŌĆö are all internal to hyper/`h2` and came free with negotiation**, because the per-request bridge `serve_request` was already protocol-agnostic (`hyper::Request<Incoming>` ŌåÆ `hyper::Response<Full<Bytes>>`, no HTTP/1-specific logic). Three pieces of wiring: **(1)** `runtime/Cargo.toml` flips on `http2` for both `hyper` (`server`/`http1`/`http2`) and `hyper-util` (`server-auto`/`tokio`/`http1`/`http2`) ŌĆö reverses the original "HTTP/1 only (locked design (i))" note; `h2 0.4.14` was already in the lockfile transitively. **(2)** ALPN is advertised (`server_config.alpn_protocols = [b"h2", b"http/1.1"]`) **at the HTTPS serve site only**, not in the shared `tls::build_server_config` ŌĆö that helper also backs the raw `std.tls` listener (`karac_runtime_tls_config_new`), a generic TLS socket that is not an HTTP server and must stay ALPN-free. **(3)** `apply_header_timeout` ŌåÆ `apply_serve_tuning`, now taking `&mut auto::Builder<TokioExecutor>` and applying the line-124 header-read timeout through the `.http1()` sub-builder ŌĆö the timeout is the **HTTP/1** slowloris guard; the h2 path needs no equivalent (h2 flow control + frame-size limits bound header buffering structurally, so the unbounded-header-accumulation vector doesn't exist). **`block_in_place` under multiplexing:** sibling streams on one connection are serialized while a handler runs (the connection future can't poll them mid-`block_in_place`), but cross-connection parallelism is preserved via tokio's worker-replacement ŌĆö exactly the per-connection shape HTTP/1.1 keep-alive already had; documented on `serve_request`. A fully-async handler ABI (concurrent streams per connection) is a separate, larger slice. **Tests** (`tests/http_server.rs`, gated `--features llvm`): the spawn-the-binary harness gained a real multiplexing h2 client (`hyper::client::conn::http2::handshake`, driven on a private current-thread tokio runtime ŌĆö added `tokio`/`hyper` client+http2/`hyper-util`/`http-body-util`/`bytes` to the **root** crate's `[dev-dependencies]`, all dev-only so the compiler's production build is unaffected). `test_http2_h2c_prior_knowledge_handler` (path-echo over real h2c, asserts `HTTP_2` version), `test_http2_multiplexed_streams` (two concurrent streams on one h2c connection), `test_http2_alpn_over_tls` (TLS handshake offering `[h2, http/1.1]` settles on `h2`; an `http/1.1`-only client falls back ŌĆö sync rustls + the existing `NoVerify` client, no async needed), `test_http1_still_served_under_auto_builder` (HTTP/1.1 no-regression pin). Gate green: fmt, clippy `--all --all-targets ┬▒llvm`, runtime units (`serve_limits` behavioral timeout tests re-verified through `auto::Builder`), full non-llvm suite, `http_server` (25 E2E + 1 pre-existing ignore), codegen + memory_sanitizer.
  - [ ] **Server push (HTTP/2 `PUSH_PROMISE`).** Won't-do for v1 unless a real consumer needs it: hyper 1.x dropped server-push support entirely, browsers have deprecated/removed it (Chrome removed it in 2022), and the parent entry already specified it default-off. If a future consumer needs push, it requires a hyper-version capability that doesn't currently exist ŌĆö re-evaluate then.
  - [ ] **SSE interop + true response streaming.** `Server-Sent Events` and chunked/streamed response bodies are gated on the line-17 response-body-streaming slice: the serve path returns `hyper::Response<Full<Bytes>>` (a single fully-buffered body) today, so a handler cannot emit an open-ended event stream over either HTTP/1.1 or HTTP/2. SSE is a thin content-type + framing convention on top of a streaming body, so it lands naturally once streaming bodies do ŌĆö build it there. (HTTP/2 itself is ready for it; the limitation is the buffered-body handler ABI, not the protocol.)
- [x] **P1 ŌĆö `std.tracing` ŌĆö structured logging + span/trace context propagation, OTel-export-ready. v1 minimum surface complete 2026-06-05.** Minimum surface: span creation + nesting, structured fields on spans, trace-context propagation across async boundaries (state-machine transform preserves the active span), exporter trait (default no-op exporter at v1; OTel exporter ships post-v1 as a community library on the same trait). Comptime-driven trace-context plumbing ŌĆö K─üra-native opportunity, no proc-macro indirection like Rust's `tracing`. **All four minimum-surface elements ship:** span creation + nesting + structured fields (`Span` / `LogEvent` / `SpanField`, commit `1d172e9`); trace-context propagation across async boundaries ŌĆö the literal "state-machine transform preserves the active span" ŌĆö via the ambient active-span mechanism (Phase 1: `with_span` + auto-stamp + par/spawn inheritance + interpreter parity; Phase 2: the coroutine suspend/resume frame save/restore, line 153, closed 2026-06-05); and the `Exporter` trait with its default `NoOpExporter` (commit `1d172e9`), beyond which the output-producing `StdoutExporter` and the `Log.{trace,debug,info,warn,error}` ambient namespace also landed. The three remaining sub-items are all **post-v1 / deferred, not v1-required**, so this flips `[x]` with them carved below ŌĆö the same parent-`[x]`-with-deferred-`[ ]`-children shape as the HTTP/2 entry above (server-push / SSE): (154) comptime trace-context plumbing is the parent's K─üra-native *opportunity*, not part of the minimum surface; (156) the configurable ambient exporter (register a sink + a process-global min-level) is gated on the ambient-mutable-state / dynamic-dispatch shape "natural once the network event loop lands"; (157) the OTel exporter is explicitly a post-v1 community library on the now-stable trait.
  - [x] `Span` data shape (root + child + `with_field`), `LogEvent` (5 levels + `with_field` + `in_span`), structured fields via `SpanField` ŌĆö commit `1d172e9`
  - [x] `Exporter` trait + `NoOpExporter` default impl; verified user `impl Exporter for X` dispatches correctly (`test_tracing_user_can_implement_exporter_trait`) ŌĆö commit `1d172e9`
  - [x] **Emission surface ŌĆö `StdoutExporter` (the first output-producing exporter) + full codegen support for `std.tracing`. Shipped 2026-06-02.** Before this, the entire `std.tracing` surface (the `1d172e9` data shapes + `Exporter` trait) was **interpreter-only** ŌĆö a *compiled* `LogEvent { ... }.message` read `0` (the seeded struct layouts were absent and the impl bodies never reached codegen), and there was no exporter that actually *emitted* anything. Two pieces shipped: **(1) the emission API** ŌĆö `struct StdoutExporter` + `impl Exporter for StdoutExporter` in `runtime/stdlib/tracing.kara`, rendering each span/event as one structured logfmt-adjacent line (`[level] message key=value ŌĆ” span_id=N` / `[span] name span_id=N parent_id=M ŌĆ”`, trace-context suffixes only when non-zero). Caller-plumbed, matching the surface's design (the ambient/registered exporter stays the separate `[ ]` item below). Added to `PRELUDE_TYPES`. **(2) first-ever codegen for a pure-K─üra stdlib surface** ŌĆö unlike the TCP/TLS/WS stdlib (which is `#[compiler_builtin]` + hand-rolled lowerings), the tracing methods are real K─üra bodies. Codegen normally skips baked-stdlib impls (`STDLIB_PROGRAMS` reaches the typechecker but not codegen), so this slice added: seed `Span`/`LogEvent`/`SpanField` layouts via `declare_structs` over the tracing program; a cached **fully-lowered** tracing program (`TRACING_LOWERED_PROGRAM`) ŌĆö the baked bodies are never type-checked anywhere, so codegen's span-keyed side tables are empty for them, fixed by running the normal pipeline over `tracing.kara` standalone (type-checks clean) and **swapping its 11 span-keyed tables in** only while emitting the tracing bodies (collision-free ŌĆö tracing AST carries `tracing.kara` spans, the user program is never active during that window); declaration of every tracing impl method so dispatch's `module.get_function("Type.method")` resolves; a **usage gate** that deletes any tracing impl-method declaration left with zero call sites after user bodies compile (keeps tracing-free binaries lean ŌĆö no dead `Vec`/f-string machinery ŌĆö and is what lets the IR-shape codegen tests stay valid); and a `Span`/`LogEvent` non-identifier-receiver re-dispatch arm so chained builders (`LogEvent.info(...).with_field(...).in_span(n)`) lower. Tests: 2 interpreter (`test_tracing_stdout_exporter_emits_{event,span}_line`), 4 codegen E2E in `tests/codegen.rs` (`e2e_tracing_stdout_exporter_emits_{events,spans}`, `e2e_tracing_noop_exporter_is_silent`, `e2e_tracing_unused_in_program_emits_no_tracing_bodies`). Gate green: fmt, clippy `--all --all-targets ┬▒llvm`, codegen, par_codegen (105), scaffold (29), memory_sanitizer (73 ASAN), full non-llvm suite. **Update 2026-06-03:** the exporter bodies use the natural multi-interpolation f-string form ŌĆö they were briefly written with `+` concat to dodge a codegen miscompile this surfaced, now fixed (the `[x]` below).
  - [x] **codegen-bug ŌĆö f-string accumulator inside a never-executed block freed uninitialized stack (double-free / SIGABRT). Fixed 2026-06-03.** Surfaced 2026-06-02 by the tracing emission bodies; reproduced in pure user code (no tracing). **Symptom:** a `fn ev(e: Struct)` body of the form `let mut line = f"[{e.a}] {e.b}"; for x in e.items { line = line + f"..." }; println(line)`, called Ōēź2├Ś, aborted on the second call with `pointer being freed was not allocated` on a `.rodata` address (a `String` literal freed as if heap). Required all of: a 2+-interpolation first f-string over owned-struct String fields, the `for`-loop reassigning the accumulator, and the fn called Ōēź2├Ś (removing any one dodged it). **Root cause:** the loop-body f-string's accumulator got a function-**entry** alloca (`create_entry_alloca`) but its `{null,0,0}` value-init was emitted at the f-string **expression site** ŌĆö inside the loop body. When the loop never ran, the alloca held uninitialized stack, and the unconditional scope-exit cleanup read a garbage `cap`: fresh-0 on call 1 (skips), but a non-zero leftover from call 1's frame on call 2 ŌåÆ `free` of a garbage/literal pointer. **Fix (`src/codegen.rs` + `src/codegen/exprs.rs`):** new `zero_init_str_acc_at_entry` emits the `{null,0,0}` store at the entry block right after the accumulator's alloca, so a never-executed f-string leaves `cap == 0` and the `cap > 0` free guard skips it; the expression-site init stays for the re-evaluated (loop) case. The `std.tracing` exporter bodies are folded back to the natural f-string form. Regression test: `tests/codegen.rs::test_e2e_fstring_in_loop_no_double_free` (the minimal two-call repro, asserts clean all-three-lines output). Touches the f-string lowering used by every f-string, so re-verified across the full codegen + memory_sanitizer suites.
  - [x] **Active-span context propagation across async boundaries (state-machine transform preserves active span ŌĆö codegen + ownership-pass work). Phase 1 shipped 2026-06-03; Phase 2 (the literal suspend/resume preservation) shipped 2026-06-05 ŌĆö closes this entry.** There was no ambient "active span" at all before this ŌĆö tracing was fully value-based (`LogEvent.in_span(id)` threaded by hand). **Phase 1 (shipped)** introduced the ambient mechanism + the propagation that doesn't require the coroutine transform: a per-thread active-span register in the runtime (`runtime/src/tracing.rs` ŌĆö `karac_tracing_{get,set}_active_span`, a `thread_local! Cell<i64>` mirroring the provider-stack head); a `with_span(span, || body)` scoped construct (mirroring `with_provider`'s closure-scoped idiom ŌĆö chosen over an `enter()`-guard because a guard across a suspend collides with the RAII-across-yield rule and the interpreter has no observable user-`Drop`) that snapshots/installs/restores the active span around the body; auto-stamping ŌĆö the `LogEvent` constructors (`Log.*` included) read `tracing_active_span()` so an event inside a `with_span` is tagged automatically, with an explicit `.in_span(id)` still overriding; **par/spawn inheritance** ŌĆö the active span is snapshotted into the par env-struct and restored in each worker (`src/codegen/par_blocks.rs`, alongside the provider-head snapshot), so a child task observes the parent's active span; and interpreter parity (an `active_span_stack` on the `Interpreter`, since the tree-walk path is synchronous and has no cross-suspend frame). Representation is the active `span_id` (i64; `0` = none) ŌĆö `Copy`, so the "ownership-pass work" is trivial; the fuller `(trace_id, span_id, task_id)` triple is an additive follow-on once `Span` grows those fields. `with_span` / `tracing_active_span` are `#[compiler_builtin]` (placeholder bodies; both codegen and the interpreter intercept the call shape) and registered in `PRELUDE_FUNCTIONS`. Tests: 3 interpreter (`test_tracing_with_span_stamps_active_span` / `_nesting_restores_outer` / `test_tracing_explicit_in_span_overrides_active`), 3 codegen E2E (`e2e_tracing_with_span_stamps_active_span` incl. nested restore, `e2e_tracing_par_branch_inherits_active_span`, plus the runtime register units). **Phase 2 (shipped 2026-06-05 ŌĆö the literal "state-machine transform preserves the active span"):** the active span now survives a *real* `suspends` park/resume. In `emit_coro_park_suspend` (`src/codegen/coro.rs`) the pre-suspend active span is snapshotted via `karac_tracing_get_active_span()` into a frame-resident i64 alloca *before* the `coro.suspend` ŌĆö the cross-suspend reload forces CoroSplit to spill it into the coro frame, the same residency mechanism the park token already relies on ŌĆö and restored via `karac_tracing_set_active_span()` on **both** post-suspend edges: the resume edge (so the post-park body logs under the pre-suspend span even though it resumes on a different dispatcher worker thread whose TLS register is `0`) and the destroy/cancel edge (so user-`Drop`s run during cooperative-cancellation teardown log under the coroutine's span). The two accessors are unconditional runtime externs (declared in `Codegen::new`, present in both the lean and full archives), so this is safe for programs that never touch `std.tracing`. A shared `emit_coro_restore_active_span` helper backs both edges. Test: `tests/coro_e2e.rs::coroutine_preserves_active_span_across_suspend` ŌĆö `main` wraps a direct-park coroutine drive in `with_span(s, ||...)` (the closure is an inlining vehicle; `build_state_struct_layouts` keys only top-level fns/impl methods, so the parking `serve_one` is the sole coroutine), the dispatcher resumes it on another thread, and the post-resume `Log.info` line is asserted to carry `span_id=7`. A/B-verified: with the resume-edge restore disabled the same line emits with no suffix (span_id=0), so the assertion is a true regression gate, not a vacuous pass.
  - [ ] Comptime-driven trace-context plumbing (K─üra-native answer to Rust `tracing`'s proc-macro indirection)
  - [x] **Ambient emission ŌĆö `Log.{trace,debug,info,warn,error}("...")`. Shipped 2026-06-03.** A `struct Log` namespace in `runtime/stdlib/tracing.kara` (in `PRELUDE_TYPES`) whose assoc fns each build the matching `LogEvent` and emit it through a fresh `StdoutExporter` ŌĆö so a program can log a message without constructing and threading an exporter value. Because these are assoc-fn bodies over the already-codegen-capable `LogEvent` / `StdoutExporter` surface, they lower through the same tracing-codegen pass and work under both `karac run` and `karac build` (E2E `e2e_tracing_log_ambient_emission` + interpreter `test_tracing_log_ambient_emission_all_levels`). **Surfaced + fixed two codegen bugs:** (a) a struct-literal `let` binding (`let s = StdoutExporter {}`) couldn't resolve its type for method dispatch when the struct lowers to an empty `{}` (collides with every other empty struct in the LLVM-identity reverse-lookup) ŌĆö fixed generally by taking the type name from the `StructLiteral` AST node (`src/codegen/stmts.rs`); (b) the tracing usage-gate deleted callees before their tracing-method callers compiled (now that tracing methods call each other) ŌĆö restructured to compile all bodies then fixpoint-prune, snapshotting/restoring the builder insert block across the prune (`src/codegen.rs`). Gate green: codegen (1016), par_codegen (105), memory_sanitizer (73 ASAN), full non-llvm, fmt, clippy `--all --all-targets ┬▒llvm`.
  - [x] **Configurable ambient exporter ŌĆö register a sink + min-level filter. Codegen half shipped 2026-06-06 ŌĆö closes this entry.** Today `Log.*` always emits to stdout via `StdoutExporter`. The configurable layer ŌĆö register a different sink (`NoOpExporter` to silence, or a custom exporter) and a process-global minimum level so production can dial verbosity ŌĆö needs ambient mutable state shared across call sites. v1-interpreter could carry it on a field, but the codegen path wants a runtime global (level) + dynamic dispatch (arbitrary registered exporter), the `with_provider`-shape the spec calls "natural once the network event loop lands." Build it there; the `Log.*` emission entry points are the single insertion point for the level gate. **Interpreter half shipped 2026-06-05.** The full surface ŌĆö `Log.set_min_level(level)` (rank trace<debug<info<warn<error; sub-threshold events dropped *without evaluating their message*), `Log.set_exporter(e)` (register `NoOpExporter {}` to silence or any custom `Exporter` ŌĆö dispatched dynamically via the interpreter's method machinery), and `Log.reset()` (restore defaults) ŌĆö is honored under `karac run`. State lives on the `Interpreter` (`tracing_min_level: i64`, `tracing_exporter: Option<Value>`); the intercept sits in `eval_call.rs::try_eval_log_call` next to the `with_span` / `tracing_active_span` intercepts, and for the default (no registered sink, level passes) it returns `None` so the existing `Log.*` K─üra body runs ŌĆö keeping the common stdout path on the already-tested lowering. The three config methods are plain empty-body `Log` assoc fns (not `#[compiler_builtin]`), so codegen lowers them as no-ops. 4 interpreter tests (`test_tracing_log_min_level_filters_below_threshold`, `_set_exporter_noop_silences`, `_reset_restores_default`, `_custom_exporter_receives_events`). **Codegen half shipped 2026-06-06 ŌĆö a compiled `Log.*` now honors the config too.** The config lives in *process-global* runtime state (`runtime/src/tracing.rs`: a `MIN_LEVEL: AtomicI64` + an `EXPORTER_DATA`/`EXPORTER_FN: AtomicPtr` pair, the latter an opaque `(value-ptr, export_event-fn-ptr)` the runtime only stores ŌĆö never derefs/calls), with six `karac_tracing_*` accessors declared unconditionally in `Codegen::new` (lean + full archives, safe for tracing-free programs). Process-global rather than the active span's thread-local-per-task register, because the min level is process-wide by spec and a sink registered on `main` must be visible to any worker thread ŌĆö so nothing to snapshot at a par/spawn boundary. The rewritten `Log.*` bodies gate on a `tracing_level_enabled(rank)` builtin (lowered to `rank >= karac_tracing_get_min_level()`, an i1 feeding the body's `if`, so a filtered level skips building the event) and emit through `tracing_emit_event(event)` (lowered to a branch on the runtime data-ptr: null ŌåÆ a direct `StdoutExporter.export_event` call, else an indirect call through the stored fn-ptr ŌĆö same `(ref self ptr, LogEvent by value)` shape, no niche-ABI on `export_event` so no packing). `Log.set_min_level` maps the name ŌåÆ rank via mutually-exclusive `if`s ŌåÆ `tracing_set_min_level`; `Log.reset` ŌåÆ `tracing_reset`. `Log.set_exporter(e)` is intercepted at its **call site** (`call_dispatch.rs` ŌåÆ `try_compile_tracing_config_builtin`/`compile_tracing_set_exporter`, not via the generic body) so the concrete exporter type is read from the argument AST exactly like `with_provider`'s provider; it heap-leaks the exporter value (`malloc`, Ōēź1 byte so an empty exporter is a unique non-null sentinel) and registers `(ptr, <Type>.export_event)`. The interpreter half is unchanged (`try_eval_log_call` still owns the no-evaluate-when-filtered drop); two `tracing_*` builtin handlers back the interpreter's default fall-through. **Surfaced + fixed a pre-existing gap:** a *user* `impl Exporter` whose method takes `LogEvent`/`Span` by value didn't codegen at all ŌĆö the baked tracing value structs weren't in `struct_types` when user functions were declared, so the param hit `llvm_type_for_name`'s i64 fall-through and the call failed module verification (same class as the `TcpListener`/`WebSocket` name-arm guards). Fixed by seeding `SpanField`/`Span`/`LogEvent` layouts in `seed_builtin_struct_types` (before user-fn declaration; LLVM canonicalizes the literal structs so they unify with the tracing pass's `declare_structs`). 5 codegen E2E (`e2e_tracing_log_{min_level_filters_below_threshold,set_exporter_noop_silences,reset_restores_default,custom_exporter_receives_events}` + `e2e_tracing_user_exporter_impl_reads_event_and_span_fields`) mirroring the interpreter tests, plus a runtime config unit test. **One backend nuance, documented in `tracing.kara`:** the interpreter drops a sub-threshold `Log.*` *without evaluating its message argument* (call-site intercept); the compiled path evaluates the argument the caller built but skips the event construction + emission. Unobservable for side-effect-free log messages (the norm); matching it under codegen would require intercepting every `Log.*` call site. Gate green: fmt, clippy `--all --all-targets ┬▒llvm`, full non-llvm suite, codegen + par_codegen + memory_sanitizer (`--features llvm`).
  - [ ] OTel exporter (post-v1 community library; depends on the trait shape being stable, which lands here)
- [x] **P1 ŌĆö `std.regex` ŌĆö compile patterns, match / find / replace.** Lifted from Phase 11 ┬¦ Scripting-critical. PCRE-like syntax (excluding backreferences for predictable runtime). Compile-once + reuse pattern; `regex.compile(s) -> Result[Regex, RegexError]`. v1 effect-free (no allocates surface ŌĆö pattern compilation pre-allocates internal buffer). Shipped pre-2026-05-16 across `runtime/stdlib/regex.kara` + typechecker arm in `stdlib_io.rs` + interpreter intrinsic in `method_call_regex.rs`; 13 tests (8 interpreter + 5 typechecker). `captures(s)` from the broader 10B surface (Scripting-critical section below) is deferred.
- [ ] **P1 ŌĆö `std.process` ŌĆö `Command` / `Child`; `ProcessTable` effect resource.** Lifted from Phase 11 ┬¦ Scripting-critical. `Command::new(prog).arg(...).env(...).spawn() -> Result[Child, IoError]`; `Child.wait()` / `Child.try_wait()` / `Child.kill()`. Effects: `sends(ProcessTable)` on spawn; effect-routes through the event loop for non-blocking wait.
  - [x] Type surface: `Command` (builder), `Child` (pid), `ExitStatus`, internal `EnvVar` row type, `ProcessTable` effect resource registered in `PRELUDE_EFFECT_RESOURCES` ŌĆö commit `efc565c`
  - [x] Pure-K─üra builder methods: `Command.new(prog) / .arg(a) / .env(k, v)` with state preserved across owned-self chain
  - [x] `sends(ProcessTable)` declared on `spawn` / `wait` / `try_wait` / `kill` signatures; verified through a user wrapper declaring the same effect (`test_process_user_can_declare_sends_process_table_effect`)
  - [x] Real `Command.spawn()` via `std::process::Command` interpreter intrinsic ŌĆö bodies flipped to `#[compiler_builtin]`, dispatch through `try_eval_process_method` in `src/interpreter/method_call_process.rs`. Pid-keyed `child_table: HashMap<i64, std::process::Child>` on the Interpreter struct holds the live handles between calls. Commit `d379b56`.
  - [x] Real `Child.wait()` / `try_wait()` / `kill()` intrinsics ŌĆö same dispatch path. `wait` removes the table entry on success; `try_wait` removes only when the child has exited; `kill` leaves the entry in place per spec (caller still needs `wait` to reap). 7 new integration tests covering real spawn + wait, try_wait still-running, kill + wait, env var propagation, and unknown-child wait ŌåÆ IoError.NotFound. Commit `d379b56`.
  - [ ] Execution verbs: `blocks` on the synchronous `wait` form; `suspends` on the future async form (depends on the network event loop). **`blocks` shipped 2026-06-05** ŌĆö `Child.wait()` now declares `with sends(ProcessTable) blocks` in `runtime/stdlib/process.kara`: the synchronous form parks the calling thread on the OS `waitpid` until the child exits, so the scheduler must place it on a blocking-capable thread (the same execution-verb the `extern "C"` ABI default uses). `try_wait()` (non-blocking poll) and `kill()` (fire-and-return) deliberately do **not** carry it. Verified against the *actual baked* `process.kara` AST via `STDLIB_PROGRAMS` (`tests/effectchecker.rs::test_process_child_wait_declares_blocks_others_do_not`), not a hand-written stand-in. **`suspends` remains** the open half: routing `wait()` through the network event loop so the task yields rather than pinning a thread ŌĆö lands with that event loop; it widens `wait`'s declared set further (non-breaking).
  - [x] **`stdin` / `stdout` / `stderr` redirection builder methods on `Command`. Shipped 2026-06-03.** New `enum Stdio { Inherit, Null }` (in `PRELUDE_TYPES`) + `Command.stdin(cfg)` / `.stdout(cfg)` / `.stderr(cfg)` owned-self builders threading three `cmd_stdin`/`cmd_stdout`/`cmd_stderr` fields (default `Stdio.Inherit`). `eval_command_spawn` reads each field and calls `std::process::Stdio::null()` only on an explicit `Stdio.Null` (`Inherit` is `std::process`'s own default, left unset) ŌĆö so `Stdio.Null` discards the child's stream (e.g. spawn a noisy command without polluting the parent's terminal). 2 interpreter tests (`test_process_stdio_builder_records_redirection`, `test_process_spawn_with_null_redirection_waits_clean`); existing 10 process tests re-verified green under the widened `Command` struct. **`Stdio.Piped` deliberately deferred:** capturing a stream needs `Child` to carry read/write handles + accessors, and an *unread* pipe deadlocks a child that fills the buffer ŌĆö shipping it without the read side would be a footgun. Tracked as the follow-on below.
  - [x] **`Stdio.Piped` + `Child.stdout()` / `.stderr()` / `.stdin()` handle accessors. Shipped 2026-06-05.** The capture half of redirection. **(1)** `Stdio.Piped` joins the `enum Stdio { Inherit, Null }` (in `PRELUDE_TYPES`); `eval_command_spawn`'s redirection now maps each stream field through `stdio_for_field` ŌåÆ `std::process::Stdio::piped()` on `Piped` / `null()` on `Null` / unset on `Inherit`. **(2)** Three new capture-handle structs ŌĆö `ChildStdout` / `ChildStderr` / `ChildStdin`, each carrying the owning child's `pid` (registered in `PRELUDE_TYPES`). The K─üra `Child` stays pid-only; the real `std::process::Child` keeps owning its pipes until taken. **(3)** `Child.stdout()` / `.stderr()` / `.stdin()` return `Option[ChildStdout/ŌĆ”]` ŌĆö they `take()` the stream off the live `std::process::Child` and move it into one of three new pid-keyed interpreter tables (`child_stdout_table` / `child_stderr_table` / `child_stdin_table`), returning `Some(handle)` or `None` (not piped / already taken / child gone), mirroring `std::process::Child`'s `Option` fields. **(4)** `ChildStdout/ChildStderr.read_to_string() -> Result[String, IoError] blocks` drains the captured read end to a String (removing the exhausted entry); `ChildStdin.write(data) -> Result[Unit, IoError] blocks` writes the pipe; `ChildStdin.close() -> Result[Unit, IoError]` drops the handle, closing the fd to **signal the child EOF** ŌĆö the load-bearing deadlock guard the parent entry flagged. Dispatch routes through `try_eval_process_method`; each handler guards on the receiver struct name and returns `None` otherwise, so the same-named `Command.<stream>(cfg)` builders / `Stdin`/`FileSystem` `read_to_string` resource methods / `File.write` fall through to their own dispatchers untouched. Interpreter-only (the whole `std.process` surface is); no codegen path. 3 tests in `tests/interpreter.rs` (`test_process_capture_stdout_via_piped`, `_stdout_not_piped_yields_none`, `_write_stdin_close_and_read_stdout_roundtrip` ŌĆö the last a full writeŌåÆcloseŌåÆread round-trip through `/bin/cat` that proves `close()` signals EOF so the child terminates and `read_to_string` doesn't deadlock). Gate green: fmt, clippy `--all --all-targets --features llvm`, full non-llvm suite, codegen, par_codegen, memory_sanitizer (ASAN), 15 process interpreter tests.
- [x] **P1 ŌĆö protobuf ŌĆö wire format + comptime codegen. Interpreter-complete (checklist was stale; state re-verified 2026-07-08).** `.proto` schema parsing at comptime; comptime emits the message type + serialize / deserialize / merge methods. No separate codegen tool. v1 surface covers proto3; proto2 if time permits. Effects: `allocates(Heap)` on decode; pure on encode. **Actual state ŌĆö the whole surface shipped as pure-K─üra comptime code (`runtime/stdlib/protobuf.kara`, 1716 lines, registered in `src/prelude.rs` `STDLIB_SOURCES`), not "unstarted" as this box implied:**
  - [x] **Slice 1 ŌĆö proto3 wire format** (`ProtoBuf` encoders + `ProtoReader` cursor): base-128 varints, ZigZag (`sint32`/`sint64`), field tags (`(field_number << 3) | wire_type`), length-delimited, fixed32/fixed64, `skip_field` by wire type. Ordinary K─üra, no compiler intrinsic. 14 tests (`tests/protobuf.rs`).
  - [x] **Slice 2 ŌĆö `#[derive(Message)]` comptime codegen**: on a struct of proto3 fields, comptime-emits `encode(ref self) -> Vec[u8]` (pure), `decode(bytes) -> Self` (`allocates(Heap)`), `merge(mut ref self, bytes)` via comptime reflection over the struct's fields. Supports scalars (`i32`/`i64`/`u32`/`u64`/`bool`/`f32`/`f64`/`String`/`Vec[u8]`), `repeated` (packed for numerics), nested messages, enums, `map`, `oneof`, and `#[karac::proto(<wire>)]` wire / field-number overrides. 61 tests (`tests/protobuf_derive.rs`).
  - [x] **Slice 3 ŌĆö `.proto` schema ŌåÆ message types** (`#[proto_schema] const S: String = "..."`): a pure-K─üra proto3 parser (`proto_parse_schema` in `protobuf.kara`) expands the schema, **before name resolution** (in `desugar` via `expand_proto_schemas`), into the `struct`/`enum` types it declares, each carrying `#[derive(Message)]`. This is the exact "generated top-level item must resolve when named by user code" ordering that `src/comptime.rs` calls out as future work ŌĆö solved for the schema path via the pre-resolve pass. Covers scalars, enums (UPPER_SNAKE ŌåÆ PascalCase, varint of declaration index), `repeated`/packed, `map<K,V>`, `oneof`, nested + forward-referenced messages, comments, non-contiguous field numbers, and malformed-schema diagnostics via `compiler.error`. 24 tests (`tests/protobuf_proto.rs`). Worked example: `examples/protobuf_schema.kara` (runs under `karac run`).
  - [ ] **Compiled/AOT path (`karac build`) ŌĆö deferred; interpreter-only at v1** (the sole real gap, root-caused 2026-07-08). `#[derive(Message)]` methods work under `karac run` but **fail codegen** (`no handler for method 'len' on variable 'bytes'` ŌĆö the `Vec[u8]` from `p.encode()` is untyped at the call site). Root cause: the pipeline runs `typecheck ŌåÆ lower ŌåÆ comptime_eval`, so derive-generated methods are spliced *after* typecheck ŌĆö the tree-walk interpreter dispatches them dynamically, but codegen has no static return-type/dispatch info for a method the typechecker never saw. Confirmed by A/B: a *hand-written* `impl Person { fn encode(ref self) -> Vec[u8] }` + `bytes.len()` codegens + runs clean, so it is not a missing `.len()` dispatcher arm ŌĆö it is the post-typecheck-generation gap. This is the same class as, and shares the fix with, the `src/comptime.rs`-documented "move `#[derive]` expansion ahead of resolution/typecheck" future work (which the `#[proto_schema]` *type* expansion already does at the pre-resolve stage, but derive *method* expansion does not). Interpreter-only is consistent with the v1 posture of `Pool[T]` / `Arena[T]` / `Interner` / `Semaphore` / `std.process` ŌĆö all interpreter-only at v1. Wiring the compiled path is a comptime-infrastructure slice (run derive expansion before typecheck so generated methods are typechecked + codegen-visible), not a protobuf-specific one.
  - [ ] **Long-tail deferred (not v1-floor):** proto2 ("if time permits" ŌĆö proto3-only shipped); `.proto`-**file** input (vs the inline `#[proto_schema]` string const ŌĆö file reading needs comptime filesystem effects, gated by `E_RUNTIME_EFFECT_AT_COMPTIME`); gRPC service/RPC codegen (post-v1, [`deferred.md ┬¦ gRPC`](../deferred.md#grpc-streaming-reflection-server--client)); well-known types (`Timestamp`/`Any`/`Duration`/wrappers); unknown-field *preservation* (v1 skips-and-drops by wire type).
- [ ] **P1 ŌĆö File-system event loop ŌĆö io_uring on Linux, sticky kqueue on BSD/macOS.** Lifts disk-I/O ceiling beyond what epoll covers. Not load-bearing for the 1M+ socket benchmark (epoll/kqueue/IOCP are sufficient there) but matters for mixed-workload demos and disk-bound backends. Cross-platform abstraction in the runtime crate, parallels the network event loop's surface. **Sole tracker for io_uring** ŌĆö de-scoped from the phase-6 M3 cross-platform-parity launch gate on 2026-06-07: io_uring is a Linux-only file-I/O perf feature, orthogonal to socket-scale/parity and not load-bearing for the 1M flagship demo (`ws_idle_holder` does no hot-path file I/O ŌĆö TLS certs are inlined PEM literals). Ships at v1 as P1, sequenced independently on a Linux dev box (can't be built/tested on macOS ŌĆö io_uring needs Linux kernel 5.x+); the `FileSystem.read_to_string` codegen gap (noted in `examples/ws_idle_holder/src/main.kara`) is a prereq for the file-I/O surface it sits under.
- [ ] **P1 ŌĆö `Pool[T]` ŌĆö connection-pool primitive.** `Pool::new(create_fn, max_connections, max_waiters)`; `pool.acquire(timeout) -> Result[PooledConnection[T], PoolError]` / drop releases automatically. Bounded waiters with timeout; health-check hook fires on acquire (callable's responsibility); evict-on-error pattern. Library-shape; community database drivers build on this.
  - [x] Type surface: `Pool[T]` / `PooledConnection[T]` (with `pool_handle_id` + `val: T` fields), `PoolError` enum (`Timeout` / `PoolClosed` / `CreateFailed`); `Pool.new(create_fn: Fn() -> T, max_connections, max_waiters)` signature via `impl[T] Pool[T] { ... }` syntax ŌĆö commit `e694f2c`
  - [x] `acquire(timeout)` signature, plus new `release(conn)` method on `Pool[T]` for explicit slot return (until drop-on-release wires up).
  - [x] Real intrinsic via `try_eval_pool_method` + `eval_pool_new` in `src/interpreter/method_call_pool.rs`. Per-pool state in `pool_table: HashMap<i64, PoolEntry>` keyed by a monotonic `handle_id`; PoolEntry holds the create_fn closure (`Value::Function`), bounds, slot vec, active_count. Single-threaded semantics: acquire serves immediately from a free slot, or mints via create_fn if under cap, or fires `PoolError.Timeout` straight away. Commit `1552c6d`.
  - [x] Closure storage on `Pool[T]` for `create_fn` ŌĆö held on `PoolEntry.create_fn` as a `Value::Function`. Closures with captures verified end-to-end (`test_pool_create_fn_can_be_a_closure_with_captures`).
  - [ ] **Real `parking_lot::Mutex` + condvar backing the semaphore** ŌĆö only matters under multi-threaded execution. The single-threaded tree-walk interpreter's collapsed semantics (immediate-serve-or-timeout) is correct for v1; the codegen/runtime path is where the bounded-waiters-with-timeout machinery becomes load-bearing. Lifts here when codegen for `std.process` / `Pool[T]` lands.
  - [x] **Drop-releases-automatically. Shipped 2026-06-06.** `impl[T] Drop for PooledConnection[T]` (`runtime/stdlib/pool.kara`) returns a connection's slot to its source pool at scope exit (NLL endpoint or block exit), so explicit `pool.release(conn)` is now optional ŌĆö it stays as an eager-hand-back convenience. The earlier blocker (this entry's prior "`eval_stmt::run_cleanup` treats `CleanupAction::Drop` as a trace-only no-op" claim) was already stale: the Phase-7 user-`impl Drop` dispatch had since landed (`invoke_user_drop_if_applicable`, fired from both the NLL-endpoint `fire_due_drops` and the scope-exit `run_cleanup` drains). This slice hangs `PooledConnection`'s release off it: the `#[compiler_builtin]` `drop` body is a no-op placeholder, and the interpreter's user-`Drop` drain routes `PooledConnection` to a native handler (`eval_stmt::try_eval_builtin_drop` ŌåÆ `method_call_pool::drop_pooled_connection`) ŌĆö mirroring codegen's stdlib-drop special-casing (`synth_drop.rs`, TlsStream/TlsListener/TaskGroup). Return is **idempotent**, keyed on a new per-checkout `conn_id` minted at `acquire` and tracked in `PoolEntry.checked_out`: an explicit `release` followed by the binding's scope-exit drop (the interpreter has no move-suppression for call-argument moves, so both fire) hands the slot back exactly once ŌĆö fixing a latent double-return that would otherwise inflate one connection into two idle slots (also covers a double explicit `release`). Interpreter-only, like the rest of `std.Pool`; the baked `impl Drop` never reaches codegen (`PooledConnection.drop` is not a lowered LLVM symbol ŌĆö the user-drop-wrapper synth's `module.get_function` lookup returns `None` and skips it), verified green across codegen + memory_sanitizer. 2 interpreter tests (`test_pool_pooled_connection_auto_releases_on_drop` ŌĆö a `let`-bound connection's scope-exit drop recycles its slot under a `max_connections = 1` pool, so a second acquire reuses it instead of timing out; `test_pool_release_then_drop_returns_slot_once` ŌĆö A/B-pinned idempotency: explicit `release` + scope-exit drop returns the slot once, asserted by the second concurrent acquire timing out). The only remaining `[ ]` child of the `Pool[T]` parent is the real `parking_lot::Mutex`/condvar backing (above), which is codegen-path / multi-threaded-only and not v1-required.
  - [x] **Health-check hook closure. Shipped 2026-06-05.** `Pool.with_health_check(check: Fn(T) -> bool) -> Pool[T]` registers an opt-in validation hook (stored as `PoolEntry.health_check: Option<Value>` alongside `create_fn`) and returns the pool so it chains off `Pool.new(...)`. On `acquire`, each idle slot popped from `slots` is passed to the hook: `true` hands it back, `false` evicts it ŌĆö and *decrements* `active_count` (the connection is destroyed, so it no longer counts against the cap), which is what lets the mint path create a fresh replacement even when the pool was at `max_connections` (the evict-on-error pattern). Slots minted on the spot are not checked ŌĆö only reused idle slots, the ones that can go stale. **Signature/shape decision:** registered opt-in via a chainable method rather than a fourth `Pool.new` parameter (the file comment's earlier sketch), so pools that don't validate keep the three-arg constructor ŌĆö the idiomatic shape (cf. r2d2 / deadpool optional validators). Dispatch: `try_eval_pool_method`'s `with_health_check` arm + the validation loop in `eval_pool_acquire` (`src/interpreter/method_call_pool.rs`); hook invoked via `invoke_function_value` on a clone of the slot value (so a healthy verdict preserves it), a non-`bool`/non-callable result treated as healthy (never silently evicts). Interpreter-only, like the rest of `Pool[T]`. 3 tests (`test_pool_health_check_passes_reuses_idle_slot`, `_fails_evicts_and_mints_fresh`, `_eviction_at_cap_does_not_timeout` ŌĆö the last pins the `active_count` decrement). `PoolError.CreateFailed` stays reserved (the hook is a `bool` predicate, not a fallible mint).
- [ ] **P1 ŌĆö Application-layer backpressure primitives.** `Semaphore::new(n)` with `acquire(timeout)` / `release`; `BoundedChannel[T]::new(capacity, OnFull::Block | OnFull::FailFast)`; `RateLimiter::new_token_bucket(rate, capacity)` with `try_acquire(key) -> bool` / `acquire(key) -> impl Future`. Effects: `Semaphore` + `RateLimiter` are pure-with-suspends; `BoundedChannel` follows the existing `Channel[T]` effect surface plus `suspends` on full-block. Complementary to deployment-layer providers (which handle per-provider concurrency caps); user code routinely needs application-layer backpressure too.
  - [x] **`Semaphore` ŌĆö `new(permits)` / `acquire(timeout)` / `release`. Shipped 2026-06-03.** New `runtime/stdlib/semaphore.kara`: `struct Semaphore { handle_id }` + `enum SemaphoreError { Timeout }` (both in `PRELUDE_TYPES`), with `#[compiler_builtin]` `new` / `acquire` / `release` dispatched through the interpreter intrinsic (`src/interpreter/method_call_semaphore.rs`, modeled on `Pool[T]`). Permit state lives in `Interpreter.semaphore_table: HashMap<i64, SemEntry { available, max }>` keyed by handle; `acquire` decrements when a permit is free (`Ok(Unit)`) else fails closed `Err(Timeout)`, `release` increments saturating at the initial budget. **v1 collapsed single-threaded semantics** (same as `Pool[T]`): an exhausted-semaphore `acquire` returns `Timeout` immediately rather than parking ŌĆö no peer can free a permit mid-call in the tree-walk interpreter; the real parking-with-`timeout` + the `suspends` execution verb land on the codegen/runtime path with the network event loop. 4 interpreter tests (grant-up-to-N-then-timeout, release-returns-a-permit, release-saturates-at-budget, hand-rolled-zero-handle-fails-closed). Gate green: fmt, clippy `--all --all-targets`, full non-llvm suite, llvm build.
  - [x] **`BoundedChannel[T]` ŌĆö `new(capacity, OnFull::Block | OnFull::FailFast)` + `send` / `recv`. Shipped 2026-06-03.** New `runtime/stdlib/bounded_channel.kara`: `struct BoundedChannel[T] { handle_id }` + companion `enum OnFull { Block, FailFast }` / `enum ChannelError { Full }` (all in `PRELUDE_TYPES`), with `#[compiler_builtin]` `new` / `send` / `recv` through the interpreter intrinsic (`src/interpreter/method_call_bounded_channel.rs`). Buffer lives in `Interpreter.bounded_channel_table: HashMap<i64, BoundedChannelEntry { capacity, fail_fast, queue: VecDeque<Value> }>` (T erases at runtime, like `Pool[T]`); `send` enqueues when under capacity (`Ok(Unit)`) else `Err(ChannelError.Full)`, `recv` dequeues FIFO (`Some(v)` / `None`). **v1 collapsed:** `OnFull.Block` cannot park in the single-threaded interpreter (no peer drains the buffer), so a full send fails like `FailFast`; `recv` returns `None` on empty rather than blocking. The real park-on-full (`suspends`, the `Channel[T]` effect surface) lands on the codegen/runtime path with the network event loop. 3 deterministic interpreter tests (send-bounds-then-FIFO-recv, Block-collapses-to-FailFast, hand-rolled-zero-handle-fails-closed). Gate green: fmt, clippy `--all --all-targets`, full non-llvm suite, llvm build.
  - [x] **`RateLimiter.new_token_bucket(rate, capacity)` + `try_acquire(key) -> bool`. Shipped 2026-06-03.** New `runtime/stdlib/rate_limiter.kara`: `struct RateLimiter { handle_id }` (in `PRELUDE_TYPES`) with `#[compiler_builtin]` `new_token_bucket` / `try_acquire`, dispatched through the interpreter intrinsic (`src/interpreter/method_call_rate_limiter.rs`). Per-limiter state in `Interpreter.rate_limiter_table: HashMap<i64, RateLimiterEntry { rate, capacity, buckets }>`; each key gets a `TokenBucket { tokens, last }` that starts full (so the first `capacity` calls burst) and **lazily refills** by `elapsed * rate` (capped at capacity) on each `try_acquire`, consuming a token when `>= 1`. Monotonic time via `std::time::Instant` read directly in the intrinsic (same pattern as the `Clock`/`RandomSource` ambient resources). 3 deterministic interpreter tests (initial-burst-then-limit, per-key independence, hand-rolled-zero-handle-fails-closed). **v1 = synchronous `try_acquire` only;** the waiting `acquire(key) -> impl Future` form is event-loop dependent ŌĆö carved below. Gate green: fmt, clippy `--all --all-targets`, full non-llvm suite, llvm build.
  - [ ] **`RateLimiter.acquire(key) -> impl Future` ŌĆö the waiting form.** Parks the caller until a token frees for `key` instead of returning `false`. Event-loop dependent (the `suspends` execution verb + the park machinery), lands on the codegen/runtime path with the network event loop. The token-bucket state and refill logic from `try_acquire` are reused; only the on-empty behavior (park-and-retry vs return-false) differs.

---

### v66 graduation P1 additions (2026-05-11)

> v1 P1 items promoted in the v66 general-purpose-foundation graduation. Full design + rationale at [`../../brainstorming/archive/v66_general_purpose_with_data_bonus.md`](../../brainstorming/archive/v66_general_purpose_with_data_bonus.md); canonical entries in [`../deferred.md`](../deferred.md) under each item's name.

- [x] **[ŌåÆ P1] `std.cli` ŌĆö argument parser, builder-style API.** `Parser::new(name) / .arg / .flag / .subcommand / .parse() -> Result[Args, CliError]`; automatic `--help` / `--version`; effect `reads(Env)` on `.parse()`. Phase 8 floor. See `deferred.md ┬¦ std.cli`.
  - [x] Pure-K─üra builder surface: `Parser.new / .about / .arg / .flag`; `Arg.string() / .required() / .help`; `Args.get_string / .get_flag`; `CliError` shape ŌĆö commit `7295af9`
  - [x] `parse()` walks `Env.args()` and produces real results (named-arg pairing, flag set tracking, positional bucketing, required-arg check)
  - [x] `reads(Env)` effect on `.parse()`
  - [x] `Parser.subcommand(name, sub_parser)` + subcommand-dispatch routing; `Args.sub: Option[SubcommandResult]`; `Args.subcommand_name() -> Option[String]`; `SubcommandResult.get_string / .get_flag`. One level of depth in v1 (matches the `deferred.md` example) ŌĆö recursive nesting waits for a real user case. Commit `54daf4a`.
  - [x] Automatic `--help` / `-h` / `--version` / `-V` short-circuit in `parse()`; `Parser.help_text(ref self) -> String` renders USAGE / ARGS / FLAGS / SUBCOMMANDS sections from the declared shape; `Parser.version_line(ref self) -> String` renders `<program_name> <version>` (or bare program name if `.version(...)` unset). Sentinel-via-message: returns `Err(CliError { message: <text> })` rather than a new enum variant so the v1 `CliError` struct shape stays stable. Commit `54daf4a`.

> **Moved (2026-06-06):** the seven v66/v67 graduation items that land in Phase 11 slices ŌĆö `std.embeddings`, hand-vectorized data-spine kernels (v67 ┬¦3), `std.simd.math`, `cpu-baseline` + `#[multiversion]`, `std.autograd`, `LazyDataFrame` (Option A), and statistical methods on `Column`/`DataFrame` ŌĆö now live in [`phase-11-stdlib-longtail.md ┬¦ Numerical and data-science stdlib`](phase-11-stdlib-longtail.md#numerical-and-data-science-stdlib) (sub-section "ML / AI-adjacent and SIMD data-spine").

- [ ] **[ŌåÆ P1] `docs/book/src/data.md` ŌĆö data chapter.** Tensor / Column / DataFrame / lazy query / Arrow IPC / Parquet / CSV; one ~50-line end-to-end example; pointers to `std.linalg` / `std.fft` / `std.einsum` / `std.embeddings` / `std.random.distributions` / `std.autograd`. Discoverability surface for the "quiet data bonus" positioning. Lands in Phase 8.5 docs window.

- [ ] **[ŌåÆ P1] `kara-postgres` ŌĆö canonical Postgres driver, project-owned package.** Dogfooding-grade ŌĆö written to exercise effect system, `Pool[T]`, auto-concurrency, `with_provider`, structured errors. Scope: TCP, prepared statements, simple-query protocol, basic type mapping (i64/String/f64/bool/bytes/NULL/timestamp/uuid), transactions, parameter binding, `Pool[T]` integration. Stdlib position (no `std.sql`) unchanged ŌĆö driver lives outside `std.*` as a project-owned package. **Handover-to-community policy explicitly deferred to engineering-start (Q3).** See `deferred.md ┬¦ Canonical Postgres Driver (kara-postgres)`.
