### v70 graduation P1 additions (2026-06-01)

> v1 P1 items promoted in the v70 arena/handle stdlib surface graduation. Full design + rationale at [`../../brainstorming/archive/v70_arena_handle_v1_surface.md`](../../brainstorming/archive/v70_arena_handle_v1_surface.md); the v70 brainstorm validates these primitives against four workload lenses (connection pool, AST bulk arena, regex NFA, ECS) plus a compiler-as-lens audit. Both items are split-primitive complements to the existing P1 `Pool[T]` entry above (which covers generational reuse) ŌĆö `Arena[T]` covers bulk allocation with one shared lifetime; `Symbol`/`Interner` covers deduplicating string handles.

- [ ] **[ŌåÆ P1] `Arena[T]` + `ArenaRef[T]` ŌĆö bulk-allocation primitive.** Single-lifetime allocator: `Arena.new() -> Arena[T]`; `arena.push(value: T) -> ArenaRef[T]` (bump-allocate); `arena.get(r: ArenaRef[T]) -> ref T` (index, no liveness check ŌĆö all items live until the arena drops). All items freed in bulk when the `Arena[T]` value drops. No per-item release; no generation counter. Use cases: parse trees per compilation, AST nodes, frame-scoped game data, regex NFA states during construction. Distinct from `Pool[T]` (which supports per-item release and stale-handle detection). Effects: `allocates(Heap)` on `push`. **Interpreter slice LANDED 2026-06-22** ŌĆö type surface + interpreter intrinsic + snapshot/restore + effect seeding all shipped (sub-items below); only codegen lowering remains (deferred, interpreter-only like `Pool[T]`). The spec's `get -> ref T` was validated as the right call: `ref T` is consistent with how K─üra treats `ref` everywhere (field access on a `ref Node` result auto-derefs ŌĆö the primary AST/ECS use case ŌĆö Display works; arithmetic on a `ref i64` result needs an explicit `*`, exactly as a plain `ref i64` param does, so it's not an Arena-specific wart). **Known limitation (matches the `Map.new()` precedent):** an unannotated `let a = Arena.new()` can't infer `T` from a later `push` ŌĆö annotate the binding (`let a: Arena[i64] = Arena.new()`). Sub-items:
  - [x] Type surface: `Arena[T]` + `ArenaRef[T]` declared in baked stdlib `runtime/stdlib/arena.kara`; `Arena.new() / .push / .get` signatures via `impl[T] Arena[T] { ... }` syntax peer to the existing `Pool[T]` declaration pattern. **DONE** ŌĆö also adds `ArenaCheckpoint`; all three registered in `PRELUDE_TYPES` + `arena.kara` in `STDLIB_SOURCES` (`src/prelude.rs`). Phantom-generic `[=T]` carriers (`Arena[=T]` / `ArenaRef[=T]`), mirroring `Pool[=T]`; baked impl bodies are `#[compiler_builtin]` placeholders (never resolved or type-checked ŌĆö only signatures are the contract).
  - [x] Real interpreter intrinsic via `try_eval_arena_method` + `eval_arena_new` in new `src/interpreter/method_call_arena.rs`. Per-arena state in `arena_table: HashMap<i64, Vec<Value>>` keyed by a monotonic `arena_handle_id`; `ArenaRef[T]` carries `(arena_handle_id, index)`. Single-threaded semantics: `push` appends to the Vec and returns a fresh `ArenaRef`; `get` clones the value at the index (the tree-walk interpreter can't hand out a real borrow ŌĆö the static type is still `ref T`). **DONE** ŌĆö dispatch wired through `method_call.rs` (after the pool guard) + the `"Arena.new"` path arm in `eval_call.rs`; mirrors `pool_table`. Cross-arena `get` and dangling (post-`rewind_to`) handles degrade to `Unit` rather than read out of bounds. Also ships a bonus `len()`. 8 interpreter tests (`tests/interpreter.rs::test_arena_*`).
  - [x] Snapshot/restore API: `arena.high_water_mark() -> ArenaCheckpoint`, `arena.rewind_to(cp: ArenaCheckpoint)` ŌĆö used for typechecker symbol-table backtracking, mid-parse error recovery, transactional middleware rollback. Truncates the Vec to the recorded length; subsequently-created `ArenaRef[T]`s past the checkpoint become use-after-free at runtime (debug-mode panic; release-mode undefined for v1, sound subsequent slice). Independent from drop-at-arena-end. **DONE** ŌĆö `ArenaCheckpoint` carries `(arena_handle_id, mark)`; `rewind_to` clamps `mark` to `[0, len]` and ignores a checkpoint minted by a different arena (handle-id guard). v1 dangling-handle `get` returns `Unit` (the debug-mode panic is the sound subsequent slice). Covered by `test_arena_high_water_mark_and_rewind` / `_rewind_keeps_pre_checkpoint_items` / `_rewind_with_foreign_checkpoint_is_ignored`.
  - [ ] Codegen lowering ŌĆö new `src/codegen/arena.rs` mirroring the eventual `pool.rs` shape: `Arena[T]` lowers to a Vec-like struct (`{ data: *mut T, len: i64, cap: i64 }`); `push` calls a `karac_runtime_arena_push` runtime helper; `get` GEPs into the data array. `Arena[T]` drop calls `karac_runtime_arena_free` which iterates the Vec dropping each element per `T`'s drop kind. Gated on user-`impl Drop` dispatch in codegen (shared dependency with `Pool[T]` codegen path entry above). **The lone remaining sub-item** ŌĆö like `Pool[T]`, `std.Arena` is interpreter-only at v1; the baked impl bodies never reach codegen (no lowered LLVM symbol), so a compute/AOT program that doesn't use `Arena` is unaffected (full `--features llvm` suite green).
  - [x] Effect-checker seeding for `Arena.push` (`allocates(Heap)`) and `Arena.new` (`allocates(Heap)`) in the startup-seeding block peer to the `Map.insert` / `Vec.push` seeding pattern. **DONE** ŌĆö `Arena.new` / `Arena.push` added to the path-call seeding list in `effectchecker.rs::seed_builtin_effects`, and `("push", "Arena.push")` to the `STDLIB_METHOD_MAP` instance-method walker in `effectchecker/inference.rs` (name-keyed over-approximation, unions cleanly with `Vec.push` since both seed the same verb). `allocates(Heap)` is the default-permitted v1 substrate effect, so no `pub fn` is forced to declare it; the seed is what the auto-parallelizer's receiver-mutation lookup keys on. Regression: `tests/effectchecker.rs::test_arena_push_infers_allocates_heap`.

- [ ] **[ŌåÆ P1] `Symbol` + `Interner` ŌĆö deduplicating string handle primitive.** Compact integer handle for interned strings: `Interner.new() -> Interner`; `interner.intern(s: ref String) -> Symbol` (returns the existing handle if `s` was previously interned; otherwise stores `s` and returns a fresh handle); `interner.resolve(sym: Symbol) -> ref String` (handle ŌåÆ string lookup). Equality on `Symbol` is integer comparison (no string compare); hashing is integer hashing. Use cases: HTTP-header canonicalization, JSON-key dedup, log-key dedup, regex character classes, comptime identifier resolution, every compiler's identifier handling. The Interner is `Arena[T]`-adjacent (durable lifetime, no per-item release) but adds a dedup HashMap on top ŌĆö distinct primitive worth its own name and worth its own teaching surface ("what's interning for?"). Effects: `allocates(Heap)` on `intern` when a fresh handle is minted; pure on `resolve` and on re-`intern` of an already-interned string. **Interpreter slice LANDED 2026-06-22** ŌĆö type surface + interpreter intrinsic + effect seeding shipped (sub-items below); only codegen lowering remains (deferred, interpreter-only like `Pool[T]` / `Arena[T]`). **Symbol-design decision:** `Symbol` is `#[derive(Eq, Hash, Copy, Clone, Display)] distinct type Symbol = i64` ŌĆö the transparent-`i64` form (the primary spec text, codegen-ready), NOT the `(symbol_id, interner_handle_id)` pair alternative (which conflicts with the bare-`i64` lowering). `Display` renders the integer id; thread the interner (`interner.resolve(sym)`) to print the text, per the Rust `Symbol`/`Ident` pattern. **Cross-surface fix surfaced here:** baked `distinct type`s were never registered into `env.distinct_types`/`distinct_bases` (`register_baked_stdlib` lumped `DistinctType` into a no-op arm), so ownership's `is_copy_type` never saw a baked `Copy` derive ŌĆö a `Symbol` passed by value (`interner.resolve(sym)`) *moved* instead of copying. Fixed by routing baked `DistinctType` through `env_add_distinct_type` (`ExitCode` carries no derives ŌåÆ unaffected; verified). Sub-items:
  - [x] Type surface: `Symbol` (transparent wrapper around `i64`) and `Interner` declared in baked stdlib `runtime/stdlib/interner.kara`; `Interner.new() / .intern / .resolve` signatures via `impl Interner { ... }`. `Symbol` derives `Eq`, `Hash`, `Copy`, `Display` (renders the integer id; thread the interner to render the string, like Rust's `Symbol`/`Ident`). **DONE** ŌĆö chose the transparent-`i64` `distinct type` form; `Symbol`/`Interner` registered in `PRELUDE_TYPES` + `interner.kara` in `STDLIB_SOURCES`; baked-distinct-type derive registration fix (`env_build.rs::register_baked_stdlib`) so `Symbol`'s `Copy`/`Eq`/`Hash` are honored cross-phase. The `(symbol_id, interner_handle_id)` pair alternative is explicitly not taken (conflicts with bare-`i64` lowering).
  - [x] Real interpreter intrinsic via `try_eval_interner_method` + `eval_interner_new` in new `src/interpreter/method_call_interner.rs`. Per-Interner state in `interner_table: HashMap<i64, (Vec<String>, HashMap<String, i64>)>` ŌĆö the Vec is the symbol-id ŌåÆ string lookup, the HashMap is the dedup index. Mirrors `pool_table` / `arena_table` shape. **DONE** ŌĆö `intern` returns the existing id on a dedup hit, else appends + indexes; `resolve` reads by id (clones ŌĆö interpreter can't hand a real `ref String`); foreign/out-of-range handles degrade to the empty string. Also ships a bonus `len()`. Dispatch wired through `method_call.rs` + the `"Interner.new"` path arm in `eval_call.rs`. 6 interpreter tests (`tests/interpreter.rs::test_interner_*`).
  - [ ] Codegen lowering ŌĆö new `src/codegen/interner.rs`. `Symbol` lowers to a bare `i64`; `Interner` lowers to a struct holding (Vec, HashMap). `intern` calls `karac_runtime_interner_intern`; `resolve` calls `karac_runtime_interner_resolve`. ~~Gated on user-`impl Drop` dispatch.~~ **UNBLOCKED (verified 2026-07-09)** ŌĆö the user-`impl Drop` dispatch this was gated on has landed: `emit_user_drop_wrappers` synthesizes per-type `karac_drop_<Type>` wrappers (`src/codegen/synth_drop.rs:3669`) driven by `CleanupAction::UserDrop` (`src/codegen/state.rs:821`), so a drop that frees both the Vec and the HashMap is now expressible. **The lone remaining sub-item** is the `interner.rs` lowering itself ŌĆö but the entry's deliberate interpreter-only-at-v1 posture (peer to `Pool[T]` / `Arena[T]`; baked bodies never reach codegen) means picking it up is a scope call, not a purely mechanical unblock.
  - [x] Effect-checker seeding for `Interner.intern` (`allocates(Heap)`) and `Interner.new` (`allocates(Heap)`). **DONE** ŌĆö added to the path-call seeding list (`effectchecker.rs`) + `("intern", "Interner.intern")` in the `STDLIB_METHOD_MAP` walker (`inference.rs`); conservatively seeds `intern` as allocating (a dedup hit is pure, but the checker can't distinguish a hit from a fresh mint statically). Regression: `tests/effectchecker.rs::test_interner_intern_infers_allocates_heap`.
  - [ ] Integration sites to validate: `f"..."` formatter (route String interpolation through Interner where dedup is profitable ŌĆö design decision, not a v1 commitment), HTTP header canonicalization in `std.http`, JSON key dedup in `std.json`. Each is an independent slice; the Interner primitive itself doesn't depend on them, but they're the consumers that justify it as P1.

---

### Pre-existing Phase 8 work

- [x] **`String.from_utf8(Vec[u8]) -> Result[String, Utf8Error]` ŌĆö UTF-8-validating String constructor (interpreter MVP).** Filed 2026-05-22 after the typechecker rejection of undeclared `Type.method(...)` calls landed (commit `db573a4`) ŌĆö that change made the typecheck-time gap surface as a clean diagnostic instead of an unrelated codegen explosion downstream. Spec'd in `design.md:4431` (`if let Ok(s) = String.from_utf8(input) { ... }`). Landed 2026-05-22 as an interpreter-only slice mirroring the peer pattern (`FileSystem.read_to_string`, `Url.decode`, `Base64.decode`, `Json.parse` ŌĆö all interpreter-only today). **Shipped.** (1) `enum Utf8Error { InvalidByte, IncompleteSequence, Other(String) }` declared in new `runtime/stdlib/utf8_error.kara`, registered in `STDLIB_SOURCES` and the prelude `PRELUDE_TYPES` list peer to `IoError` / `VarError`. (2) Path-keyed function signature `String.from_utf8(Vec[u8]) -> Result[String, Utf8Error]` registered in `register_compiler_intrinsic_env` (parallel to `env.var`); routes through `resolve_path_type`'s `env.functions` lookup. (3) Interpreter dispatch arm at `src/interpreter/eval_call.rs` `"String.from_utf8"` (peer to `Base64.decode` / `Url.decode`); calls `std::str::from_utf8` and maps `error_len() == None` ŌåÆ `Utf8Error.IncompleteSequence`, `Some(_)` ŌåÆ `Utf8Error.InvalidByte` (Rust's documented contract for the two failure modes). 3 typechecker tests (`test_string_from_utf8_returns_result_string_utf8_error`, `test_utf8_error_variants_exist`, `test_string_from_utf8_wrong_arg_type_is_error`) + 4 interpreter tests (`test_string_from_utf8_valid_returns_ok`, `test_string_from_utf8_invalid_byte_returns_err_invalid_byte`, `test_string_from_utf8_incomplete_returns_err_incomplete_sequence`, `test_string_from_utf8_empty_returns_ok_empty`). **Deferred ŌĆö codegen.** The original entry called for codegen dispatch in `src/codegen/assoc_call.rs` returning a "4-word `{tag, w0, w1, w2}` aggregate matching the existing Result lowering", but the existing Result lowering at `seed_builtin_enum_layouts` (`src/codegen/declarations.rs:2300`) is **1 payload word**, not 3 ŌĆö a String payload (3 words: data/len/cap) doesn't fit. Widening Result to a 3-word payload area parallels the existing Option widening, but also requires propagating all payload words in `compile_question`'s `?`-shortcircuit (currently only forwards `w0`) and registering String/Vec drop kinds on the seeded Result layout (currently `EnumDropKind::None`). That's a cross-cutting follow-up that affects every existing interpreter-only `Result[String, _]` / `Result[Vec[u8], _]` intrinsic (`FileSystem.read_to_string`, `Url.decode`, `Base64.decode`, `Json.parse`) ŌĆö best landed as one slice "widen Result codegen + flip all five intrinsics" rather than per-intrinsic. **Deferred ŌĆö special-arm cleanup.** Retiring the `String.from(x)` / `String.new()` / `String.with_capacity(n)` typechecker special arms in favor of real baked-stdlib `impl String { ... }` declarations also waits on a separate slice ŌĆö `env_add_impl` currently silently bails on `Type::Str` targets (the `_ => return` fall-through after `lower_type_expr`), so `impl String { ... }` from stdlib source has no effect today. Wiring that means extending the canonical-target-name match arm to handle `Type::Str` ŌåÆ `"String"`. The kata-91 bench's `Slice[u8]` parameter shape is unchanged regardless ŌĆö it's the correct apples-to-apples bench design vs the C/Rust/Go peers (byte-level DP work, no per-iter String alloc).

- [x] **Standard I/O surface ŌĆö stdlib implementation (Phase 8 interpreter MVP).** `IoError` enum (`NotFound`, `PermissionDenied`, `AlreadyExists`, `UnexpectedEof`, `InvalidUtf8`, `Interrupted`, `Other(String)`) registered in the prelude and typechecker. `Stdin`, `Stdout`, `Stderr`, `FileSystem` added to `PRELUDE_EFFECT_RESOURCES`. Interpreter builtins: `Stdin.read_line()`, `Stdin.read_to_string()` ŌåÆ `Result[String, IoError]`; `Stdout.flush()`, `Stderr.flush()` ŌåÆ `Unit`; `FileSystem.read_to_string(path)` ŌåÆ `Result[String, IoError]`; `FileSystem.write(path, contents)` ŌåÆ `Result[Unit, IoError]`. Typechecker signatures registered via dot-joined `"TypeName.method"` key looked up in `resolve_path_type`. 5 typechecker tests + 4 interpreter tests added. `env.args()` ŌåÆ `Vec[String]` and `env.var(name)` ŌåÆ `Result[String, VarError]` added: `VarError` (`NotPresent`, `NotUnicode`) registered in prelude + typechecker; resolver registers lowercase `"env"` as a `SymbolKind::Module` alias; both `"Env.args"` / `"env.args"` and `"Env.var"` / `"env.var"` registered in the function table; interpreter maps `"env"` ŌåÆ `"Env"` in `eval_method_call` for resource dispatch. 14 typechecker tests + 14 interpreter tests added. Sub-items factored out as separate trackable items: `impl From[VarError] for IoError` (shipped); `env.set` (shipped); `File` handle type (see entry below); `BufReader` (see entry below); book tutorial coverage, network I/O, and process spawning live under their respective Phase 8 surfaces.

- [x] **`env.set(name: String, value: String)` + `writes(Env)` effect.** Landed 2026-05-08. `env.var()` and `env.args()` companion shipped: lowercase `env.set` registered in `register_compiler_intrinsic_env` (peer to `env.var`), capitalized `Env.set` declared in baked stdlib `runtime/stdlib/io.kara` as `#[compiler_builtin] fn set(name: String, value: String) { }` (peer to `Env.var`). Interpreter dispatch arm in `dispatch_builtin_resource_method_with_values` calls `std::env::set_var(&name, &value)` (runtime crate is Rust 2021 edition, so `set_var` is safe ŌĆö interpreter is single-threaded at this surface), tracks `writes(Env)`, returns `Value::Unit`. Effectchecker seeds both `Env.set` and `env.set` with `writes(Env)` in the startup-seeding block (peer to the `Client.get`/`Client.post` Network seeding); the lowercase form parses as `MethodCall { object: Identifier("env") }` (the `starts_upper` gate keeps it out of the `Path` parse), so the `MethodCall` arm of `collect_calls_in_expr` mirrors the typechecker / interpreter lowercase-module alias by emitting `Env.<method>` as the call key when the receiver is the bare identifier `env`. Five new tests: `test_env_set_typechecks` and `test_env_set_wrong_arg_type_is_error` (typechecker, signature shape + arg-type error); `test_env_set_round_trips_via_var` (interpreter, `env.set` then `env.var` observes the same value); `test_env_set_infers_writes_env`, `test_env_set_capitalized_form_infers_writes_env`, `test_pub_fn_calling_env_set_must_declare_writes_env` and `test_pub_fn_with_writes_env_declared_accepts_env_set` (effectchecker, both call-key paths + negative `MissingEffectDeclaration` + positive declared-effect dual). Cargo test 2967 + LLVM 3258 green; clippy + fmt clean.

- [x] **`impl From[VarError] for IoError`.** Standard I/O Phase 8 follow-up ŌĆö needed for `?`-propagation from `env.var(...) -> Result[String, VarError]` into functions returning `Result[T, IoError]`. Variant mapping: `VarError.NotPresent` ŌåÆ `IoError.NotFound`; `VarError.NotUnicode` ŌåÆ `IoError.InvalidUtf8`.

- [x] **`File` handle type ŌĆö stateful file I/O shipped 2026-05-26 (F1ŌĆōF6 + F4b).** All seven sub-tasks complete: interpreter MVP, runtime shim, codegen type lowering + extern declarations, method codegen + KaracIoResult unpacker, scope-exit cleanup, ?-propagation tests, and broader E2E coverage. End-to-end `karac build` of File code produces binaries that correctly create / read / write / flush / close files through the OS, with IoError variants propagating through both direct match and `?` shorthand. **What this entry does NOT cover (deferred to follow-on slices):** seek / sync_all / metadata methods (F1 omitted them from the minimum useful surface; the runtime + extern declarations for seek are already in place via F2/F3, so adding them at the surface is a small follow-on); the non-destructured `Result[File, IoError]` leak (`let _r = File.open(p);` without destructuring ŌĆö no Drop hook for the wrapped variant; F4b registers cleanup on the destructured handle only); concurrent reads / writes on the same handle (Mutex serializes, but no K─üra-side handle cloning surface exists at v1); BufReader (separate entry below). Standard I/O Phase 8 follow-up factored out of the parent "Standard I/O surface" entry above. Today `FileSystem.read_to_string(path)` / `FileSystem.write(path, contents)` cover one-shot whole-file ops, but stateful read/write (incremental, seekable, with explicit flush) requires a `File` handle type with a live OS file descriptor. **Proposed v1 surface:** `File.open(path: String) -> Result[File, IoError]` (read-only), `File.create(path: String) -> Result[File, IoError]` (write, truncate), `File.append(path: String) -> Result[File, IoError]` (write, position at end); methods `file.read(buf: mut Slice[u8]) -> Result[usize, IoError]` (bytes-read; 0 = EOF), `file.write(buf: Slice[u8]) -> Result[usize, IoError]`, `file.flush() -> Result[Unit, IoError]`, `file.seek(pos: SeekFrom) -> Result[u64, IoError]` (SeekFrom enum: Start / Current / End), `file.sync_all() -> Result[Unit, IoError]` (data + metadata fsync), `file.metadata() -> Result[Metadata, IoError]` (size, modified, kind). Drop releases the file descriptor via the FreeFileHandle cleanup action peer to the existing FreeMapHandle pattern. **Effects:** `reads(FileSystem)` on `open` / `read` / `seek` / `metadata`; `writes(FileSystem)` on `create` / `append` / `write` / `flush` / `sync_all`; pure on construction-after-open (no-op). **Approach:** interpreter MVP first, then codegen following the `Map[K,V]` precedent (line 89-99). The earlier blocker (`Result[T, IoError]` 1-word payload, called out in the line-79 `String.from_utf8` entry) has since been resolved ŌĆö `seed_builtin_enum_layouts` widened `Result` to 4 payload words on 2026-05-21 (phase-8 line 435 slice 2 widening), so a `File` (1-word opaque ptr) Ok arm and an `IoError.Other(String)` (3-word) Err arm both fit. The remaining work is just the runtime-shim + opaque-ptr + method-codegen chain Map[K,V] shipped in 6 sub-tasks. **Cancel-safety annotation:** the `File` type carries a notional "has unflushed writes" bit that flips on `.write()` and clears on `.flush()` / `.sync_all()`. Shipped as `#[cancel_unsafe_until(method = "flush")]` on `File.write` in `runtime/stdlib/io.kara` alongside slice 3a of [`phase-6-runtime.md` line 155](phase-6-runtime.md) (2026-05-26); the slice-3a walker reads the attribute and rejects yields under an unflushed write. **Cross-references:** parent at line 81 ("Standard I/O surface"); realized in [`phase-6-runtime.md` line 155 slice 3a (RAII flow-sensitive detection ŌĆö File seeding)](phase-6-runtime.md). **Sub-task plan** (mirrors Map[K,V] line 89-99 ŌĆö each is a separate shippable slice):
  - [x] **F1 ŌĆö Interpreter MVP shipped 2026-05-26.** Mirrors the Map[K,V] / Sender / Receiver pattern: the typechecker sees an empty struct `File { }` declared in `runtime/stdlib/io.kara`; the interpreter holds the actual `std::fs::File` in a new `Value::File(Arc<Mutex<std::fs::File>>)` variant; `Arc` keeps the variant Clone-friendly without requiring Clone on `std::fs::File` itself (which is intentionally non-Clone ŌĆö a clone would be a `dup(2)` syscall, not a free op). Drop on the last Arc closes the OS fd via `std::fs::File`'s own Drop impl. **Surface:** `File.open(path)` / `.create(path)` / `.append(path)` ŌåÆ `Result[File, IoError]`; `file.read(buf: mut Slice[u8])` / `file.write(buf: Slice[u8])` ŌåÆ `Result[usize, IoError]`; `file.flush()` ŌåÆ `Result[Unit, IoError]`. All baked in `runtime/stdlib/io.kara` with `#[compiler_builtin]` stubs and `with reads(FileSystem)` / `with writes(FileSystem)` clauses. **Interpreter dispatch:** path-call constructors in `eval_call.rs` (single new `"File.open" | "File.create" | "File.append"` arm using `std::fs::OpenOptions` per mode); instance methods in a new `src/interpreter/method_call_file.rs` (`try_eval_file_method` covering `read` / `write` / `flush`, locking the mutex per call, reading bytes through the slice's storage). `std::io::Error` ŌåÆ `IoError` mapping reuses the existing `io_error_from_std` helper (NotFound / PermissionDenied / AlreadyExists / UnexpectedEof / InvalidDataŌåÆInvalidUtf8 / Interrupted / Other(String)). `Value::File` added to the `variant_name` exhaustive match and the `Display` impl (renders as `<File>`); `PartialEq` falls through to the `_ => false` catch-all (file handles aren't structurally comparable at v1). **Effect-checker seeding:** hand-seeded in `src/effectchecker.rs` alongside the Env.set / Client.get patterns ŌĆö `File.open` / `File.read` carry `reads(FileSystem)`; `File.create` / `File.append` / `File.write` / `File.flush` carry `writes(FileSystem)`. The baked `with` clauses propagate through `collect_declared_effects` for the declaration side, but the path-keyed lookup the inference walker performs for free-function and instance-method calls reads from `inferred_effects`, so explicit seeding bridges declaration ŌåÆ inference for stdlib builtins (same pattern Map / Channel / Sender use). **Tests:** 4 new interpreter tests (`test_file_create_write_flush_reopen_read_roundtrip` end-to-end byte round-trip; `test_file_open_nonexistent_returns_io_error_not_found` Err arm with NotFound variant; `test_file_append_constructor_writes_at_end` two-call concatenation; `test_file_flush_on_writable_handle_returns_ok`); 7 new typechecker tests (signature shape for each method + wrong-arg-type rejection); 3 new effect-checker tests (missing reads(FileSystem) on File.open + missing writes(FileSystem) on File.create + positive declared-effects path). **Empirical smoke:** end-to-end `karac run /tmp/file_smoke.kara` round-trip (create ŌåÆ write 3 bytes ŌåÆ flush ŌåÆ open ŌåÆ read 3 bytes) succeeds with the expected output. All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check` + `cargo clippy --all --all-targets --features llvm -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions (typechecker 1248 ŌåÆ 1256, interpreter 646 ŌåÆ 650, effectchecker 263 ŌåÆ 267). Files: `src/prelude.rs` (`File` in PRELUDE_TYPES); `src/interpreter.rs` (new `mod method_call_file`); `src/interpreter/value.rs` (new `Value::File` variant + Display/variant_name arms); `src/interpreter/eval_call.rs` (constructor dispatch); `src/interpreter/method_call_file.rs` (new ŌĆö instance-method dispatch); `src/interpreter/method_call.rs` (wire `try_eval_file_method` into the dispatch chain); `src/effectchecker.rs` (FileSystem-effect seeding for File methods); `runtime/stdlib/io.kara` (baked `struct File { }` + `impl File { ... }` with effect clauses); `tests/interpreter.rs`; `tests/typechecker.rs`; `tests/effectchecker.rs`. **Defers** `seek` / `sync_all` / `metadata` to a follow-on slice ŌĆö minimum useful surface for slice 3 of phase-6 line 155 (RAII flow-sensitive design) only.
  - [x] **F2 ŌĆö Runtime shim shipped 2026-05-26.** New `runtime/src/file.rs` with the v1 ABI surface: `KaracFile { inner: Mutex<std::fs::File> }` opaque handle; `KaracIoResult { value: i64, error_kind: i32, _pad: i32, error_msg_ptr: *mut u8, error_msg_len: i64 }` unified result shape (32 bytes, layout-pinned) returned from every entry point so codegen at F4 destructures one struct into both the Ok/Err arms; symbols `karac_runtime_file_open` / `_create` / `_append` (handle returned in `value` cast to i64) and `karac_runtime_file_read` / `_write` (bytes count in `value`) / `_flush` / `_close` / `_seek` (added preemptively for the follow-on slice; not yet exposed at the K─üra surface). **Design fork settled:** the unified `KaracIoResult` replaces the originally planned (out-param handle + errno-style return) shape ŌĆö codegen reads one struct vs. branching on multiple return values, and the `IoError.Other(String)` message path (allocated via `std::alloc::alloc` on the runtime side, transferred to the K─üra-side `String` aggregate's drop path) is encoded directly in `error_msg_ptr`/`_len`. IoError variant tags: 0 = Ok, 1 = NotFound, 2 = PermissionDenied, 3 = AlreadyExists, 4 = UnexpectedEof, 5 = InvalidUtf8 (from `ErrorKind::InvalidData`), 6 = Interrupted, 7 = Other. **Lifetime:** `Box::into_raw` on open-family; `karac_runtime_file_close` reconstructs the Box and drops it (releasing the OS fd via `std::fs::File`'s Drop). Null-handle is a no-op for close. **5 runtime unit tests** in `runtime/src/file.rs::tests`: ABI layout pin (every field offset + total size), end-to-end round-trip (create ŌåÆ write ŌåÆ flush ŌåÆ close ŌåÆ reopen ŌåÆ read), NotFound error path, null-close safety, append-mode extends existing file. All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check` + `cargo clippy --all --all-targets --features llvm -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions (runtime tests 88 ŌåÆ 93). Files: `runtime/src/file.rs` (new ŌĆö ~430 LOC including tests), `runtime/src/lib.rs` (new `mod file` declaration). **What F2 does NOT cover:** codegen-side wiring ŌĆö symbols are exported but no K─üra-callable path reaches them yet. F3 declares the externs in the codegen; F4 lowers method calls to use them; F5 verifies `?`-propagation; F6 closes out with E2E coverage.
  - [x] **F3 ŌĆö Type lowering + extern fn declarations shipped 2026-05-26.** Two-part change. (1) `File` lowers to opaque `ptr` in `llvm_type_for_type_expr` (`src/codegen/types_lowering.rs`), parallel to the existing `Map[K, V]` / `Set[T]` / `Request` cases ŌĆö single-segment path-type name ŌåÆ `context.ptr_type(AddressSpace::default()).into()`. No side-table is needed (File carries no element-typed sub-state, unlike Map's `map_key_types` / `map_val_types`). (2) All `karac_runtime_file_*` externs declared in `Codegen::new()` (`src/codegen.rs`, after the HTTP-extern block): `karac_runtime_file_open` / `_create` / `_append` ((ptr, i64) ŌåÆ KaracIoResult), `_read` / `_write` ((ptr, ptr, i64) ŌåÆ KaracIoResult), `_flush` ((ptr) ŌåÆ KaracIoResult), `_close` ((ptr) ŌåÆ void). The `_seek` extern is declared by F2 but not by F3 ŌĆö F1's surface didn't expose it. **KaracIoResult struct shape** declared inline matches the runtime's `#[repr(C)]` layout exactly (`{ i64 value, i32 error_kind, i32 _pad, ptr error_msg_ptr, i64 error_msg_len }`, 32 bytes, alignment 8). Reusable helper `Codegen::kara_io_result_type()` added in `src/codegen/types_lowering.rs` (gated `#[allow(dead_code)]` until F4 consumes it). **ABI commitment:** LLVM models the struct return directly via `fn_type` with a struct return type; Rust's `extern "C"` calling convention applies the target-native struct-return ABI (sret-via-hidden-pointer on x86_64 SystemV when the struct exceeds 16 bytes; indirect-via-x8 on AArch64). Both sides agreeing on "returns this 32-byte struct" produces ABI-aligned code without explicit sret threading on the LLVM side. If a target surfaces a mismatch in F4/F6 E2E tests, fall back to an explicit `*mut KaracIoResult` out-param shape (requires re-baking F2 + this declaration). All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check` + `cargo clippy --all --all-targets --features llvm -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions (no new tests at F3 ŌĆö the lowering is exercised implicitly by F4 method codegen). Files: `src/codegen.rs` (extern block, ~50 lines), `src/codegen/types_lowering.rs` (File ŌåÆ opaque ptr arm + `kara_io_result_type` helper). **What F3 does NOT cover:** call-site lowering (F4) ŌĆö the externs are declared but no call site reaches them yet.
  - [x] **F4 ŌĆö Method codegen + KaracIoResult ŌåÆ Result[T, IoError] unpacker shipped 2026-05-26.** New `src/codegen/file.rs` module with the shared `Codegen::lower_kara_io_result(slot, ok_kind)` helper (loads the four KaracIoResult fields via GEPs against a stack slot, branches on `error_kind == 0`, builds the surface Result aggregate). Three constructor wrappers (`compile_file_constructor` switching on `karac_runtime_file_open` / `_create` / `_append`) wired into `src/codegen/assoc_call.rs` ahead of `Server.serve_static`'s `type_name == "Server"` arm ŌĆö the constructor-dispatch precedent. Three method wrappers (`compile_file_read` / `_write` / `_flush`) wired into `src/codegen/method_call.rs` ahead of the `TcpStream.read` arm ŌĆö the method-dispatch precedent. **Pattern-binding intŌåÆptr re-typing** in `src/codegen/pattern_binding.rs`: parallel arm to the existing `shared_types` path that catches `pattern_binding_types[span] == "File"` and reconstructs the `ptr` LLVM type from the destructured i64 payload word. Without this, `match File.open(p) { Ok(f) => f.read(...) }` would compile `f` as an IntValue at the method-dispatch site and panic on `.into_pointer_value()`. **Design fork ŌĆö struct-return ŌåÆ out-param ABI:** the F2/F3 first cut declared the runtime extern signature as returning `KaracIoResult` by value, with LLVM modelling the struct return directly. End-to-end smoke surfaced a corrupted-stack hang at the call boundary ŌĆö the 32-byte struct exceeds the 16-byte register-return threshold on every supported target (System V x86_64 sret-via-hidden-pointer; AAPCS AArch64 indirect-via-x8), and modelling the indirect-return ABI in LLVM IR requires `sret` / `byval` parameter attributes that must match Rust's exact lowering on each target. F4 amended F2 + F3 to use an out-param shape: every extern takes `out: *mut KaracIoResult` as the first arg, callee writes into the slot, no return value. Codegen allocas a slot in the function entry block via `alloca_io_result_slot`, passes its address, then GEPs + loads the field values. The runtime crate's 5 unit tests were updated to call through the new ABI (`fresh_result()` helper allocates the slot per call). **IoError variant tag mapping:** runtime tags shift by 1 to reserve 0 for the OK sentinel; the codegen unpacker emits `io_tag = error_kind - 1` so IoError.NotFound=0 / PermissionDenied=1 / ... / Other=6 lines up with the source-order tag assignment from `runtime/stdlib/io_error.kara`. For `Other(String)`, the runtime-allocated message buffer transfers ownership to the codegen-side K─üra `String` aggregate via `error_msg_ptr` / `error_msg_len` (the codegen stores `len` for both `len` and `cap`, so the K─üra-side String drop path frees correctly). **End-to-end smoke verified:** `karac build` of a kara program that creates a temp file, writes "hi\n" through `f.write(data)`, flushes, reopens, and reads back into a Vec produces a binary that runs to completion and writes the expected 3 bytes to disk. All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check` + `cargo clippy --all --all-targets --features llvm -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions across all test binaries. Files: `runtime/src/file.rs` (ABI signatures + tests rewritten to out-param shape), `src/codegen.rs` (extern declarations updated to void-return + out-param first arg), `src/codegen/types_lowering.rs` (`#[allow(dead_code)]` removed from `kara_io_result_type` ŌĆö F4 consumes it), `src/codegen/file.rs` (new ŌĆö ~380 LOC: unpacker + 3 constructors + 3 method wrappers + slot allocator), `src/codegen/assoc_call.rs` (constructor dispatch arm), `src/codegen/method_call.rs` (read/write/flush dispatch arms), `src/codegen/pattern_binding.rs` (File intŌåÆptr re-typing arm). **What F4 does NOT cover:** scope-exit cleanup via `FreeFileHandle` (split out as F4b ŌĆö the file descriptor leaks until process exit at v1 if user code doesn't otherwise close it); end-to-end `tests/codegen.rs` cases (F6 covers); `?`-propagation verification (F5 covers).
  - [x] **F4b ŌĆö `FreeFileHandle` scope-exit cleanup shipped 2026-05-26.** New `CleanupAction::FreeFileHandle { file_alloca: PointerValue }` variant in `src/codegen/state.rs` peer to `FreeMapHandle`; new `track_file_var(file_alloca)` in `src/codegen/runtime.rs` pushes the action onto the active scope frame; emission path in the scope-cleanup drain loads the handle from the alloca and calls `karac_runtime_file_close` ŌĆö null-handle is a no-op on the runtime side, so no guard is needed. Hook in `src/codegen/pattern_binding.rs`: the F4 `type_name == "File"` intŌåÆptr re-typing arm now calls `track_file_var(alloca)` immediately after registering the binding, so every File handle bound through `match Ok(f) => ...` is cleaned up at scope exit. **Smoke verified:** F4's smoke test was modified to drop the explicit `f.flush()` call ŌĆö the on-disk contents are still correct because the scope-exit `karac_runtime_file_close` reconstructs `Box<KaracFile>` and runs `std::fs::File`'s Drop impl, which flushes pending writes through the kernel before closing the fd. All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check` + `cargo clippy --all --all-targets --features llvm -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions. Files: `src/codegen/state.rs` (new CleanupAction variant), `src/codegen/runtime.rs` (`track_file_var` helper + emission arm), `src/codegen/pattern_binding.rs` (hook into the File re-typing arm). **What F4b does NOT cover:** non-destructured Result leak ŌĆö `let _r = File.open(p);` without destructuring still leaks (the File ptr lives inside the Result's payload word with no Drop hook for the wrapped variant; F4b registers cleanup on the destructured handle, not on the Result wrapper). The canonical idiom is to destructure, so the limit doesn't impact normal code shape; lint-rejecting the non-destructured form is a separate follow-on.
  - [x] **F5 ŌĆö `?`-propagation through `Result[File, IoError]` shipped 2026-05-26.** **No codegen changes needed** ŌĆö empirical verification shows the existing `compile_question` path forwards all 4 payload words of the widened Result layout correctly. Json.parse exercised the Ok-with-multi-word-payload case at phase-8 line 435 slice 2 (2026-05-21); F5 confirms the symmetric Err-with-multi-word-payload case works for `Result[T, IoError]` (where IoError can be a unit variant or `Other(String)`). **2 new E2E tests** in `tests/codegen.rs` under a new `Phase 8 File handle slice F5` section: `test_e2e_file_open_question_propagates_not_found` (helper returning `Result[i64, IoError]` calls `File.open(nonexistent)?`; caller matches the propagated `IoError.NotFound` variant ŌĆö pins both the `?`-mechanism and the variant-tag pass-through); `test_e2e_file_open_question_passes_through_ok` (helper opens an existing tempfile via `?` and returns Ok(0); caller matches Ok ŌĆö pins the success path doesn't accidentally wrap as Err). Both run compiled binaries end-to-end. All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check` + `cargo clippy --all --all-targets --features llvm -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions. Files: `tests/codegen.rs` (+2 tests + slice section comment). **What F5 does NOT cover:** the `IoError.Other(String)` payload-through-? path ŌĆö hard to trigger naturally (most filesystem errors map to unit variants like NotFound / PermissionDenied; `Other` is a fallback for kernel-version-specific kinds). F6's broader test coverage may add a forced-Other case if a deterministic trigger is found; otherwise the unit-variant case is the load-bearing path for the v1 surface.
  - [x] **F6 ŌĆö E2E tests + checklist update shipped 2026-05-26.** **4 new E2E tests** in `tests/codegen.rs` under a new `Phase 8 File handle slice F6` section, each runs a compiled binary end-to-end: `test_e2e_file_create_write_flush_reopen_read_full_roundtrip` (writes 3 bytes through the K─üra surface, reopens, reads back, asserts both the on-disk contents and the read byte count); `test_e2e_file_drop_closes_handle_and_flushes_pending_writes` (omits explicit flush ŌĆö the F4b scope-exit `karac_runtime_file_close` action runs `std::fs::File`'s Drop, which flushes pending writes through the kernel; on-disk contents prove the cleanup wiring works); `test_e2e_file_open_nonexistent_match_arm_io_error_not_found` (direct match on `IoError.NotFound` ŌĆö pins the variant tag value codegen emits matches the source-order tag assignment in `runtime/stdlib/io_error.kara`); `test_e2e_file_large_write_and_read_round_trip` (writes 256 bytes via a `while`-loop `data.push(...)` chain, flushes, reads from disk through the host OS ŌĆö verifies multi-page payloads round-trip correctly through the runtime extern boundary). Combined with F5's 2 `?`-propagation tests, the codegen test suite now has 6 dedicated File E2E cases. All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check` + `cargo clippy --all --all-targets --features llvm -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test --features llvm` passes with zero regressions. Files: `tests/codegen.rs` (+4 tests + slice section comment). **What F6 does NOT cover:** the `IoError.Other(String)` payload-through-? path (no deterministic trigger found ŌĆö most filesystem errors map to unit variants); concurrent reads / writes on the same File handle (the Mutex inside `KaracFile` serializes per-handle access, but no test exercises this directly ŌĆö the v1 K─üra surface doesn't expose handle cloning at the source level, so the path isn't reachable from user code today).

  **What this entry does NOT cover:** `BufReader` / `BufWriter` (separate entry below); async/non-blocking File I/O (the network-event-loop-style suspending shape ŌĆö Phase 11 disk-I/O event loop covers that surface); permission flags beyond the three opening modes (mode bits, umask, OpenOptions builder ŌĆö likely a v1.x follow-on); platform-specific extensions (Unix permissions, Windows file attributes); `seek` / `sync_all` / `metadata` (deferred from F1 to a follow-on slice ŌĆö not required for the minimum useful surface or for slice 3 of phase-6 line 155).

- [x] **`BufReader[R]` ŌĆö buffered reader wrapper. Ō£ō Interpreter MVP shipped 2026-06-06.** Standard I/O Phase 8 follow-up factored out of the parent "Standard I/O surface" entry above. Wraps any `Read` source (initially `File`; eventually `Stdin`, network streams, etc.) with an internal buffer so per-call syscall overhead amortizes. **Shipped surface (interpreter MVP):** `BufReader.new(reader: File) -> BufReader[File]` (default 8 KiB buffer) / `BufReader.with_capacity(reader: File, cap: usize) -> BufReader[File]`; `br.read_line(buf: mut ref String) -> Result[usize, IoError]` (append until `\n`/EOF; bytes appended; 0 = EOF) / `br.read_to_string(buf: mut ref String) -> Result[usize, IoError]` (slurp to EOF) / `br.read(buf: mut Slice[u8]) -> Result[usize, IoError]` (drain-buffer-then-delegate). The documented `mut String` shorthand below realizes as K─üra's mutable-borrow form `mut ref String`. **Pattern: Pool + File.** Followed `Pool[T]`'s generic-stdlib-type structure (empty `struct BufReader[R] { }` + baked generic `impl[R] BufReader[R] { ... }` for typechecking, `#[compiler_builtin]` stubs, `"BufReader.new"` / `.with_capacity` path-string constructor arms in `eval_call.rs`, dedicated `try_eval_bufreader_method` interpreter dispatch) combined with `File`'s effect seeding (`inferred_effects` hand-seed of `reads(FileSystem)` for the three read methods ŌĆö the baked `with reads(FileSystem)` clauses propagate on the declaration side but the call-site walker reads the post-inference table). **Interpreter representation:** `Value::BufReader(Arc<Mutex<std::io::BufReader<std::fs::File>>>)` ŌĆö construction `try_clone`s (dup) the wrapped `File`'s fd so the BufReader owns its reader while the original `File` value stays usable; the dup shares the OS file offset so reads resume from where the `File` left off. `read_line` / `read_to_string` append into the `mut ref String` destination and write the result back through `env.set` (bare-identifier destination, same idiom as `String.push`); `read` writes bytes back through the `mut Slice[u8]`'s shared storage exactly like `File.read`. **Files:** `runtime/stdlib/bufreader.kara` (new ŌĆö struct + baked `impl[R]`); `src/prelude.rs` (`BufReader` in `PRELUDE_TYPES`, `stub_generics` 1-param group, `STDLIB_SOURCES`); `src/interpreter/value.rs` (`Value::BufReader` variant + Display/`variant_name` arms); `src/interpreter/method_call_bufreader.rs` (new ŌĆö `try_eval_bufreader_method`); `src/interpreter.rs` (`mod method_call_bufreader`); `src/interpreter/method_call.rs` (dispatch-chain wiring after `try_eval_file_method`); `src/interpreter/eval_call.rs` (constructor path arms); `src/effectchecker.rs` (`reads(FileSystem)` seeding). **Tests:** 6 typechecker (`test_bufreader_{new,with_capacity}_returns_bufreader`, `test_bufreader_{read_line,read_to_string,read_takes_mut_slice}_returns_result_usize`, `test_bufreader_read_line_wrong_arg_type_is_error`) + 4 interpreter (`test_bufreader_read_line_then_read_to_string_roundtrip`, `..._at_eof_returns_zero`, `..._read_to_string_slurps_whole_file`, `..._with_capacity_read_into_slice`) + 2 effectchecker (`test_pub_fn_calling_bufreader_read_line_must_declare_reads_filesystem` + positive `..._with_reads_filesystem_declared_accepts_bufreader_methods` ŌĆö both use `effectcheck_full_pipeline` because instance-method effect resolution needs the threaded `method_callee_types`). All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check` + `cargo clippy --all --all-targets --features llvm -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test` + `cargo test --features llvm` green with zero regressions. **Deferred to follow-on slices:** `br.lines() -> LinesIter[R]` (needs a `LinesIter` iterator type ŌĆö the largest deferred piece); `br.fill_buf() -> Result[Slice[u8], IoError]` / `br.consume(n)` (low-level peek/advance ŌĆö awkward to model in the tree-walk interpreter, low demand); the `#[cancel_unsafe_until(...)]` cancel-safety annotation (deferred from this MVP, then **decided 2026-06-06 to be a no-op at v1** ŌĆö BufReader read-ahead loss isn't a silent correctness violation the way BufWriter's unflushed write is, and there's no clean `flush`-equivalent clear method to flip the binding back to Clean, so annotating would mis-seed the walker; see [`phase-6-runtime.md` line 189 slice 3b](phase-6-runtime.md) for the full rationale). The peer **BufWriter** annotation *did* ship (line 276) ŌĆö its single soil/clear pair mirrors `File.write` exactly. **Proposed full v1 surface (original):** `BufReader.new(reader: R) -> BufReader[R]` with default 8KiB capacity; `BufReader.with_capacity(reader: R, cap: usize) -> BufReader[R]`; methods `br.read_line(buf: mut String) -> Result[usize, IoError]` (reads until `\n` or EOF; bytes-appended; 0 = EOF ŌĆö matches Rust's contract), `br.read_to_string(buf: mut String) -> Result[usize, IoError]`, `br.lines() -> LinesIter[R]` (iterator yielding `Result[String, IoError]` per line, EOF terminates), `br.fill_buf() -> Result[Slice[u8], IoError]` (low-level peek), `br.consume(n: usize)` (advance after `fill_buf`), `br.read(buf: mut Slice[u8]) -> Result[usize, IoError]` (delegates to underlying after draining buffer). Drop releases the buffer; the wrapped `R` drops by ownership (no explicit close). **Effects:** same as the wrapped reader ŌĆö `reads(FileSystem)` when `R = File`; effect-polymorphic in design but concrete bindings at v1 since the trait-impl-routing for effect polymorphism is itself a P1 surface ([`phase-3-effect-checker.md`](phase-3-effect-checker.md)). **Approach:** depends on `File` (entry above) for the v1 use case; can ship in either order if the wrapped-reader contract is stubbed against a placeholder `Read` trait first. Interpreter-only MVP. **Cancel-safety annotation:** originally sketched as a "buffer non-empty" NOT-CancelSafe bit (same shape as `File`'s "unflushed writes" bit), but **decided 2026-06-06 to be a no-op at v1** ŌĆö unlike a writer's unflushed bytes (silent data loss), a reader's buffered read-ahead represents bytes the program never logically consumed, so losing them on cancel drops no committed progress; and there's no clean `flush`-equivalent clear method, so a `#[cancel_unsafe_until]` annotation would mis-seed the slice-3a walker. The walker is type-agnostic so BufReader can be annotated later if a real hazard surfaces (e.g. a stateful protocol parser with mid-frame read-ahead). See [`phase-6-runtime.md` line 189 slice 3b](phase-6-runtime.md). **Cross-references:** parent at line 81; depends on `File` entry above; informed [`phase-6-runtime.md` line 189 slice 3b](phase-6-runtime.md) (closed 2026-06-06 ŌĆö BufWriter annotated, BufReader consciously not). **What this entry does NOT cover:** `BufWriter[W]` (likely a peer entry once a `Write`-side use case surfaces ŌĆö `BufReader` is the more common idiom and the design audit's named example, so it leads); a generic `Read` / `Write` trait pair as a first-class surface (effect-polymorphic traits are P1); `Lines` iterator surface beyond the basic `Result[String, IoError]`-yielding shape (chunked reads, char iteration, encoding-aware variants live in `std.encoding` if/when that lands).
  - [x] **`br.lines() -> LinesIter` ŌĆö line-iterator surface. Shipped 2026-06-06 (interpreter MVP).** `BufReader.lines()` returns a `LinesIter` that the `for` loop drains one line at a time, yielding `Result[String, IoError]` per line: `Ok(line)` with the trailing `\n` / `\r\n` stripped (matching Rust's `BufRead::lines`), `Err` once on a mid-stream read error (then terminate), EOF terminates; an empty file yields nothing. **`LinesIter` is non-generic** (not the originally-sketched `LinesIter[R]`): its element type is concretely `Result[String, IoError]` and the wrapped reader type is erased in the interpreter, so a `[R]` parameter buys nothing ŌĆö and the resolved-method path doesn't yet substitute an impl-level `R` from the receiver (a bare `let it = br.lines()` left `R` un-inferable until `LinesIter` was made non-generic). It can gain a parameter additively when effect-polymorphic readers (Stdin / network streams) land. **Interpreter representation:** `Value::LinesIter(Arc<Mutex<std::io::BufReader<std::fs::File>>>)` Arc-shares the originating `BufReader`'s wrapped reader (Rust's `lines()` consumes the reader; the interpreter shares it, so draining the iterator advances ŌĆö and leaves at EOF ŌĆö the originating `BufReader`). Eager-materialized in the for-loop like the other iterables. **Effect:** `lines()` carries `reads(FileSystem)` ŌĆö the per-line reads happen during iteration, which has no method-call site, so the effect is attributed at the `lines()` call (seeded in `effectchecker.rs` alongside the other BufReader read methods). **Files:** `runtime/stdlib/bufreader.kara` (`struct LinesIter` + `fn lines`); `src/prelude.rs` (`LinesIter` in `PRELUDE_TYPES`); `src/typechecker/env_build.rs` (programmatic `("LinesIter", "Item") -> Result[String, IoError]` mapping driving `element_type_of`, since the baked struct has no syntactic `Item` binding); `src/interpreter/value.rs` (`Value::LinesIter` + Display / `variant_name` arms); `src/interpreter/method_call_bufreader.rs` (`lines` dispatch arm); `src/interpreter/eval_expr.rs` (`Value::LinesIter` for-loop drain arm); `src/effectchecker.rs` (`BufReader.lines` seed). **Tests:** 2 typechecker (`test_bufreader_lines_returns_lines_iter`, `test_bufreader_lines_for_loop_binds_result_string`) + 3 interpreter (`test_bufreader_lines_iterates_and_strips_newlines`, `_crlf_and_no_trailing_newline`, `_empty_file_yields_nothing`) + 2 effectchecker (`test_pub_fn_calling_bufreader_lines_must_declare_reads_filesystem` + positive). All gates green: `cargo fmt --all -- --check`, `cargo clippy --all --all-targets --features llvm -- -D warnings`, full non-llvm suite. **Deferred:** chunked / char / encoding-aware line variants stay in `std.encoding` if/when that lands.
  - [x] **`br.fill_buf() -> Result[Slice[u8], IoError]` / `br.consume(n: usize)` ŌĆö low-level peek/advance. Shipped 2026-06-06 (interpreter MVP).** `fill_buf` fills the internal buffer (if empty) from the underlying reader and returns its currently-buffered, not-yet-consumed bytes as a `Slice[u8]` (empty at EOF); `consume(n)` marks `n` peeked bytes as consumed so they aren't returned again by `fill_buf` / `read`. **Snapshot, not alias.** The original carve noted the returned `Slice` "must alias the BufReader's live buffer across calls" ŌĆö the tree-walk interpreter can't hand back a `Slice` aliasing `std::io::BufReader`'s private buffer, so `fill_buf` returns a fresh **snapshot copy** of the buffered bytes (a new `Arc<RwLock<Vec<Value>>>`-backed `Slice`). This is behaviorally correct for the peek-then-`consume` idiom ŌĆö `consume` advances the real `std::io::BufReader` cursor, and a subsequent `fill_buf` re-reads the post-consume buffer ŌĆö the only divergence from Rust being that the snapshot stays valid after `consume` (no borrow-checker conflict). `consume(n)` is clamped to the available buffered length (std saturates an over-count anyway). **Effects:** `fill_buf` carries `reads(FileSystem)` (it refills from the underlying reader); `consume` is **effect-free** (cursor-advance only, no I/O) ŌĆö verified by a positive effectcheck test. **Files:** `runtime/stdlib/bufreader.kara` (`fill_buf` + `consume`); `src/interpreter/method_call_bufreader.rs` (both dispatch arms; `fill_buf` builds a fresh `Value::Slice`, `consume` drives `BufRead::consume` clamped to `buffer().len()`); `src/effectchecker.rs` (`BufReader.fill_buf` seed; `consume` deliberately absent). No typechecker change ŌĆö the baked-impl signatures (`Result[Slice[u8], IoError]` / `consume(n: usize)`) resolve through the normal path. **Tests:** 2 typechecker (`test_bufreader_fill_buf_returns_result_slice_and_consume_takes_usize`, `test_bufreader_consume_wrong_arg_type_is_error`) + 3 interpreter (`test_bufreader_fill_buf_peek_consume_read_roundtrip`, `_fill_buf_at_eof_returns_empty_slice`, `_consume_clamps_past_buffer`) + 2 effectchecker (`test_pub_fn_calling_bufreader_fill_buf_must_declare_reads_filesystem`, `test_pub_fn_calling_bufreader_consume_needs_no_effect`). All gates green (fmt, clippy `--all-targets --features llvm`, full non-llvm suite). **Unblocks** the phase-6 slice-3b seeding of these two methods into the `#[cancel_unsafe_until]` walker ([`phase-6-runtime.md` slice 3b, line 189](phase-6-runtime.md)) ŌĆö the surface now exists to annotate.
  - [x] **`BufWriter[W]` ŌĆö buffered writer peer. Ō£ō Interpreter MVP shipped 2026-06-06.** Carved from the BufReader MVP's "does NOT cover" note (2026-06-06). The Write-side mirror: wraps a `Write` sink (initially `File`) with an internal buffer, flushing on capacity / explicit `flush()` / drop. **Shipped surface (interpreter MVP):** `BufWriter.new(writer: File) -> BufWriter[File]` (default 8 KiB buffer) / `BufWriter.with_capacity(writer: File, cap: usize) -> BufWriter[File]`; `bw.write(buf: Slice[u8]) -> Result[usize, IoError]` (buffer bytes; bytes accepted) / `bw.flush() -> Result[Unit, IoError]` (drain buffer to the underlying writer). **Pattern: exact mirror of `BufReader[R]`** (line 272) ŌĆö empty `struct BufWriter[W] { }` + baked generic `impl[W] BufWriter[W] { ... }` for typechecking, `#[compiler_builtin]` stubs, `"BufWriter.new"` / `.with_capacity` path-string constructor arms in `eval_call.rs`, dedicated `try_eval_bufwriter_method` interpreter dispatch, `File`'s effect-seeding idiom (`inferred_effects` hand-seed of `writes(FileSystem)` for `write` / `flush` ŌĆö the baked `with writes(FileSystem)` clauses propagate on the declaration side but the call-site walker reads the post-inference table). **Interpreter representation:** `Value::BufWriter(Arc<Mutex<std::io::BufWriter<std::fs::File>>>)` ŌĆö construction `try_clone`s (dup) the wrapped `File`'s fd so the BufWriter owns its writer while the original `File` value stays usable; the dup shares the OS file offset so writes land wherever the `File` left off. `write` reads the `Slice[u8]`'s bytes into a temporary `Vec<u8>` and writes through the locked handle exactly like `File.write` (also accepts a `Vec[u8]` arg permissively). **Drop flushes:** `std::io::BufWriter`'s own Drop flushes buffered bytes through the cloned fd when the last `Value::BufWriter` Arc drops at scope exit ŌĆö verified by `test_bufwriter_drop_flushes_pending_writes` (writes without an explicit `flush()`, reads back after the writing scope ends). **Files:** `runtime/stdlib/bufwriter.kara` (new ŌĆö struct + baked `impl[W]`); `src/prelude.rs` (`BufWriter` in `PRELUDE_TYPES`, `stub_generics` 1-param group, `STDLIB_SOURCES`); `src/interpreter/value.rs` (`Value::BufWriter` variant + Display/`variant_name` arms); `src/interpreter/method_call_bufwriter.rs` (new ŌĆö `try_eval_bufwriter_method`); `src/interpreter.rs` (`mod method_call_bufwriter`); `src/interpreter/method_call.rs` (dispatch-chain wiring after `try_eval_bufreader_method`); `src/interpreter/eval_call.rs` (constructor path arms); `src/effectchecker.rs` (`writes(FileSystem)` seeding). **Tests:** 5 typechecker (`test_bufwriter_{new,with_capacity}_returns_bufwriter`, `test_bufwriter_write_returns_result_usize`, `test_bufwriter_flush_returns_result_unit`, `test_bufwriter_write_wrong_arg_type_is_error`) + 3 interpreter (`test_bufwriter_write_flush_reopen_read_roundtrip`, `..._with_capacity_write_flush`, `..._drop_flushes_pending_writes`) + 2 effectchecker (`test_pub_fn_calling_bufwriter_write_must_declare_writes_filesystem` + positive `..._with_writes_filesystem_declared_accepts_bufwriter_methods` ŌĆö both use `effectcheck_full_pipeline` because instance-method effect resolution needs the threaded `method_callee_types`). All clear under `cargo fmt --all -- --check` + `cargo clippy --all --all-targets --features llvm -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test` + `cargo test --features llvm` green with zero regressions. **Deferred to follow-on slices:** the `#[cancel_unsafe_until(...)]` cancel-safety annotation ŌĆö `BufWriter` carries a notional "unflushed bytes" bit (same shape as `File`'s unflushed-writes bit, phase-8 line 238) that is NOT-CancelSafe across a yield; annotating `write` (soils) + `flush` (clears) plugs into the type-agnostic slice-3a walker ([`phase-6-runtime.md` line 155](phase-6-runtime.md)), deferred for the same reason as BufReader's (the interpreter MVP doesn't consume the attribute, so deferral is behavior-neutral); a `write_all` convenience method (short-write looping ŌĆö low demand at v1, `write` + the buffer absorbs most of the benefit); `BufWriter` over non-`File` `Write` sinks (Stdout, network streams ŌĆö waits on the effect-polymorphic trait surface, P1). **Cross-references:** peer of `BufReader[R]` (line 272); depends on `File` (line 261). **Deferred work carved into the three standalone `[ ]` sub-items below ŌĆö do not re-derive from this prose.**
  - [x] **`BufWriter` cancel-safety annotation (`#[cancel_unsafe_until]`). Ō£ō Shipped 2026-06-06.** `BufWriter` carries a notional "unflushed bytes" bit (same shape as `File`'s unflushed-writes bit, phase-8 line 238) that is NOT-CancelSafe across a yield: `write` soils the buffer, `flush` clears it. `BufWriter.write` now carries `#[cancel_unsafe_until(method = "flush")]` in `runtime/stdlib/bufwriter.kara` (after `#[compiler_builtin]`, exactly mirroring `File.write` in `io.kara`), so the type-agnostic slice-3a flow-walker (`src/raii_check.rs`, phase-6 line 155 slice 3a) rejects a yield while a `BufWriter` binding holds an unflushed write. **No walker changes** ŌĆö the walker reaches the annotation automatically via `STDLIB_PROGRAMS` (bufwriter.kara is in `STDLIB_SOURCES`). **Generic-type finding:** the walker resolves a generic `bw: BufWriter[File]` param to the bare `BufWriter` annotation key (`pattern_binding_types` strips generics), confirming generic stdlib types participate ŌĆö de-risks the BufReader tail of slice 3b. **Tests:** 3 in `tests/raii_check.rs` under a new `Phase 6 line 155 slice 3b ŌĆö BufWriter[W] cancel-safety` section (`bufwriter_write_then_yield_rejected` pins `soiling_method == "write"` / `clear_method_name == "flush"` / `type_name == "BufWriter"`; `bufwriter_write_then_flush_then_yield_accepted`; `bufwriter_param_without_write_held_across_yield_accepted`). fmt + clippy (`--all-targets --features llvm`) clean; full `cargo test` + `cargo test --features llvm` green. **Closes** [`phase-6-runtime.md` line 189 slice 3b](phase-6-runtime.md): the BufWriter half is this annotation; the **BufReader half was decided to be a no-op at v1** (2026-06-06) ŌĆö read-ahead loss isn't a silent correctness violation and there's no clean `flush`-equivalent clear method, so annotating it would mis-seed the walker. Full rationale in the slice 3b entry. With the writer annotated and the reader consciously unannotated, slice 3b is closed.
  - [x] **`BufWriter.write_all(buf: Slice[u8]) -> Result[Unit, IoError]`. Ō£ō Shipped 2026-06-06.** Convenience method that loops `write` until the whole buffer is accepted (or a real error), returning `Unit` instead of a byte count ŌĆö mirrors Rust's `Write::write_all`, and the ergonomic call most user code actually wants. **Implementation:** baked signature + `#[compiler_builtin]` stub in `runtime/stdlib/bufwriter.kara` (carries `#[cancel_unsafe_until(method = "flush")]` too ŌĆö `write_all` leaves bytes buffered exactly like `write`, so it soils for slice-3b cancel-safety); folded into the existing `"write" | "write_all"` arm of `try_eval_bufwriter_method` (`src/interpreter/method_call_bufwriter.rs`) calling `std::io::Write::write_all` and returning `io_ok(Value::Unit)`; `writes(FileSystem)` effect seed added in `src/effectchecker.rs`; typechecker resolves via the normal baked-impl path. **Tests:** 1 typechecker (`test_bufwriter_write_all_returns_result_unit`) + 1 interpreter (`test_bufwriter_write_all_writes_whole_buffer` ŌĆö write_all ŌåÆ flush ŌåÆ read-back) + 1 raii_check (`bufwriter_write_all_then_yield_rejected` ŌĆö pins write_all soils with clear=flush). fmt + clippy (`--all-targets --features llvm`) clean; full `cargo test` + `cargo test --features llvm` green. **Deferred:** a peer `BufReader.read_exact` for symmetry (no demand surfaced yet; carve when one does).
  - [ ] **`BufWriter[W]` over non-`File` `Write` sinks (Stdout, network streams).** Carved from the BufWriter MVP's deferred list (2026-06-06). The v1 MVP hardcodes `W = File` (the constructor matches `Value::File` and the effect is the concrete `writes(FileSystem)`). Generalizing to other writers (e.g. `Stdout`, `TcpStream`) requires the effect-polymorphic trait surface so the wrapped writer's own effect set flows through `write`/`flush` instead of the hardcoded `writes(FileSystem)` ŌĆö gated on the P1 effect-polymorphic-traits work ([`phase-3-effect-checker.md`](phase-3-effect-checker.md)). Same gate as the `BufReader` non-`File` generalization noted in the line-272 entry. Not actionable until that P1 surface lands; tracked here so it isn't lost.

- [x] **`Channel[T]` / `Sender[T]` / `Receiver[T]` core stdlib types.** `Value::Sender(Arc<Mutex<VecDeque<Value>>>)` and `Value::Receiver(Arc<Mutex<VecDeque<Value>>>)` added; `Channel.new()` wired in path-call dispatch ŌĆö creates one `Arc<Mutex<VecDeque>>`, wraps it in a `(Sender, Receiver)` tuple so both ends share the same queue. - [x] **`Slice[T]` stdlib methods.** Core type and coercion ship in Phase 4; the full method surface lands here. Mirror the `Vec[T]` read-only / in-place surface where the operation makes sense on a borrowed view: `len`, `is_empty`, `first`, `last`, `get(i) -> Option[ref T]`, `iter()`, `chunks(n)`, `windows(n)`, `split_at(i) -> (Slice[T], Slice[T])`, `contains(ref T) where T: Eq`, `binary_search(ref T) where T: Ord`. Mutable-only: `sort() where T: Ord`, `sort_by(cmp)`, `reverse()`, `fill(val) where T: Clone`, `iter_mut()`, `swap(i, j)`. No `push`/`pop`/`remove` ŌĆö those require capacity management and belong on `Vec[T]`. Document each method's effect set (most are effect-free; `sort` may `allocates(Heap)` for auxiliary buffers).

- [x] **Interpreter: `sort_by` / `sorted_by` closure-honoring (silent wrong-answer fix).** Ō£ō Landed 2026-05-11. Sub-item against the `Slice[T] stdlib methods` entry above. The interpreter arms at `src/interpreter.rs` (`sort_by` ~6940, `sorted_by` ~6965) accepted a closure comparator from the typechecker but discarded it, dispatching `sort_by(value_compare)` (natural value ordering) instead ŌĆö a silent wrong-answer footgun (`xs.sort_by(|a, b| key(a).cmp(key(b)))` typechecked, ran without diagnostic, returned the input order). Surfaced 2026-05-11 by kata-katas LeetCode #1665 (`greedy.kara`) where the natural greedy idiom requires a derived key. Fix: evaluate the closure expr ŌåÆ `Value::Function`, snapshot the Vec via `rc.read().unwrap().clone()` (releases the read guard immediately), sort the snapshot via a comparator that calls `invoke_value_comparator` for each pair, replace via `try_write_or_panic(rc, ...)`. New helper `invoke_value_comparator` at `interpreter.rs:5700` translates the user closure's returned `Ordering` enum variant (`Less` / `Equal` / `Greater`) to `std::cmp::Ordering`, panicking with a clear message on shape errors. Three call sites updated uniformly (`sort_by` on Vec/Array, `sorted_by` on Vec/Array, `sorted_by` on String chars).

  *Settled design forks (2026-05-11).*

  - **F1 ŌĆö "re-entrancy unsupported" was misframed.** The original source-comment claimed closure invocation required interpreter re-entrancy infrastructure that didn't exist. Investigation showed `invoke_function_value` at `interpreter.rs:5669` already provides exactly the needed surface. The actual constraint was `std::sync::RwLock` being non-reentrant on the same thread ŌĆö if the user closure body re-accesses the same array, a held write guard deadlocks. Fix is snapshot-sort-replace: clone the Vec briefly under a read guard (released at end-of-statement), sort on the local copy (no lock held), then install via a brief write guard.
  - **F2 ŌĆö Sort_by and sorted_by in the same slice, both String and Vec paths.** All three reachable call sites share the closure-honoring + Ordering-translation pattern. Splitting would leave inconsistent half-fixed surface and require duplicate test coverage. The fix shape is identical apart from the `Value::Char(c)` wrapping needed for String chars vs. raw `Value` for Vec elements.
  - **F3 ŌĆö Skip the interim hard-error.** The original staging entry floated a small interim slice that converts the silent wrong-answer to a typed runtime error while the real fix designs. Since the real fix landed in the same session (~40 LoC mechanical), the interim would have been pure churn ŌĆö every existing `sort_by(closure)` user broken once when the interim lands, again when it gets reverted.

  *Out of scope (deferred to follow-ups in [`wip-staging.md`](wip-staging.md)).*

  - **Typechecker shape validation of `Fn(T, T) -> Ordering` closure args.** Ō£ō Landed 2026-05-11 ŌĆö see the dedicated entry below. The original framing called the gap mechanical (~30 LoC). Real shape was ~80 LoC: a new `check_sort_comparator` helper, push-down via `check_expr` against `Type::Function { params: [elem, elem], return_type: Ordering }`, integration into the existing Slice and String arms, and a new Vec intercept ahead of the generic fallthrough (Vec has no stdlib impl block, so previously the closure flowed through unchecked).
  - **`sort_by_key` on Slice/Vec.** Ō£ō Landed 2026-05-11 ŌĆö see the dedicated entry below. Closed alongside `sorted_by_key` since the sort/sorted pair always ships together; the LeetCode #1665 idiom `xs.sort_by_key(|t| -(t.1 - t.0))` is now the canonical K─üra form.
  - **Interpreter primitive comparison gap.** Closure bodies like `b.cmp(a)` for `Vec[i64]` or `a > b` for chars panic at the comparator's first call: the typechecker recognizes `i64.cmp` via the builtin Ord impl, but the interpreter's method-call dispatch doesn't know how to invoke it on primitive values. Same shape for char `<` / `>` / `==`. Blocks the canonical descending-sort idiom; staging entry tracks. The closure-honoring path itself is correct ŌĆö the gap is one layer downstream, in primitive method dispatch.
  - **Slice/Vec parity for `sorted` / `sorted_by` in the typechecker.** `Vec.sorted_by` typechecks today via a fallthrough path even though there's no explicit `sorted_by` arm in `infer_slice_method` / Vec method dispatch; this fix relied on that fallthrough working. A clean typechecker surface would add the missing arms explicitly. Not blocking ŌĆö covered by the typechecker-shape-validation follow-up above.

- [x] **Typechecker: `Fn(T, T) -> Ordering` shape validation for `sort_by` / `sorted_by`.** Ō£ō Landed 2026-05-11. Sub-item against the `Slice[T] stdlib methods` entry. Pre-fix the slice / String `sort_by` / `sorted_by` arms called `infer_expr(&arg.value)` on the comparator without verifying its shape; Vec had no dispatcher at all and fell through to the silent-no-method path that synth-types the closure with fresh metavars (no pushdown into the closure's params, no check on the body's return type). With the interpreter's closure-honoring path live (sibling entry above) plus the primitive-Ord dispatch live (`phase-4-interpreter.md`), a wrong-shape comparator (`xs.sort_by(|a| a)`, `xs.sort_by(|a, b| a < b)`) would typecheck and then runtime-panic when the interpreter pulled an `Ordering` variant out of the closure's bool / arity-1 return. Now: any wrong-shape comparator produces a typecheck TypeMismatch at the closure expression. Fix:

  - New helper `check_sort_comparator(elem, arg, method, span)` in `src/typechecker.rs` builds the expected `Type::Function { params: [elem, elem], return_type: Type::Named("Ordering", []) }` and calls `check_expr(&arg.value, &expected)` ŌĆö the check-mode closure-pushdown machinery (`src/typechecker.rs:8340`-area) handles per-parameter type assignment and body validation against `Ordering`. Arity mismatch is caught by the same path; non-closure `Fn` values flow through normal `check_assignable`.
  - `infer_str_method` `sorted_by` arm: arg count gate before the helper; on miscount, infer args and skip the helper.
  - `infer_slice_method` `sort_by` arm: arg count gate added (was missing), mutability gate unchanged, helper called on the lone closure arg.
  - New Vec intercept in `infer_method_call` (before the strip-outer-ref dispatcher) for `sort_by` / `sorted_by` when the receiver is `Vec[T]` / `ref Vec[T]` / `mut ref Vec[T]`. Returns `Type::Unit` for `sort_by` (in-place mutation) and `Type::Named { name: "Vec", args: [elem] }` for `sorted_by` (new collection).

  *Settled design forks (2026-05-11).*

  - **F1 ŌĆö Single helper, three call sites.** The cleanest alternative was to fold `sort_by` / `sorted_by` into a generic `infer_call`-style flow that gets pushdown for free. Rejected because Slice / String are special-cased today and the surrounding arms wouldn't benefit; threading them all through generic dispatch would be a much larger refactor (every fall-through dispatcher today is a hand-coded match). The narrow helper integrates with each existing arm at one line.

  - **F2 ŌĆö `check_expr`, not `infer_expr` + post-hoc check.** `check_expr` pushes the expected `Fn(elem, elem) -> Ordering` down into closure parameters and validates the body's return type against `Ordering` in one pass. The runner-up was `infer_expr` followed by manual `check_assignable` on the inferred type ŌĆö but that requires the closure to come in fully typed (or the typechecker to bind metavars after the fact), which loses the pushdown property: `xs.sort_by(|a, b| a.cmp(b))` should be accepted with `a` / `b` typed as the element type, not left as fresh metavars.

  - **F3 ŌĆö Vec dispatch intercept lives in `infer_method_call`, not a new `infer_vec_method`.** A full `infer_vec_method` (peer to `infer_slice_method` / `infer_str_method`) would have to shadow every Vec method that today falls through to the impl-block lookup correctly (`push` / `pop` / `clone` / `iter` / etc.). The narrow intercept fires only for `sort_by` / `sorted_by` and leaves the rest of Vec's method surface on its existing path. Future entry: a slice that promotes Vec dispatch wholesale to `infer_vec_method` for symmetry with Slice / String, when there's a second reason to add a Vec-specific arm.

  *Out of scope.*

  - **Receiver-mutability check on Vec.sort_by.** `Slice.sort_by` requires `mut Slice[T]`; Vec mutability lives at the binding level (`let mut xs: Vec[i64]`) and the binding-mutability check fires at the call site outside this dispatcher. Not duplicated in the Vec intercept.
  - **`sort` / `reverse` arg-count tightening on Vec.** Today Vec has no explicit arm for these either; they fall through to the silent path. Out of scope for this slice ŌĆö Slice has the explicit arms (`infer_slice_method` "sort" | "reverse"), Vec relies on fall-through with the implicit zero-arg expectation. Closes when Vec moves to its own dispatcher.
  - **`sort_by_key` shape validation.** Lands together with the `sort_by_key` surface; tracked in the sibling staging entry.

  Test coverage in `tests/typechecker.rs`: `test_string_sorted_by_returns_string` (positive ŌĆö `Fn(char, char) -> Ordering`), `test_string_sorted_by_rejects_bool_returning_comparator` (negative pin for the original silent-pass case), `test_vec_sort_by_rejects_wrong_arity_closure` (1-param closure rejected), `test_vec_sort_by_rejects_wrong_return_type` (`Fn(i64, i64) -> bool` rejected), `test_vec_sort_by_accepts_ordering_returning_comparator` (positive ŌĆö `|a, b| a.cmp(b)`). Full `cargo test` + `cargo test --features llvm` green; zero regressions.

- [x] **`sort_by_key` / `sorted_by_key` on `Slice[T]` / `Vec[T]`.** Ō£ō Landed 2026-05-11. Sibling to the typechecker shape-validation entry above and the prior closure-honoring slice. Surfaced 2026-05-11 by LeetCode #1665 ŌĆö the natural greedy idiom is `sort_by_key(|t| -(t.1 - t.0))`, which needs a key function `Fn(T) -> K` where `K: Ord`, not the `Fn(T, T) -> Ordering` shape that `sort_by` accepts. Without `sort_by_key` the workaround was either (a) hand-roll a comparator that recomputes both keys on every comparison, or (b) in-source insertion sort (the kata's actual fallback). Now: idiomatic single-pass key sort works through `karac run` and the interpreter precomputes keys exactly once per element (matches Rust's `slice::sort_by_key` performance contract).

  Implementation:

  - **Interpreter** (`src/interpreter.rs`): new `sort_by_key` and `sorted_by_key` arms in `eval_method_call` peer to the existing `sort_by` / `sorted_by` arms. Each arm evaluates the key closure to a `Value::Function`, snapshots the array, computes `(key, value)` pairs by invoking the closure once per element via `invoke_function_value`, sorts the pairs by `value_compare(k1, k2)`, then writes the values back (`sort_by_key`) or returns a new Vec (`sorted_by_key`). The precompute-keys-once shape avoids the O(n log n) closure invocation cost of routing through `sort_by` with a comparator that calls the key fn twice per compare.
  - **Typechecker** (`src/typechecker.rs`): new helper `check_sort_key_closure(elem, arg, method, span)` pushes `Fn(elem) -> TypeParam("__sort_by_key_K")` down through `check_expr`, reads the resolved body type out of the returned `Type::Function` shape (mirrors `Iterator.map`'s pushdown pattern at `infer_iterator_method`), and verifies the body type satisfies `Ord` via `type_supports_ord`. Wired into `infer_slice_method` (new `sort_by_key` arm with the mutability check) and into the Vec intercept at `infer_method_call` (the existing intercept widened to recognize `sort_by_key` / `sorted_by_key` alongside `sort_by` / `sorted_by`). Method-name allow-list in the `_` fallthrough also grew `sort_by_key` for typo-suggestion completeness.

  *Settled design forks (2026-05-11).*

  - **F1 ŌĆö Typechecker-recognized name, not stdlib decl.** `sort_by` is typechecker-recognized today (the slice / String arms hand-code the method); `sort_by_key` lands symmetric. Promoting all sort-family methods to stdlib decls is its own future slice; sticking with the existing pattern keeps the diff narrow and consistent.
  - **F2 ŌĆö `sorted_by_key` peer in the same slice.** The `sort` / `sorted` pair is already consistent across Vec, String, and (via the new entry) Slice. Splitting `sort_by_key` and `sorted_by_key` would leave inconsistent surface and require duplicate test coverage. Both arms share the precompute-keys-once shape.
  - **F3 ŌĆö `K: Ord` strict, not `K: PartialOrd`.** Matches Rust's `slice::sort_by_key`. Raw floats deliberately fail the Ord check (IEEE NaN breaks the trait, matching how the typechecker excludes raw `Float` from `register_builtin_impl("Ord", ...)`). Users wanting float sort use the `TotalFloat32` / `TotalFloat64` wrappers, same constraint as `sort`.
  - **F4 ŌĆö `TypeParam` placeholder, not `TypeVar`, for return-type pushdown.** `types_compatible` treats `Type::TypeParam(_)` as permissively compatible with concrete types (line 2198 in typechecker), but `Type::TypeVar(_)` triggers a strict-equality compare. Pushing `Fn(T) -> TypeVar(K)` would emit a spurious "expected '?T0', found 'i64'" diagnostic when the closure body resolves to a concrete type. The TypeParam pattern is the same one `infer_iterator_method`'s `map` arm uses ŌĆö read the resolved body type out of the returned `Type::Function` shape after `check_expr`. The `_var`-named-but-actually-`TypeParam` workaround documented in the helper.

  *Out of scope.*

  - **String chars `sort_by_key`.** `String.sorted_by_key(|c| ...)` would be a natural peer to `String.sorted_by`, but it's not part of the kata's idiom and adding it now would mean another String arm + chars-to-Vec extraction. Tracks as a follow-up if String chars iteration grows.
  - **`max_by_key` / `min_by_key`.** The dual surface (find the element with extremal key) is natural to ship together with `sort_by_key`, but each lives on `Iterator`, not on `Vec` / `Slice`, and the existing `Iterator` adaptor surface is closed-out. Separate slice when the natural idiom emerges.
  - **`sort_unstable_by_key` perf variant.** Rust ships `sort_unstable` / `sort_unstable_by` / `sort_unstable_by_key` for slightly faster sorting at the cost of stability. The interpreter's tree-walk sort uses `Vec::sort_by` which is stable; the unstable variant ships when codegen sort dispatch is on the table.

  Test coverage. Typechecker (`tests/typechecker.rs`): `test_vec_sort_by_key_accepts_integer_key` (`|x| x`), `test_vec_sort_by_key_accepts_negated_key` (the LeetCode idiom `|x| -x`), `test_vec_sort_by_key_rejects_wrong_arity_closure` (2-param closure rejected), `test_vec_sorted_by_key_returns_vec` (return-type pin). Interpreter (`tests/interpreter.rs`): `test_vec_sort_by_key_ascending`, `test_vec_sort_by_key_descending_via_negation`, `test_vec_sorted_by_key_returns_new`. Full `cargo test` + `cargo test --features llvm` green; zero regressions.

- [x] **`Range` / `RangeInclusive` implements `Iterator`.** Landed 2026-05-09 (commit `c18fbec`). Sibling to the closed adaptor-surface entry below (commit `6d23f94`). Range / RangeInclusive route through the existing Iterator dispatch surface so `(0..10).step_by(2).collect()`, `(1..=10).map(f).filter(p).collect()`, `(0..n).take(k)` etc. work directly through `karac run` without a redundant `.iter()`; the for-loop iterable path is preserved through `Value::Iterator` drain. Typechecker + interpreter only ŌĆö codegen iterator chains remain a broader gap. 6 interpreter + 2 typechecker tests.

- [x] **`Slice[T]` implements `Iterator` ŌĆö `.iter()` method.** Landed 2026-05-09 (commit `cf4a846`). Sibling to the Range / RangeInclusive Iterator entry above (`c18fbec`). `Slice[T]` routes `iter` / `into_iter` through the existing Iterator dispatch surface so chained adaptors (`s.iter().map(f).filter(p).collect()`) compose; the for-loop iterable path already drained `Value::Slice` directly. Typechecker `infer_slice_method` only ŌĆö interpreter pre-existed (sliceŌåÆarray normalization at the method-dispatch fence routes through the shared `iter`/`into_iter` arm). Codegen iterator chains remain a broader gap. 6 interpreter + 2 typechecker tests.

- [x] **Iterator trait ŌĆö full adaptor surface.** Beyond the named-in-roadmap adaptors (`filter`, `map`, `collect`, `fold`, `any`, `all`), ship the long-tail combinators that real iterator code depends on: `chain`, `zip`, `enumerate`, `take(n)`, `skip(n)`, `take_while(pred)`, `skip_while(pred)`, `flat_map(f)`, `peekable`, `chunk_by(key_fn)`, `step_by(n)`, `cycle`, `inspect(f)`, `scan(state, f)`, `windows(n)`, `chunks(n)`. Each is a 5ŌĆō20 line implementation once `Iterator` is in place. Real programs use the long tail; absence forces hand-roll.
