Most are effect-free; ones that buffer (`chunk_by`, `windows`) may `allocates(Heap)`. Closed 2026-05-04. Final commit `6d23f94` (`chunks(n)` / `windows(n)` on Iterator). Shipped surface: terminals `next`, `count`, `collect`, `fold`, `any`, `all`; step-layer adaptors `map`, `filter`, `enumerate`, `take(n)`, `skip(n)`, `take_while(pred)`, `skip_while(pred)`, `step_by(n)`, `inspect(f)`, `scan(init, f)`; source-layer adaptors `iter` / `into_iter` (Eager), `chain(other)`, `zip(other)`, `flat_map(f)`, `cycle()`, `peekable()`, `chunk_by(key_fn)`, `chunks(n)`, `windows(n)`; plus `peek()` exclusive to the `Peekable[T]` named type returned by `peekable()`. Heap-allocating adaptors with `allocates(Heap)` seeded in the effectchecker: `Iterator.chunk_by`, `Iterator.chunks`, `Iterator.windows` (and route via `STDLIB_METHOD_MAP` so `Vec.chunks` / `Vec.windows` callers also pick up the effect, closing a pre-existing under-report). Test coverage: **227** dedicated iterator tests ŌĆö 133 interpreter, 91 typechecker, 3 effectchecker. Implementation rides `Value::Iterator { source: IteratorSource, steps: Vec<IteratorStep> }` with 9 source variants (`Eager`, `Chain`, `Zip`, `FlatMap`, `Cycle`, `Peekable`, `ChunkBy`, `Chunks`, `Windows`) and 10 step variants (`Map`, `Filter`, `Enumerate`, `Take`, `Skip`, `TakeWhile`, `SkipWhile`, `StepBy`, `Inspect`, `Scan`). Notable design choices documented inline at the variant doc-comments: `Peekable[T]` is a distinct named type that loses peek-capability after any adaptor (matching Rust's `Map<Peekable<I>>`); `scan` deviates from Rust's `Fn(&mut St, T) -> Option<B>` to `Fn(A, T) -> Option<(A, U)>` because tree-walk closures snapshot captures and there's no `mut ref` parameter mode; multi-source / lookahead adaptors (`chunk_by`, `chunks`, `windows`, `flat_map`, `peekable`, `cycle`) are sources rather than steps because they break the 1:1 source-pull ŌåÆ output-item assumption that Steps make.

- [x] **`std.encoding` ŌĆö base64, hex, URL encode/decode.** Closed 2026-05-03. Interpreter-only namespace under `Base64.*` / `Hex.*` / `Url.*` (mirrors the `Stats` / `Regex` precedent ŌĆö typechecker registers each function name in `env.functions`, interpreter dispatches on the path string). Functions: `Base64.encode(bytes: Slice[u8]) -> String` (standard alphabet, `=`-padded), `Base64.encode_url_safe(bytes: Slice[u8]) -> String` (URL-safe alphabet, no padding), `Base64.decode(s: String) -> Result[Vec[u8], DecodeError]` (accepts both alphabets, ignores ASCII whitespace), `Hex.encode(bytes: Slice[u8]) -> String` (lowercase), `Hex.encode_upper(bytes: Slice[u8]) -> String`, `Hex.decode(s: String) -> Result[Vec[u8], DecodeError]` (case-insensitive, even-length only), `Url.encode(s: String) -> String` (RFC 3986 percent-encoding ŌĆö preserves the unreserved set `A-Za-z0-9-._~`, percent-encodes everything else), `Url.decode(s: String) -> Result[String, DecodeError]`. The original spec called for "standard + URL-safe via flag" / "lowercase + uppercase via flag" ŌĆö K─üra has no default-arg or boolean-flag-arg idiom in its stdlib (Stats, Regex use the separate-function form); the implementation mirrors the precedent. New `DecodeError { message: String }` struct registered in the typechecker (parallels `RegexError`); decode failures populate the message. New types added to `PRELUDE_TYPES`: `Base64`, `Hex`, `Url`, `DecodeError`. 22 new tests (8 typechecker ŌĆö signature shape per function ŌĆö + 14 interpreter ŌĆö RFC 4648 base64 vectors with 1/2/3-byte padding + URL-safe alphabet + base64 round-trip + invalid-char rejection / hex lower & upper + mixed-case decode + odd-length rejection / URL preserves unreserved set + percent-encode + round-trip + invalid percent-encoding rejection). No codegen support today (parallels `Regex`); compiled-binary support is a follow-up if/when needed. Files: `src/prelude.rs`, `src/typechecker.rs`, `src/interpreter.rs`, `tests/typechecker.rs`, `tests/interpreter.rs`.

- [x] **Lexer: reserve `expr_<NNNN>` fragment-specifier identifier namespace.** Closed 2026-05-04 in commit `1559772`. The check lives in `src/lexer.rs` `identifier()`'s fallthrough arm via the `is_reserved_fragment_specifier_namespace` helper (manual byte-class check; no regex on the hot path). Raw-escape exemption is structural ŌĆö `r#expr_2026` flows through `raw_identifier()`, which never enters the keyword match path, so no `was_raw_escaped` flag is needed at the token level. 7 tests in `tests/lexer.rs` cover boundary years (2020 / 2026 / 2099) at let / fn / struct-field positions, both fix-its in the diagnostic, the raw-escape exemption, and every accept-path negative case (no prefix, different prefix, non-year suffix, year out of range on both sides, wrong digit count). Original spec preserved below for the historical record. Spec at `design.md ┬¦ Reserved Fragment-Specifier Identifier Namespace` (v60 item 62). Slices: (1) **Lexer regex check.** In `src/lexer.rs`, after recognising an identifier token, run a pattern check against `^expr_(\d{4})$`. If the regex matches AND the captured digit string parses as a year in the range `2020`..=`2099` inclusive, emit `error[E_RESERVED_FRAGMENT_SPECIFIER_NAMESPACE]: 'expr_<NNNN>' is a reserved identifier name; this naming convention is reserved for future edition-versionable syntax categories in macros / comptime fragment specifiers ŌĆö use 'r#expr_<NNNN>' if you need this exact identifier today, or rename to a non-year-suffixed form` with the offending span underlined and the two fix-its (the raw-identifier escape OR a rename suggestion). (2) **Raw-identifier exemption.** When the identifier is preceded by `r#` (raw-identifier escape per item 39), the reservation does NOT fire ŌĆö `r#expr_2026` parses as the bare identifier `expr_2026` and is accepted. The exemption falls out of the existing raw-identifier handling: the regex is checked AFTER the raw-prefix has been stripped, so `r#expr_2026` strips to `expr_2026` for downstream consumers but the reservation is checked against the *original lexed form* before stripping. Implementation detail: track a `was_raw_escaped` flag on the identifier token; if true, skip the namespace check. (3) **Narrow scope at v1.** The reservation matches ONLY the `expr_` prefix. Other plausible fragment-specifier prefixes (`pat`, `ty`, `stmt`, `block`, `tt`, `ident`, `lit`, `path`, `vis`, `meta`, `item`, `lifetime`) are NOT reserved at v1 ŌĆö extending the reservation post-v1 to additional prefixes is non-breaking-additive (existing user identifiers using those prefixes continue to work). (4) **Year range.** `2020`..=`2099` inclusive. Years outside this range (e.g., `expr_1999`, `expr_3000`) parse as ordinary identifiers without rejection. The range matches the realistic edition-year window for any K─üra release. (5) **Diagnostic shape.** Span underlines the full identifier including the year suffix. Help line offers the raw-escape fix-it (`r#expr_2026`) and the rename fix-it (`expression_2026` or similar). (6) **No connection to literal year value.** The reservation is purely a namespace allocation, not tied to a specific year value. `expr_2026` is reserved today even though K─üra's current edition is `2026`; `expr_2099` is reserved even though no compiler will see it for decades. (7) **Test coverage.** Positive ŌĆö `let x = 1;` (no prefix) accepts; `let expression = 1;` accepts; `let expr_v2 = 1;` accepts (non-year suffix); `let version_2026 = 1;` accepts (different prefix); `let expr_1999 = 1;` accepts (year out of reserved range); `let expr_3000 = 1;` accepts (year out of reserved range); `let r#expr_2026 = 1;` accepts (raw-escape exemption); function declaration `fn expr_v2() { }` accepts. Negative ŌĆö `let expr_2020 = 1;` rejected with `E_RESERVED_FRAGMENT_SPECIFIER_NAMESPACE`; `let expr_2026 = 1;` rejected; `let expr_2099 = 1;` rejected; function declaration `fn expr_2026() { }` rejected at function-name lex; struct field `struct S { expr_2030: i64 }` rejected at field-name lex; the diagnostic includes both fix-its inline. Phase target: 1 (Lexer) ŌĆö small lex-time check; reuses the existing identifier tokenisation path. No P1 carve-out ŌĆö the reservation ships at v1 to lock in the namespace before users can rely on it.

- [x] **Per-stdlib-type variance declarations + verifier + user-side rejection.** Spec at `design.md ┬¦ Variance` (v60 item 57). Three layers: a parser/AST surface for `+T` / `-T` / `=T` markers, a stdlib-side verifier that proves the markers consistent with the type's structure, and a user-side rejection diagnostic that reserves the syntax for v1. The covariant types (`Option`, `Result`, `Iterator`, `TaskHandle`, `AlreadySetError`) are the load-bearing payoff ŌĆö they unlock subtyping that today's all-invariant rule blocks. **Shipped 2026-06-07.** Implementation home: `src/typechecker/variance.rs` (rejection + verifier + lint), `prelude::STDLIB_VARIANCE` (per-type variance table), `types.rs::types_compatible`/`is_subtype` (use-site rule).

  1. [x] **Lexer.** `+`, `-`, `=` already lex as symbols; no new token kinds. Verified ŌĆö no lexer change shipped.
  2. [x] **Parser + AST.** `parse_generic_params` accepts an optional leading `+`/`-`/`=` before the parameter identifier; the marker attaches to the parameter, not the bound (`+T: Ord` is `(+ T) (: Ord)`). AST: `GenericParam` gained `variance: Variance { Covariant, Contravariant, Invariant }` plus `variance_span: Option<Span>` ŌĆö the span is `Some` only for an explicit marker, which is how the stdlib lint distinguishes explicit `=T` from the implicit default and how diagnostics underline the marker itself. Markers on const / shape-variadic / effect params (both the `with E` and `E: Effect` spellings) get a focused parse rejection. Formatter round-trips all three markers, including explicit `=`.
  3. [x] **User-side rejection at v1.** Implemented in the **typechecker decl pass, not the resolver** ŌĆö the `stdlib_origin` flag (CR-202) lives on the AST items the typechecker walks, and the `error[E_..._NOT_YET]`-style reservation diagnostics already live there (`E_TRAIT_ALIAS_NOT_IMPLEMENTED_YET` precedent). Non-stdlib struct/enum decls plus fn / trait / impl / type-alias generic params (regardless of origin ŌĆö markers are a nominal-type-decl property) reject `+`/`-` with `error[E_VARIANCE_USER_DECL_NOT_YET]: variance declarations are reserved for stdlib types in v1; remove the marker ŌĆö the parameter will be invariant`. Explicit `=T` is accepted everywhere (identical to the default). Stdlib identification = the existing `stdlib_origin` flag flipped by the prelude baker, not a package-name/attribute scheme.
  4. [x] **Variance verifier ŌĆö stdlib-side enforcement.** `src/typechecker/variance.rs::stdlib_variance_decl_errors` runs at type-decl time (via `check_struct_variance` / `check_enum_variance` in `check_items`, covering gated-module splices) and as a baked-stdlib hygiene test (`baked_stdlib_variance_declarations_are_explicit_and_consistent` ŌĆö the stdlib is baked into the binary, so `cargo test` IS the stdlib build step). Walks the type's **data structure** ŌĆö fields (`mut` ŌćÆ invariant base polarity), variant payloads (covariant), `ref`/`mut ref`/`weak`/`mut Slice` targets, fn-type args (flip) and returns, nested named types composing each slot's declared variance via the standard variance transform. **Deliberate narrowing vs the spec text: method signatures do NOT constrain a type's variance** ŌĆö a widening coercion re-types the whole value and method calls resolve at the widened type, so only stored data can witness the old parameter (counting methods would falsely flunk `Option[+T]` on `unwrap_or(self, default: T)`). Failure emits `E_VARIANCE_DECLARATION_INCONSISTENT` naming param/marker/position with the fix-it suggesting `=T`.
  5. [x] **Position-based variance pass ŌĆö verified, three real gaps found and FIXED.** The pre-existing layer was *not* compliant: (a) `mut ref T` was **covariant** in both `types_compatible` and `is_subtype` (incl. the ownedŌåÆmut-ref call-boundary coercion), letting owned `Positive` flow into a `mut ref i64` slot ŌĆö the callee could write a refinement-violating value back; now invariant per the soundness pin. (b) Function-type arguments in `types_compatible` were checked **covariantly** (accepting the unsound direction, rejecting the sound one); now contravariant, matching the `is_subtype` arm which was already correct. (c) `Rc`/`Arc`/`Array`/`Slice` (both mutabilities, incl. all `Vec`/`Array`ŌåÆ`Slice` coercion arms) and `*mut T` recursed covariantly; now invariant per the audit table. Invariance is implemented as *mutual* compatibility, so symmetric permissive arms (TypeParam wildcards, integer-width compat, Never/Error) keep working during inference.
  6. [x] **Stdlib audit ŌĆö applied.** All 21 parametric types in `runtime/stdlib/*.kara` marked: `Option[+T]`, `Result[+T, +E]`, `TaskHandle[+T]` covariant; `Vec`/`Map`/`Set`/`VecDeque`/`SortedSet`/`Atomic`/`Mutex`/`Channel`/`BoundedChannel`/`Sender`/`Receiver`/`Entry`/`Peekable`/`Pool`/`PooledConnection`/`BufReader`/`BufWriter`/`Tensor` explicit `=`. `Iterator[+T]` and `Array[=T]` have **no syntactic declaration surface** (compiler-intrinsic pseudo-structs; the `Iterator` *trait* is non-parametric) ŌĆö they are hardcoded entries in `prelude::STDLIB_VARIANCE`. `Box`/`RwLock`/`LazyLock`/`OnceLock`/`OnceCell`/`MaybeUninit`/`PhantomData`/`AlreadySetError` do not exist in stdlib yet ŌĆö when each ships, the explicit-marker lint forces a declaration and the design.md audit table says which (`AlreadySetError[+T]`, rest `=`). `Slice` is structural (`Type::Slice`), handled in slice 5's arm fixes.
  7. [x] **Stdlib lint.** `error[E_STDLIB_VARIANCE_IMPLICIT]` ŌĆö every type param of a parametric stdlib type must carry an explicit marker (const/variadic-shape exempt); fires in `check_items` for stdlib-origin decls and in the baked hygiene test. A second hygiene test (`baked_stdlib_has_no_markers_outside_type_decls`) keeps markers off stdlib fn/trait/impl/alias params. User code unaffected.
  8. [x] **Subtyping rule ŌĆö at use sites.** `types_compatible`'s Named-type arm consults `prelude::STDLIB_VARIANCE` per slot: `+T` ŌåÆ directional (refinement-to-base widening allowed), `-T` ŌåÆ flipped, `=T`/absent ŌåÆ mutual. `Iterator[Positive]` widens to `Iterator[i64]`; `Vec[Positive]` does NOT widen to `Vec[i64]` ŌĆö note this **tightens** previous behavior, which recursed covariantly through every generic slot. Known v1 narrowing (documented at the table): the lookup is name-keyed, so a user type shadowing a covariant stdlib name (`Option`, `Result`, `Iterator`, `TaskHandle` ŌĆö resolver allows prelude shadowing) inherits that entry's variance; the fix requires def-site identity on `Type::Named`.
  9. [x] **Test coverage.** Parser: 7 tests (all markers, bound attachment, enum form, const/variadic/effect rejections, formatter round-trip idempotence). Verifier/lint (in `variance.rs`): 9 tests incl. the spec's `struct Cell[+T] { mut field: T }` rejection, fn-arg contravariant rejection, `-T` accept/reject pair, nested-slot composition (`Option[T]` keeps covariance, `Vec[T]` forces invariance), `mut ref`/`weak`/`Atomic` interiors, explicit-`=` unrestricted, lint + exemptions, plus both baked-stdlib hygiene gates. Use-site (tests/typechecker.rs): covariant widening for `Option`/`Result`/`Iterator`/`TaskHandle` (TaskHandle via argument position ŌĆö ScopeLocal forbids return), `Vec`/`Sender` invariance rejections, user-type invariance, owned-`Positive`ŌåÆ`mut ref i64` rejection, `E_VARIANCE_USER_DECL_NOT_YET` across struct/enum/fn/trait/alias, user explicit-`=` accepted.

  **Phase target:** 5.2 (Language Features) ŌĆö parser + AST + variance verifier; the stdlib audit landed in the same CR (the lint makes a split unviable: unmarked stdlib types fail the hygiene gate). No P1 carve-out for the verifier itself ŌĆö option (a) of v60 item 57 ships at v1. The user-side variance declaration surface IS the P1 follow-up; the v1 reservation (focused diagnostic) ensures the surface lands later without source breaks.

- [~] **Stdlib lint ŌĆö `drop_carries_soundness` audit checklist.** Spec at `design.md ┬¦ Drop > Destructors are NOT soundness mechanisms` (v60 item 56 ŌĆö Tier-E pin). **Slices 1 + 3 + 4 shipped 2026-06-07; slice 2 deferred (sub-entry below); slice 5 holds by construction.** What shipped, against the stdlib as it actually exists (the original slice-3 audit list ŌĆö `MutexGuard` / `RwLockReadGuard` / `RwLockWriteGuard` / `RefCellRefGuard` / `RefCellMutGuard` / IRQ-disable guard ŌĆö predates shipped stdlib; **none of those types exist yet**, and per the design pin's own enforcement table the mutex story is `lock { }` block grammar, not a guard type; the audit list refreshes whenever the first real guard type ships):
  - **Slice 3 ŌĆö one-time audit, applied to the real 7-impl set.** Every `impl Drop` in baked + gated stdlib audited: `PooledConnection[T]` (skip ŌćÆ pool slot stranded ŌĆö capacity leak; release idempotent on `conn_id`), `TcpListener` / `TcpStream` / `WebSocket` (skip ŌćÆ fd leak), `TlsListener` (skip ŌćÆ fd + rustls config-allocation leak), `TlsStream` (skip ŌćÆ fd + runtime `SESSIONS`-entry leak) ŌĆö all cleanup-only, no UB. `TaskGroup` is the one type whose Drop runs a soundness-*adjacent* action (the child join): per the design table row 1 the join-before-scope-exit invariant rests on the structural join barrier + `ScopeLocal`, NOT on Drop ŌĆö the Drop impl is the v1 emission vehicle for the barrier, and every v1 Drop-skip path (double-panic, panic=abort, process.exit) terminates the process, so no child can observe a freed frame. A future `forget`-style primitive must not skip the scope-exit join. **The audit surfaced one real gap + two codegen defects:** the structural escape rejection for `TaskGroup` *itself* is unimplemented (only `TaskHandle[T]` carries `ScopeLocal`) ŌĆö tracked at `phase-6-runtime.md ┬¦ TaskGroup escape rejection` (bidirectional); the two codegen defects on escape/capture shapes (TaskGroup-return invalid IR; aggregate-capture spawn ICE at `codegen/task_group.rs:85`) are triaged in `bugs.md` (2026-06-07).
  - **Slice 4 ŌĆö doc-comment line at every impl.** Each of the 7 sites carries a `Drop-skip-sound:` comment block naming what leaks and where soundness derives from.
  - **Slice 1 ŌĆö checklist, realized as a hygiene gate (not a PR template ŌĆö wrong shape for this repo).** `src/prelude.rs::baked_stdlib_drop_impls_are_audited_drop_skip_sound`, mirroring the variance hygiene gate: (a) parse-level ŌĆö every stdlib `impl Drop for X` must have `X` on the audited allowlist, with an exact-set assertion (stale entries prune; an empty scan fails); (b) source-level ŌĆö the contiguous comment block directly above each `impl ŌĆ” Drop for ŌĆ”` must contain the `Drop-skip-sound:` marker. A new stdlib Drop impl fails `cargo test` until the audit question is answered at the impl site and the type appended ŌĆö the reviewer-must-answer discipline, mechanized.
  - [ ] **Slice 2 ŌĆö "Drop-skip soundness" negative-test convention ŌĆö deferred until the first lock-guard-shaped type ships.** No `forget` primitive exists at v1, and for the current fd/connection/pool types the test is vacuous (process exit reclaims fds; there is no aliasing invariant to violate, which is exactly what the slice-3 audit pinned). The convention has teeth the day a type whose Drop releases an *aliasing-relevant* hold lands (`MutexGuard`-shaped guard, `RefCell` guards) ŌĆö at that point the design answer must be grammar/borrow-checker enforcement (per the design table), and the negative test pins it. Original convention spec preserved below.

  Original spec (for the record): (1) **Stdlib code-review checklist.** Add the question to the stdlib PR template (or equivalent). Reviewers explicitly call out the answer in the PR body when adding a new `Drop` impl, especially on shared / public stdlib types. (2) **Negative-test convention.** New stdlib types with `Drop` impls add a "Drop-skip soundness" test that exercises the type's safety properties in the absence of the destructor running ŌĆö typically by holding the type past a panic-under-abort path, or (post-v1, when a forget primitive ships) by explicitly skipping Drop and checking that the type remains sound. The test pins the invariant at the test layer; if a future change introduces Drop-dependent soundness, the test fails. (3) **Audit existing stdlib types.** One-time review of every stdlib type with a `Drop` impl as of v1 ŌĆö `MutexGuard`, `RwLockReadGuard`, `RwLockWriteGuard`, `RefCellRefGuard`, `RefCellMutGuard`, IRQ-disable guard, future RAII guards ŌĆö confirming each one satisfies the principle. The audit produces a per-type note in the stdlib documentation explaining where the soundness comes from (typically: the borrow checker enforces the lock's aliasing rules; Drop only runs the unlock action). (4) **Documentation cross-reference.** Every `impl Drop` in stdlib gets a doc-comment line explaining "soundness derives from the type system; this destructor runs cleanup." The line is template boilerplate but reinforces the principle at every site reviewers encounter. (5) **No new compiler diagnostic.** This is a checklist + documentation discipline, not a compile-time enforcement ŌĆö the principle is too semantic to mechanize ("would skipping Drop cause UB?" is a meta-question about every API the type touches, not a local property). The compiler does enforce the related rules (e.g., `Drop` body must be `panics`-free, `Drop` and `Copy` mutually exclusive) ŌĆö those land in their own checklist entries. **Test coverage.** Per-stdlib-type "Drop-skip soundness" assertions (point 2 above) ŌĆö exact form depends on the type; generally constructs the value, holds it across a panic-under-abort code path or a process.exit, asserts the program exits cleanly without UB. These tests run alongside the regular stdlib test suite. Phase target: Phase 8 (Standard Library ŌĆö Floor) ŌĆö bundled with each stdlib type's own implementation; no separate slice. The audit of existing types runs once at the v1 freeze before stdlib API stabilization.

- [x] **`marker trait` syntax + stdlib marker migration.** Spec at `design.md ┬¦ Marker Traits` (v60 item 55). Slices: (1) **Lexer.** Add `marker` to the keyword arm in `src/lexer.rs` (currently a free identifier). The keyword token kind is unconditional; users with a local binding named `marker` must rename or use `r#marker`. (2) **Parser.** Recognize `[ATTRIBUTES] [VIS] "marker" "trait" IDENT [GENERIC_PARAMS] [":" SUPERTRAIT_BOUNDS] [WHERE_CLAUSE] (";" | "{" "}")` per syntax.md ┬¦3.4. AST: new `Item::MarkerTrait { name, generic_params, supertraits, where_clause, vis, attributes, span }`. Body must be either bare semicolon or empty `{ }` ŌĆö both forms produce identical AST representation; the parser distinguishes only for round-trip formatting. Methods, associated types, associated consts inside the body are rejected at parse with `error[E_MARKER_TRAIT_HAS_METHOD]: marker traits cannot declare methods; remove the method or change 'marker trait' to 'trait'` or `E_MARKER_TRAIT_HAS_ITEM` (for type/const items), each with the suggested-fix span pointing at the `marker` keyword (offering "remove `marker`") and at the offending body content (offering "remove this method/item"). (3) **Resolver.** Register the marker trait in the trait namespace alongside ordinary traits. Marker-trait resolution participates in trait-bound resolution, supertrait check, and impl coherence the same as regular traits ŌĆö the marker-ness is a definition-site property, not a use-site property. (4) **Empty-impl-body enforcement.** When an impl block targets a trait that resolves to `Item::MarkerTrait`, verify the impl body is empty `{ }`. Methods, associated types, default-method overrides inside the body are rejected with `error[E_MARKER_IMPL_HAS_METHOD]: impl of marker trait '<name>' cannot contain methods or items; the body must be empty`. The check runs at the impl-resolution step in the typechecker, after the impl's target trait is identified. (5) **Auto-implementation forbidden** ŌĆö verify (no enforcement work; just confirm the typechecker never generates `impl Marker for T { }` from auto-trait inference). The closed compiler-known marker traits (`ScopeLocal`, future `Concurrent`) have compiler-emitted impls for a small fixed set of types; users cannot manually implement them (sealed). (6) **Stdlib migration ŌĆö convert existing markers to `marker trait`.** Touch the source declarations of `Eq`, `Pod`, `ScopeLocal`, `Sealed`, future `Concurrent`. The migration is mechanical: change `trait Name { }` to `marker trait Name;` (or `marker trait Name: Supertrait;`). All existing impl blocks (which are already empty by construction) require no changes. Verify the migration in stdlib tests. (7) **Diagnostics on misuse.** `marker trait Foo { fn method(); }` rejected at parse with `E_MARKER_TRAIT_HAS_METHOD`; `marker trait Foo { type Item; }` rejected with `E_MARKER_TRAIT_HAS_ITEM`; `impl Pod for u8 { fn extra() { } }` rejected with `E_MARKER_IMPL_HAS_METHOD` after the impl's target trait `Pod` resolves to a marker. (8) **Formatter.** Round-trips `marker trait Foo;` and `marker trait Foo { }` to canonical form (`marker trait Foo;` is the canonical short shape; `{ }` form is preserved if the user wrote it explicitly). (9) **Test coverage.** Positive ŌĆö `marker trait Pod;` parses and registers; `marker trait Concurrent: Sized;` parses with supertrait; `marker trait Sealed[T];` parses with generics; `marker trait Storeable[T: Clone] where T: Default;` parses with where-clause; `impl Pod for u8 { }` accepted; `impl[T: Clone] Storeable[T] for Box[T] { }` accepted (conditional impl); generic bound `fn f[T: Pod](x: T) { }` accepts; impl-of-marker-trait coherence rejects duplicate impls; orphan rule applies (impl of foreign marker for foreign type rejected). Negative ŌĆö `marker trait Foo { fn bar(); }` rejected with `E_MARKER_TRAIT_HAS_METHOD` and both fix-its; `marker trait Foo { type Item; }` rejected with `E_MARKER_TRAIT_HAS_ITEM`; `marker trait Foo { const N: usize; }` rejected with `E_MARKER_TRAIT_HAS_ITEM`; `impl Pod for u8 { fn x() { } }` rejected with `E_MARKER_IMPL_HAS_METHOD`; user-side `impl ScopeLocal for MyType { }` rejected (sealed marker ŌĆö separate diagnostic). Phase target: 5.2 (Language Features) ŌĆö lexer + parser + AST + resolver + typechecker + formatter; stdlib migration is a coordinated CR with the language work landing first. No P1 carve-out ŌĆö option (a) of v60 item 55 ships the full surface at v1; user-extensible auto-marker derivation is permanently rejected per item 61.

- [x] **Raw-pointer method dispatch requires known pointee ŌĆö `E_RAW_POINTER_UNRESOLVED_POINTEE`. Ō£ō DONE (2026-07-11).** Spec at `design.md ┬¦ Method Resolution > Method dispatch on raw pointers requires a known pointee` (v60 item 54). Landed as the immediate follow-up to the deref/method surface (line 817): the size/stride-dependent methods (`read`/`write`/`offset`/`add` + unaligned/volatile) now emit `error[E_RAW_POINTER_UNRESOLVED_POINTEE]` at the RECEIVER span, naming the unresolved pointee, with the annotate-the-binding + turbofish-the-constructor guidance (slice 1). `is_null` is exempt (pointee-agnostic; accepts unresolved `T` ŌĆö slice 6). A generic parameter `T` in scope does NOT fire (`find_unbound_type_param` consults the enclosing bounds ŌĆö slice 4). Construction stays safe: `check_unsolved_type_param` now defers on a `Type::Pointer` binding, so `let p = ptr.null()` no longer errors at the binding and the focused diagnostic is the SINGLE report at the use site (slice 1's "underlines the read site, not the construction"). The method arm returns `Type::Error` to suppress the cascade. Tests: 8 typechecker (unresolved read/write/offset rejected with no redundant binding error; is_null / annotated / turbofish / generic-param / construction-alone all accept). **Residuals (deferred):** (a) the machine-applicable FixIt *span* (slice 2's constructor walk-back) ŌĆö the two suggestions are textual in the message today, no auto-apply edit; (b) unsolved-TypeVar pointees (vs the observed un-turbofished-generic `TypeParam` case) are not separately detected ŌĆö rare, and any TypeVar path still rejects downstream; (c) the turbofish fix-it it recommends (`ptr.null[u8]()`) has a PRE-EXISTING codegen gap (typechecks, but `p.read()` fails codegen ŌĆö [B-2026-07-11-1](../bug-ledger.md)); the annotation fix-it is the reliable one until that lands. Original (obsolete) blocker note follows: **Blocked on the "Raw-pointer deref/method surface" entry below (next to the `CString` entry) ŌĆö verified 2026-06-07:** the diagnostic guards method dispatch on `*const T` / `*mut T` receivers, and that dispatch surface does not exist yet. `infer_method_call` (`src/typechecker/expr_method_call.rs`) has no `Type::Pointer` receiver arm; `read` / `write` / `offset` exist in **no** form ŌĆö the live `ptr.*` module is constructors + provenance only (`addr` / `with_addr(_mut)` / `expose(_mut)` / `from_exposed(_mut)` / `container_of(_mut)` / `null(_mut)` / `dangling(_mut)` / free-fn `is_null`, registered at `src/typechecker/env_build.rs:756ŌĆō945`); and method-call turbofish is hardcoded `None` at `src/parser/exprs.rs:129` (free-function turbofish ŌĆö the fix-it's actual target, `ptr.null[u8]()` ŌĆö parses fine). Every test program in slice (6) below is unwritable today; slice (5) holds vacuously. What's already in place for when this unblocks: `Type::Pointer { is_mut, inner }` (`src/typechecker/types.rs:103`), the `Type::TypeVar`-vs-`Type::TypeParam` distinction slice (4) relies on (`types.rs:109`, `type_is_fully_concrete` at `:541`), and the multi-fix-it diagnostic infra (`type_error_with_fix_it`). Implement this check as part of (or immediately after) the deref-surface slice ŌĆö that slice is also where the method-vs-free-function shape decision gets made, which determines this entry's hook point. Slices: (1) **Typechecker check at method dispatch.** When method resolution evaluates `expr.method(args)` and `expr` has type `*const T` or `*mut T`, check whether `T` contains an unresolved type metavariable. If yes, emit `error[E_RAW_POINTER_UNRESOLVED_POINTEE]: method '<name>' on raw pointer requires a known pointee type` with the pointer expression's span underlined and the two fix-it suggestions: (a) annotate the binding's declared type (`let p: *const u8 = ...`), (b) use turbofish on the originating constructor when identifiable (`ptr.null[u8]()`). If the originating constructor cannot be identified syntactically (e.g., the pointer flowed in through a function argument), only the binding-annotation fix-it is offered. (2) **Constructor identification helper.** Walk back from the pointer expression through the binding's initializer (one level ŌĆö not a full DFA). If the initializer is a direct call to `ptr.null()` / `ptr.null_mut()` / `ptr.dangling()` / `ptr.dangling_mut()`, identify it as the originating constructor and offer the turbofish fix-it pointing at its call site. Otherwise fall through to the binding-annotation-only fix-it. (3) **`unsafe { }` orthogonality.** The check fires regardless of whether the call is inside an `unsafe { }` block ŌĆö the diagnostic is about type-system tractability, not safety contract. Verify the existing `unsafe`-required check still fires on raw-pointer method calls separately; the two diagnostics are independent and can both fire on the same expression. (4) **Generic-parameter case.** When the pointer's element type is a generic parameter `T` in scope (not a metavariable), the check passes ŌĆö `T` will be resolved at monomorphization, and the dispatch is checked against `T` symbolically. The distinction is between "type metavariable awaiting solving" and "generic type parameter" ŌĆö the typechecker's existing infrastructure already distinguishes these. (5) **No autoref / auto-deref through raw pointers ŌĆö verify.** Method-resolution Step 1 builds the receiver candidate list from `T`, `ref T`, `mut ref T`, plus `shared struct` / Rc / Arc deref steps. Raw pointers are NOT part of the chain ŌĆö verify the existing implementation does not accidentally include them. A method declared on the pointee type `T` is not reachable via `p: *const T` without an explicit `*p` dereference; the call resolves only against inherent methods on `*const T` / `*mut T` themselves. (6) **Test coverage.** Positive ŌĆö `let p: *const u8 = ptr.const(some_byte); unsafe { p.read(); }` accepts (T pinned by binding annotation); `let p = ptr.null[u32](); unsafe { p.read(); }` accepts (T pinned by turbofish); `fn f[T](p: *const T) { unsafe { p.read(); } }` accepts (T is a generic param, resolved at mono); pointer arithmetic `p.offset(4)` follows the same rule; `p.is_null()` accepts even with unresolved T (no read of the pointee, no T-dependent lowering). Negative ŌĆö `let p = ptr.null(); unsafe { p.read(); }` rejected with `E_RAW_POINTER_UNRESOLVED_POINTEE`, span on `p`, both fix-its offered (binding annotation + turbofish on `ptr.null`); `let p = ptr.dangling(); unsafe { p.write(0); }` rejected, both fix-its offered; pointer flowing through a function argument with no annotation rejected with binding-annotation fix-it only; pointer in a `Vec[*const _T]` whose element type is unsolved rejected at the `.read()` site. Phase target: 5.2 (Language Features) ŌĆö typechecker-only work; reuses the existing metavariable / generic-parameter distinction infrastructure. No P1 carve-out ŌĆö the rule is a single typechecker check; the diagnostic + fix-it are the only new compiler emission.

- [x] **Trait method parameters require names ŌĆö focused diagnostic for anonymous-parameter form.** Spec at `design.md ┬¦ Trait method parameter names ŌĆö required` (v60 item 53). The grammar already enforces this ŌĆö `PARAM = IDENT ":" TYPE | PATTERN ":" TYPE` per syntax.md ┬¦3.1, no anonymous alternative ŌĆö so the rule fires automatically as a generic parse error today. This entry's work is the **focused diagnostic upgrade**: when the parser sees a type token in parameter position with no preceding name, recognize the user intent and emit `E_TRAIT_METHOD_ANONYMOUS_PARAM` (or `E_FN_ANONYMOUS_PARAM` for free functions) with the type-only span underlined and the `_: i32` / `arg: i32` fix-it suggestion inline. Slices: (1) **Parser recognition.** In `parse_param` (or wherever parameters parse), detect the case where the token sequence starts with a type-class-looking IDENT not followed by `:` (or, more broadly, any token sequence that would form a valid TYPE in this position without a preceding name+colon). When this pattern matches, recover the type from the token stream as if a name had been provided, then emit the focused diagnostic naming the missing-name span and the type. (2) **Diagnostic shape.** `error[E_TRAIT_METHOD_ANONYMOUS_PARAM]: trait method parameters require a name` (or `E_FN_ANONYMOUS_PARAM` for free functions, which fall under the same rule but a slightly different help line ŌĆö the trait diagnostic mentions "trait method", the free-fn one says "function"). Span underlines the offending type-only token range. Help line: `write '_: <type>' for an unused parameter, or 'arg: <type>' for a meaningful name`. The `<type>` placeholder is filled with the recovered type so the fix-it is exactly applicable. (3) **Recovery ŌĆö keep parsing.** After emitting the diagnostic, recover by treating the missing-name case as if `_` had been written; the parser produces a `_`-pattern parameter and continues. This lets the rest of the trait method (and the rest of the file) parse so the user sees every error in one pass rather than cascading parse failures. (4) **Distinguish from other parse errors.** When a parameter genuinely has malformed syntax (unbalanced parens, missing comma, etc.), the focused anonymous-param diagnostic must NOT fire ŌĆö it should only fire on the specific shape "valid type in parameter position, no preceding name+colon, would parse as a type if positioned in a return-type slot." The detection is: peek ahead, attempt a type parse; if it succeeds and consumes tokens up to a `,` or `)`, the user wrote a type-only parameter ŌĆö emit `E_TRAIT_METHOD_ANONYMOUS_PARAM`. Otherwise fall through to the generic parse-error path. (5) **Test coverage.** Positive ŌĆö `trait V { fn visit(ref self, node: Node); }` parses; `trait V { fn visit(ref self, _: Node); }` parses; `trait V { fn visit(ref self, _: i32, _: i32); }` parses (multiple `_` in the same signature accepted); `fn free(_: i32) { }` parses (free-fn equivalent); `impl V for X { fn visit(ref self, n: Node) { ... } }` accepts the impl using a different parameter name than the trait declared (names are local). Negative ŌĆö `trait V { fn visit(ref self, Node); }` rejected with `E_TRAIT_METHOD_ANONYMOUS_PARAM`, span on `Node`, help line offering `_: Node` and `node: Node`; `fn free(i32) { 0 }` rejected with `E_FN_ANONYMOUS_PARAM`; multiple anonymous params in one signature emit one diagnostic per occurrence. Phase target: Phase 2 (Parser & AST) ŌĆö parser diagnostic upgrade. Verify the existing parser already produces *some* error on the type-only form (it should, via the generic "expected `:` after identifier" path); this entry replaces that with the focused diagnostic. No P1 carve-out ŌĆö the change is parser-local; the grammar-level rule is already in place, only the diagnostic needs sharpening.

- [x] **`@` binding semantics ŌĆö match-arm-mode propagation + composition checks.** Spec at `design.md ┬¦ @ Bindings` (v60 item 52). Phase 2 parser already supports `@` bindings (`PatternKind::AtBinding` recognized in `parse_pattern`); this entry covers the typechecker semantics and composition rules. Slices 1ŌĆō3, 5ŌĆō8 verified or shipped earlier (drive-by refutable-let fix: `let PAT = expr;` previously accepted refutable patterns silently ŌĆö now rejects via `is_irrefutable_param_pattern`, which `AtBinding` inherits transparently from its inner pattern); 7 parser + 5 typechecker tests from that round. **Slice 4 + the `ref IDENT @ PATTERN` form shipped 2026-06-07, closing the entry.** That round surfaced and fixed two gaps the earlier slice-3 `[x]` had overclaimed/missed: (a) **`ref IDENT @ PATTERN` did not parse** ("Expected pattern, found Ref") despite slice 3 claiming the annotation participates in mode propagation ŌĆö now a real parse form (`PatternKind::AtBinding` gained `by_ref: bool`; `ref` anywhere else in a pattern gets a focused rejection since binding modes otherwise flow from the scrutinee type); the typechecker flips the whole subtree to `Ref` mode (outer alias `ref T`, inner bindings borrows ŌĆö design.md ┬¦ @ Bindings "Explicit `ref`"), both ownership walkers treat the subtree as non-consuming (legacy `pattern_binds_anything` in `ownership/expr_check.rs` AND the CFG-predicate's duplicate in `use_classifier.rs` ŌĆö the UAM diagnostics come from the predicate pass, so missing the second one leaves "moved here" errors; `let` / `let-else` RHS flips to read mode in both `ownership/block_stmt.rs` and `use_classifier.rs`), and codegen binds the subtree with cleanup registration suppressed (`pattern_binding_is_borrow` save/set/restore in `bind_pattern_values`' AtBinding arm) while `pattern_consumes_field` returns false so the source keeps its drop ŌĆö ASAN-verified single-free on struct-String-field and Option-String-payload shapes. (b) **Pre-existing silent-zero miscompile on the `@` alias**: `check_pattern_against`'s AtBinding arm never wrote the `pattern_binding_types` surface-type side-tables (only the `Binding` leaf arm did), so `x @ Foo { ŌĆ” }` left `x` untyped in codegen's `var_type_names` and `x.field` silently read 0 ŌĆö extracted the side-table block into `record_pattern_binding_surface_types`, called from both arms; E2E-pinned (`test_e2e_match_at_binding_struct_alias_field_access`). Tests this round: 3 parser (`ref x @` match/let + ref-without-@ rejection), 9 typechecker (3 double-consume negatives incl. let-form + struct-shorthand, nested per-enclosing-outer granularity ├Ś2 asserts, Copy/wildcard/borrow-scrutinee/ref-@ positives), 3 ownership (ref-@ match + let non-consuming, plain-@ consume control), 2 interpreter, 3 codegen E2E, 2 ASAN.

  1. [x] **Verify parser handles all positions.** `IDENT @ PATTERN` parses at top level (match arm), nested inside struct/tuple-variant patterns (`Response { status: code @ 500..=599, body }`), inside or-patterns (`x @ A | x @ B`), and inside `let` patterns (`let x @ Foo { a } = foo`). The existing parser already covers these; each case has a parser test.
  2. [x] **Typechecker ŌĆö type assignment.** The `@` binding's `IDENT` takes the type of the scrutinee at its position in the pattern tree. For top-level `x @ pattern`, `x` has the scrutinee type; for nested `Response { status: code @ ... }`, `code` has the field type. Existing pattern-typechecking machinery handles this; the AtBinding arm in `infer_pattern` propagates the type correctly.
  3. [x] **Match-arm binding mode propagation.** Tie the `@` binding into the existing scrutinee-mode-propagation pass (`design.md ┬¦ Match Arm Binding Modes`): owned scrutinee ŌåÆ `@` binding consumes; `ref T` scrutinee ŌåÆ `@` binding is `ref T`; `ref IDENT @ PATTERN` annotation ŌåÆ borrows even under owned scrutinee. The propagation pass already runs over all bindings; AtBinding nodes participate the same as regular IDENT bindings. **Correction (2026-06-07):** the original `[x]` overclaimed the third clause ŌĆö `ref IDENT @ PATTERN` didn't even parse until the slice-4 round implemented it end-to-end (see the entry header for the full fix list).
  4. [x] **Cannot-double-consume rule (`E_AT_BINDING_DOUBLE_CONSUME`).** Shipped 2026-06-07. When the scrutinee is owned and an `@` binding's outer IDENT would consume the value (non-Copy) while a sub-pattern binding inside it would also consume a non-Copy field, reject with `error[E_AT_BINDING_DOUBLE_CONSUME]: cannot bind both '<outer>' and '<inner>' as owned ŌĆö '<outer>' would consume the whole value while '<inner>' would consume a field; use 'ref <outer>' to borrow, or omit one of the two bindings` (exact spec wording). **Implementation home moved vs the original plan:** the check lives in the *typechecker* (`check_pattern_against`, per design.md's "the typechecker rejects" ŌĆö the ownership pass's partial-move analysis never sees pattern claims), via an `owned_at_binding_outers` stack on the checker: a consuming `@` outer (Owned mode, `!by_ref`, non-Copy via `is_copy_type_during_check`) pushes; by-move non-Copy leaf bindings (the `Binding` arm + the struct-shorthand-field site) and nested consuming `@`s fire against the nearest enclosing entry ŌĆö which gives slice 8's granularity (`outer @ Foo { f: inner @ Bar(s) }` reports `inner`-vs-`outer` and `s`-vs-`inner`). Copy inner/outer types exempt (`x @ Some(y)` over `Option[i64]` accepts; reproduced before fixing: ALL double-consume shapes were silently accepted, match and let forms both). Let-form coverage required routing `@`-bearing `let` patterns through `check_pattern_against` (new `Pattern::contains_at_binding` gate in the typechecker's `Let` arm ŌĆö ordinary lets keep the `bind_pattern_types`-only path; `let-else` already routed). New `TypeErrorKind::AtBindingDoubleConsume` ŌåÆ `E0261` (cli.rs) / `DC::OwnershipBorrowConflict` (karac-explain class).
  5. [x] **Refutability for `let` patterns.** Drive-by fix: existing irrefutable-pattern check on `let` and `let ... else` now handles `@` bindings transparently ŌĆö the `@` itself is irrefutable, so the inner pattern's refutability determines the whole pattern's refutability. `let x @ Some(y) = opt;` is rejected by the refutability check; `let x @ Foo { a } = foo;` is accepted.
  6. [x] **Or-pattern alignment.** `x @ Some(_) | x @ None` accepts (same name, same type); `x @ Some(_) | y @ None` rejects with the existing or-pattern "every alternation must introduce the same set of names" diagnostic enriched to mention the `@`-binding sites.
  7. [x] **`mut` rejection inside patterns.** `mut x @ pattern` rejected at parse with the existing "mut not valid inside patterns" diagnostic; suggested fix-it points at `let mut x = ...` rebind in the arm body.
  8. [x] **Nested `@` bindings.** `outer @ Foo { field: inner @ Bar(value) }` binds three names with correct types; the partial-move check fires at the right granularity if both `outer` and `inner` would consume an overlapping subtree.

  **Test coverage** (mirrored against the slices above). Positive ŌĆö `match val { x @ Some(_) => ... }` binds `x: Option[T]`; `match val { Response { status: code @ 500..=599, body } => ... }` binds `code: i32` and `body: ...`; `match val: ref Foo { x @ Foo { field } => ... }` binds `x: ref Foo` and `field: ref FieldType` (via match-ergonomics); `ref x @ Some(y) => ...` over an owned scrutinee binds `x: ref Option[T]` without consuming; nested `outer @ Foo { field: inner @ Bar(v) }` binds three names; `x @ Some(_) | x @ None` accepts (same name + same type); `let x @ Foo { a } = foo` accepts (irrefutable); `n @ MIN_AGE..=MAX_AGE` accepts with const-expression range bound (composition with item 51). Negative ŌĆö `x @ Some(y)` with owned scrutinee where `y` would consume a field that `x` already owns rejected with `E_AT_BINDING_DOUBLE_CONSUME` (slice 4); `let x @ Some(y) = opt` rejected with refutability diagnostic; `mut x @ pattern` rejected at parse; `x @ Some(_) | y @ None` rejected with or-pattern same-names diagnostic; `x @ Some(_) | x @ Some(true)` (different inner types in alternation reaching the same name) rejected.

  **Phase target:** 5.2 (Language Features) ŌĆö typechecker-only work; the parser already supports the form and the existing match-arm-binding-mode pass handles the propagation. No P1 carve-out ŌĆö option uniform-with-existing-rules ships the full surface at v1.

- [x] **Half-open range patterns + const-expression bounds.** **Slices 2ŌĆō7 shipped 2026-06-08** ŌĆö the const-expression-bound extension is complete. AST gained `PatternKind::RangePattern { start/end: Option<RangeBound>, .. }` where `RangeBound = Literal(LiteralPattern) | Path { segments, span }` (slice 2). The parser accepts a const path in either bound position (`MIN..=MAX`, `0..=MAX`, `..MAX`, `MIN..`, qualified `Limits.HIGH..=ŌĆ”`) and rejects non-literal/non-path bounds at parse with `E_RANGE_PATTERN_BOUND_NOT_SIMPLE` (slice 7). Typecheck resolves a path bound via `eval_const_expr` (`check_range_pattern_bounds` in `typechecker/patterns.rs`) ŌĆö failure or a non-int/char value ŌåÆ `E_RANGE_PATTERN_BOUND_NOT_CONST` (`TypeErrorKind::RangePatternBoundNotConst` ŌåÆ `E0263`); on success it enforces bound-ordering (lower Ōēż upper, slice 4) and type-matching (char-vs-int family + integer width, slice 5). Each backend resolves a path bound through its own const mechanism ŌĆö interpreter via runtime `env`, codegen by re-compiling the named const's initializer (`compile_range_bound`), and exhaustiveness via a new `TypeEnv::const_values` map (populated after env build) so a const range never silently widens to a catch-all (slice 6 needs no new logic). 6 parser + 6 typechecker + 2 interpreter + 1 codegen-E2E tests; all gates green incl. `--features llvm` (1372 codegen). Original entry follows. Spec at `design.md ┬¦ Range Patterns` (v60 item 51). The five-form coverage and exhaustiveness rules are already specced; this entry covers verifying the parser/typechecker for half-open forms and adding the const-expression-bound extension. Slice 1 shipped with two real fixes ŌĆö bounded-exclusive `lo..hi` was missing from integer/char range arms (parse path now disambiguates `lo..` vs `lo..hi` by peeking for a literal after `..`); and `match value_class_var { ..lit => ... }` previously misparsed as struct-update because `looks_like_struct_literal` matched `{ ..ident }` for any identifier (now gated on `starts_upper(name)`). Interpreter `try_match_pattern` for `RangePattern` was also a "simplified" stub returning true unconditionally; replaced with proper `value_in_range_pattern` handling all five forms via i128 keys. 4 parser + 1 typechecker + 3 interpreter tests. Slices 2ŌĆō7 (const-expression bounds via `QUALIFIED_PATH`) remain ŌĆö needs a new `RangeBound { Literal | Path }` AST split + const resolution in the typechecker.

  1. [x] **Verify parser already accepts all five forms.** The grammar in `syntax.md ┬¦5.6` covers `CONST_PAT_BOUND ".." CONST_PAT_BOUND`, `CONST_PAT_BOUND "..=" CONST_PAT_BOUND`, `CONST_PAT_BOUND ".."` (unbounded above), `".." CONST_PAT_BOUND` (exclusive end), `"..=" CONST_PAT_BOUND` (inclusive end). All five forms now recognized in `parse_pattern`; the bounded-exclusive and value-class-scrutinee fixes shipped here.
  2. [x] **AST representation for range patterns.** Shipped as `PatternKind::RangePattern { start: Option<RangeBound>, end: Option<RangeBound>, inclusive: bool }` (kept the existing variant name/field names rather than the spec's `Pattern::Range`/`lo`/`hi`), with `enum RangeBound { Literal(LiteralPattern), Path { segments: Vec<String>, span: Span } }`. The `Option`s capture the half-open variants (`None` for the missing bound).
  3. [x] **Const-expression-bound resolution at typecheck.** A `Path` bound resolves via `eval_const_expr` in `check_range_pattern_bounds` (the same const-eval driver that powers array sizes / refinement bounds). **Deviation from the spec text:** the resolved value is NOT folded back into the AST (typecheck takes `&Program`); instead each backend resolves the path through its own const mechanism at the use site (interpreter `env`, codegen `consts`, exhaustiveness `TypeEnv::const_values`). Resolution failure / a non-int-or-char value emits `E_RANGE_PATTERN_BOUND_NOT_CONST` (`E0263`).
  4. [x] **Bound-ordering check after resolution.** `lower > upper` rejected on resolved values (so `MAX..=MIN` with MAX<MIN fails); an exclusive range whose bounds are equal (empty) is also rejected. Note: no literal-form ordering check existed before this slice ŌĆö it is net-new, not "the existing diagnostic".
  5. [x] **Type-matching check after resolution.** `range_bounds_type_conflict` rejects char-vs-integer family mismatches and two explicitly-typed integer bounds of differing width (`0i32..=MAX_I64`); a suffix-less integer literal adopts the other bound's width. Also net-new (no pre-existing pattern-bound type check).
  6. [x] **Exhaustiveness ŌĆö no change beyond existing rule.** Confirmed: `exhaustive.rs` lowers a range to an `IntRange` interval on resolved values; const bounds resolve through `TypeEnv::const_values` (a valid const bound is recorded before exhaustiveness runs, so a const range never silently widens to a catch-all ŌĆö the soundness pin at the range arm holds).
  7. [x] **No function-call expressions in pattern position (`E_RANGE_PATTERN_BOUND_NOT_SIMPLE`).** `parse_range_bound` accepts only a literal or an identifier-rooted path; anything else (e.g. `0..=(1 + 2)`) is rejected at parse with `E_RANGE_PATTERN_BOUND_NOT_SIMPLE`.

  **Test coverage.** Positive ŌĆö bounded `0..=9` accepts; bounded `'a'..='z'` accepts; half-open `..0`, `0..`, `..=0`, `0..=10` all parse and match (slice 1 Ō£ō); const-bound `match age { MIN_AGE..=MAX_AGE => ... }` resolves and matches (slice 3); const-bound + or-pattern `0..=9 | TEEN_MIN..=TEEN_MAX => ...`; const-bound + `@` binding `n @ MIN_AGE..=MAX_AGE => ...` (composition with item 52); mixed literal + const `0..=MAX_AGE` resolves correctly. Negative ŌĆö `MAX..=MIN` (where MAX < MIN as resolved values) rejected with bound-ordering diagnostic (slice 4); mixed-type `0i32..=MAX_I64` (where MAX_I64: i64) rejected with same-type diagnostic naming both resolved types (slice 5); non-const path `match age { local_var..=10 => ... }` rejected with `E_RANGE_PATTERN_BOUND_NOT_CONST` (slice 3); arbitrary expression `match age { (10 + 5)..=20 => ... }` rejected at parse with `E_RANGE_PATTERN_BOUND_NOT_SIMPLE` (slice 7); float bounds `match x { 1.0..=2.0 => ... }` rejected (existing rule); bare `..` as a pattern rejected with the existing "use `_`" diagnostic.

  **Phase target:** 5.2 (Language Features) ŌĆö typechecker-only work; reuses existing const-evaluation machinery for path resolution. No P1 carve-out ŌĆö option (b) of v60 item 51 ships the const-expression-bound extension at v1; refinement and distinct-type range patterns (option c of the decision matrix) are intentionally not in v1 and are additive-later if a workload demands them.

- [~] **Type alias bounds enforced at use sites.** Spec at `design.md ┬¦ Type Aliases` (v60 item 50). **Core shipped 2026-06-08 ŌĆö slices 1, 2, 7 + a missing prerequisite the spec assumed already existed.** The spec's slice-2 claim ("the existing alias-expansion machinery already substitutes the alias's body when a use site is type-checked") was **false**: `resolve_alias_deep` resolved a generic alias by *name only*, dropping the use-site generic args entirely ŌĆö so `type Pair[T] = Vec[T]; let p: Pair[i64] = ŌĆ”; p.push("s")` was **silently accepted** (the body kept a dangling `Type::TypeParam("T")` that unifies with anything). That silent type-hole is now closed: `lower_path_type`'s alias branch routes generic aliases through a new `instantiate_alias` (`src/typechecker/lowering.rs`) that (a) substitutes the supplied args into the resolved body via `substitute_type_params`, (b) arity-checks the arg count against the declared params, and (c) enforces each parameter's trait bounds against the corresponding arg via `type_satisfies_bound` ŌĆö `TypeParam` args are deferred (re-checked at monomorphization, mirroring `lower_vector_type`'s `Numeric` rule). Alias params are stored at decl time in a new `env.type_alias_params: HashMap<String, GenericParams>` (populated in `env_add_type_alias`; non-generic aliases get no entry and keep the transparent fast path). Bound failures emit `E_TYPE_ALIAS_BOUND_NOT_SATISFIED` (`TypeErrorKind::TypeAliasBoundNotSatisfied` ŌåÆ `E0262` / `DC::TraitBoundNotSatisfied`) naming the arg, trait, alias, and parameter. 12 typechecker tests (substitution catches wrong-type-through-alias, bound satisfied/violated, multi-bound partial failure, deferred-on-TypeParam-arg, arity mismatch, non-generic-alias-unaffected). All gates green incl. `--features llvm` codegen E2E (1369) ŌĆö substitution is strictly more correct than the leaked-TypeParam status quo, so no codegen relied on the old shape. **Remaining sub-slices get their own entries below.** Slice 4 (refinement-`where` coexistence) and slice 6 (TAIT ŌĆö the bound check fires before the existing `E_TAIT_NOT_IMPLEMENTED_YET` stub) hold by construction. Original spec preserved below.

  - [ ] **Type alias bounds ŌĆö slice 3: redundant-bound lint (`redundant_alias_bound`).** When a declared bound on an alias param is already implied by the underlying type's own param bounds (`type SortedKeyMap[T: Ord] = TreeMap[T, i32]` where TreeMap already requires `K: Ord`), emit a suppressible `warning[redundant_alias_bound]` with a remove-the-bound fix-it. Deferred from the core: needs alias-param-position ŌåÆ underlying-type-param ŌåÆ its-bound mapping + implication check; and the motivating stdlib type `TreeMap` doesn't exist yet ŌĆö **tracked at `phase-11-stdlib-longtail.md` ┬¦ General-purpose collections (`TreeMap[K: Ord, V]` / `TreeSet[T: Ord]`)**, which is the prerequisite for this slice. Not load-bearing (a warning).
  - [ ] **Type alias bounds ŌĆö slice 5: cross-package interface surface.** `pub type` alias bounds are part of the API contract ŌĆö the exporter pass must record them in the package interface descriptor so downstream consumers' use sites fire the same `E_TYPE_ALIAS_BOUND_NOT_SATISFIED` (with the alias-decl span surfaced as a note). Weakening a bound is non-breaking, tightening is breaking (same rule as `pub fn` signatures). Deferred: depends on the package-interface-descriptor emission surface ŌĆö **tracked as its own entry above (`Separate-compilation package-interface descriptor`)**, the prerequisite for this slice. The in-package check (above) is the load-bearing half.

  Original spec (for the record). Spec at `design.md ┬¦ Type Aliases` (v60 item 50). Slices: (1) **Parser ŌĆö already accepts bound forms.** The `GENERIC_PARAMS` rule in `syntax.md ┬¦3.12` shares grammar with struct/fn declarations, so `type Index[T: Eq + Hash] = HashMap[T, usize]` already parses. AST: ensure `Item::TypeAlias { generic_params: Vec<GenericParam>, ... }` records the bounds; verify the existing AST representation captures them (it should, since the same `GenericParam` shape is used elsewhere). (2) **Typechecker ŌĆö bound substitution and check at use sites.** The existing alias-expansion machinery already substitutes the alias's body when a use site is type-checked. Extend the substitution to walk the alias's generic-parameter bounds in the same pass: for each `GenericParam { name, bounds }`, after binding `name` to the use-site's concrete argument, check each bound against the bound argument via the existing trait-resolution machinery (the same code path that handles `fn foo[T: Ord]` use-site bound checks). On failure, emit `error[E_TYPE_ALIAS_BOUND_NOT_SATISFIED]: '<arg>' does not satisfy '<bound>' required by alias '<alias_name>'` with the use-site span as the primary, the alias declaration's span as the note, and the standard "type does not implement trait" help line. (3) **Redundant-bound lint.** When the typechecker resolves the alias body and discovers that a declared bound is already implied by the underlying type's existing bounds (e.g., `type SortedKeyMap[T: Ord] = TreeMap[T, i32]` ŌĆö TreeMap already requires K: Ord), emit `warning[redundant_alias_bound]: bound '<bound>' on alias '<alias_name>' is implied by the underlying type '<body>'; consider removing` with a fix-it removing the bound. The lint is suppressible via `#[allow(redundant_alias_bound)]` on the alias declaration. (4) **Composition with refinement `where`.** The existing refinement-predicate check at `where REFINEMENT_PRED` is value-level and orthogonal; the new bound check is type-level. Both run at independent times: bound check at use-site type-resolution, refinement at construction. No interaction beyond co-existence on the same alias declaration. (5) **Cross-package surface.** `pub type` alias bounds are part of the API contract ŌĆö verify the exporter pass records the bounds in the package's interface descriptor so downstream consumers see them; weakening a bound is non-breaking, tightening is breaking (same rule as `pub fn` signatures). (6) **TAIT interaction.** Bounds on a type-alias-`impl Trait` declaration (`type IterOf[T: Display] = impl Iterator[Item = T]`) are checked at every use-site of `IterOf[U]` against `U`; the check is independent of the witness-inference machinery (which is P1). The v1 stub for TAIT (per item 41) already produces the `E_TAIT_NOT_IMPLEMENTED_YET` diagnostic at witness-dependent use sites; bounds on the alias's generic parameters fire the bound check first, then the TAIT stub if the bound passes. (7) **Test coverage.** Positive ŌĆö `type Index[T: Eq + Hash] = HashMap[T, usize]; let x: Index[String] = HashMap.new();` accepts `String` (satisfies `Eq + Hash`); `type SortedVec[T: Ord] = Vec[T]; let v: SortedVec[i32] = Vec.new();` accepts `i32` (satisfies `Ord`); generic alias with multi-bound `type Cache[K: Eq + Hash, V: Clone] = Map[K, V]; let c: Cache[String, Vec[i32]] = Map.new();` accepts when both bounds hold; aliases without bounds (`type UserId = i64`, `type Callback = Fn(Event) -> Result[(), Error] with _`) continue to work unchanged; bound-on-alias composition with refinement (`type SortedNonEmpty[T: Ord] = Vec[T] where self.len() > 0`) parses, and use-site `SortedNonEmpty.try_from(some_vec)` runs both the bound check (compile-time) and the refinement (run-time). Negative ŌĆö `type Index[T: Eq + Hash] = HashMap[T, usize]; let x: Index[Vec[i32]] = HashMap.new();` rejected at the use site with `E_TYPE_ALIAS_BOUND_NOT_SATISFIED` naming `Vec[i32]` and the missing `Hash` bound; redundant `type SortedKeyMap[T: Ord] = TreeMap[T, i32]` emits `warning[redundant_alias_bound]` (suppressible); cross-package ŌĆö exporter declares `pub type Index[T: Eq + Hash] = HashMap[T, usize]`, downstream consumer's use site fails the bound check with the alias-declaration span surfaced in the diagnostic note. Phase target: 5.2 (Language Features) ŌĆö typechecker-only work; reuses existing trait-resolution machinery for bound checking. No P1 carve-out ŌĆö option (a) of v60 item 50 ships the full surface at v1; the spec is a single typechecker rule, not a multi-phase rollout.

- [ ] **Separate-compilation package-interface descriptor ŌĆö `pub` API surface emission + consumption.** Foundational compiler capability with **no prior tracker entry until 2026-06-08**: the compiler is whole-program today (it discovers and compiles all `.kara` under `src/` as one package ŌĆö `design.md ┬¦ Module System`, line ~1077), so there is no on-disk descriptor recording a package's `pub` API for a *downstream* package to type-check against. This entry tracks that descriptor: the exporter pass serializes each `pub` item's externally-visible signature ŌĆö `pub fn` signatures *including their declared effect set* (already an API-contract guarantee per `design.md` line ~167), `pub type` alias bodies **and their generic-parameter bounds**, `pub struct`/`enum`/`trait` shapes ŌĆö into a package-interface descriptor; the importer reads it so a consumer's use sites type-check (and re-fire the exporter's diagnostics) without re-compiling the dependency. Breaking-vs-non-breaking rules are uniform across the surface (weakening a bound/effect is non-breaking, tightening is breaking ŌĆö same rule `design.md` states for `pub fn` signatures). **This is the blocker for the type-alias-bounds slice 5 below** (cross-package alias-bound enforcement) and for any future cross-package contract checking; the in-package half of alias bounds already shipped (see the `[~]` type-alias entry above). Large standalone slice (the whole separate-compilation / external-dependency surface is unbuilt ŌĆö there is no package-manager / dependency-resolution entry anywhere yet either); not v1-load-bearing on its own (v1 ships whole-program), build when multi-package consumption lands. Spec home: `design.md ┬¦ Module System`.

- [x] **Saturating floatŌåÆint + every-`as`-cast-pair fully defined. COMPLETE 2026-06-09.** Spec at `design.md ┬¦ Numeric Semantics > as-cast semantics` (v60 item 49). Two halves: typechecker cast-pair rules (which pairs are accepted/rejected and with which fix-its) and codegen lowering (saturating LLVM intrinsics + four method families on `f32`/`f64`). All nine sub-slices done: slice 1 (typechecker rejection rules + bool/char-wide acceptance), slice 2 (stdlib method families ŌĆö typechecker + interpreter + effect, 2026-06-08), slices 3/8/9 (decisions / boolŌåÆint / charŌåÆint-wide), slice 4 (codegen `fptosi.sat`/`fptoui.sat` + the four families' compiled forms, 2026-06-08 ŌĆö `f as iN` now saturates; was raw `fptosi`/poison), and the existing-behavior verifications: slice 5 (intŌåÆint trunc/sext/zext, 2026-06-08), slices 6/7 (intŌåÆfloat sitofp/uitofp + floatŌåÆfloat fptrunc/┬▒Inf, 2026-06-09). Every `as`-cast pair is now defined and codegen-verified against the interpreter oracle.

  1. [x] **Typechecker ŌĆö cast-pair rejection rules.** Four new error codes for the rejected forms specced in design.md: `E_CHAR_AS_NARROW_INT` (rejected at `char as u8/u16/i8/i16` ŌĆö fix-it suggests `c as u32 as uN` for explicit truncation OR `c.encode_utf8(buf)` for proper UTF-8 encoding), `E_INT_AS_CHAR` (rejected at `iN/uN as char` ŌĆö fix-it suggests `char.try_from(n)`), `E_INT_AS_BOOL` (rejected at `iN/uN as bool` ŌĆö fix-it suggests `n != 0`), `E_FLOAT_AS_BOOL` (rejected at `f32/f64 as bool` ŌĆö meaningless). Each rejection runs at the typechecker's cast-resolution step; the existing redundant-cast lint (`bool as bool` etc.) is preserved.
  2. [x] **Stdlib ŌĆö floatŌåÆint method families. Shipped 2026-06-08 (typechecker + interpreter + effect halves; codegen is slice 4).** `f.saturating_to_iN()` / `f.wrapping_to_iN()` / `f.checked_to_iN() -> Option[iN]` / `f.trunc_to_iN()` on every `f32` / `f64` ├Ś every integer target, plus the symmetric `i.to_f32()` / `i.to_f64()` on every integer. **Spec correction:** the target set is the **11 representable integer types** ŌĆö signed `i8`..`i128` and unsigned `u8`..`u128` + `usize`. The original "`isize`" was an error: `isize` is **not a K─üra type** (the language has `usize` but no signed-pointer-width integer ŌĆö see `typechecker/lowering.rs::primitive_type`), so `trunc_to_isize` etc. are intentionally not registered (they fall through to the numeric NoMethodFound tightening). **Implementation:** a new pure, backend-agnostic module `src/numeric_conv.rs` holds the nameŌåÆ(family, target, bits, signed) parse + the conversion semantics (saturating = native saturating `as` / NaNŌåÆ0; wrapping = modular `2^bits` truncation; checked = `None` on NaN/out-of-range else `Some(trunc)`; trunc = trap on NaN/out-of-range else `trunc`), with its own unit tests. The typechecker arm (`expr_method_call.rs`, beside `abs`) types `checked_*` ŌåÆ `Option[target]` and the rest ŌåÆ `target` (target `Type` via the now-`pub(super)` `primitive_type`); the interpreter arm (`method_call.rs`) computes via `numeric_conv` and raises a structured `"float-to-int out of range"` runtime error for the `trunc_*` trap. **Effect:** `trunc_to_*` carries `panics` (seeded under the `float.trunc_to_int` key in `seed_builtin_effects`; every `trunc_to_<target>` method name routed to it in `effectchecker/inference.rs`) ŌĆö unlike the arithmetic-overflow traps (`abs` on `iN::MIN`) which are deliberately outside the effect system; the other three families are effect-free. The four-method family parallels the (not-yet-implemented) integer arithmetic `checked_*`/`wrapping_*`/`saturating_*`/`overflowing_*` family at the spec level. **Interpreter caveat:** `Value::Int` is `i64`, so `u64`/`u128`/`i128` results beyond `i64` range are stored truncated (a pre-existing interpreter wide-int limitation, not specific to these methods; codegen in slice 4 is bit-exact). **`karac build`** of one of these methods errors loudly with an "interpreter-only, slice 4" message (codegen guard at the `compile_method_call` fall-through) rather than ICE-ing or miscompiling. Tests: 6 `numeric_conv` units + 5 typechecker + 5 interpreter + 2 effectchecker; all gates green incl. `--features llvm` (codegen 1384, par_codegen 140, memory_sanitizer 109).
  3. [x] **`AllocError`-style not-needed.** Out-of-range floatŌåÆint conversions saturate at the `as` site, so no error type is required for the default form. The `checked_to_iN()` method returns `Option[iN]` (using the existing `Option` type) for users who want the explicit-failure form; no new error type. Decision recorded; no implementation work.
  4. [x] **Codegen ŌĆö Phase 7 lowering. Shipped 2026-06-08.** `f as iN` now lowers to LLVM `llvm.fptosi.sat` (signed target) / `llvm.fptoui.sat` (unsigned target) ŌĆö the saturating intrinsic, single instruction, available on every supported target (was raw `fptosi`, which is *poison* on out-of-range ŌĆö the bug this entry exists to fix). `f.saturating_to_iN()` lowers to the same intrinsic. All in `codegen/expr_ops.rs`: `compile_cast` gained a `target_is_unsigned` parameter (the LLVM `IntType` target carries no K─üra signedness; both call sites ŌĆö the `as` lowering in `exprs.rs` and the SIMD-lane cast in `method_call.rs` ŌĆö compute it from the target type name), and a new `emit_float_to_int_sat` helper declares + calls the intrinsic (`Intrinsic::find` + `get_declaration` over `[int_ty, float_ty]`). The method families dispatch through `emit_float_to_int_conv` (replacing the slice-2 interpreter-only guard in `method_call.rs`): **`wrapping_to_iN`** = `trunc(llvm.fptosi.sat.i128(f), iN)` ŌĆö modular truncation, target-independent by construction (no legacy-ARM polyfill needed; the spec's raw-`fptosi` plan would have been poison). **`checked_to_iN`** and **`trunc_to_iN`** share one `emit_float_to_int_rangecheck` that decides representability in *exact integer arithmetic* ŌĆö a wider saturating cast (`iW`, `W=128` for Ōēż64-bit targets, `256` for the 128-bit ones via `custom_width_int_type`) then narrow + re-extend + compare, plus an `fcmp oeq f, f` NaN guard ŌĆö sidestepping all float-bound rounding. `checked_to_iN` builds the `Option[iN]` branch-free via two `select`s into the seeded Option aggregate (`Some(narrowed)` / `None`); `trunc_to_iN` branches to `emit_panic("float-to-int out of range")` (carries the `#[track_caller]` location, as wired in slice 2's `panics` effect). `i.to_f32()`/`i.to_f64()` lower to `sitofp`/`uitofp` per source signedness. **Two bring-up bugs fixed:** the `signed`ŌåÆ`target_unsigned` polarity was inverted (made `saturating_to_i32` emit `fptoui.sat`), and unsigned method results sign-extended on the print path (`expr_is_unsigned_int` gained an arm for the unsigned-target bare-int conversion methods). **Drive-by fix:** `expr_is_unsigned_int` also gained a `Cast` arm, so `println(x as u8)` no longer sign-extends (a pre-existing gap affecting *any* unsigned as-cast in value position, not just floatŌåÆint). All compiled outputs verified bit-identical to the slice-2 interpreter oracle across every family, both signednesses, in/out-of-range, NaN/┬▒inf, and 128-bit targets. **Interpreter-parity caveat (documented):** `checked_to_i128/u128` Option payloads beyond i64 truncate (the Option payload word is i64; same wide-int limitation the interpreter has). 2 IR-pin + 6 E2E codegen tests; gates green incl. `--features llvm` (codegen 1398).
  5. [x] **IntŌåÆint casts ŌĆö verified spec-compliant 2026-06-08.** Confirmed `compile_cast`'s intŌåÆint lane (`codegen/expr_ops.rs`) emits the documented instructions: narrowing ŌåÆ `trunc` (low M bits), signed-source widening ŌåÆ `sext`, unsigned-source widening ŌåÆ `zext` (the `zext` lane gated on the caller's `source_is_unsigned` flag, from the kata-91 hot-loop fix). Compiled output verified bit-identical to the interpreter across the design.md vectors ŌĆö `0x1FFi32 as u8 == 255`, `-1i32 as u8 == 255`, `300i32 as i8 == 44`, `-1i8 as u8 == 255`, `(-5i8) as i64 == -5` (sext), `(200u8) as i64 == 200` (zext). No code change needed; added a `sext` IR pin (`test_ir_int_signed_widen_emits_sext`, completing the trunc/sext/zext IR triple alongside the pre-existing `test_ir_int_truncate` / `test_ir_u8_cast_to_i32_emits_zext`) and a consolidated spec-case E2E (`test_e2e_int_to_int_cast_spec_cases`).
  6. [x] **IntŌåÆfloat casts ŌĆö verified spec-compliant 2026-06-09.** `compile_cast` emits `sitofp` (signed source) / `uitofp` (unsigned source) ŌĆö IEEE 754 round-to-nearest-even, never panics. Verified compiled == interpreter: `5i64 as f64 == 5.0`, `255u8 as f64 == 255.0` (uitofp, not sitofp ŌåÆ not -1.0), and large-value rounding via a round-trip through a non-f64-representable source (`2^60 + 1` ŌåÆ `2^60`, shown as a stable integer to avoid float-format dependence). No code change; added `test_ir_uint_to_float_emits_uitofp` (completing the sitofp/uitofp IR pair) + `test_e2e_int_to_float_casts`.
  7. [x] **FloatŌåÆfloat casts ŌĆö verified spec-compliant 2026-06-09.** Widening (`f32`ŌåÆ`f64`) is value-preserving and implicit (`as` also accepted); narrowing via `as` uses `fptrunc` (round-to-nearest-even); narrowing overflow produces `┬▒Infinity` per IEEE 754, never a trap. Verified compiled == interpreter: `2.5f32 as f64 == 2.5`, `1.5f64 as f32 == 1.5`, `1e300f64 as f32 == inf`, `-1e300f64 as f32 == -inf`. No code change; added `test_ir_float_narrow_emits_fptrunc` + `test_e2e_float_to_float_casts`.
  8. [x] **BoolŌåÆint casts.** `false as iN/uN` produces `0`; `true as iN/uN` produces `1`. Codegen emits `zext` from `i1` (the LLVM bool type). Accepted as of slice 1.
  9. [x] **CharŌåÆint casts (wide targets).** `char as u32` and `char as i32` produce the Unicode scalar value (range `0..=0x10FFFF`, fits in 21 bits); codegen emits `zext` from the `i32`-internal char representation. Wide-target casts accepted as of slice 1; narrow-target casts (`char as u8/u16/i8/i16`) rejected via `E_CHAR_AS_NARROW_INT` (slice 1).

  **Test coverage.** Positive ŌĆö `f64.NAN as i32 == 0`; `f64.INFINITY as i32 == i32.MAX`; `f64.NEG_INFINITY as i32 == i32.MIN`; `1e30f64 as i32 == i32.MAX`; `(-1e30f64) as i32 == i32.MIN`; `1e30f64 as u8 == 255`; `(-1.0f64) as u8 == 0`; `3.7f64 as i32 == 3`; `(-3.7f64) as i32 == -3`; `(2_i64.pow(60)) as f64` rounds to nearest; `i64.MAX as f64` rounds upward past i64.MAX; `0x1FFi32 as u8 == 0xFFu8`; `(-1i32) as u8 == 0xFFu8`; `300i32 as i8 == 44i8`; `(-1i8) as u8 == 255`; `'A' as u32 == 65`; `'A' as i32 == 65`; `false as u8 == 0`; `true as u8 == 1`; `f.saturating_to_i32() == f as i32`; `f.NaN.checked_to_i32() == None`; `1e30f64.checked_to_i32() == None`; `1.5f64.checked_to_i32() == Some(1)`. Negative ŌĆö `'A' as u8` rejected with `E_CHAR_AS_NARROW_INT` and the two fix-its; `'A' as i16` rejected; `65u8 as char` rejected with `E_INT_AS_CHAR` and the `char.try_from` fix-it; `1i32 as bool` rejected with `E_INT_AS_BOOL` and the `n != 0` fix-it; `1.0f64 as bool` rejected with `E_FLOAT_AS_BOOL`; `f.NaN.trunc_to_i32()` panics with the "float-to-int out of range" message and a `#[track_caller]` source location at the call site, not inside the stdlib.

  **Phase target:** Phase 5.2 (typechecker rejection rules + new error codes ŌĆö slice 1 shipped; the method-family typechecker/interpreter/effect surface ŌĆö slice 2 ŌĆö shipped 2026-06-08); Phase 7 (codegen `fptosi.sat` / `fptoui.sat` lowering + the four method families' compiled forms ŌĆö slice 4 ŌĆö shipped 2026-06-08). All nine sub-slices are done (implementation: 1/2/3/4/8/9; verification: 5/6/7, all closed 2026-06-08/09) ŌĆö the entry is complete. No P1 carve-out ŌĆö v60 item 49 ships the full saturating + every-pair-defined surface at v1; the additional method families on `f32` / `f64` parallel existing integer method-family ergonomics and require no new infrastructure beyond the codegen step.

- [x] **PREREQUISITE ŌĆö `[profile]`-table typed knobs + `ProfileConfig` threading ŌĆö SHIPPED 2026-06-09.** Shared substrate for every per-profile boolean/string knob (`panic_on_alloc_failure`, `panic = "unwind"|"abort"`, future `bounds_checks`/`overflow_checks`). Original ground truth (2026-06-09): the only profile state was the scalar `[package].profile` ŌåÆ `CompileProfile` enum (`Default`/`Embedded`/`Kernel`, no `isr`/`gpu`) with just `parse`/`as_str`; forbidden-effects-per-profile was a doc-comment table (`manifest.rs:55-62`) duplicated as *two* hand-written match tables (`effectchecker/extern_ffi.rs::profile_forbids` for build-profile gating + `effectchecker/profile_compat.rs::profile_forbids_effect` for `#[profile(...)]`-attribute gating); no `[profile]` table parsing; the only per-knob precedent was the top-level `public_effects` knob. **What shipped, by slice:**
  - **Slice 2 ŌĆö queryable forbidden-effect table.** `CompileProfile::forbids(&EffectVerbKind, &str) -> bool` + `forbids_effect(&Effect)` + `forbidden_effects() -> Vec<Effect>` (manifest.rs) make the doc-comment table queryable and are now the **single source of truth**: both previously-duplicated match tables (`extern_ffi::profile_forbids`, `profile_compat::profile_forbids_effect`) were deleted and re-pointed at `forbids_effect`. `forbids` preserves exact prior semantics (kernel forbids `allocates` of *any* resource; embedded only `allocates(Heap)`); `forbidden_effects()` returns the canonical representative list (heap form) for introspection. 2 manifest unit tests pin both against the doc table; the existing 18 extern/attribute profile tests confirm zero behavior change.
  - **Slice 1 ŌĆö `[profile]` table parse.** `parse_profile_table` (manifest.rs) mirrors `parse_wasm_table`/`parse_release_table`: recognizes the top-level `[profile]` knob table, distinct from the `[package].profile` *selector* (selection unchanged). No knob keys are recognized yet ŌĆö downstream entries each add a recognized-key arm ŌĆö so every key soft-warns (drop-on-the-floor discipline); a non-table value hard-errors (`InvalidFieldType`). 3 manifest tests (absent/empty ŌåÆ knobless config; unknown-key soft-warn; non-table hard-error).
  - **Slice 3 ŌĆö `ProfileConfig` carrier + threading.** `ProfileConfig { profile: CompileProfile, guarded_knobs: Vec<ProfileKnob> }` (manifest.rs) **subsumes** the bare profile so the active profile + its knobs travel as one object. Lives on `Manifest.profile_config` (populated by `parse_profile_table`; realigned on `[target.*.profile]` override in `merge_target_overlay`) and on `Pipeline.profile_config`. Threaded **live** into the effect checker: `EffectChecker` now stores `profile_config` (the bare `profile` field is gone ŌĆö a `profile()` accessor reads `profile_config.profile`); `effectcheck_with_typecheck_data` takes `impl Into<ProfileConfig>` (with `From<CompileProfile>`), so the ~20 existing `CompileProfile`-passing callers are untouched while `Pipeline::effectcheck` threads the full carrier via the new `EffectChecker::with_profile_config` builder. 1 effect-checker test threads a full `ProfileConfig` end-to-end (carrier-built `embedded` rejects extern `allocates(Heap)`).
  - **Slice 4 ŌĆö moot-flag rejection scaffold.** `ProfileConfig::moot_knob_errors()` (manifest.rs) is the reusable pass: for each registered `ProfileKnob`, if the active profile already `forbids` the guarded effect, emit a "knob is moot" message. Surfaced at **manifest-parse time** as a hard `ManifestError::ProfileKnobMoot` (the downstream entries' "rejected (parse error)" contract). Wired into `parse_profile_table` (no-op until a knob registers). 1 manifest test exercises the logic with a synthetic `panic_on_alloc_failure`-shaped knob (moot on embedded/kernel, live on default; empty knob set never fires).
  - **Scope boundary (honest, not dropped):** the carrier is threaded live to the **effect checker**; the **typechecker** and **codegen** legs were *not* pre-threaded ŌĆö they have no reader until their consumer knob lands, and adding dead params now would be speculative scaffolding (per [`feedback_v1_ship_reality_not_promises`](../../CLAUDE.md)). Each consumer threads `Pipeline.profile_config` the same one-line `impl Into<ProfileConfig>` way the effect-checker leg does: `panic_on_alloc_failure`'s typechecker rejection pass and `panic`'s codegen split. Custom-profile `no_effects` kara.toml enforcement is explicitly **out of scope** ŌĆö it is the separate phase-5-diagnostics.md:507 `profiles = [...]`/custom-profile sub-open entry. **Gates:** `cargo fmt --all -- --check` + `cargo clippy --all --all-targets -- -D warnings` clean; manifest 101ŌåÆ107, effectchecker 364ŌåÆ365, full non-codegen suite green. **Files:** `src/manifest.rs` (CompileProfile query methods + `ProfileConfig`/`ProfileKnob` + `parse_profile_table` + `ProfileKnobMoot` + 6 tests), `src/effectchecker.rs` (`profile`ŌåÆ`profile_config` field + `profile()` accessor + `new_with_policy_and_config`/`with_profile_config`), `src/effectchecker/extern_ffi.rs` + `src/effectchecker/profile_compat.rs` (dedup ŌåÆ `forbids_effect`), `src/lib.rs` (`impl Into<ProfileConfig>`), `src/cli.rs` (`Pipeline.profile_config` field + populate + thread), `src/dep_graph.rs` + `src/dep_resolver.rs` (test-helper `Manifest` literals), `tests/effectchecker.rs` (carrier end-to-end test). **Phase target:** Phase 8 (manifest + threading). Surfaced + shipped 2026-06-09 grounding the Fallible-allocation entry against source.
