- [~] **Fallible-allocation API split ŌĆö `try_*` companions on every alloc-bearing method + `panic_on_alloc_failure` profile flag.** Spec at `design.md ┬¦ Fallible Allocation API and OOM Handling` (v60 item 46). Full v1 implementation. Two parallel surfaces: (a) the `try_*` companion methods on every alloc-bearing stdlib type, available always; (b) a profile flag that, when `false`, rejects every panicking-alloc call site at typecheck. Hard mode for embedded/kernel-adjacent profiles; opt-in elsewhere. **Status 2026-06-10: sub-items 1ŌĆō7 + 9 DONE; item 8 (Phase-7 codegen) `[~]` partial ŌĆö runtime allocator wrappers (`karac_alloc_fallible`/`karac_alloc_or_panic`) + the panicking-collection-alloc reroute + `Vec.try_push`/`VecDeque.try_push_back` fallible codegen shipped; the remaining `try_*` codegen arms are scoped under item 8 (mechanical follow-ons of the proven `try_push` pattern, except `Map`/`Set` `try_insert` which need fallible runtime FFI, and `try_with_capacity` which needs element-type recovery through the `Result` wrapper).** Codegen-unimplemented `try_*` companions are still rejected by `karac build` with an actionable "item 8" message (see item 2); `karac run` supports them all. The front-end rejection passes (items 4ŌĆō6) need no codegen.

  1. [x] **`AllocError` prelude type ŌĆö interpreter-complete 2026-06-09.** Registered `enum AllocError { OutOfMemory { requested_bytes: usize }, CapacityOverflow }` as a baked prelude type (parallel to `IoError`/`VarError`): new `runtime/stdlib/alloc_error.kara` (`#[derive(Debug, Display, Eq, Copy)]`), added to `prelude.rs` `PRELUDE_TYPES` + `STDLIB_SOURCES`, and codegen layout-seeded in `seed_builtin_enum_layouts` (declarations.rs, 2-word `{tag, payload}`). Available everywhere without import; `Result[(), AllocError]` / `Result[T, AllocError]` need no qualification. Fully working under `karac run`: construction (both variants), `==`, Display, `match` with field binding, `?`-propagation through `Result[T, AllocError]` ŌĆö 1 interpreter test (`alloc_error_prelude_type_usable_without_import`). **This entry surfaced ŌĆö and the work fixed ŌĆö two general enum gaps that the slice assumed already existed** (both committed separately, with their own tests): (a) **interpreter enum/struct `==`** was an ICE for *every* enum (Option/Result/Ordering included) ŌĆö `eval_binary` had no `EnumVariant`/`Struct` arm; (b) **source-level enum struct-variant construction** (`Enum.Variant { f: v }`) was mis-typed as a struct literal (built `Value::Struct`, "is not a struct"). **Remaining follow-ups (codegen + Display refinement), tracked below:** the codegen path is unit-variant-only (the struct-variant construction *lowering* and a sound codegen enum `==` are not done ŌĆö see the new `[ ]` entries directly below), and Display currently uses the default `OutOfMemory { requested_bytes: N }` rendering, not the design's custom `N bytes` / `"capacity overflow"` wording (a custom `impl Display` refinement). None of these block slices 2/7/3 (the typechecker now accepts the type + construction); they gate the eventual codegen E2E + the polished diagnostic text.

  - [x] **FOLLOW-UP ŌĆö codegen lowering for enum struct-variant construction ŌĆö DONE 2026-06-09.** Codegen's `StructLiteral` arm (`exprs.rs`) now detects an enum-qualified path (`path[len-2]` names an enum whose `Variant` is in its layout) and routes to `compile_enum_struct_variant_init` (call_dispatch.rs), which builds the seeded enum aggregate: maps each *named* field init onto the variant's declared position via `enum_variant_struct_field_names` (scans the user program + `STDLIB_PROGRAMS` so prelude enums like `AllocError` resolve) ŌåÆ `field_word_offsets` slot, coercing payload words (with `maybe_defensive_copy_param_arg` for owned String/Vec params). **Also fixed the match-side mirror that this surfaced:** `Enum.Variant { field }` patterns parse as `PatternKind::Struct`, and codegen's `bind_pattern_values` Struct arm only knew real structs (ŌåÆ "Undefined variable") ŌĆö added an enum-struct-variant branch that extracts named fields by positionŌåÆword-offset (the named twin of the `TupleVariant` arm). Verified E2E: `AllocError` + user `Shape { Circle { r }, ŌĆ” }` construct, match-bind, and flow through `Result` under `karac build`.

  - [x] **FOLLOW-UP ŌĆö sound codegen enum `==` (unit/scalar-payload) ŌĆö DONE 2026-06-09.** Root cause (IR-confirmed): enum construction used `get_undef`, so a multi-word enum's unit variant was `{ tag, undef }`; the word-wise `compile_struct_eq` then did `undef == undef` ŌåÆ folded to `undef`, making `E.B == E.B` wrong. Fix: zero-initialize (`const_zero`) at every enum-aggregate construction site (`exprs.rs` `compile_path_expr` unit-variant ŌĆö the actual `E.B` builder, since `Enum.Variant` parses as `Path`; `call_dispatch.rs` `try_unit_enum_variant`, `build_nonshared_enum_value`, the non-shared tuple aggregate, the `Option` builder, and the new struct-variant builder). Unused payload words are now deterministically `0`, so word-wise tag+payload comparison is **sound for unit/scalar-payload enums** (`AllocError`, `Ordering`, `Option[scalar]`/`Result[scalar]`, user enums with int fields). E2E verified incl. payload discrimination (`OutOfMemory{2048} != OutOfMemory{99}`). The earlier "zero-init didn't work" note was a stale-binary artifact ŌĆö the live `E.B` builder was `compile_path_expr`, not the edited `try_unit_enum_variant`. **Phase target:** Phase 7.

  - [x] **FOLLOW-UP ŌĆö sound codegen enum `==` for heap-payload variants (concrete types) ŌĆö DONE 2026-06-09.** Added `compile_enum_eq` (expr_ops.rs): a variant-aware comparator that compares the tag, then `switch`es on it and compares **only the active variant's payload, type-aware** ŌĆö each field is rebuilt from its payload words at its declared LLVM type (`rebuild_value_from_payload_words`) and recursed through `compile_binop(Eq)`, so a `String`/`Vec` payload compares by content (`compile_string_binop`), not by pointer word. The `Binary` arm (exprs.rs) routes `==`/`!=` to it when an operand resolves to an enum (`enum_name_of_expr`: variable / `Enum.Variant` / constructor-call / struct-variant-literal) **and** that enum has a heap-payload variant (`enum_has_heap_payload`, via `field_drop_kinds == VecOrString`); unit/scalar enums keep the cheaper word-wise path. Verified E2E: a user `enum Msg { Text(String), Code(i64), Empty }` compares `Text("a"+"b") == Text("ab")` ŌåÆ `true` (distinct allocations, equal content) while scalar/unit/cross-variant stay correct. No regression (142 enum/match/Option/Result + ASAN green). Nested-enum and >3-word payload fields fall back to a word compare (rare).

  - [x] **FOLLOW-UP ŌĆö sound codegen enum `==` for GENERIC heap-payload enums (`Option[String]`, `Result[_, String]`, generic user enums) ŌĆö DONE 2026-06-09.** `Some("a"+"b") == Some("ab")` and `Ok`/`Err`-of-`String` now compare by **content** under `karac build`, matching `karac run`. **How the instantiation reaches the binop site:** the typechecker already records each expression's fully-instantiated `Type` in `expr_types`; the lowering pass (`src/lowering.rs`) now surfaces the generic `Named` ones into a new `Program.enum_inst_type_exprs` span table (`EnumInstTypeExprsTable`, sibling to `owned_temp_drops`), which codegen loads. `compile_enum_eq` gained an `inst: Option<&TypeExpr>` parameter: it builds a paramŌåÆarg substitution from the enum decl's generic params (`enum_generic_param_names`) + the instantiation's args, substitutes into each variant's field types (`subst_type_params`), and rebuilds + recurses per field ŌĆö so the `Some`/`Ok`/`Err` payload reconstructs as a `String` and compares via `compile_string_binop`. **Three correctness fixes were needed beyond the plumbing:** (a) offsets are now computed from the (substituted) field word counts (`payload_word_count_for_type_expr`) instead of `layout.field_word_offsets` ŌĆö the seeded `Result` layout records each variant's *whole* payload span (`Ok`/`Err` ŌåÆ `(0,5)`, union-overlaid), which would have shoved a 3-word `String` into the >3-word word-wise fallback; computing per-field offsets matches how the user-enum layout builder packs and leaves the concrete path identical; (b) `type_to_type_expr` lowers `Type::Str` to the internal spelling `"str"`, but the codegen classifiers (`enum_drop_kind_for_type_expr` routing, `payload_word_count_for_type_expr`) match the *source* spelling `"String"` ŌĆö `canonicalize_payload_type_names` rewrites it; (c) **routing resolves an identifier operand's instantiation by *variable name*** (`enum_inst_var_types`, populated at let + parameter binding sites, cleared per-function) rather than by the use-site span, because **f-string-interpolated spans collide** (see `bugs.md` B-2026-06-09-1) ŌĆö without this, `f"{opti64_a == opti64_b}"` and `f"{optstr_a == optstr_b}"` alias and a scalar `==` mis-routes to the String comparator. A name-match guard on the span fallback prevents any cross-enum mis-route. **Verified:** `tests/codegen.rs::e2e_generic_enum_heap_payload_eq_compares_by_content` (inline-f-string regression guard for the span collision) + `e2e_generic_enum_heap_eq_through_params` (parameter-binding leg); full codegen suite 1427 green, ASAN 153 green, FE suites green, clippy/fmt clean. **Residual:** non-identifier operands (direct `Some(x)` constructor) compared *inline inside an f-string* still degrade to the word-wise path ŌĆö same root cause as B-2026-06-09-1, no regression. **Phase target:** Phase 7. Surfaced + closed 2026-06-09.
  2. [x] **`try_*` companion methods on every alloc-bearing collection type ŌĆö interpreter + typechecker + effect complete 2026-06-09.** A `try_<base>` companion types identically to its panicking `<base>` counterpart but returns `Result[<base-ret>, AllocError]`; the only difference is the return type. Implemented uniformly via a **single recognized-companion registry** (`src/fallible_alloc.rs`, the pure backend-agnostic peer of `numeric_conv.rs`) consumed by all three phases, rather than ~30 hand-written per-method arms: (a) **typechecker** ŌĆö `infer_method_call` (instance) and `infer_call` (static constructor) intercept a recognized `try_<base>`, recurse into the base method to reuse its argument validation + return-type synthesis verbatim, then wrap in `Result[_, AllocError]` (`result_alloc_error_type`); the instance interception is gated on a builtin-collection receiver (`receiver_is_alloc_collection`) so a user type's own `try_push`/`try_clone` is never shadowed; (b) **interpreter** ŌĆö `eval_method_call`/`eval_call` run the base op and wrap the value in `Result.Ok(_)` (the tree-walk host allocator never OOMs, so the companion always succeeds ŌĆö failure injection arrives with the codegen runtime allocator wrappers, item 8); (c) **effect** ŌĆö every companion carries `allocates(Heap)` (instance forms route to a seeded `__builtin_try_alloc` key in the `MethodCall` walker; static forms seeded by their `Type.try_<base>` key). **Shipped surface** (mirrors only operations whose panicking base exists today): instance ŌĆö `Vec.try_push` / `try_extend_from_slice` / `try_clone`, `String.try_push` / `try_push_str` / `try_clone`, `VecDeque.try_push_back` / `try_push_front` / `try_clone`, `Map.try_insert` / `try_clone`, `Set.try_insert` / `try_clone`, `SortedSet.try_insert` / `try_clone`; static constructors ŌĆö `Vec.try_with_capacity` / `try_from_slice`, `VecDeque.try_with_capacity`, `String.try_with_capacity`. **`?`-propagation through `AllocError` works with no new machinery** (item 7 below ŌĆö same-error-type propagation through the existing `?` rule, verified). **Codegen is item 8 (Phase 7), out of scope here:** the typechecker accepts the companions, so `karac build` reaches codegen ŌĆö both dispatch entries (`compile_method_call` instance, `compile_assoc_call` static) now **reject loudly** with an actionable "interpreter-only; lowering is item 8" message (the static path previously fell through to `compile_assoc_call`'s silent `Ok(const 0)` default ŌĆö a miscompile this guard closes). **Tests:** 10 interpreter (happy-path + user-method non-shadowing) + 9 typechecker (return-type shapes + `?`-propagation + scalar-mismatch rejection) + 3 effect (`allocates(Heap)` inferred/declared) + 2 codegen-guard (clean rejection, no link). All gates green incl. `--features llvm` (codegen 1433). **Deferred ŌĆö base operation does not exist yet** (each is its own future stdlib-floor slice; the companion lands when its base does): `Vec.try_insert` / `try_extend` / `try_reserve` / `try_reserve_exact` / `try_append` / `try_resize` / `try_from_iter` (no `Vec.insert`/`reserve`/`append`/`resize`/`from_iter`/`extend` base), `String.try_reserve` / `try_with_capacity`-reserve (no `String.reserve`), `Map`/`Set`/`SortedSet`/`VecDeque` `try_reserve` and `Map`/`Set` `try_with_capacity` (no path-form `Map.with_capacity`/`Set.with_capacity` constructor in the typechecker), and `Box`/`Rc`/`Arc.try_new` (no user-facing `Box.new`/`Rc.new`/`Arc.new` constructor ŌĆö Rc/Arc are minted by the auto-RC fallback, not an explicit constructor). **Residual caveat:** an instance `try_*` on a *non-identifier* receiver (e.g. `make_vec().try_push(x)`) re-evaluates the receiver once in the interpreter recursion ŌĆö harmless for the dominant place-expression receivers (shared `Arc` storage), a documented edge for temporaries (mutating a temporary is meaningless; cloning one double-evaluates). **Phase target:** Phase 8 (interpreter/typechecker/effect); codegen = item 8 (Phase 7).

[x] **Panicking-allocator rejection check (`E_PANICKING_ALLOC_REJECTED`) ŌĆö DONE 2026-06-09.** Under `panic_on_alloc_failure = false`, a dedicated post-typecheck pass (`src/typechecker/alloc_rejection.rs`, run from `check()` after `check_items`) walks every function/method/trait-default body and flags each panicking heap-allocating site against the fallible-allocation registry (`crate::fallible_alloc`): (a) **base alloc methods on a builtin collection** (`v.push` / `s.push_str` / `m.insert` / `.clone` / `q.push_back` / `v.extend_from_slice`) ŌåÆ fix-it points at the `try_*` companion; (b) **panicking constructors** (`Vec.with_capacity` / `VecDeque.with_capacity` / `String.with_capacity` / `Vec.from_slice`) ŌåÆ `try_*` companion; (c) **implicit-allocation lowering primitives** with no companion (a restructure hint): `[...]` Vec literal, `Vec[...]`/`Set[...]` prefix literal, `Map[k: v]` literal, `[v; n]` Vec repeat-literal, f-string interpolation, `String` `+` and `+=` concatenation. Each emits `error[E0264] (E_PANICKING_ALLOC_REJECTED): <subject> may panic on allocation failure; use \`<try_companion>\` instead under \`panic_on_alloc_failure = false\`` (companion form) or the build-it-explicitly restructure hint (no-companion form). **Why a dedicated source-AST walk, not inline emission during inference:** it sees the literal `try_push` / `try_with_capacity` source node and never flags the companion (the fix); and it is immune to the `check_expr`-vs-`infer_call` divergence an annotated `let v: Vec[i64] = Vec.with_capacity(8)` takes (the constructor isn't re-typed through `infer_call` in check mode). **Receiver-type recovery:** a `MethodCall`'s span equals its *receiver's* span, so `expr_types` at that span holds the method's *return* type, not the receiver's ŌĆö `infer_method_call` therefore records the builtin-collection receiver name keyed by the call span (`method_receiver_collections`, populated only under hard mode) for the pass to read. **Threading:** `TypeChecker` gained `profile_config` (`with_profile_config`, accepting `impl Into<ProfileConfig>` like the effect-checker leg) + `panics_on_alloc_failure()` gate; `Pipeline.typecheck` threads `Pipeline.profile_config` (realigned to the active profile) via the new `typecheck_with_lint_overrides_and_profile` entry (`typecheck_with_profile_config` is the override-free form for tests). New `TypeErrorKind::PanickingAllocRejected` ŌåÆ `E0264` (cli code map) ŌåÆ `OTHER` diagnostic class. **Deferred long-tail:** `Vec.collect` (no `try_collect` companion exists; flagging it leaves no fix) and derived-`clone`-body call sites (that is item 5, `E_DERIVE_CLONE_ALLOCATES`, which walks the *synthesized* clone). 13 typechecker tests (each registry site rejected + `try_*` accepted + default-mode allows all + non-allocating ops + user-method-named-`push` not flagged). All gates green (typechecker 1623ŌåÆ1636, clippy/fmt clean). **Phase target:** Phase 8 (typechecker pass; reads the item-3 manifest knob).

[x] **`#[derive(Clone)]` rejection under fallible-alloc (`E_DERIVE_CLONE_ALLOCATES`) ŌĆö DONE 2026-06-09.** Under `panic_on_alloc_failure = false`, `validate_derive_clone_allocates` (`src/typechecker/derives.rs`, run from `check()` after `build_type_env`) walks every `#[derive(Clone)]` struct/enum and, if its synthesized `clone` would reach a panicking allocator, rejects with `error[E0265] (E_DERIVE_CLONE_ALLOCATES): '#[derive(Clone)]' on type 'T' generates a 'clone' that may panic on allocation failure (field 'name' of type 'F' allocates); write a manual 'try_clone' method instead, or suppress with '#[allow(derive_clone_allocates)]' if you accept the panic`. **Allocation analysis** (`clone_allocates`): a field/variant-payload type clone-allocates if it is an owned heap collection (`Vec` / `String` / `Map` / `Set` / `VecDeque` / `SortedSet` / `Box`), transitively if it is a user struct/enum with such a field (cycle-guarded), or an `Option`/`Result`/tuple/array wrapping one; **not** for primitives, refs, or `Rc`/`Arc`/`Weak`/`shared` (clone is a refcount bump). The first allocating field/variant is named in the message. **Suppression** reads the type's `lint_overrides` for `#[allow(derive_clone_allocates)]` (per-type, not project-wide) ŌĆö **this fulfils item 9** (the lint is registered in `STARTER_LINTS` so the `#[allow]` is a recognised name, no `unknown_lint` warning). New `TypeErrorKind::DeriveCloneAllocates` ŌåÆ `E0265`. 7 typechecker tests (String/Vec field rejected + named, all-Copy allowed, enum String-payload rejected, transitive-field rejected, `#[allow]` suppresses, default-mode allows). All gates green (typechecker 1636ŌåÆ1643, clippy/fmt clean). **Phase target:** Phase 8.

[x] **Auto-RC fallback rejection (`E_RC_FALLBACK_ALLOCATES_UNDER_FALLIBLE_PROFILE`) ŌĆö DONE 2026-06-09.** Under `panic_on_alloc_failure = false`, `emit_rc_fallback_fallible_profile_errors` (`src/ownership/rc_promote.rs`, run from `check()` right after `emit_rc_fallback_notes` so the RcŌåÆArc promotion flavor is settled) iterates the existing `rc_values` records and converts each into a hard `error[E_RC_FALLBACK_ALLOCATES_UNDER_FALLIBLE_PROFILE]: auto-RC fallback for '<binding>' at this site emits '<Rc|Arc>.new(...)' which may panic on allocation failure; restructure to remove the fallback (a \`shared struct\`/\`shared enum\`, a lifetime adjustment, or an ownership reshape into a single ownership path) or use '<Rc|Arc>.try_new(...)?' with explicit '?'-propagation` ŌĆö the constructor is `Arc` for parallel-region-crossing (promoted) bindings, `Rc` otherwise. **No new dataflow** ŌĆö a pure profile-flag-gated transformation of the records the RC-fallback pass already produces. **Deliberately NOT suppressed by `#[allow(rc_fallback)]`:** accepting the RC for *performance* is a different decision than accepting an *OOM panic*, so every fallback site is reported regardless of the perf-note suppression set (the perf note remains separately suppressible). **Threading:** `OwnershipChecker` gained `panic_on_alloc_failure: bool` (`with_profile_config(impl Into<ProfileConfig>)`, defaulted `true`); `Pipeline.ownershipcheck` threads `Pipeline.profile_config` via the new `ownershipcheck_with_profile_config` entry.   7. [x] **`?`-propagation through `AllocError` ŌĆö VERIFIED 2026-06-09 (no new mechanism).** `AllocError` rides the standard `?` `From`-chain exactly like every other error type. Two legs verified: (a) **same error type** ŌĆö a fn returning `Result[T, AllocError]` propagates a `try_*` result's `AllocError` directly (`test_try_companion_question_propagates_alloc_error`, shipped with item 2); (b) **cross error type** ŌĆö a fn returning `Result[T, AppError]` with a user `impl From for AppError { fn from(e: AllocError) -> AppError { ŌĆ” } }` converts the propagated `AllocError` via the existing `find_from_impl` path (`test_question_alloc_error_converts_via_from_impl`), and the absence of that `impl` is rejected with the standard missing-`From` diagnostic (`test_question_alloc_error_without_from_impl_rejected`). No code change ŌĆö the `?` machinery (`typechecker/expr_ops.rs::infer_question`) already handled it; this entry is the regression-pinning verification. **Phase target:** Phase 8.

  - [x] **SURFACED + FIXED 2026-06-10 ŌĆö unit-payload variant constructor (`Ok(())` / `Some(())`) inferred an empty-tuple type instead of `Unit`.** Originally framed as a cross-error `?` + `Ok(())` quirk, but the real root cause was simpler and broader: the **empty-tuple literal `()`** inferred as `Type::Tuple(vec![])` (`typechecker/exprs.rs`, the `ExprKind::Tuple` arm), which `type_display`s identically to `()` but is **not** `types_compatible` with the `()` *type* (`Type::Unit`, what the `()` annotation lowers to). So **any** `fn f() -> Result[(), E] { Ok(()) }` / `fn g() -> Option[()] { Some(()) }` failed typecheck with the baffling `expected 'Result<(), E>', found 'Result<(), E>'` / `expected 'Option<()>', found 'Option<()>'` ŌĆö no `?` or cross-error needed (the rigid-`E` framing in the original note was a red herring: `TypeParam` is treated permissively, so the real mismatch was the `Tuple([])`-vs-`Unit` *payload*). **Fix:** the `ExprKind::Tuple` inference arm canonicalises the empty tuple to `Type::Unit` (unit *is* the empty tuple). 7 typechecker regression tests (bare `Ok(())`/`Some(())`, let-annotated, `()`-as-unit, `?`+`Ok(())` same- and cross-error, and the `try_*`+`?`+`Ok(())` fallible-alloc shape) + 1 codegen E2E (the newly-enabled `Ok(())`/`Some(())` build path compiles + runs). All gates green incl. `--features llvm`. **Phase target:** Phase 5.2 (typechecker inference).

       - [x] **`Vec.try_extend_from_slice` codegen ŌĆö DONE 2026-06-10.** Fallible `extend_from_slice`: the grow allocation goes through `karac_alloc_fallible`; a null result short-circuits to `Result.Err(AllocError.OutOfMemory{requested_bytes})` (shared `build_alloc_oom_result`), the success path returns `Result.Ok(())`.        - [x] **`try_with_capacity` codegen (`Vec` / `VecDeque` / `String`) ŌĆö DONE 2026-06-10.** All three fallible constructors codegen: reservation via `karac_alloc_fallible` (null ŌåÆ `Err(AllocError.OutOfMemory{bytes})`, success ŌåÆ `Ok({buf, len=0, cap=n})`), registered in `CODEGEN_FALLIBLE_STATIC`. `VecDeque` rides the Vec arm (shared `{ptr,len,cap}` storage + `pending_let_elem_type` element recovery); `String` reserves `n` bytes (`u8` element, no element recovery needed). **Element-type recovery** (the flagged blocker) solved at the typechecker: two check-mode `check_expr` adopt arms pin `T` for the match form (`let r: Result[Coll[T], _] = Coll.try_with_capacity(n)`) and the annotated `?`-form, covering Vec/VecDeque/String. **Prereqs fixed along the way** (both were base crashes ŌĆö B-2026-06-10-3, now resolved + deleted from bugs.md): (a) the *panicking* `VecDeque.with_capacity` / `String.with_capacity` had no codegen arm (fell through to `Ok(const 0)` ŌåÆ SIGTRAP) ŌĆö added both to `compile_assoc_call`; (b) a `VecDeque` payload bound out of an `Option`/`Result` via `match` was reconstructed with the 1-word default (the payload word-count / LLVM-type / dispatch-registration gates handled `Vec`/`String` but not `VecDeque`) ŌåÆ malformed value, free-time crash ŌĆö added `VecDeque` to all four gates (`control_flow_match.rs` ├Ś3 + `pattern_binding.rs`).          - [x] **FOLLOW-UP (surfaced here) ŌĆö `?` multi-word Ok-payload reconstruction ŌĆö DONE 2026-06-10.** Pre-existing general `?` codegen bug: the success path returned only the first payload word (`w0`), so a 3-word `Vec`/`String` (or 2-word `Slice`, small struct) lost its `len`/`cap` ŌåÆ malformed value, SIGTRAP on first use. Blocked every `?` on a multi-word Ok payload ŌĆö `Result[String, _]?`, `Result[Vec[T], _]?` (incl. `try_from_slice(src)?` shipped last slice), user `fn -> Result[String/Vec/tuple]` + `?`. Fixed in `compile_question` (`reconstruct_question_ok_payload`): recover the operand's Ok type from `string_typed_exprs` (String) / `enum_inst_type_exprs` (Vec/generic ŌĆö the `?` result type is recorded at the operand span) and rebuild all words via `rebuild_value_from_payload_words`. Scalar/pointer payloads keep `w0`. Verified: E2E (String / Vec via `?`) + ASAN (unwrapped heap value owned/freed once) + single-word `?` regression green.
       - [x] **`try_clone` codegen (Vec / VecDeque / String / Tuple-of-supported) ŌĆö DONE 2026-06-10.** `recv.try_clone()` lowers to `Result[Self, AllocError]` via a new **fallible clone fn family** (`emit_try_clone_fn_for_type_expr`, `src/codegen/clone_drop.rs`) ŌĆö the `i1`-returning mirror of `emit_clone_fn_for_type_expr`: signature `i1 karac_try_clone_<T>(*const T, *mut T, *mut i64)`, returns `true` on success / `false` after freeing any partial heap + storing the failed byte count through the out-param. Per-shape: **primitive** (memcpy, never fails), **String** (inlined fallible `len+1` buffer alloc, no panicking `karac_string_clone`), **Vec[T]** (fallible buffer + per-element recursion; on element-`i` failure drops the `[0..i)` already-cloned elements via the per-element drop fn (`emit_drop_fn_for_type_expr`, now live) + frees the buffer), **Tuple** (per-field recursion + static cleanup of `[0..i)`). Dispatch: `try_compile_try_clone` (`src/codegen/entry_chains.rs`) derives the receiver `TypeExpr` from the side-tables (shared `receiver_collection_type_expr`, extracted from `try_compile_clone`), emits dst + `failed`-bytes slots, calls the fallible fn, and phi-merges `Ok(cloned)` / `Err(AllocError.OutOfMemory{bytes})`. The cloned Vec/String (3-word) packs inline into the 5-word Result payload ŌĆö reuses the oversized-payload + multi-word `?` + match-binding reconstruction infra from items above. Registered `clone` in `CODEGEN_FALLIBLE_INSTANCE_BASES` (so the interpreter-only guard passes) + wired `method == "try_clone"` in `method_call.rs` next to `clone`. **Map/Set/SortedSet-bearing receivers deferred** ŌĆö their fallible clone needs a fallible `karac_map_*` runtime API (the **same blocker as `try_insert`**, item 8 / line 479); `try_compile_try_clone` rejects them loudly with the actionable item-8 message (`type_expr_try_clone_supported` gates the whole type tree). Verified: 6 codegen E2E (Vec[scalar] independence, String, Vec[String] deep, `?`-unwrap multiword, VecDeque, Vec[(i64,i64)] tuple) + 3 ASAN (Vec[String] deep independent-free, `?`-unwrap single-free, Vec[(i64,i64)] tuple) + the instance-companion reject test repointed to `Map.try_clone` (typechecker/interpreter already shipped, item 2). **Surfaced + filed (NOT a regression):** `Vec[(.., String)]` ŌĆö a Vec of tuple-with-heap-element ŌĆö UAFs in `karac_string_clone` under the *panicking* `.clone()` too (pre-existing deep-copy gap); filed as bugs.md B-2026-06-10-5; `try_clone` tuple coverage scoped to non-heap tuple fields until that lands. **Phase target:** Phase 7 codegen.
       - [x] **`Map.try_insert` / `Set.try_insert` codegen ŌĆö DONE 2026-07-09 (B-2026-07-09-15).** The prereq fallible `karac_map_*` runtime API shipped: `karac_map_try_insert(map, key, val, out_old_val, out_failed_bytes) -> i32` (`runtime/src/map.rs`), the fallible sibling of `karac_map_insert_old`. Growth is the *only* allocation an insert performs (the slot write is copy-only), so a new `KaracMap::try_resize` ŌĆö backed by `alloc_storage_fallible` (null-checks `alloc`, releases any partial, returns `None` on OOM) ŌĆö makes the whole op fallible while leaving the map **completely unchanged** on OOM (new storage is allocated *before* any `self` field is touched, so no rollback). Return code: `0` = fresh (`Ok(None)`), `1` = updated (`Ok(Some(old))`, old copied out), `2` = OOM (`Err(AllocError.OutOfMemory{*out_failed_bytes})`, map untouched). **Codegen:** `compile_map_method`'s `try_insert` arm (`src/codegen/maps.rs`) builds `Result[Option[V], AllocError]` ŌĆö reusing the panicking `insert` arm's `Option[V]` construction verbatim (`coerce_to_payload_words` + `build_option_some_via_phis`), wrapping it in `Result.Ok`, and branching to `build_alloc_oom_result` on status 2; `compile_set_method`'s `try_insert` arm builds `Result[bool, AllocError]` (`Ok(status==0)` ŌĆö Set lowers to `Map[T, ()]`, sharing the same runtime symbol). Mono maps use the SAME `#[repr(C)] KaracMap` struct, so the single generic runtime symbol covers `Map[i64,i64]` too ŌĆö the mono + borrowed-key fast paths are perf optimizations orthogonal to fallibility and are intentionally not mirrored. The heap-value/-key/-element no-adopt frees (duplicate-key/element buffer orphan, B-2026-06-20-9/12 siblings) are mirrored on the fallible path. Registered `insert` in `CODEGEN_FALLIBLE_INSTANCE_BASES` so the item-2 guard passes it to dispatch. **Verified:** 4 codegen E2E (`Map[i64,i64]` fresh/update/growth, `Map[i64,String]` heap-value Option packing, `Set[i64]`, `Map.try_insert?` propagation) byte-identical to the `karac run` interpreter oracle + 3 memory_sanitizer (heap-value overwrite move-out, heap-key duplicate no-adopt, `Set[String]` element duplicate no-adopt) green under **Linux ASAN+LSan** (`scripts/lsan-local.sh`), not just macOS ASAN + runtime unit test `try_insert_fresh_update_and_growth`. Gates: codegen 2116, memory_sanitizer, interpreter 1138, typechecker 1938, effect 388; fmt + clippy (--all-targets --features llvm) clean.
       - [x] **`SortedSet` codegen (incl. `SortedSet.try_insert`) ŌĆö DONE 2026-07-09 (B-2026-07-09-16).** `SortedSet[T]` now lowers under `karac build`: it shares `Set`'s `KaracMap`-backed storage (so `new`/`insert`/`contains`/`remove`/`len`/`is_empty`/`try_insert`/`union`/`intersection`/`difference` reuse `compile_set_method` verbatim ŌĆö this **unblocks the `SortedSet.try_insert` half of B-2026-07-09-15**), and observes keys in ASCENDING order at the iteration + `min`/`max` sites via a new `karac_map_sorted_keys(map, out_len, cmp_fn)` runtime helper (materializes a malloc'd, comparator-sorted copy of the keys). The comparator is a codegen-emitted `karac_sortcmp_<T>` (`emit_sorted_key_cmp_fn`, integer + `String` keys, mirroring `Vec.binary_search`); the `for`-loop walks the sorted buffer (element binding identical to the hash path ŌĆö a borrow-like alias, so `SortedSet[String]` carries over), and `min`/`max` read `buf[0]`/`buf[len-1]` and CLONE the heap element so the returned `Option[T]` owns its payload. Vars are marked in `sorted_collection_vars` (from the `SortedSet[T]` annotation) so plain `Set` is untouched. **Verified:** byte-identical to the `karac run` (`BTreeMap`) oracle for int + String (ascending for-loop, min/max, emptyŌåÆNone, dedup, `union`); 2 codegen E2E + 1 memory_sanitizer (String iter+min/max) green under **Linux ASAN+LSan**; codegen 2116, interpreter 1138, typechecker 1938, effect 388, fmt + clippy clean. **SCOPE:** `let`-bound `SortedSet` with integer/`String` elements. **Follow-ons (own leaf below):** derived-`Ord` struct/enum elements are rejected at `emit_sorted_key_cmp_fn` (interpreter-only for now); an INLINE set-op iterable (`for x in a.union(b)` without a `let`) is not yet marked sorted (the `let`-bound result is).
       - [x] **`SortedMap.*` codegen ŌĆö DONE 2026-07-09 (B-2026-07-09-17), the map sibling of `SortedSet`.** `SortedMap[K, V]` now lowers under `karac build`: registered in the map recognition helpers (`extract_map_kv_types` / `extract_map_key_name` / `map_kv_type_exprs` / `is_map_new_call` accept `SortedMap`) + marked in `sorted_collection_vars`, so it shares `Map`'s `KaracMap` storage ŌĆö `new`/`insert`/`get`/`get_or`/`contains_key`/`remove`/`len`/`is_empty`/`try_insert`/`entry` reuse `compile_map_method` verbatim (the `SortedMap.new` codegen reject at `call_dispatch.rs` is removed). The four ordered producers materialize ASCENDING key order via `karac_map_sorted_keys` + a per-key `karac_map_get`: `compile_sorted_map_kvg` (keys/values/entries ŌĆö `values` is emitted in KEY order, which cannot be post-sorted since it carries no key) and a sorted `for (k,v)` branch in `compile_for_map_var`. keys/values/entries DEEP-CLONE each half into the owned result `Vec` (owned-Vec contract, no aliasing the map's buffers); the `for`-loop binds borrow-like aliases and frees only the sorted-key scratch buffer. **Verified:** byte-identical to the `karac run` (`BTreeMap`) oracle for int + String keys (ascending keys/values/entries/for-(k,v), values-in-key-order, `try_insert`/`get`); 2 codegen E2E + 1 memory_sanitizer (`SortedMap[String,String]` keys+for-loop) green under **Linux ASAN+LSan**; the old interpreter-only guard test inverted to `test_sorted_map_codegen_now_compiles`; codegen 2119, interpreter 1138, typechecker 1938, effect 388, fmt + clippy clean. **SCOPE / follow-ons** (shared with `SortedSet`): integer/`String` keys (derived-`Ord` keys rejected at `emit_sorted_key_cmp_fn`, interpreter-only); INLINE producers without a `let` binding. **[self-hosting: NOT a prereq]** ŌĆö the compiler-in-K─üra uses neither `SortedMap` nor sorted iteration.

[x] **`#[allow(derive_clone_allocates)]` lint suppression ŌĆö DONE 2026-06-09 (with item 5).** `derive_clone_allocates` registered in `STARTER_LINTS` (`src/lints.rs`, `default_level: Deny` reflecting its error class) so `#[allow(derive_clone_allocates)]` is a recognised lint name (no `unknown_lint` warning), parallel to `rc_fallback`. The suppression is honoured per-type by `validate_derive_clone_allocates` reading the type declaration's `lint_overrides` for an `Allow` of this name (item 5) ŌĆö opt-in to "I accept the derived clone panicking on OOM here" at the type definition, not project-wide. Test: `test_hard_mode_derive_clone_allocates_suppressed_by_allow`. **Phase target:** Phase 8.

  **Test coverage** (typechecker + interpreter + codegen, Phase 8 stdlib + Phase 7 runtime). Positive ŌĆö under `panic_on_alloc_failure = true` (default), `Vec.push(42)` and `Vec.try_push(42)?` both type-check and run; `AllocError` is in the prelude scope without import; `try_with_capacity(usize.MAX)` returns `Err(AllocError.CapacityOverflow)`; `try_clone` available on every alloc-bearing collection. Under `panic_on_alloc_failure = false` ŌĆö `Vec.try_push(42)?` accepted; `Vec.push(42)` rejected with `E_PANICKING_ALLOC_REJECTED` and the fix-it; `s += other` on String rejected; `let v: Vec[i64] = [1, 2, 3]` collection literal rejected; `f"hello {name}"` rejected; `Box.new(x)` rejected; `let v: Vec[i64] = (0..1024).collect()` rejected; `#[derive(Clone)] struct S { v: Vec[i64] }` rejected with `E_DERIVE_CLONE_ALLOCATES`; auto-RC fallback site rejected with `E_RC_FALLBACK_ALLOCATES_UNDER_FALLIBLE_PROFILE`; same struct under `#[allow(derive_clone_allocates)]` accepted with the lint suppression visible in `karac query lint-suppressions`.   **Phase target:** Phase 8 (stdlib types + diagnostics + manifest flag); Phase 7 (runtime allocator wrapper). No P1 carve-out ŌĆö option (a) of v60 item 46 ships the full surface at v1; the optional future `#[derive(TryClone)]` companion derive (a sibling that produces fallible `try_clone`) is non-breaking-additive and is not on the v1 critical path.

- [ ] **`panic = "unwind" | "abort"` profile flag + per-profile defaults + abort-mode codegen ŌĆö unwind surface re-tiered to v1.x (2026-06-08; THIS is the single substrate home for the v1.x unwind block).** **SLICES 1ŌĆō2 DONE 2026-07-11.** SLICE 1 (manifest parse + defaults + validation): `src/manifest.rs` recognizes `[profile] panic = "unwind" | "abort"` ŌĆö a new `PanicStrategy { Unwind, Abort }` enum (parse/as_str), a typed `ProfileConfig.panic: Option<PanicStrategy>` field, and `ProfileConfig::panic_strategy()` (the effective value). An unknown value hard-errors via `InvalidFieldType` naming the valid set (the manifest layer's convention for invalid enum-value strings ŌĆö it carries no symbolic `E_` codes, so the spec's `E_INVALID_PANIC_STRATEGY` name is realized as that Display-formatted error, matching how an unknown `[package].profile` string is rejected). No `ProfileKnob` registered ŌĆö the strategy is meaningful under every profile, never moot. **v1 default correction:** `panic_strategy()` defaults **every** profile to `Abort` at v1 (not `default ŌåÆ unwind` as the spec's per-profile table lists). Per the re-tiering note below, v1 is abort-only and defaulting `app`/`lib` to `unwind` would reverse the binary-size win; the spec's `app ŌåÆ unwind` default is the *v1.x* end-state (the `default` arm flips to `Unwind` when slice 9 lands). SLICE 2 (threading + build gate): the codegen build path resolves the effective strategy (`manifest_panic_strategy_for` for single-file via the lazy manifest walk-up; `mf.profile_config.panic_strategy()` for project builds) and `reject_unsupported_panic_strategy` fails the build loudly on `Unwind` before codegen ŌĆö so an *explicit* `panic = "unwind"` (the only way to select it at v1) gets a clear "abort-only, v1.x feature" error instead of a broken build (structurally, codegen never emits invoke/landingpad, so unwind cannot be honored). The gate is `llvm`-gated (`karac run` has no abort/unwind distinction). SLICE 5 (`extern "C-unwind"` rejection under abort): the effect checker (`verify_extern_cunwind_requires_unwind_profile`) rejects every `"C-unwind"` site ŌĆö foreign-import declarations in `unsafe extern "C-unwind" { ŌĆ” }` blocks and K─üra `extern "C-unwind" fn` exports ŌĆö with `error[E_EXTERN_C_UNWIND_REQUIRES_UNWIND_PROFILE]` (E0415) when `panic_strategy() == Abort`. It runs at effect-check (so `karac check` catches it, not just build) and is strategy-driven, so it lifts automatically once a build can select `panic = "unwind"` (slice 9). It supersedes the E0413 "must declare `panics`" refinement under abort (`verify_extern_export_panics` returns early there), so a C-unwind export reports E0415 not E0413. The pre-existing codegen rejection (`src/codegen/functions.rs`, "requires the panic-unwind substrate") stays as the build-stopper defense-in-depth (native effect errors are non-fatal). The spec's "reject at parse" is realized at effect-check instead ŌĆö parse has no profile context. Existing C-unwind effect-inference / E0413 tests migrated to run under an explicit `panic = "unwind"` profile (new `effectcheck_with_profile_config` API + `effectcheck_ok_unwind` helper). `#[panic_handler]` (slice 7), the library-vs-binary advisory (slice 3), `catch_panic` rejection (slice 4), and the abort-vs-unwind *codegen* split (slice 9, the v1.x gate that flips the default + lifts these rejections) remain OPEN. Tests: 9 manifest unit tests + 2 CLI E2E (slice 2) + 4 new effect-checker tests (import/export rejected under abort, permitted under unwind, `extern "C"` untouched) + migrated C-unwind effect-default/E0413 tests (slice 5). Spec at `design.md ┬¦ Panic Strategy: panic = "unwind" | "abort"` (v60 item 47). The narrative spec already exists across 6+ scattered references in design.md; this entry consolidates the implementation work behind the new dedicated section. Slices: (1) **Manifest parsing.** `src/manifest.rs` recognizes `panic = "unwind" | "abort"` in `[profile]` blocks. **Prerequisite SHIPPED 2026-06-09 (the `[profile]`-table typed-knob + `ProfileConfig`-threading entry above the Fallible-allocation entry)** ŌĆö the `[profile]` table parser (`parse_profile_table`) now exists; add a recognized `panic` arm to its key loop (parse `"unwind"`/`"abort"`, else `E_INVALID_PANIC_STRATEGY`) and store it as a typed field on `ProfileConfig`. Default value is profile-dependent: `app`/`lib` ŌåÆ `unwind`; `embedded`/`kernel`/`isr`/`gpu` ŌåÆ `abort`. Custom profiles default to `unwind` unless explicitly set. Unknown values produce `error[E_INVALID_PANIC_STRATEGY]` naming the valid set. The setting is threaded through `Pipeline.profile` to the typechecker, effect checker, and codegen. (2) **Panic-strategy threading at compilation entry.** `Compilation.panic_strategy: PanicStrategy { Unwind, Abort }` field populated at pipeline init from the active profile. Available to every downstream phase via the existing `Pipeline` reference. (3) **Library-vs-binary advisory check.** When linking a library whose declared `panic` differs from the leaf binary's setting, emit `warning[W_PANIC_STRATEGY_MISMATCH]: package 'foo' declares panic = "...", this build uses panic = "..."` with the library's name and both settings. The library is recompiled under the binary's setting; the warning is informational. Detection happens at the build-system layer (`cmd_build_project`), not at the typechecker ŌĆö it requires multi-package context. (4) **`catch_panic` rejection under abort** ŌĆö already specced at `design.md ┬¦ Catching Panics`; the typechecker check that gates `catch_panic` calls reads `Compilation.panic_strategy` and rejects with `E_CATCH_PANIC_REQUIRES_UNWIND` under `Abort`. (5) **`extern "C-unwind"` rejection under abort** ŌĆö already specced at `design.md ┬¦ FFI`; both declarations and calls are rejected at parse with `E_EXTERN_C_UNWIND_REQUIRES_UNWIND_PROFILE` under `Abort`. (6) **Effect-checker pass ŌĆö drop-body panic-freedom enforcement** is unchanged (`Drop` body must be `panics`-free regardless of strategy; the existing rule already covers this). (7) **Custom panic handler attribute.** `#[panic_handler]` on a free function is recognized when `panic_handler = "custom"` is set in the active profile. The handler signature is fixed: `fn(info: ref PanicInfo) -> ()` (or `Never`). The handler must itself be `panics`-free (effect checker rejects otherwise ŌĆö same rule as `Drop`); under abort, it's the only user code that runs between panic site and termination. Multiple `#[panic_handler]` declarations across the project's source tree produce `error[E_DUPLICATE_PANIC_HANDLER]` naming all spans. Zero declarations + `panic_handler = "custom"` set produces `error[E_MISSING_PANIC_HANDLER]` with a fix-it skeleton. (8) **Default panic handler** ŌĆö when `panic_handler` is unset (the default), the runtime supplies a built-in handler. Under `unwind`, it walks the stack via the unwinder and writes the JSON crash report per `design.md ┬¦ Crash Report Format`. Under `abort`, it emits a single-`write(2)` line containing panic site, panic kind, and panic message to stderr, then calls `__kara_abort()`. Both are provided by `karac-runtime`. (9) **Codegen ŌĆö Phase 7.** Under `Compilation.panic_strategy = Unwind`, the existing LLVM `invoke` + personality + landingpad lowering applies (already part of the catch_panic / drop / RC-fallback / extern-C-unwind work). Under `Compilation.panic_strategy = Abort`, switch to plain `call` instructions and skip personality function attachment, skip cleanup landingpad emission, skip DWARF unwind-table emission (`.eh_frame`, `.gcc_except_table`). Panic-emitting primitives (`unwrap`, `expect`, index-OOB, divide-by-zero, explicit `panic()`) compile to `call __kara_panic_handler(info)` followed by `call __kara_abort()` (the latter marked `noreturn` so LLVM dead-code-eliminates everything past the panic site). RC decrements at scope exit are still emitted under abort (they happen on normal exit paths); the difference is they are not reached on panic paths because there is no unwind. (10) **Build-system ŌĆö link-time panic-strategy check.** When the build links a binary, verify all participating object files were compiled under the same `panic_strategy`; emit `error[E_PANIC_STRATEGY_LINK_MISMATCH]` if mismatched. This is a defensive check ŌĆö the per-binary-recompile rule should make mismatches impossible at v1, but the check guards against future ABI-stable library distribution. (11) **Manifest-flag interaction with `no_effects = ["panics"]`** ŌĆö when the active profile already forbids the panics effect, the `panic` setting still applies to runtime-internal panics (allocator failures from non-fallible code, double-panic on the abort path). Setting `panic = "unwind"` on a `no_effects = ["panics"]` profile is legal but unusual; emit a hint pointing out that user code cannot generate panics so the unwind tables are mostly dead weight. (12) **Composition with `panic_on_alloc_failure`.** The two flags are orthogonal; the typechecker pass for OOM rejection runs independently of the panic strategy. A profile setting both `panic = "abort"` and `panic_on_alloc_failure = false` is the canonical fault-tolerant-system shape. **Test coverage** (typechecker + manifest + codegen, Phase 7 + Phase 8): positive ŌĆö `panic = "abort"` parsed in `[profile]`; `panic = "unwind"` parsed; default for `app` profile is `unwind`; default for `embedded` is `abort`; default for `kernel` is `abort`; custom profile defaults to `unwind`; `[profile] name = "small_server" panic = "abort"` parses and applies; panic strategy threaded to typechecker; `#[panic_handler]` recognized; LLVM IR under unwind contains `invoke` + personality + landingpads; LLVM IR under abort contains plain `call` + no personality + no `.eh_frame`. Negative ŌĆö `panic = "fast"` rejected with `E_INVALID_PANIC_STRATEGY`; `catch_panic` under abort rejected with `E_CATCH_PANIC_REQUIRES_UNWIND` (existing test, verified still passes); `extern "C-unwind"` under abort rejected with `E_EXTERN_C_UNWIND_REQUIRES_UNWIND_PROFILE` (existing test, verified); two `#[panic_handler]` decls rejected with `E_DUPLICATE_PANIC_HANDLER`; missing handler with `panic_handler = "custom"` rejected with `E_MISSING_PANIC_HANDLER` and the fix-it; `#[panic_handler]` body that calls a `panics`-effect function rejected with the existing `panics`-in-handler diagnostic; library declaring `panic = "abort"` linked into `unwind` binary emits `W_PANIC_STRATEGY_MISMATCH` warning. Phase target: Phase 7 (codegen split ŌĆö invoke vs call, personality, landingpads, DWARF emission); Phase 8 (manifest parsing, profile defaults, threading, advisory warnings, `#[panic_handler]` attribute). **Tiering ŌĆö re-tiered 2026-06-08: the `unwind` surface is v1.x; v1 ships abort-only.** (Supersedes the prior "No P1 carve-out ŌĆö ships the full surface at v1" wording, which had drifted from reality per [`feedback_v1_ship_reality_not_promises`](../../CLAUDE.md).) v1's panic model is **abort** ŌĆö currently hardcoded (`[profile.release] panic = "abort"`, the "Phase 1 binary-size optimization" close-out in phase-7-codegen.md), not yet flag-driven. This entry's **`unwind` half ŌĆö the LLVM invoke/personality/landingpad codegen split (slice 9) plus its three consumers: `catch_panic[T]`, `extern "C-unwind"` export propagation (phase-6-runtime.md ┬¦ "Panic semantics at the FFI boundary", case 2), and `errdefer(e)` panic-path payload threading (phase-7-codegen.md ┬¦ "errdefer(e) binding: panic-path payload threading") ŌĆö is v1.x**, and this entry is the single substrate home for that block (the three consumers all light up from the same invoke/landingpad work). **Rationale:** it's a large cross-cutting codegen change (`call ŌåÆ invoke` + cleanup-on-landingpad at *every* call site) whose payoff ŌĆö C++-exception FFI + custom-scheduler panic recovery ŌĆö sits outside the v1 backend/concurrency/small-binary thesis; and defaulting `app`/`lib` to `unwind` reverses the binary-size win the launch leads with (the `.eh_frame`/unwind tables + the DWARF symbolizer come back). abort-only is a *principled* v1 stance (panics are bugs ŌåÆ recover via `Result`/`?`; design.md already frames `catch_panic` as "not a try/catch substitute"), and the loud `catch_panic` / `extern "C-unwind"` rejections are the correct interim posture. **Demand trigger, not wait** (per [`feedback_simulate_demand_dont_wait`](../../CLAUDE.md)): a flagship demo / kata that genuinely needs `catch_panic` or C++ interop pulls this into v1 ŌĆö simulate it with a kata first, then reconsider. The manifest-flag + abort-mode plumbing (slices 1ŌĆō8, 10ŌĆō12) may land at v1 independently if a profile needs explicit `panic` selection, but the **unwind codegen (slice 9) is the v1.x gate**. The cleanup-contract semantics under abort match Rust precedent and don't require a K─üra-specific cleanup-walk path.

- [x] **P0 ŌĆö Module-level `let` / `let mut` bindings ŌĆö implementation per design.md ┬¦1278-1330.** Slice 1 (parser surface) landed 2026-05-21; slice 3 (resolver) landed 2026-05-22; slice 4 (typechecker compile-time-constant initializer rule) landed 2026-05-22; slice 5 (typechecker binding-type inference + mutability check) landed 2026-05-22; slice 6 (effect-checker synthetic per-binding resources + `#[thread_local]` resource wrapping) landed 2026-05-22 ŌĆö the new `src/effectchecker/modbind_synth.rs` submodule owns the surface: `collect_module_let_mut_bindings` walks `program.items` once, capturing each `let mut BINDING`'s resource name (`<NAME>_resource` for the bare case, `ThreadLocal[<NAME>_resource]` when `#[thread_local]` is present per ┬¦1330) into a new `EffectChecker.modbind_let_mut: HashMap<String, ModBindingInfo>` field; immutable `let` bindings declare no synthetic resource and are skipped (reads remain free per ┬¦1322). `seed_modbind_synth_effects` seeds `inferred_effects` with a per-binding pair of synthetic callee keys (`__modbind_read.<NAME>` carrying `reads(<resource>)`, `__modbind_write.<NAME>` carrying `writes(<resource>)`) so the existing call-graph propagation machinery (`get_callee_effects` ŌåÆ `infer_function_effects`) carries the synthetic effect through callers without any change to the propagation logic. The body walker `collect_modbind_synth_calls_in_block` is a fresh shadow-aware traversal: a `ModBindingSynthWalker` maintains a `Vec<String>` shadow stack seeded with the function's parameter names, then pushes/pops as it enters `let` / `let-else` / `if-let` / `while-let` / `for` / `match-arm` / `closure-param` scopes ŌĆö a local binding of the same name as a module binding suppresses the synthetic attribution (mirrors the slice-5 typechecker behaviour where local shadow takes precedence over the module-binding LHS-mutability check). The walker treats bare `Identifier(name)` (and single-segment `Path { segments }`) as a read site; `Assign { target: Identifier(name), value }` is a pure write (no spurious read on the LHS) while `CompoundAssign { target: Identifier(name), value, .. }` contributes both reads and writes (`COUNTER += 1` is load+store at codegen). The walker is invoked from `infer_function_effects` after the existing `collect_calls_in_block`, and its synthetic call entries are merged into the shared `calls` vec ŌĆö the call-graph filter in `build_call_graph` naturally excludes them (the synthetic keys aren't in `all_fn_names`), so SCC detection and the polymorphic-callee classification remain unchanged. Per-binding granularity is preserved (`COUNTER_resource` and `FLAG_resource` are distinct resources ŌĆö two writers don't serialize against each other), and reader-writer-across-functions correctly produces the asymmetric effect sets that slice 7's par-block conflict rule will consume. `#[thread_local]` lands the resource wrapping at declaration time (the per-task disjoint-instance semantics per ┬¦1330; `Atomic[i64]`-vs-`#[thread_local]` is a user choice between shared-cell and per-task storage). Gpu-profile rejection of `#[thread_local]` per ┬¦1330 ("permitted in every profile except `gpu`") is **deferred until the `Gpu` variant of `CompileProfile` lands** ŌĆö the current enum has only `Default` / `Embedded` / `Kernel`, so there's no profile state to dispatch against; the rejection lives as a single-line `if profile == Gpu` site when the variant arrives. Slice 5's prior surface (env_build module-binding type registration + the ┬¦1284 `StringSlice` carve-out + the ┬¦1297 heap-`String` rejection + the immutability check) is unchanged. Slice 4's const-init structural walk + heap-`String` rejection on declared types are unchanged. Slice 2 (AST + formatter) was rolled into slice 1. **Slice 7** (par-block conflict rule ┬¦1328) landed 2026-05-22 ŌĆö `check_modbind_par_conflicts` runs as the final Phase B step in `effectchecker.rs::check()`. Each function/method body is walked via `collect_par_blocks_in_block` to find every `ExprKind::Par(block)` (nested par blocks included), and each par block's transitive effect set is computed via `collect_calls_in_block` + slice-6 `collect_modbind_synth_calls_in_block` ŌåÆ `get_callee_effects`. Any `writes(<resource>)` resolving (via the new `lookup_modbind_by_resource` helper) to an unwrapped `let mut` binding ŌĆö neither a concurrency primitive (root type-name match: `Atomic` / `Mutex` / `RwLock` / `Arc`, detected by the new `is_concurrency_primitive` flag on `ModBindingInfo` populated at collection time from the binding's `ty` AST) nor `#[thread_local]` (`ThreadLocal[<NAME>_resource]` resources are filtered by prefix ŌĆö per-task disjoint instances by construction never conflict) ŌĆö fires `error[E_MODULE_BINDING_WRITE_IN_PAR]` (code `E0408`) with the ┬¦1328 verbatim fix-it text (`wrap in Atomic[T], Mutex[T], or use #[thread_local] for per-task state`) and the binding-decl line embedded in the message (the secondary span lives in the message text ŌĆö adding a structured secondary span would require expanding the shared `EffectError` struct beyond slice 7's scope; the line-in-message form preserves the locator information). `ModBindingInfo` gained `decl_span` and `is_concurrency_primitive`. Deduplication: one diagnostic per offending binding per par block, not one per write site (two `COUNTER = ŌĆ”` writes in the same par block produce one error). Reader+reader stays legal (the rule fires on `writes` only); reader+writer cross-branch is caught via the writer branch's write; writer+writer fires once per offending binding (two distinct bindings ŌåÆ two diagnostics). **Known limitation (deferred):** the par-block check's synth walker doesn't track function-level local shadows introduced before the par block ŌĆö the slice-6 walker's shadow stack is per-walk, and the slice-7 sub-block walk starts fresh, so a function-local `let counter` declared before a `par { counter = 1; }` would spuriously over-attribute the synthetic write onto a module binding named `COUNTER`. Module bindings are Const-class (SCREAMING_SNAKE_CASE); local Const-class shadows are exotic in practice ŌĆö a focused follow-up if real-world code surfaces the corner case. Slice 6's prior surface (synthetic-resource attribution + `#[thread_local]` resource wrapping) is unchanged. **Slice 8** (`pub fn` synthetic-resource rejection ┬¦1326) landed 2026-05-22 ŌĆö `verify_pub_fn_no_synthetic_resource` runs as a new Phase-B step in `effectchecker.rs::check()`, right after `verify_declarations`. Only fires under `public_effects = "declared"`; iterates `function_bodies` + `method_bodies`, filters to `function_visibility[name] == true`, and walks each public function's inferred effect set looking for synthetic per-binding resources (decoded via the slice-7 `lookup_modbind_by_resource` helper). Each `(public fn, offending binding)` pair fires `error[E_PUB_FN_SYNTHETIC_RESOURCE]` (code `E0409`) with the ┬¦1326 verbatim escape-hatch text (the four concurrency primitives spelled out ŌĆö `Atomic[T]`, `Mutex[T]`, `RwLock[T]`, `Arc[shared struct S]` ŌĆö plus the `public_effects = "inferred"` project-level escape) and the binding's decl line embedded in the message. Concurrency-primitive escape (┬¦1326 path (a)): `is_concurrency_primitive` from slice 7's `ModBindingInfo` short-circuits the rejection so a `pub fn` against an `Atomic[i64]` / `Mutex[T]` / `RwLock[T]` / `Arc[...]` binding is accepted without further annotation. `#[thread_local]`: the `ThreadLocal[BINDING_resource]` resource is per-task disjoint by construction, so the public-boundary synchronisation concern doesn't apply ŌĆö `verify_pub_fn_no_synthetic_resource` filters those resources by prefix, matching the slice-7 pattern. `Inferred` policy escape (┬¦1326 path (b)): the entire pass returns early under `PublicEffectsPolicy::Inferred` ŌĆö synthetic effects continue to participate in conflict analysis (slice-7 par-block rule still fires), they just aren't declaration violations. Deduplication: `seen: HashSet<String>` keyed by binding name guarantees one diagnostic per `(function, binding)` pair, so a pub fn that both reads and writes the same binding produces one diagnostic, while a pub fn that touches two distinct synthetic bindings produces two. **Filter wiring in `verify_declarations`:** the new `EffectChecker::is_synthetic_modbind_resource(resource)` helper (sibling to `lookup_modbind_by_resource`) is threaded into all four arms of `verify_declarations` (Polymorphic / PolymorphicWithFixed / Explicit / None) so synthetic-modbind effects are skipped from the generic `MissingEffectDeclaration` / over-declared paths ŌĆö the "Add: writes(COUNTER_resource)" fix-it from the None arm would otherwise suggest a name the user cannot legally write in source. Slice 8's dedicated rejection owns those diagnostics end-to-end. The `EffectErrorKind::PubFnSyntheticResource` variant and the `E0409` JSON dispatch arm in `src/cli.rs` complete the wiring. 13 slice-8 tests in `tests/effectchecker.rs` cover: direct-write rejection, direct-read rejection (reads carry the synthetic resource just as writes do), transitive write via private callee, inferred-policy escape, `Atomic`/`Mutex`/`RwLock` concurrency-primitive escapes, `#[thread_local]` escape, immutable-`let` no-rejection, private-fn no-rejection, two-binding-two-diagnostic dedup, single-binding-reads+writes single-diagnostic dedup, no-double-fire-with-MissingEffectDeclaration, and pub-method (impl-block) coverage. **Slice 9** (codegen lowering) landed 2026-05-22 ŌĆö the new `src/codegen/module_bindings.rs` submodule owns the surface. `declare_module_bindings` runs once at the start of `compile_program` (after `Item::ConstDecl` collection, before any function compilation) and emits one LLVM global per `Item::ModuleBinding`: immutable `let X: T = INIT` ŌåÆ `@X = internal constant T INIT` (set via `set_constant(true)`); `let mut X: T = INIT` ŌåÆ `@X = internal global T INIT` (`set_constant(false)`); `#[thread_local]` attribute ŌåÆ `set_thread_local_mode(Some(GeneralDynamicTLSModel))` on the global (portable across ELF/Mach-O). Internal linkage on both shapes so the binding doesn't escape the translation unit. The `ModuleBindingInfo<'ctx> { global, llvm_ty, is_mut }` carrier lives in `Codegen.module_bindings: HashMap<String, ModuleBindingInfo>`. Initializer surface for v1: the primitive literal shapes (Integer / Float / Bool / Char / Byte) lower via the existing `const_int_for_suffix` / `const_float_for_suffix` / `bool_type().const_int` helpers; `StringLit` (with or without an explicit `StringSlice` annotation per ┬¦1284) lowers to a `(ptr, len, cap=0)` aggregate constant ŌĆö the byte payload becomes its own `internal constant` global named `modbind.str.<index>` so the runtime scope-exit cleanup never frees the static buffer (the `cap=0` marker is the same convention `Vec`/`String` literals use); `Unary { op: Neg, operand: Integer/Float }` is recursively unwrapped so negative-literal initialisers work. Composite initialisers (struct / enum / tuple / special-form constructors) return `None` from `module_binding_init` and are deferred to slice 10's wrapper-type coordination ŌĆö the typechecker (slice 4) already rejects shapes outside the permitted surface, so the codegen surface only needs to handle the shapes that reach it. **Identifier read path** in `compile_expr` Identifier arm gains a `try_load_module_binding(name)` short-circuit positioned AFTER the local-variable check (so local shadowing works) and BEFORE the `consts` / `try_unit_enum_variant` / external-function lookups ŌĆö when the name resolves to a module binding, `builder.build_load(info.llvm_ty, info.global.as_pointer_value(), "modbind.load")` returns the loaded `BasicValueEnum`. **Identifier write paths** in `StmtKind::Assign` and `StmtKind::CompoundAssign` gain a parallel `try_store_module_binding(name, val)` short-circuit that fires before the local-slot store; CompoundAssign also routes its load through `try_load_module_binding` because `load_variable` errors when the name has no entry in `self.variables`. The typechecker (slice 5) rejects writes to immutable bindings before codegen runs, and LLVM's `constant` global flag catches any missed case as a verifier error ŌĆö no silent corruption surface. 13 slice-9 codegen E2E tests in `tests/codegen.rs` cover: immutable-let read, let-mut read+write across functions, compound-assign (`+=` / `-=` / `*=`), StringSlice literal, `#[thread_local]` read+write, bool let-mut, float immutable-let, negated int literal, two independent let-mut bindings, write-then-read-from-callee global-state visibility, local-shadow precedence; plus 2 IR-shape tests that assert `@X = internal constant i64 100`, `@COUNTER = internal global i64 0`, and the `thread_local` keyword on the `#[thread_local]` global. **Slice 10** (cross-coordination + composite-initialiser codegen) landed 2026-05-22 ŌĆö the const-init special-form recognition was already wired in slice 4 (`module_binding_call_is_special_form` in `src/typechecker/items.rs` recognises `LazyLock.new(|| ŌĆ”)`, `OnceLock.new()`, `OnceCell.new()`, `Atomic.new(LITERAL)`, `Mutex.new(LITERAL)`); slice 10 reaudited the surface and confirmed no additional wiring was needed at the typechecker layer (the OnceLock/OnceCell entry directly below + the `Atomic[T]` / `Mutex[T]` entries elsewhere in this file own their own codegen-side const-init lowering when they ship ŌĆö the typechecker side is already permissive). The codegen composite-initialiser surface in `src/codegen/module_bindings.rs` gained the slice-10 forms: `ExprKind::Tuple` ŌåÆ anonymous struct constant (heterogeneous field types preserved via `context.const_struct`); `ExprKind::ArrayLiteral` ŌåÆ `[N x T]` constant via the `array_type_of` / `const_array_of` BasicTypeEnum-variant dispatchers (homogeneous element type re-validated at the value level so a typechecker miss surfaces as `None` rather than an LLVM panic); `ExprKind::RepeatLiteral { type_name, value, count }` ŌåÆ `[N x T]` constant with the element constant replicated, count-folded from an `Integer` literal (other shapes return `None`); `ExprKind::StructLiteral` ŌåÆ `struct_ty.const_named_struct` driven by `struct_types[Name]` + `struct_field_names[Name]` so source-order `{ b: ŌĆ”, a: ŌĆ” }` field listings land each value in the correct LLVM slot; `ExprKind::Path { segments: [EnumName, UnitVariant] }` ŌåÆ enum layout's struct constant with the tag in field 0 and the payload words zero-initialised (payload-bearing `EnumName.Variant(args)` deferred ŌĆö its word-stream encoder is builder-driven). The string-literal arm now serves nested positions as well (a `StringSlice` field inside a struct lowers through `modbind_string_slice_const`); the new helpers `array_type_of` / `const_array_of` / `basic_zero_const` dispatch over `BasicTypeEnum` variants so any element type the value-recursion produces (Int / Float / Bool / Pointer / Struct / Array) is supported uniformly. **Cross-function visibility fix:** `ModuleBindingInfo` gained a `declared_type: Option<TypeExpr>` field, and a new `reseed_module_binding_side_tables` helper re-registers `var_type_names` / `vec_elem_types` / etc. at the start of every function body (`compile_function` and `compile_mono_function` clear those tables per function ŌĆö module bindings live for the program's lifetime but their codegen-side registrations would otherwise be invisible inside function bodies). The path-expression dispatcher in `src/codegen/exprs.rs::compile_path_expr` gained a leading module-binding arm: `Path { segments: [BINDING, field] }` where `BINDING` resolves to a module binding routes to a `load + extractvalue` against the global (the parser emits `CFG.field` as a 2-segment Path because the leading segment is Const-class; without this arm the access would have fallen through to the enum unit-variant path's silent-`0` placeholder). The Array fast path in `src/codegen/collections.rs::compile_index` gained a fall-back from the local-variable lookup to `self.module_bindings.get(name)` so `ARR[0]` against a module-bound `Array[T, N]` uses the global's pointer + `llvm_ty` for the GEP. **Remaining (deferred, non-blocking):** the `#[thread_local]` gpu-profile rejection still waits on `CompileProfile::Gpu` (the current enum has only `Default` / `Embedded` / `Kernel`); the par-block-walker function-level-shadow tracking still waits on a real-world surface for the corner case; codegen lowering for the special-form constructors (`LazyLock.new` / `OnceLock.new` / `OnceCell.new` / `Atomic.new` / `Mutex.new`) lands under each wrapper type's own codegen entry (typechecker accepts them; codegen returns `None` from `module_binding_init` for now, deferring to those entries). 9 slice-10 codegen tests in `tests/codegen.rs` cover: struct literal field access, source-order != declaration-order field listings, fixed-size array literal indexed read, repeat literal with summed access, enum unit-variant match against two distinct modules bindings, struct with negative-int field via `Unary { Neg }` recursion; plus 2 IR-shape tests asserting `@CORNER = internal constant { i64, i64 } { i64 3, i64 7 }` and `@ARR = internal constant [3 x i64]`. Spec is already complete in design.md and (post-slice-5) the parser + resolver + typechecker accept the form; the effect-checker / par-block / codegen wiring is the remaining gap. Surfaced 2026-05-21 by backend-kata probes (see `wip-todo-api-kata.md ┬¦ Decisions log 2026-05-21` for the empirical write-up ŌĆö every approach to shared mutable state across HTTP handler calls bottoms out at the same parser rejection, and the existing corpus (`examples/parallax/`, `examples/elevator/`) uses only `const` at module scope, so this work also has no regression baseline beyond `const`). **Why P0 v1:** the OnceLock/OnceCell entry directly below and the `LazyLock` / `Mutex` / `Atomic` / `Arc[shared struct S]` primitives (each their own existing or implied stdlib entry) all declare as `let X: LazyLock[T] = LazyLock.new(...)` at module scope and are unbuildable until module-level `let` works; the synthetic-per-binding effect resources at ┬¦1322 are core to the v1 effect system and feed conflict analysis (Feature 2) for any code touching global state; every backend kata in `kara-katas/PLAN.md` axes 1-3 (backend-service, CLI, systems / data-pipeline) needs at least one of these surfaces; and embedded-profile MMIO / DMA / hardware-register patterns per ┬¦1320 ("primarily intended for embedded and bare-metal code") have no alternative. Slices: (1) **Parser** ŌĆö replace `src/parser/items.rs:1439 reject_top_level_let`'s hard-rejection with a real module-binding parse arm. Accept `[ATTRIBUTES] [VIS] let [mut] IDENT [: TYPE] = CONST_EXPR ;` at item position, reusing the existing statement-form `let`-binding parser for the body shape but treating the result as an `Item::ModuleBinding { name, mutable, vis, attributes, ty: Option<Type>, init: Expr, span }` rather than a `Stmt::Let`. The `parse_const_expr` machinery already used by `Item::Const` parses the RHS. Item-recovery: same skip-to-next-item dance the current hard-reject uses, so a malformed module binding doesn't poison downstream item parsing. (2) **AST + formatter** ŌĆö `Item::ModuleBinding` with fields above; formatter emits `[attrs] [pub] let [mut] NAME[: TYPE] = INIT;` with the same one-space-around-`=` convention as `const`. (3) **Resolver** ŌĆö register the binding's identifier in the Const-class namespace per design.md ┬¦273 + ┬¦300; enforce that the identifier matches the Const-class naming convention (all-caps with optional digits and underscores) and emit `error[E_MODULE_BINDING_NAMING]` naming the offending identifier if a lowercase form is used (parallels the existing const-naming check). Visibility forms (`pub`, `pub(crate)`, default-private) round-trip per the existing rules; module bindings participate in import resolution exactly like consts. Shadowing within a module is rejected at parse ŌĆö same identifier declared twice at module scope is `E_DUPLICATE_MODULE_BINDING`. (4) **Compile-time-constant initializer rule** per design.md ┬¦1280-1297 ŌĆö new typechecker pass that walks the `init` expression and rejects if any sub-expression requires runtime evaluation. Permitted forms: literals of any primitive type (with the ┬¦1284 rule that string literals have type `StringSlice` at module scope rather than the function-body default `String` ŌĆö `String` itself is heap-allocated and forbidden per ┬¦1297); references to other module-level bindings (same module or imported); arithmetic, boolean, and comparison ops applied to permitted forms; struct constructors whose every field is a permitted form; enum variant constructors whose every payload is a permitted form; tuple / fixed-size array literals over permitted forms; the compiler-recognized constant-init special forms `LazyLock.new(|| ...)`, `OnceLock.new()`, `OnceCell.new()`, `Atomic.new(LITERAL)`, `Mutex.new(LITERAL)` ŌĆö recognized at the path-call dispatch in a way parallel to today's `LazyLock.new` recognition (see entry directly below for the OnceLock/OnceCell side). Rejected: any function call that is not a recognized special form; any method call; any allocator-touching construct including bare `Vec.new()` / `Map.new()` / `Set.new()` / `String.from` (use `LazyLock[Vec[T]]` etc. as the ┬¦1297 work-around); effectful calls per ┬¦1309 ŌĆö emit `error[E_MODULE_BINDING_EFFECTFUL_INIT]: module-level binding initializer cannot carry effects ('NAME' carries 'effect_set')` with the offending sub-expression's span. (5) **Typechecker ŌĆö binding type inference and mutability check** ŌĆö when `: TYPE` is absent, infer from `init`; reject reassignment of immutable `let` bindings via the existing assignment-LHS check extended to recognize module-scope `let` (versus `let mut`). (6) **Effect-checker ŌĆö synthetic per-binding resources** per design.md ┬¦1322. For every module-level `let mut BINDING` (immutable `let` declares no synthetic resource ŌĆö there's nothing to write), declare an internal `effect resource BINDING_resource;` that is not exportable and not nameable in user source. Read sites contribute `reads(BINDING_resource)` to the enclosing function's inferred effect set; assignment sites contribute `writes(BINDING_resource)`. The synthetic resource participates in normal conflict analysis: `reads` + `reads` is non-conflict, `reads` + `writes` is conflict, `writes` + `writes` is conflict. The per-binding granularity (not a single `GlobalModule` bucket) is deliberate per the design ŌĆö otherwise every module-level mutation serializes against every other. **`#[thread_local]` variant** per ┬¦1330: when the binding carries `#[thread_local]`, the synthetic resource is `ThreadLocal[BINDING_resource]` (a parameterized resource that never conflicts with itself across tasks because each task holds a disjoint instance). Reject `#[thread_local]` under the `gpu` profile (no thread-local execution-model analog). (7) **Par-block conflict rule** per design.md ┬¦1328 ŌĆö extend the existing `par { }` checker so any branch whose transitive effect set contains `writes(BINDING_resource)` for a `let mut BINDING` whose type is not an explicit concurrency primitive (`Atomic[T]`, `Mutex[T]`, `RwLock[T]`, `Arc[shared struct S]`) is rejected with `error[E_MODULE_BINDING_WRITE_IN_PAR]: module-level let mut 'BINDING' cannot be written from inside par { } ŌĆö wrap in Atomic[T], Mutex[T], or use #[thread_local] for per-task state` with the par-block span and the binding-decl span both labeled. Reader-reader across branches stays legal; reader-writer across branches is rejected by the existing conflict analysis once the synthetic resource is in the effect sets. The diagnostic copies the fix-it from ┬¦1328 verbatim. (8) **`pub fn` and synthetic resource** per design.md ┬¦1326 ŌĆö a `pub fn` that directly mutates a module-level `let mut` cannot satisfy `public_effects = "declared"` because the synthetic resource is not nameable in the public declaration. Two supported paths: (a) wrap the binding in a named concurrency primitive (`Atomic[T]`, `Mutex[T]`, `RwLock[T]`, `Arc[shared struct S]`) and declare effects on those well-known resources at the public surface; (b) `public_effects = "inferred"` at the project level (the `embedded`-profile device-driver escape hatch) ŌĆö the synthetic resource is then displayed in `karac explain` output but does not need to appear in the declaration. Diagnostic at the `pub fn` decl when the function's inferred effect set contains a `writes(SYNTH_resource)` and the project is on `public_effects = "declared"`: `error[E_PUB_FN_SYNTHETIC_RESOURCE]: pub fn 'NAME' writes module-level 'BINDING' whose synthetic resource cannot appear in a declared effect set ŌĆö wrap 'BINDING' in Atomic/Mutex/RwLock/Arc[shared struct], or switch the project to public_effects = "inferred"` with the function decl + binding decl spans both labeled and the two fix-its enumerated in the help. (9) **Codegen** ŌĆö lower immutable module-level `let X: T = INIT;` to an LLVM `@X = internal constant T INIT` global with the appropriate constant initializer for the permitted-form expression tree (literal ŌåÆ LLVM constant; struct constructor ŌåÆ LLVM struct constant; etc.). Lower `let mut X: T = INIT;` to `@X = internal global T INIT`. The synthetic-resource analysis from slice (6) does not change codegen ŌĆö it lives in the effect system only. `#[thread_local]` lowers to an LLVM `thread_local` global with the platform-appropriate TLS model. Reads in function bodies lower to LLVM `load`; writes lower to LLVM `store`. The compiler-recognized special-form initializers (`LazyLock.new(|| ...)`, `OnceLock.new()`, etc.) emit the runtime-side cell representation per the existing/forthcoming stdlib entries ŌĆö coordinate with the OnceLock/OnceCell entry below so the closure-as-function-pointer storage for `LazyLock.new(|| ...)`'s initializer fits the synthetic-resource model. (10) **Cross-coordination with `OnceLock`/`OnceCell`/`LazyLock`/`Mutex`/`Atomic` entries** ŌĆö the slice that wires the const-init permitted-special-forms list to the compiler-recognized constructors is the touch point with the entry directly below (and with the `Atomic[T]` / `Mutex[T]` / `RwLock[T]` entries elsewhere in this file once they're filed). Land slice (1)-(5) first as the parser-through-typechecker foundation; (6)-(8) as the effect-system layer; (9) as the codegen layer; (10) as the integration with the wrapper-type entries. **Test coverage**: positive ŌĆö `let MAX: i64 = 100;` parses, resolves, type-checks, lowers; `let mut COUNTER: i64 = 0;` + free-fn that increments + read at module scope works end-to-end (a single binary that prints the incremented counter); `let GREETING: StringSlice = "hello";` works (StringSlice type, no heap allocation); `let mut TODOS: LazyLock[Mutex[Vec[Todo]]] = LazyLock.new(|| Mutex.new(Vec.new()));` parses + resolves once the wrapper-type entries land; `#[thread_local] let mut TLS_COUNTER: i64 = 0;` parses + emits as thread-local + non-conflicting across tasks; `pub fn bump() { COUNTER = COUNTER + 1; }` accepted under `public_effects = "inferred"`, rejected under `"declared"`; reader+reader across `par { }` branches accepted; reader+writer rejected. Negative ŌĆö `let mut V: Vec[i64] = Vec.new();` rejected with `E_MODULE_BINDING_EFFECTFUL_INIT` (or the heap-allocation rejection diagnostic ŌĆö final code name to be decided during impl); `let mut S: String = "x".to_owned();` rejected per ┬¦1297; `let mut N: i64 = compute();` rejected because `compute()` is not a recognized special form; immutable `let X: i64 = 0; ... X = 1;` rejected at the assignment site with the existing immutable-reassignment diagnostic; same-name `let mut X` declared twice at module scope rejected with `E_DUPLICATE_MODULE_BINDING`; lowercase identifier `let mut counter: i64 = 0;` rejected with `E_MODULE_BINDING_NAMING`; `writes(COUNTER_resource)` from inside a `par { }` branch when `COUNTER: i64` (not wrapped) rejected with `E_MODULE_BINDING_WRITE_IN_PAR`; `pub fn bump()` under `"declared"` with no concurrency wrapper rejected with `E_PUB_FN_SYNTHETIC_RESOURCE`; `#[thread_local]` under the `gpu` profile rejected with `E_THREAD_LOCAL_INVALID_PROFILE`. **Probe fixtures already on disk** at `/tmp/kara-probes/q1_module_let_mut.kara`, `q1c_const_mut.kara`, `q3_module_vec.kara`, `q4_lazylock.kara` ŌĆö minimal regression seeds for slices (1)-(4). Phase target: 5.2 (parser, AST, resolver ŌĆö slices 1-3); Phase 3 (typechecker + effect-checker ŌĆö slices 4-8); Phase 7 (codegen ŌĆö slice 9); Phase 8 (stdlib coordination ŌĆö slice 10). Cross-reference: design.md ┬¦1278-1330 (spec); ┬¦1322 (synthetic-resource rule); ┬¦1328 (par-block conflict rule); ┬¦1330 (`#[thread_local]`); ┬¦1343 (`LazyLock`); ┬¦1374 (`OnceLock`); `src/parser/items.rs:1439 reject_top_level_let` (current hard-reject ŌĆö replaced by slice 1); `examples/parallax/bench/kara/server.kara` + `examples/elevator.kara` (existing `const`-only corpus ŌĆö regression baseline); `kara-katas/PLAN.md` Priority 1 (backend-service kata that needs this); entry directly below (`OnceLock`/`OnceCell`) and `LazyLock`/`Mutex`/`Atomic` entries (downstream consumers of the const-init special-form recognition); `wip-todo-api-kata.md ┬¦ Decisions log 2026-05-21` (probe results that surfaced this gap).

- [x] **`Vec.new()` / `VecDeque.new()` as module-binding const-init.** First wrapper-type follow-on to the ┬¦1278-1330 umbrella above ŌĆö the slice-10 doc-comment listed these as deferred ("wait on the wrapper-type entries"). Landed 2026-05-22 at `d92f3da` as a focused two-edit slice: (1) `src/typechecker/items.rs::module_binding_call_is_special_form` gained a `"Vec" | "VecDeque" => args.is_empty()` arm alongside the existing `OnceLock` / `OnceCell` / `Atomic` / `Mutex` arms, and the `E_MODULE_BINDING_EFFECTFUL_INIT` diagnostic message gained the two new forms in its enumeration; (2) `src/codegen/module_bindings.rs::modbind_init_from_value` gained an `ExprKind::Call { callee, args } if args.is_empty()` arm delegating to a new `modbind_empty_vec_const` helper that recognises 2-segment Path callees `Vec.new()` / `VecDeque.new()` and emits LLVM `const_struct({ptr null, i64 0, i64 0})` matching `vec_struct_type` ŌĆö the runtime invariant for an empty Vec (`{ptr=null, len=0, cap=0}` per `assoc_call.rs:1256`'s shared `Vec/VecDeque && method == "new"` arm). LLVM prints this aggregate as `zeroinitializer`. No heap allocation needed; the value is a true compile-time constant. `Map.new()` was investigated and explicitly excluded ŌĆö the runtime calls `karac_map_new` to install hash seeds, so it can't be a compile-time constant. Filed as the `Map.new()` / `Set.new()` module-binding entry directly below (different mechanism ŌĆö static-init prologue rather than const struct). Regression tests: `tests/typechecker.rs::test_module_binding_vec_new_init_accepted` (positive ŌĆö Vec.new(), VecDeque.new(), immutable form); `tests/typechecker.rs::test_module_binding_vec_new_with_args_rejected` (negative ŌĆö `Vec.new(1)` still rejected); `tests/codegen.rs::test_ir_modbind_vec_new_emits_empty_aggregate` + `test_ir_modbind_vecdeque_new_emits_empty_aggregate` (IR shape pins).
