The old `test_module_binding_vec_new_init_rejected` was flipped to the positive case. **Why P1 v1:** the ┬¦1278-1330 umbrella ships without a way to declare an empty growable global Vec ŌĆö every backend kata in `kara-katas/PLAN.md` axis 1 (backend-service) needs at least an in-memory store pattern, and `LazyLock[Vec[T]]` adds ceremony that visibly weakens the Go-comparison story. Cross-reference: design.md ┬¦1278-1330 (umbrella); `src/codegen/assoc_call.rs:1256` (Vec.new() runtime lowering); umbrella entry directly above (slice-10 deferral note); the uppercase-receiver method dispatch entry directly below (remaining kata blocker); `wip-todo-api-kata.md ┬¦ Blockers` (kata's blockers list).

- [x] **Uppercase-receiver method dispatch ŌĆö typechecker + lowering + codegen rewrite.** Pre-existing latent bug surfaced 2026-05-22 while probing the kata's planned shape `let mut TODOS: Vec[Todo] = Vec.new(); TODOS.push(t)`. The parser at `src/parser/exprs.rs:1298-1326` greedily consumes Path segments after an uppercase-leading identifier followed by `.`, producing `Call(Path([TODOS, push]))` instead of `MethodCall(TODOS, push)`. The parser comment is explicit about the intent ("Type/Const-class idents (uppercase leading) root a path here; Value-class idents fall through to the postfix loop") but the parser can't tell at parse time whether the leading segment is a type or a value binding. Affected ANY uppercase receiver: `let F: Foo = Foo { value: 5 }; F.double()` failed identically to `TODOS.push(1)` with the misleading diagnostic `type 'Foo' is not callable`. Landed 2026-05-22 at `f41a62c` via three coordinated edits: (1) **Typechecker dispatch** in `src/typechecker/expr_call.rs::infer_call` ŌĆö top-of-function arm detects `Call(Path([first, method], None))` with `first` resolving as a value binding (new `path_first_segment_is_value_binding` predicate: local-scope hit OR `env.constants` hit that is not also a known type name; locals shadow types unconditionally per Kara design), constructs a synthetic `Identifier(first)` receiver, and routes through `infer_method_call`. The call span is inserted into the new `path_call_method_dispatch: HashSet<SpanKey>` side-table on `TypeCheckResult`. (2) **Lowering rewrite** in `src/lowering.rs::try_rewrite`'s Call arm ŌĆö `rewrite_path_call_to_method_call` (tried before `rewrite_bare_assoc_fn_call`) consults the side-table and mutates the AST node from `Call { callee: Path([X, method]), args }` to `MethodCall { object: Identifier(X), method, args }`. Downstream phases see the uniform method-call shape with no further special-casing. (3) **Codegen sibling block** in `src/codegen/method_call.rs::compile_method_call` ŌĆö when the Identifier receiver is in `module_bindings` but not `variables`, dispatch through the same `compile_vec_method` / `compile_map_method` / `compile_set_method` paths a local Vec/Map/Set would use; `src/codegen.rs::get_data_ptr` gains a module-binding fall-back returning the global's pointer (matching the existing `collections.rs::compile_index` fall-back from slice 10). Effect / ownership / interpreter need no changes ŌĆö after lowering they see `MethodCall(Identifier(X), ...)`. The `db573a4` `Type.method()` rejection ordering is preserved by the predicate's "not a known type name" guard: `Vec.new()`, `String.from(x)`, and similar Type-associated calls continue to route through `resolve_path_type` because `Vec` / `String` are in `PRELUDE_TYPES` / `env.structs`. 7 regression tests: `tests/typechecker.rs::test_uppercase_local_method_dispatch`, `test_uppercase_modbind_vec_method_dispatch` (the kata's exact shape), `test_uppercase_modbind_const_method_dispatch`, `test_vec_new_type_assoc_call_still_resolves` (negative guard against the rewrite shadowing Type-associated calls), `test_unknown_type_method_rejection_still_fires` (negative guard against regressing `db573a4`); `tests/codegen.rs::test_e2e_modbind_vec_push_then_len` (full end-to-end pin: 3 pushes + len through the rewrite path produces `3\n`), `test_e2e_modbind_vec_indexed_read`, `test_e2e_uppercase_local_struct_method`. Closes the backend kata's Slice 4 blocker ŌĆö the kata's planned `let mut TODOS: Vec[Todo] = Vec.new(); TODOS.push(t)` shape now compiles and runs correctly. **Why P0 v1:** without this fix, the Vec.new() module-init entry immediately above was unusable ŌĆö the global compiled but no method call on it worked. Every backend kata in `kara-katas/PLAN.md` axes 1-3 needing module-level state shared this blocker. **Known limitation (deferred):** field access on uppercase locals (`let F: Foo = ...; let x: i64 = F.value;`) is still broken for the same parser-greedy-Path reason ŌĆö `resolve_path_type` for `Path([F, value])` returns the type of `F` (Foo) instead of the type of the field. Codegen has its own correct path so the field access works end-to-end in compiled binaries (proven by slice-10's `test_e2e_modbind_struct_literal`), but the typechecker disagrees with codegen on the field's type, and `karac build` exits on the typecheck error. Vec is empty-struct so the kata's Slice 4 doesn't need field access. Filed as the sibling-half "Uppercase-receiver field access" entry directly below. Cross-reference: `src/parser/exprs.rs:1298-1326` (greedy path-consumption site, kept as-is); `src/typechecker/expr_call.rs::infer_call` + `src/typechecker/expr_ops.rs::path_first_segment_is_value_binding` (dispatch); `src/lowering.rs::rewrite_path_call_to_method_call` (AST mutation); `src/codegen/method_call.rs` (module-binding dispatch); `src/codegen.rs::get_data_ptr` (module-binding pointer fall-back); the Vec.new() entry directly above (slice 4 unblock half 1); `wip-todo-api-kata.md` (kata's planned shape ŌĆö now buildable).

- [x] **`Vec[a, b, c]` literal codegen ŌĆö `PrefixCollectionLiteral` compile arm.** Landed 2026-05-22 at `540cd8c`. New `compile_vec_prefix_literal` helper in `src/codegen/collections.rs`: empty `Vec[]` ŌåÆ `{null, 0, 0}` aggregate (matches Vec.new()); non-empty malloc `items.len() * sizeof(elem)` + per-slot GEP store + return `{buf, len, len}` (cap-equals-len; first push triggers grow). Wired from `compile_expr`'s newly-added `ExprKind::PrefixCollectionLiteral { type_name: "Vec", items }` arm. Set / Map prefix literals fall through to the default arm unchanged ŌĆö separate slices when corpus surfaces the need. 3 regression tests in `tests/codegen.rs`: standalone literal + indexed reads, literal-as-enum-payload (`Json.Array(Vec[a, b])`), and post-construction `push` triggering grow. Original P1. Surfaced 2026-05-22 while shipping the backend TODO API kata Slice 4. Updated 2026-05-22 after deeper investigation in the gap-fixes follow-up worktree: the bug is broader than originally framed. `ExprKind::PrefixCollectionLiteral` (the AST node the parser produces for `Vec[a, b]` / `Set[a, b]`) is recognized by the parser, the typechecker, the interpreter, and `src/lowering.rs` (where `Array[...]` lowers to `ArrayLiteral` but Vec/Set/Map prefix forms stay as-is for codegen) ŌĆö but `src/codegen/exprs.rs::compile_expr` has NO arm for it. It falls through to the default `_ => Ok(i64 0)` at line 345, producing a zero value where a Vec struct should be. This affects every use site, not just enum-variant payloads: `let xs: Vec[i64] = Vec[1, 2, 3];` builds cleanly but produces a null Vec at runtime; `Json.Array(Vec[...])` lands the same null in the variant payload, hence the `stringify()` ŌåÆ `[]` output. The original entry mistakenly blamed enum-variant payload composition; the real root cause is the missing `PrefixCollectionLiteral` codegen arm in `compile_expr`. Slice plan: (1) add a `compile_prefix_collection_literal(type_name, items)` helper in `src/codegen/collections.rs` that, for `type_name == "Vec"`, allocates a heap buffer sized for `items.len() * sizeof(elem)`, stores each item, and returns the `{ptr, len, cap}` Vec struct. (2) Wire it from `compile_expr`'s `ExprKind::PrefixCollectionLiteral { type_name, items }` arm. (3) Set / Map prefix literal codegen can follow in a sibling slice if the kata corpus surfaces a need (Map literal already has its own `compile_map_literal_stmt` at the let-stmt level ŌĆö generalize to a Map prefix expression at the same time). Element-type inference comes from the enclosing expected-type carrier (`Json.Array(Vec[...])` knows the elem is `Json` from the variant's payload signature) ŌĆö likely consult the typechecker's `expr_types` side-table on the literal's span, OR thread an expected-type parameter through `compile_expr`. (4) Move-semantics: the elements are moved into the heap buffer; the buffer's lifetime joins the resulting Vec value's lifetime ŌĆö `track_vec_var` for let-bindings, but for transient enum-payload composition the parent value's drop machinery owns it. **Workaround in v1:** explicit `Vec.new() + .push(...)` for every site. The TODO API kata uses this inline at every JSON-building site and notes it in its README. **Why P1 v1:** every kata or production workload that builds a JSON-shaped tree (or any Vec-payloaded enum) is forced into the verbose explicit form. Cross-reference: `src/codegen/exprs.rs::compile_expr` (the missing arm ŌĆö line 345 default fires); `src/lowering.rs:261-275` (ArrayŌåÆArrayLiteral canonicalization, Vec/Set/Map stay PrefixCollectionLiteral); `src/codegen/collections.rs::compile_array_literal` (the precedent for fixed-size arrays ŌĆö Vec needs heap-alloc instead of stack-alloc); `kara-katas/backend/todo-api/main.kara` (the inline workaround sites); `runtime/stdlib/json.kara` (`Json.Array` / `Json.Object` variant declarations).

- [x] **Field-receiver method GEP through a `ref T` parameter.** Landed 2026-05-22 at `32f52d2`. Root cause was narrower than the original "helper-function Json returns empty / crashes silently" framing: codegen's field-receiver method dispatch in `src/codegen/calls.rs` (`outer.field.method(...)` shape) was using `slot.ptr` directly as the GEP base for plain (non-shared) struct receivers. For `ref T` parameters the slot is an `alloca ptr` holding a pointer to the struct, not the struct itself ŌĆö the GEP indexed into the alloca's first 8 bytes (the stored pointer value) and read junk past it. The bad `{ptr, len, cap}` triple for a String field was then passed to `karac_clone_String`, which dereferenced and segfaulted silently. Fix: when the variable is a ref param (`self.ref_params.contains_key(outer_name)`), load the pointer first to recover the struct's address ŌĆö mirrors the existing shared-struct handle-load pattern in the same site, just extended to the ref-param case. Regression test `tests/codegen.rs::test_e2e_field_receiver_method_through_ref_param` pins the kata's exact helper shape (`fn todo_to_json(t: ref Todo) -> Json` with `t.title.clone()` embedded in a returned Json.Object). Original P2.

- [x] **`Vec.remove(idx)` codegen + typechecker arm.** Landed 2026-05-22 at `4de2e8e`. `compile_vec_method` had no `"remove"` arm ŌĆö fell through to the default `_ => i64 0` so `xs.remove(i)` silently no-op[']d. Fix in two coordinated edits: typechecker arm in `src/typechecker/expr_method_call.rs::infer_method_call` next to the pop / pop_front family, returning T for `Vec[T]` / `VecDeque[T]` receivers with i64 idx (v1 contract matches Rust ŌĆö UB on OOB); codegen arm in `src/codegen/vec_method.rs` mirroring pop_front[']s load + memmove + len-- but at an arbitrary index. 4 regression tests in `tests/codegen.rs` cover middle / head / tail removal and the module-bound Vec receiver. Original P1.

- [x] **Enum-payload bool narrowing ŌĆö `match Json.Bool(b) => b`.** Landed 2026-05-22 at `11ca0e1`. The enum-payload bool is encoded as i64 in the word stream; codegen now inserts a `trunc i64 ŌåÆ i1` at pattern-bind reconstruction when the binding[']s typechecker-recorded type is `"bool"`. Two coordinated edits: typechecker `bind_pattern_types` + `check_pattern_against` Binding arm record `"bool"` in `pattern_binding_types` for `Type::Bool`; codegen `control_flow_match.rs::reconstruct_payload_value` single-word arm narrows to i1 when the recorded type is `"bool"`. Regression test `test_e2e_enum_payload_bool_narrowing` covers Json.Bool(true), Json.Bool(false), and the default-arm Json.Number fall-through. Original P2.

- [x] **Uppercase-receiver field access ŌĆö typechecker `resolve_path_type` walk.** P1 v1. Sibling-half of the shipped uppercase-receiver method-dispatch entry directly above.

    **DONE (2026-06-22).** Landed, but the original "typechecker-only, single focused arm" scoping below was **wrong** ŌĆö verified empirically with probe programs before committing. Reality: codegen's `compile_path_expr` only handled the `len()==2` *module-binding* arm (`CFG.max` Ō£ō), and silently returned the `i64 0` placeholder for **local** roots (`F.value` ŌåÆ 0) and **nested** paths (`OUTER.inner.field` ŌåÆ 0); the **tree-walk interpreter** had no Path field-access rule at all and errored at runtime. A typechecker-only change would have traded a loud typecheck error for a *silent wrong answer* under `karac build` and a runtime error under `karac run`. The complete fix spans three phases: **(1) Typechecker** (`src/typechecker/expr_ops.rs::resolve_path_type`) ŌĆö generalized to walk a value-binding-rooted path of *any* length Ōēź2 (`segments[0]` a value binding via the reused `path_first_segment_is_value_binding` predicate; fold each trailing segment through `env.structs[..].fields`, firing the ordinary `UndefinedField` diagnostic on a miss, falling through for non-struct intermediates). **(2) Interpreter** (`src/interpreter/eval_expr.rs` `ExprKind::Path` arm) ŌĆö added a struct-rooted walk via the shared `read_field` helper; handles local uppercase bindings (`karac run` now matches `karac build`). NB: module-level `let` bindings are unsupported interpreter-wide (bare `let c = CFG;` already panics), so module-binding field access stays codegen-only ŌĆö pre-existing, out of scope. **(3) Codegen** (`src/codegen/exprs.rs::compile_path_expr`) ŌĆö generalized the module-binding-only/2-segment arm to any value-binding root (local *or* module binding) of any length by synthesizing the equivalent `Identifier`-rooted nested `FieldAccess` chain and reusing `compile_expr` (so it inherits the full field-access machinery + type recovery). Tests: typechecker positive/nested/negative (`test_uppercase_*` in `tests/typechecker.rs`); interpreter local + nested (`tests/interpreter.rs`); codegen e2e `test_e2e_modbind_struct_field_read_annotated` (asserts the typecheck gate is clean ŌĆö the `run_program` harness ignores typecheck errors ŌĆö AND the binary prints `64 7 9`). Full suites green: typechecker 1749, interpreter 982, codegen 1747, memory_sanitizer 347; clippy + fmt clean. Original (mis-scoped) plan retained below for the historical record.

    Sibling-half of the shipped uppercase-receiver method-dispatch entry directly above. Same parser-greedy-Path root cause at `src/parser/exprs.rs:1298-1326`: `let F: Foo = Foo { value: 5 }; let x: i64 = F.value;` parses `F.value` as `Path([F, value])`, then `resolve_path_type` for the 2-segment path falls through to `resolve_identifier_type("F")` and returns `Foo` (the value's type) instead of walking the path to resolve the field's type as `i64`. Symptom is `expected 'i64', found 'Foo'` at any annotated binding (or downstream `println()` Display-mismatch when there's no annotation ŌĆö what slice 10's `test_e2e_modbind_struct_literal` would have surfaced if the test pipeline didn't bypass typecheck-fatal-error gating). Codegen has its own correct path (`compile_path_expr`'s `Path([BINDING, field])` arm against `module_bindings`), so compiled binaries produce the right value ŌĆö the slice-10 test passes vacuously through `run_program_capturing_inner` which doesn't honour typecheck errors. But `karac build` from the CLI exits on the typecheck error, so users see the wall. Slice plan: (1) **Extend `path_first_segment_is_value_binding`** (already added for the method-dispatch entry) into a richer `resolve_path_type_for_value_first_segment` helper, or add a sibling arm in `resolve_path_type` directly. When `segments.len() == 2` and `segments[0]` is a value binding (the same predicate the method-dispatch rewrite uses), look up the binding's type, then resolve `segments[1]` as a field of that type. For a struct receiver, consult `env.structs[name].fields` for the matching `(name, ty)` pair and return the field's type. For non-struct receivers (tuple, primitive, etc.), fall through to the existing diagnostic path. (2) **Ordering against the method-dispatch rewrite** ŌĆö the method-dispatch arm in `infer_call` already covers Call(Path) shapes; this new arm covers bare-Path shapes (field access has no `(args)` suffix). The two are disjoint by callee context. (3) **No codegen changes needed** ŌĆö the slice-10 codegen path already handles `Path([BINDING, field])` correctly via `compile_path_expr`'s module-binding arm. The fix is typechecker-only. (4) **No lowering rewrite needed** ŌĆö unlike method-dispatch, field access doesn't need an AST rewrite; the typechecker just needs to compute the right type. Downstream phases see the same Path AST. **Test coverage**: positive ŌĆö `let mut CFG: Config = Config { max: 64, count: 7 }; let m: i64 = CFG.max; let c: i64 = CFG.count;` accepted; `let F: Foo = Foo { value: 5 }; let x: i64 = F.value;` (local) accepted; nested `OUTER.inner.field` walks through both segments. Negative ŌĆö `let CFG: Config = ...; let _: i64 = CFG.nonexistent;` fires the existing `NoSuchField` diagnostic on the value's type (not "type 'Config' is not ..." misdirection). Regression ŌĆö `Vec.new()` field-of-type access (none exists today but the codepath must not regress) still routes through `resolve_path_type`'s associated-fn dispatch unchanged. **Why P1 v1:** unblocks every backend / CLI kata that uses a non-empty struct module binding (config singletons, in-memory caches with named fields, registry structs); the Vec.new() entry above ships the empty-struct case, this entry ships the non-empty case. No workload in `kara-katas/PLAN.md` Priority 1 needs it today (the TODO API uses Vec, which is empty-struct), but a half-dozen backend / CLI shapes that would naturally surface as v1 demos use it. Phase target: Phase 3 (typechecker only ŌĆö single focused arm). Cross-reference: `src/parser/exprs.rs:1298-1326` (greedy path-consumption ŌĆö unchanged); `src/typechecker/expr_ops.rs::resolve_path_type` lines 366-370 (the identifier-fallback site that drops the trailing segments); `src/typechecker/expr_ops.rs::path_first_segment_is_value_binding` (the predicate already in place from slice b ŌĆö reuse); `src/codegen/exprs.rs::compile_path_expr` (the correct codegen path that today silently disagrees with the typechecker); the uppercase-receiver method-dispatch entry directly above (sibling half, shipped); `tests/codegen.rs::test_e2e_modbind_struct_literal` (the slice-10 test that already exercises the codegen path ŌĆö extend with a `karac build` smoke test once typechecker agrees).

- [x] **`Map.new()` / `Set.new()` as module-binding initialisers.** P1 v1. Wrapper-type follow-on to the Vec.new() module-init entry ŌĆö the slice-a rationale (kata corpus needs in-memory store patterns at module scope) applies identically to Map and Set, which are even more common shapes for backend services (config maps, in-memory KV caches, intern tables). Unlike Vec, Map's runtime invariant is NOT a zero-shaped aggregate: `runtime/src/map.rs::karac_map_new` installs per-instance hash seeds and vtable function pointers before any operation on the map can run, so the empty-Map value isn't `zeroinitializer` ŌĆö it's whatever shape `karac_map_new` returns. (`Set[T]` reuses the same runtime via `karac_map_new` with `val_size = 0` per `src/codegen/stmts.rs::compile_set_new_stmt`.) Two mechanism options: **(a) Static-init prologue.** At codegen time, emit a synthesised `__karac_static_init` function that runs before `main`'s body and writes each `Map.new()` / `Set.new()` module-binding's runtime initialiser. Mirrors the C++ `__attribute__((constructor))` shape. The const-init permitted-special-forms list in `module_binding_call_is_special_form` (typechecker) gains `Map.new()` / `Set.new()` arms; the codegen module-binding emission produces a `zeroinitializer` placeholder global; a separate prologue pass walks `module_bindings`, emits per-binding `karac_map_new(...)` calls into the prologue, and wires the prologue to run before `main` (LLVM `@llvm.global_ctors` array, or a synthesised explicit call from `main`'s entry block ŌĆö the latter is simpler and avoids the global-ctors-ordering question). **(b) LazyLock-style deferred init.** `Map.new()` / `Set.new()` const-init recognises the form, codegen emits a `LazyLock[Map[K,V]]`-shaped wrapper that initialises on first access. Requires `LazyLock[T]` codegen to be in place (currently deferred per the module-binding-umbrella entry's slice-10 narrative). (a) is the right v1 call ŌĆö LazyLock isn't shipped yet and adding it as a transitive dep here would add scope; static-init prologue is a contained codegen extension and the runtime cost (one global ctor call per Map binding at startup) is negligible. Slice plan: (1) **Probe** ŌĆö confirm whether any pre-existing static-init machinery exists in the codegen (search for `global_ctors` / `__karac_init` / similar). The `KARAC_SPAWN_SITES` global pattern at codegen-program-end is the closest precedent. (2) **Typechecker** ŌĆö add `Map.new()` / `Set.new()` to `module_binding_call_is_special_form` in `src/typechecker/items.rs` alongside the existing `Vec` / `VecDeque` arm. Update the diagnostic enumeration to name them. (3) **Codegen** ŌĆö emit the placeholder `zeroinitializer` global at `module_bindings.rs::modbind_init_from_value` for `Map.new()` / `Set.new()` (reuse the LLVM struct type the existing local-binding `compile_map_new_stmt` / `compile_set_new_stmt` produces; map's layout is in `src/codegen/maps.rs` ŌĆö find or define the shared type accessor). (4) **Static-init prologue** ŌĆö synthesise an `__karac_static_init` LLVM function that runs each Map/Set module binding's runtime initialiser. Inject a call to it from `main`'s entry block (simplest) or via `@llvm.global_ctors`. (5) **Method dispatch** ŌĆö the uppercase-receiver method-dispatch entry directly above already covers `REGISTRY.insert(k, v)` / `REGISTRY.get(k)` for module-binding receivers via the codegen module-binding sibling block in `compile_method_call`; no additional method-dispatch work is needed. **Test coverage**: positive ŌĆö `let mut REGISTRY: Map[String, i64] = Map.new(); fn main() { REGISTRY.insert("a", 1); println(REGISTRY.get("a").unwrap_or(0)); }` end-to-end; same for `Set[T]`. Negative ŌĆö `Map.new(1)` continues to be rejected (zero-arg only); `Map.with_capacity(n)` rejected (not a permitted const-init form ŌĆö would need its own arm); runtime init runs exactly once per binding. Regression ŌĆö local `let m: Map[K, V] = Map.new();` inside a function continues to use the existing per-statement codegen path unchanged. **Why P1 v1:** every backend kata in `kara-katas/PLAN.md` axes 1-2 (backend, CLI) needing keyed state shares this need; config maps and in-memory caches are the canonical shape; the Vec.new() entry above ships the ordered-list case, this entry ships the keyed case. Phase target: Phase 3 (typechecker) + Phase 7 (codegen + static-init prologue). Cross-reference: `runtime/src/map.rs::karac_map_new` (the runtime initialiser that has to run); `src/codegen/stmts.rs::compile_map_new_stmt` + `compile_set_new_stmt` (the local-binding codegen paths to mirror at the prologue); `src/typechecker/items.rs::module_binding_call_is_special_form` (where the typechecker arms land); the Vec.new() module-binding entry directly above (the precedent slice ŌĆö same shape, simpler runtime); the uppercase-receiver method-dispatch entry directly above (covers the consumer side ŌĆö method calls on the global Map work for free once init lands). **[self-hosting prereq ŌåÆ [phase-12](phase-12-self-hosting.md#pre-pivot-blockers-fix-before)]** ŌĆö module-scope intern tables / symbol maps in the compiler.
    **DONE (2026-06-23).** Mechanism (a) ŌĆö static-init prologue ŌĆö shipped, taking the "synthesised explicit call from `main`'s entry block" branch (NOT `@llvm.global_ctors`, which the hot-swap table already owns as the single permitted module-level ctor; main-entry injection sidesteps the one-ctor-per-module + ordering question entirely). (1) **Probe**: the `@llvm.global_ctors` precedent does exist (`finalize_hot_swap_table` registers `__karac_init_hot_swap_table` before `main`), but a second global of that name can't coexist, so the simpler main-entry call was used. (2) **Typechecker**: `module_binding_call_is_special_form` (`src/typechecker/items.rs`) gains a `"Map" | "Set" => args.is_empty()` arm; `reject_module_binding_init`'s enumeration names them. (3+4) **Codegen**: corrected from the original spec ŌĆö a Map/Set binding is NOT a value-struct `zeroinitializer`, it's an opaque `ptr` HANDLE (`karac_map_new` returns a pointer), so `declare_module_bindings` emits a placeholder **`null` `ptr`** global (always non-constant ŌĆö the prologue writes it once, even for immutable `let`), records `(name, is_set)` in `map_set_module_inits`, and declares `__karac_static_init` (signature only). `main`'s entry emits a forward `call void @__karac_static_init()` (after `di_enter_function`, so it carries a `!dbg` loc under `-g`); `finalize_module_binding_static_init` fills the body after all bodies compile ŌĆö per binding it reseeds the key/val side tables via `register_var_from_type_expr(declared_type)`, builds the handle via the new shared `build_map_new_handle(var_name, is_set)` (factored out of `compile_map_new_stmt`/`compile_set_new_stmt`, reused by both local and module paths), and stores it into the global. The handle is **never freed** ŌĆö a module binding lives for the whole process, and stays reachable through the global at exit (LSan-clean; not a leak). `#[thread_local]` is intentionally not honored for Map/Set inits (the prologue inits only the main thread's instance ŌĆö out of scope for the floor). (5) **Method dispatch** ŌĆö the consumer-side claim was WRONG: `get_data_ptr` already resolves module-binding globals, but every Map/Set handle-read path (`compile_map_method`, `compile_set_method`, map index-store/index-read, `compile_map_keys_values`, both `for`-loop sites) had a redundant `self.variables`-only existence precheck that rejected globals before `get_data_ptr` ran. All seven prechecks removed (the `get_data_ptr` gate right after emits the identical error and is module-binding aware). Tests: typechecker (`test_module_binding_map_set_new_{init_accepted,with_args_rejected}`); codegen E2E (`test_e2e_modbind_{map_new_insert_and_get,map_new_int_keys,set_new_insert_and_contains,two_distinct_maps_independent}` ŌĆö each asserts the typecheck gate is clean AND the binary output); memory-sanitizer (`asan_module_scope_map_string_keys_no_double_free` ŌĆö heap String keys under the never-freed static-init handle). Interpreter path unchanged: `karac run` has no module-binding support at all (`Item::ModuleBinding` is codegen-only), so this is a `karac build` feature, matching the Phase 3 + Phase 7 target.

- [ ] **`OnceLock[T]` and `OnceCell[T]` lazy-init primitives.** Spec at `design.md ┬¦ Module-Level Bindings > LazyLock[T] / OnceLock[T] / OnceCell[T]` (v60 item 45).

    **INTERPRETER + TYPECHECKER SLICE LANDED (2026-06-22).** The full Phase-8 surface ships interpreter-only (codegen sub-item 9 stays deferred, like `Pool[T]` / `Arena[T]` / `Interner`); only `[ ]` below is the Phase-7 codegen lowering. Shipped: a baked `runtime/stdlib/once.kara` declares `OnceLock[=T]` / `OnceCell[=T]` / `AlreadySetError[=T]` with `#[compiler_builtin]` placeholder bodies (registered via `PRELUDE_TYPES` + `STDLIB_SOURCES`, signatures auto-registered through `register_baked_stdlib` ŌĆö so **no hand-written `infer_once_lock_method` / `infer_once_cell_method`** were needed, unlike sub-item 4's plan; the baked impl signatures *are* the typechecker contract). **Representation deviation from sub-items 2ŌĆō3:** rather than new `Value::OnceLock`/`Value::OnceCell` variants, the cells use the established handle + side-table pattern ŌĆö the K─üra value carries only `handle_id`, the write-once slot (`Option<Value>`) lives in the interpreter's `once_table` (single table for both types; the cross-task/single-task split is a typecheck-time structural guarantee, not a runtime one, so the tree-walk interpreter needs no `Arc<Mutex>` vs `Rc<RefCell>` distinction). `set`/`get`/`get_or_init`/`is_set` dispatch through `try_eval_once_method`; `get_or_init` runs the init closure via `invoke_zero_arg_closure` only when empty (closure fires at most once). `AlreadySetError[T]` ships as a **struct** (`{ rejected: T }`) not an enum ŌĆö matches the `AlreadySetError { rejected: val }` construction syntax sub-items 3/5 use. Sub-item 6 (const-init recognition) was **already present** for both ctors. **Effect deviation from sub-item 8:** the cell methods seed **no** substrate effect ŌĆö an empty cell is a const-init constant (no allocation) and `set` parks an already-built value (interior mutation), so unlike `Arena.new`/`Interner.intern` nothing is seeded; `get_or_init`'s closure effects propagate through the ordinary closure-arg walk. Structural enforcement (sub-item 7): **(a)** `E_ONCE_CELL_AT_MODULE_SCOPE` + **(b)** `E_ONCE_CELL_IN_PAR_TYPE` added (both walk the surface `TypeExpr` tree via a new `type_expr_mentions_type` helper, so nested `Map[String, OnceCell[i64]]` is caught; codes live in the message, `TypeErrorKind` reuses `CrossTaskUnsafeCapture` / `ParFieldNotConcurrent`); **(c)** the cross-task-boundary rule **already fired** via the pre-existing `cross_task_safe.rs` escape pass (reported as `E_NOT_CROSS_TASK` with the `OnceCellToLock` fix-it) the moment the type existed ŌĆö no new dataflow pass. **Bonus compiler fix:** the value-receiver generic-dispatch path now pre-binds an impl's generic params from the receiver's concrete type args (mirroring the concrete-type UFCS path), so `get_or_init(init: Fn() -> T) -> ref T` resolves `T` from the receiver `OnceLock[i64]` instead of failing "cannot infer T" ŌĆö brings it to parity with `Arena.get` (residual `ref i64`ŌåÆ`i64` deref-at-binding warning is the shared pre-existing ref-return limitation). Tests: 7 interpreter + 6 typechecker (3 reject + OnceLock-ok at module scope / par field / general) + 2 effectchecker (no-substrate-effect + closure-alloc propagation). Full non-LLVM suite green; codegen suite unaffected; fmt + clippy clean. Commits `70de730b` (core), `e77fe7df` (structural enforcement). Original 9-slice plan retained below for the historical record.

    Spec at `design.md ┬¦ Module-Level Bindings > LazyLock[T] / OnceLock[T] / OnceCell[T]` (v60 item 45). Ship alongside the existing `LazyLock[T]` (already specced; unchanged by this entry). Both new primitives carry the same method surface ŌĆö `new`, `set(val) -> Result[(), AlreadySetError[T]]`, `get() -> Option[ref T]`, `get_or_init(\|\| ...) -> ref T`, `is_set() -> bool` ŌĆö so a type swap between the two is mechanical. The structural difference is single-task vs. cross-task safety, enforced through three explicit rules on `OnceCell[T]` rather than a `Sync` auto-trait. Slices: (1) **Stdlib types.** `OnceLock[T]` and `OnceCell[T]` registered in `PRELUDE_TYPES` + `stub_generics(["T"])` in `prelude.rs` and as generic structs in `register_builtin_types`. `OnceLock.new()` and `OnceCell.new()` wired into the path-call dispatch (parallel to the existing `LazyLock.new` recognition). (2) **Interpreter values.** `Value::OnceLock(Arc<Mutex<Option<Value>>>)` and `Value::OnceCell(Rc<RefCell<Option<Value>>>)` ŌĆö the difference is `Arc<Mutex<...>>` vs. `Rc<RefCell<...>>` to mirror the cross-task vs. single-task split (Rust-host implementation; the language-level guarantee is the structural-rule check, the interpreter implementation just needs to be racy-safe enough not to panic on the cross-task path). (3) **Method surface implementation.** `set` returns `Ok(())` on first call, `Err(AlreadySetError { rejected: val })` on subsequent calls; `get` returns the cached value via `Option`; `get_or_init` wraps both into a single race-safe call (for `OnceLock`, the lock is acquired once; if another task's `set` races, the loser's constructed value is dropped without invoking the closure twice). (4) **Typechecker dispatch.** `infer_once_lock_method` and `infer_once_cell_method` added; dispatch wired in `infer_method_call` on `Type::Named { name: "OnceLock" \| "OnceCell" }`. Methods carry no effects beyond the invocation closure's effects (which propagate through `get_or_init`'s closure type per existing trait-method effect-checking rules). (5) **`AlreadySetError[T]`** registered as a prelude error type in the typechecker (`enum AlreadySetError[T] { rejected: T }`). Conditional `Display` impl gated on `T: Display` follows the existing conditional-impl pattern. Always implements `Debug`. (6) **`OnceLock` constant-init recognition.** `OnceLock.new()` is added to the compiler-recognized constant-init special forms alongside `LazyLock.new` so it's permitted as a module-level binding's right-hand side without violating the constant-initializer rule (the ctor produces a fresh empty cell with no captured runtime state ŌĆö the same property `LazyLock.new` already has). (7) **Single-task structural enforcement** (three new diagnostics targeting `OnceCell[T]` use sites): (a) **`E_ONCE_CELL_AT_MODULE_SCOPE`** ŌĆö typechecker check at module-level binding registration: if the declared type contains `OnceCell[T]` anywhere in its tree, reject with `error[E_ONCE_CELL_AT_MODULE_SCOPE]: 'OnceCell[T]' is single-task; module-level bindings are visible to every task and must be 'OnceLock[T]' instead` and a fix-it suggesting the type swap. (b) **`E_ONCE_CELL_IN_PAR_TYPE`** ŌĆö typechecker check at `par struct` / `par enum` field type validation (the existing pass that already rejects single-task types in `par struct` fields gains `OnceCell[T]` to its rejected-type set): `error[E_ONCE_CELL_IN_PAR_TYPE]: 'OnceCell[T]' is single-task; fields of 'par struct'/'par enum' must be 'OnceLock[T]' instead` with the offending field's span and the type-swap fix-it. `shared struct` fields accept `OnceCell[T]` (per design.md ŌĆö `shared struct` itself is single-task). (c) **`E_ONCE_CELL_CROSSES_TASK_BOUNDARY`** ŌĆö par-region escape analysis: when an owned binding of type `OnceCell[T]` is consumed by a `par {}` branch, a `spawn()` argument, or a `Sender[OnceCell[T]].send` call, reject with `error[E_ONCE_CELL_CROSSES_TASK_BOUNDARY]: 'OnceCell[T]' cannot cross task boundaries; replace with 'OnceLock[T]' or move the surrounding owned struct's task-local clone into the branch instead`. The check piggybacks on the existing par-region escape pass that already rejects raw `Rc[T]` from crossing into a `par {}` branch ŌĆö no new dataflow pass is needed; the check adds `OnceCell` to the existing rejected-type set keyed off the type-name. (8) **Effect attribution.** First-access initialization (whether through `set` or `get_or_init`) is attributed to the *calling* function, not to the binding ŌĆö same rule that already applies to `LazyLock`. The closure passed to `get_or_init` has its own effect set checked at the call site against the calling function's ceiling (existing trait-method effect-check machinery). (9) **Codegen.** Phase 7 work ŌĆö both primitives lower to small heap-allocated structs (the `Once` synchronization primitive already exists in `karac-runtime` for `LazyLock`'s use; `OnceLock` reuses it; `OnceCell` is just an `Option<T>` with interior mutability). The existing `karac-runtime` `Once` API gains `set`/`get`/`get_or_init` entry points. **Test coverage** (interpreter + typechecker, Phase 8): positive ŌĆö `let CFG: OnceLock[Config] = OnceLock.new();` accepted at module scope; `CFG.set(Config { ... })` returns `Ok(())` on first call; `CFG.get()` returns `Some` after `set`, `None` before; `CFG.set(other)` after first set returns `Err(AlreadySetError { rejected: other })`; `CFG.get_or_init(\|\| compute())` runs closure exactly once across multiple calls; `OnceCell[Vec[Token]]` field on a non-`par` struct accepted; `parser.tokens()` lazy-init pattern type-checks and runs end-to-end; struct containing `OnceCell` may be moved into a non-`par` block. Negative ŌĆö `let X: OnceCell[i64] = OnceCell.new();` at module scope rejected with `E_ONCE_CELL_AT_MODULE_SCOPE` and fix-it; `par struct Foo { cell: OnceCell[i64] }` rejected with `E_ONCE_CELL_IN_PAR_TYPE`; `par { let cell = OnceCell.new(); cell.set(1).unwrap(); }` accepted (cell is born inside the branch, doesn't cross); `let cell = OnceCell.new(); par { cell.set(1).unwrap(); }` rejected with `E_ONCE_CELL_CROSSES_TASK_BOUNDARY`; `Channel[OnceCell[i64]]` declared then `tx.send(cell)` rejected at the send call site with the same error. Phase target: **Phase 8** (Standard Library ŌĆö Floor) for stdlib types + interpreter + typechecker + structural-enforcement diagnostics; Phase 7 for codegen. No P1 carve-out ŌĆö option (a) of v60 item 45 ships the full surface at v1; `LazyCell[T]` (the embedded-init non-Sync sibling) is intentionally not in v1 and is non-breaking-additive if a workload demands it later.

Spec at `design.md ┬¦ Collection Core Methods > Map[K, V]` (line 1548) and `design.md ┬¦ Iteration order is unspecified` (line 1588). All subtasks closed; Display split into its own canonical bullet at `phase-7-codegen.md ┬¦ Phase 7.2` since recursive Display codegen is its own scope. Closed 2026-05-04. Subtasks:
  - [x] **1. Catch-all hardening** ŌĆö replaced the silent fallback at `src/codegen.rs:4945` with `Err(format!("codegen: Map.{method} not yet implemented"))`. No existing test triggered the catch-all (full LLVM suite still green at 2495 tests); hardening is purely preventative against future drift between typechecker-accepted methods and codegen-implemented methods. Commit `4a3bc3e`.
  - [x] **2. `m[k]` index op (read)** ŌĆö extended `compile_index` with an early dispatch (mirrors slice early-dispatch shape) keyed off `self.map_key_types.contains_key(name)` to a new `compile_map_index` helper. Helper loads the map handle, allocates key/val slots, calls `karac_map_get`, and branches on the i1: missing ŌåÆ `emit_panic("Map index: key not present")` + unreachable; found ŌåÆ load val and return. Limitation: only direct-identifier paths wired (same as slice early-dispatch). Returned value is a bit-copy of the bucket ŌĆö matches existing `Map.get` behavior; proper `ref V` return is a uniform follow-up across `[]` and `Map.get`. Tests: `test_e2e_map_index_get_existing_i64`, `test_e2e_map_index_get_existing_string_key`, `test_e2e_map_index_panics_on_missing`. Commit `ca94b9f`.

Fresh-insert and overwrite are handled uniformly by the runtime call. Tests: `test_e2e_map_index_set_fresh_and_overwrite`, `test_e2e_map_index_set_string_key`. Commit `3f08a39`.

Extern declared in `Codegen::new()`. `clear` arm added to `infer_map_method` (Unit return), `eval_method_call` on `Value::Map`, and `compile_map_method`. Returns the Vec struct `{data, len, cap=len}` directly; receiving binding's let-statement registers cleanup via existing `vec_elem_types` path.   - [x] **7. `Map[k: v, ...]` prefix-literal K/V inference** ŌĆö turned out to need parser + codegen, not pure typechecker. Parser was rejecting `Map[k: v]` outright ("Expected RightBracket, found Colon"); the AST node `PrefixCollectionLiteral.items` is a `Vec<Expr>` that can't represent key-value pairs. Fix: when type_name is "Map" and first expr is followed by `:`, parser switches to key-value parsing and emits `ExprKind::MapLiteral` (same AST as the bare `["k": v]` form, so existing typechecker case applies unchanged). Codegen for MapLiteral was also missing ŌĆö silent-0 catch-all at `compile_expr` line 2837 swallowed it. Added `compile_map_literal_stmt` (new + insert-loop) and a let-statement-level recognizer that dispatches both bare and prefix forms. Tests: `test_map_prefix_literal_string_keys` / `test_map_prefix_literal_int_keys` (interpreter); `test_e2e_map_prefix_literal_string_keys` / `test_e2e_map_prefix_literal_int_keys` / `test_e2e_map_bare_literal_with_annotation` (codegen). Closes `phase-4-interpreter.md` line 13. Commit `1678d0a`.

- [x] **`Set[T]` LLVM codegen.** Lower `Set[T]` to `Map[T, ()]` at the codegen layer and reuse the `karac_map_*` C runtime ŌĆö the canonical implementation strategy used by Rust's `HashSet<T>` (defined as a wrapper around `HashMap<T, ()>`) and equivalent in every mainstream stdlib. The existing runtime at `runtime/src/map.rs` already handles zero-size values correctly via `(key_size + val_size).max(1)` at line 71, so no new C code is required; `Set[T]` keeps its own type identity in the parser/typechecker/interpreter/effect-checker layers and the lowering happens entirely below LLVM IR. Spec at `design.md ┬¦ Collection Core Methods > Set[T]` (line 1590). Subtasks:
  - [x] **1. Codegen state** ŌĆö `set_elem_types: HashMap<String, BasicTypeEnum<'ctx>>`, `set_elem_type_names: HashMap<String, String>`, and `set_elem_type_exprs: HashMap<String, TypeExpr>` added next to the Map side-tables in `Codegen`. New `extract_set_elem_type`, `extract_set_elem_name`, `set_inner_type_expr` helpers parallel `extract_map_kv_types` / `extract_map_key_name` / `map_kv_type_exprs`. Side-tables populated both at the let-statement type-annotation site and via `register_var_from_type_expr` (the latter already runs for for-loop bindings). Type lowering at `llvm_type_for_type_expr` already lowers `Set[T]` to opaque `ptr` so no change there.
  - [x] **2. `Set.new()` path-call dispatch** ŌĆö `is_set_new_call` predicate + `compile_set_new_stmt` added next to the Map versions. Lowers to `karac_map_new(elem_size, 0, hash_fn, eq_fn)` ŌĆö the runtime's `(key_size + val_size).max(1)` keeps the bucket allocation valid for `val_size = 0`. Hash/eq fns selected via `emit_hash_fn_for_type_expr` so compound element shapes (tuples, derived-Hash structs) compose. Cleanup is the existing `FreeMapHandle` action; `track_map_var` is reused.
  - [x] **3. `compile_set_method`** ŌĆö new function parallel to `compile_map_method`. Implements `len` ŌåÆ `karac_map_len`; `is_empty` ŌåÆ `karac_map_len == 0`; `insert(v)` ŌåÆ `karac_map_insert_old(map, &v, &dummy, &dummy)` then XOR with `1` (returns `true` on fresh insert, matching Rust `HashSet::insert`); `contains(v)` ŌåÆ `karac_map_contains`; `remove(v)` ŌåÆ `karac_map_remove_old(map, &v, &dummy)` returning the existed bit; `clear()` ŌåÆ `karac_map_clear`. The dummy unit/out is a single shared `i8` alloca per function ŌĆö `val_size = 0` in the runtime makes the actual store a no-op. Method dispatch wired in the method-call routing site at `compile_method_call` alongside Map.
  - [x] **4. `for x in s`** ŌĆö `compile_for_set_var` mirrors `compile_for_map_var`, swapping the val out-slot for a single shared `i8` alloca and binding the element directly (no `(k, v)` destructuring). Dispatch wired in the for-loop routing site at `compile_for`.
  - [x] **5. `union` / `intersection` / `difference`** ŌĆö three new arms in `compile_set_method` route through a shared `emit_set_op_iter` helper that walks `karac_map_iter_*` over the source, optionally probes a "filter set" via `karac_map_contains`, per-element-clones survivors via `emit_clone_fn_for_type_expr`, and inserts into a freshly-allocated destination handle. `union` calls the helper twice ŌĆö unfiltered from `self`, filtered against `self` from `other` ŌĆö so duplicate elements never get double-cloned (which would leak the second clone since `karac_map_insert` overwrites in-place without freeing the prior key bytes). `intersection` uses `ContainsIn(other)`; `difference` uses `NotContainsIn(other)`. Hash/eq/elem-size pulled from the receiver's `set_elem_type_exprs` entry so compound element types compose. Result-handle scope-cleanup integration: extended the let-binding fallback path to call `track_map_var` when the RHS is a fresh-handle-producing method call (`clone` / `union` / `intersection` / `difference`); previously only `Vec`/`String` got auto-tracking, so `let n = m.clone();` was silently leaking the cloned handle on macOS (Apple ASAN has no LeakSanitizer; Linux + LSAN would have caught it). Restricted to `MethodCall` RHS so move-via-Identifier (`let n = m;`) keeps the source's existing track as the unique cleanup owner ŌĆö no double-free risk. 5 codegen E2E tests (`union_i64`, `intersection_i64`, `difference_i64`, `union_string`, `difference_independent_after_source_mutation`) + 1 ASAN test (`asan_set_union_string_independent_handles`) added.
  - [x] **6. E2E codegen tests** ŌĆö 9 baseline tests in `tests/codegen.rs` (search `test_e2e_set_`): `i64_insert_contains`, `i64_insert_returns_bool` (false on duplicate, true on fresh), `i64_remove`, `i64_len_is_empty`, `i64_for_loop_sum` (iteration-order-independent sum), `string_insert_contains`, `string_remove`, `string_for_loop_count`, `clear`. Plus the 5 set-op tests landed with subtask 5. Compound-key coverage (`Set[(i32, i32)]`, `Set[(String, (i32, i32))]`) deferred ŌĆö Hash machinery is shared with the Map suite which already exercises both compound-key recursion and cache reuse.
  - [x] **7. ASAN test** ŌĆö `tests/memory_sanitizer.rs::asan_set_new_insert_scope_exit_free` verifies the `FreeMapHandle` cleanup fires on Set drop. `asan_set_string_scope_exit_free` covers `Set[String]` with static-buffer (cap = 0) string literals to verify the bucket-array free fires while the static String buffers are correctly left alone.
  - [x] **8. `Set[v1, v2, ...]` prefix-literal element type inference** ŌĆö typechecker arm added in `infer_expr` for `ExprKind::PrefixCollectionLiteral { type_name: "Set", items }`. Element type is unified from items via `check_assignable`; empty `Set[]` falls to `Type::Error` for the element and recovers via the binding-site annotation per `design.md` line 1462. 4 typechecker tests: `test_set_prefix_literal_infers_i64`, `test_set_prefix_literal_infers_string`, `test_set_prefix_literal_mismatched_elements_rejected`, `test_set_prefix_literal_empty_with_annotation`. Closes `phase-4-interpreter.md` line 12 ŌĆö flip that checkbox when this lands too.

- [x] **Clone trait surface for collections ŌĆö vertical implementation (typechecker + interpreter + codegen + runtime).** Spec at `design.md ┬¦ Iteration` line 1692: *`Vec`, `Map`, `Set`, `VecDeque`, `TreeMap`, and `SortedSet` implement `Clone`*. Today **every layer is missing** ŌĆö typechecker has no `clone` method registration on these types (the only `"clone"` arm is for `Sender`); interpreter's `eval_method_call` falls through to "method 'clone' not found on type" panic; codegen has zero `"clone"` method dispatch and zero per-type clone fn emission. Compiled and interpreted binaries calling `Vec.clone()` / `String.clone()` / `Map.clone()` / `Set.clone()` fail today; this is a present-day v1 surface bug, not a future enhancement.

  **Priority: P0** ŌĆö covers v1 stdlib API surface methods that currently produce wrong behavior at every layer.

  **Consumers blocked on this** (cross-references; flip their checkboxes when the relevant subtask lands):
  - ~~`Set[T] LLVM codegen` subtask 5 (`union` / `intersection` / `difference`)~~ ŌĆö landed 2026-05-04 on top of `emit_clone_fn_for_type_expr`; per-element cloning routes through `emit_set_op_iter`.
  - `Vec.filled[T: Clone]` per `design.md ┬¦ 1488` ŌĆö every fill slot is a per-element clone.
  - Future stdlib generics with `T: Clone` bounds (e.g., `Vec.dedup_by_key`, `Vec.split_off` on non-Copy element types).
  - `#[derive(Clone)]` on user structs whose fields are non-Copy ŌĆö the synthesized body is field-wise per-type clone.

  **Subtasks (split by layer):**

  - [x] **1. Typechecker ŌĆö `clone` method registration on collection types.** Per-collection method-inference functions register `clone(ref self) -> Self` against `Vec[T]`, `String`, `Map[K, V]`, `Set[T]`, `VecDeque[T]`, `SortedSet[T]`, `TreeMap[K, V]`. The existing `infer_map_method` (`src/typechecker.rs:8275`) gets a `"clone"` arm; `Vec`/`String`/`Set` need their own (today the `Sender.clone()` arm at line 8892 is the only one in the typechecker). The `T: Clone` bound on collection element types is enforced via the existing trait-bound checking ŌĆö `Vec[T]: Clone where T: Clone`. Negative test: `Vec.clone()` on a `Vec[NonCloneStruct]` rejected with the bound-violation diagnostic.

  - [x] **2. Interpreter ŌĆö `clone` dispatch on collection values.** Add a `"clone"` arm to `eval_method_call` (`src/interpreter.rs`) that matches each `Value::Vec` / `Value::String` / `Value::Map` / `Value::Set` / `Value::SortedSet` shape and produces a deep copy via Rust-side `Vec::clone` / `String::clone` / etc. The Rust-side clones are correct by construction (each `Value` variant is itself `Clone`); this is purely dispatch wiring.

  - [x] **3. Codegen ŌĆö per-type clone fn emission machinery (`emit_clone_fn_for_type_expr`).** TypeExpr-aware emit fn paralleling `emit_hash_fn_for_type_expr` / `emit_eq_fn_for_type_expr` / `emit_display_fn_for_type_expr`. New `clone_fn_cache: HashMap<String, FunctionValue<'ctx>>` keyed on `display_mangle_te(te)`. Function signature is uniform `void karac_clone_<typename>(*const T src, *mut T dst)` ŌĆö caller provides both source and destination addresses, callee writes the cloned value into the destination slot. Cases:

    - **Primitive (Copy)** ŌĆö `i8`/`i16`/`i32`/`i64`/`u8`/`u16`/`u32`/`u64`/`isize`/`usize`/`f32`/`f64`/`bool`/`char`/`unit` ŌĆö single `load src` + `store dst`, no allocation.
    - **String** ŌĆö call new runtime helper `karac_string_clone` (subtask 4 below). Receives a String struct `{data, len, cap}`; allocates `cap` bytes (or `len` if `cap == 0` for static literals ŌĆö the cloned buffer needs `cap > 0` so its scope-exit cleanup fires), `memcpy`s `len` bytes, writes `{new_data, len, new_cap}` to `dst`.
    - **Vec[T]** ŌĆö recursive: load `data`/`len`/`cap` from src; emit `karac_clone_<elem_mangled>` for `T` (via `emit_clone_fn_for_type_expr(elem_te)`); `malloc(cap * elem_size)` for the new buffer; loop `i in 0..len` calling the elem clone fn with `src.data + i*elem_size` / `dst.data + i*elem_size`; write `{new_data, len, new_cap}` to `dst`. Empty Vecs (`cap == 0`) skip the malloc per the existing String-literal cap=0 convention.
    - **Map[K, V]** ŌĆö emit `karac_map_new(key_size, val_size, hash_fn, eq_fn)` for the destination; iterate the source via `karac_map_iter_*`; for each pair, alloca'd K and V copies (clone via per-K, per-V emit_clone fns), then `karac_map_insert_old` into the destination. Hash/eq fn pointers come from `emit_hash_fn_for_type_expr` / `emit_eq_fn_for_type_expr` (already exist).
    - **Set[T]** ŌĆö same as Map[T, ()] ŌĆö single-element clone per iteration, val_size = 0 with shared dummy slot.
    - **Tuple `(T1, T2, ..., Tn)`** ŌĆö typed entry `emit_clone_fn_for_tuple(elems)`; field-wise recurse into per-field clone fn via struct GEP. Mirror the tuple Hash/Eq/Display pattern.
    - **`#[derive(Clone)]` struct** ŌĆö synthesized body is field-wise recurse. Emit at the derive-site by walking the struct's `field_types` and calling `emit_clone_fn_for_type_expr` per field, then GEP+store into `dst` per field. The derived `clone` method gets registered as the user struct's `Type.clone` so method-call dispatch finds it.

  - [x] **4. Runtime ŌĆö `karac_string_clone(*const String) -> String` helper.** New extern in `runtime/src/string.rs` (or a dedicated `runtime/src/clone.rs`). Allocates a fresh buffer via the runtime's allocator (same path as `karac_vec_grow`), `memcpy`s `len` bytes from the source data pointer, returns the new `{ptr, len, cap}` struct. For static literals (`cap == 0`), allocates `len`-byte buffer with `cap = len` so the cloned String's scope-exit cleanup correctly frees it (the source's `cap = 0` keeps the static buffer untouched). Declared in `Codegen::new()` alongside the existing `karac_*` externs.

  - [x] **5. `compile_method_call` dispatch wiring.** Add `"clone"` arms to each per-collection method handler ŌĆö `compile_vec_method`, `compile_map_method`, `compile_set_method`, plus a String-method handler if one exists separately. Each wires the source variable's slot through to the corresponding `emit_clone_fn_for_type_expr` and writes the result to a fresh stack alloca + side-table registration so the cloned value participates in scope cleanup correctly.

  - [x] **6. Scope-cleanup integration.** A cloned `Vec` / `Map` / `Set` / `String` is a fresh heap-owning value ŌĆö register the appropriate `FreeVecBuffer` / `FreeMapHandle` cleanup action on its scope frame. Goes through the existing `track_vec_var` / `track_map_var` machinery; the only new piece is recognizing that `let w = v.clone()` produces a heap-owning bound name and calling the right tracker.

  - [x] **7. ASAN tests** in `tests/memory_sanitizer.rs`: `asan_vec_clone_independent_buffers` (verify the source's buffer is freed once and the cloned buffer is freed once ŌĆö no aliasing); `asan_string_clone_static_literal` (source has `cap = 0`, clone has `cap > 0` and gets freed, source untouched); `asan_map_clone_independent_handle` (verify both maps free their bucket arrays separately, and any heap-bearing key/value bytes ŌĆö String keys especially ŌĆö clone correctly so neither map points at the other's strings); `asan_set_clone_string_elements` (per-element String clone integrity).

  - [x] **8. E2E tests** in `tests/codegen.rs` + `tests/interpreter.rs`: `vec_clone_preserves_contents`, `vec_clone_grows_independently` (mutate source after clone, verify clone unchanged), `string_clone_independent_buffer`, `map_clone_preserves_entries` (single-key cases for deterministic output; multi-key behavior verified via the cardinality-equality / per-key lookup pattern that Map tests already use), `set_clone_preserves_membership`, `derive_clone_struct_with_vec_field` (whole-struct clone produces independent inner Vec).

  - [x] **9. Empty-collection clone fast path.** `Vec.new().clone()` doesn't need to allocate; same for the other empty collections. Either special-case `len == 0` in the emitted body (skip the malloc; produce a `cap = 0` placeholder) or rely on the runtime's `malloc(0)` defined-behavior path. The former is cleaner and saves an allocation per empty clone.

- [x] **`Map.entry(k)` + `Entry[K, V]` enum ŌĆö in-place insert-or-modify.** The idiomatic O(1) insert-or-modify pattern `self.table.entry(key).or_insert_with(Vec.new).push(row)` avoids the double-hash that `if !m.contains_key { m.insert(...) }` produces. Without this, every word-count / group-by / counter-style program either double-hashes or threads an explicit `match m.get(...)` / `insert` pair through the call site. Spec at `design.md ┬¦ Entry[K, V]` (around line 1565). Subtasks:
  - [x] **1. Parser/AST verification** ŌĆö confirmed: `m.entry(k)` parses as a `MethodCall` AST node with no new grammar, and the `.or_insert / .or_insert_with / .and_modify` chain composes through the standard method-call grammar. `tests/parser.rs::test_map_entry_chain_parses` covers the four canonical chain shapes.
  - [x] **2. `Entry[K, V]` enum prelude registration** ŌĆö `Entry` added to `PRELUDE_TYPES` (with `K, V` arity in `stub_generics`); `Occupied` / `Vacant` added to `PRELUDE_VARIANTS`. The full `EnumInfo` in `register_builtin_types` defines `Occupied { value: mut ref V }` / `Vacant { key: K, map: mut ref Map[K, V] }`. First stdlib type using `mut ref` on a variant payload ŌĆö typechecker accepts the borrow-typed fields without changes.
  - [x] **3. `Entry` methods** ŌĆö new `infer_entry_method` keyed off `Type::Named { name: "Entry", args: [K, V] }`, wired into `infer_method_call`'s named-type dispatch chain. `or_insert(default: V) -> mut ref V`, `or_insert_with(f: Fn() -> V) -> mut ref V` (closure-pushdown solves the closure return type from V), `and_modify(f: Fn(mut ref V)) -> Entry[K, V]` (returns Entry for chaining). Effect polymorphism on the closure-taking forms propagates through the existing closure-effect-checking pass.
  - [x] **4. Interpreter** ŌĆö `Value::Entry { map_var: Option<String>, key: Box<Value>, slot_idx: Option<usize> }`. The `entry` arm in `eval_method_call` linear-searches `Value::Map` for the key, builds the Entry. `or_insert` / Vacant arm of `or_insert_with` push onto the live Map and write back via `env.set` (the standard interpreter mut-ref-self idiom); the Occupied arm returns the cloned slot value. `and_modify` aliases the slot via `Value::SharedCell` and runs the closure with `[SharedCell]` as the arg so `|v| { v += 1 }` mutates through. The fully-aliased pattern `m.entry(k).or_insert_with(Vec.new).push(row)` is interpreter-incompatible without invasive Map representation changes ŌĆö codegen handles that case correctly.
  - [x] **5. Runtime ŌĆö `karac_map_entry` and `karac_map_lookup_slot`** ŌĆö two C ABI fns in `runtime/src/map.rs`. `karac_map_entry` (insert-on-vacant) is used by chains terminating in `or_insert` / `or_insert_with`; `karac_map_lookup_slot` (read-only) is used by chains terminating in bare `and_modify` so a missing key never causes an insertion side-effect. Both: out-pointer + bool-return shape mirroring `karac_map_get`, resize before probing so the slot pointer is stable for the rest of the call, pointer valid until the next mutating call (`HashMap::entry`'s lifetime contract).
  - [x] **6. Codegen** ŌĆö `try_compile_entry_chain` in `compile_method_call` peels `and_modify` wrappers off the receiver and matches `m.entry(k)` at the chain root. One runtime call (terminal-driven choice between `karac_map_entry` and `karac_map_lookup_slot`) followed by branch blocks for each step, sharing a single slot pointer ŌĆö exactly one hash per chain. `or_insert(d)` stores the default through the slot on Vacant; `or_insert_with(f)` uses the fat-pointer indirect-call path; `and_modify(f)` inlines the closure body directly (binds closure param to a stack alloca initialised from the slot, evaluates the body, stores back through the slot pointer) so `|v| { v += 1 }` mutates the map slot without needing closure-param-as-pointer codegen surgery. Restricted to inline `ExprKind::Closure` ŌĆö named-fn forms are spec-out-of-scope at v1. The terminal-`.push(row)` form on `or_insert_with(Vec.new).push(row)` is its own piece of work that co-evolves with the per-type Clone codegen bullet (both need a slot-ptr-receiver path on `Vec.push`); the typechecker accepts that chain shape today.
  - [x] **7. Test coverage** ŌĆö 11 typechecker + 7 interpreter + 7 codegen E2E tests. Codegen E2E (search `test_e2e_map_entry_`): or_insert vacant insert / occupied passthrough; or_insert_with closure fires only when vacant / skipped when occupied; and_modify runs only when occupied / skipped when vacant; the canonical `and_modify(|v| { v += 1; }).or_insert(1)` chain across three calls. Negative: `or_insert_with` closure body that re-borrows the map remains rejected by the existing borrow checker (no Entry-specific work needed since the `mut ref Map` borrow conflict is in the existing infrastructure).

- [x] **Effect-checker wiring for `Map[K, V]` and `Set[T]` methods.** Ō£ō DONE (2026-05-04). Wired the per-method allocator surface into `src/effectchecker.rs` via the existing seed-`inferred_effects` + `STDLIB_METHOD_MAP` mechanism rather than a new `infer_*_method_effects` function (the architecture is data-driven through these tables, not per-type inference functions like the typechecker has). Subtasks:

  - [x] **5. Test coverage** ŌĆö added 11 tests under `// ŌöĆŌöĆ Per-method effect surface for Map / Set ŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆ` in `tests/effectchecker.rs`.
