### Auto-Concurrency Codegen ŌĆö Debugger Contract

Co-developed with the auto-concurrency codegen slate (slices 1ŌĆō2 in `phase-7-codegen.md` ┬¦ "Par codegen: auto-parallelization of non-`par` regions") because this is the moment the runtime first emits `par`/`suspend` code at compiler-inferred sites; the contract has to be in place or it gets locked in by accident. Specified in design.md ┬¦ AI-First Compiler Interface > Debugger Contract; v1 deliverables are the runtime metadata emission and the `std.runtime` enumeration surface (consumer tools ŌĆö gdb/lldb plugins, DAP, profiler GUIs ŌĆö are out of v1 scope). The contract is four pieces split across three slices:

- Slice 3 (this section, drafted): SpawnSiteId metadata table ŌĆö the foundation. Slice 4 builds parent-frame ref + await-chain pointer on top; slice 5 exposes the table to K─üra-callable code via `std.runtime`.
- Profile-gated via `runtime_debug_metadata = true|false`. Slices 3ŌĆō5 implement the knob via `KARAC_RUNTIME_DEBUG_METADATA=1|0` env-var override during the v1 demo-build window; the TOML-config home for the knob lands as a separate slice in Phase 8.5 Track 2 (Build & Dependency Tooling). Default-on for dev (today's `karac build` posture); release / embedded / `isr` profile defaults land alongside the Phase 8.5 lift.

- [x] **Debugger Contract slice 3 ŌĆö SpawnSiteId metadata table emission. DONE ŌĆö verified 2026-07-11 (reconciliation sweep).** `record_spawn_site` (src/codegen.rs) mints the per-`par` `SpawnSiteId` inside `emit_par_run` (both explicit `par {}` and auto-par paths); `emit_spawn_sites_metadata` emits the populated `KARAC_SPAWN_SITES` / `_LEN` / `_ENABLED` globals (gated by `runtime_debug_metadata_enabled`). Four IR-level tests in tests/codegen.rs assert the emitted globals (populated LEN=2, empty-table LEN=0, gate-off ENABLED=false). The slice's own note already anticipated this flip. First of three slices for the four-piece Debugger Contract. Mint a static `u32` `SpawnSiteId` per `par {}` block during codegen and emit a global metadata table `KARAC_SPAWN_SITES` mapping each ID to its source location. The IDs are stable per-binary and serve as the join key every later contract piece (parent-frame ref, await-chain pointer, runtime introspection) references. Sequencing: drafted 2026-05-08 before slices 1 and 2; slices 1 and 2 landed first (commits `c0e72fc` / `8bc3bab`), so slice 3 now retrofits onto the post-slice-2 codegen shape. **Updated post-slice-2:** the `par_counter` increment that slice 3 originally targeted in `compile_par_block` now lives in the new `emit_par_run(stmts, span)` helper that both `compile_par_block` (explicit `par {}`) and `compile_function_body` (auto-par dispatch) call. This is good news ŌĆö slice 3's recording-helper insertion is now a one-place change inside `emit_par_run`, and both spawn-site varieties (explicit + inferred) gain SpawnSiteIds in the same step. Sub-step (d) below updated accordingly. **READY / appears ALREADY LANDED (verified 2026-07-09):** slices 1 & 2 are `[x]` (corroborated by slice 4 at `[x]` and slice 6 depending on `8bc3bab`), and the insertion point is the single `emit_par_run` helper (`src/codegen/par_blocks.rs:583`, called from both `compile_par_block` at `par_blocks.rs:236` and the auto-par path at `src/codegen/stmts.rs:508`) ŌĆö so the internal-sequence dependency is unblocked. Beyond that, the slice-3 deliverable itself appears to have shipped: `record_spawn_site` (`src/codegen.rs:5986`) mints the per-`par` `SpawnSiteId` inside `emit_par_run` (`par_blocks.rs:748`), and `emit_spawn_sites_metadata` (`src/codegen.rs:8024`, invoked at `src/codegen.rs:7131`) emits the populated `KARAC_SPAWN_SITES` + `_LEN` + `_ENABLED` globals (gated by `runtime_debug_metadata_enabled` / `KARAC_RUNTIME_DEBUG_METADATA`), with four IR-level tests at `tests/codegen.rs:33806+`. The unchecked `- [ ]` box therefore looks stale ŌĆö a maintainer should confirm and flip it to `[x]`.

- [x] **Debugger Contract slice 4 ŌĆö parent-frame ref + await-chain pointer.** Items (2) + (3) of the four-piece contract. **Item 2 (parent-frame ref) ships real machinery for v1**: every worker frame produced by a `par {}` block carries a pointer back to the frame that created it, with a `null` sentinel for the root task. Slice 5's `std.runtime::list_par_blocks()` walks this graph to reconstruct the structured-concurrency tree. **Item 3 (await-chain pointer) ships contract surface only for v1**: `KaracWaitTarget` enum and the `wait_target` field on `KaracFrame` are defined and stable, but always populated as `None` because v1's blocking runtime has no real suspension to track ŌĆö `Receiver.recv()` returns `Unit` on empty rather than blocking, no event loop exists yet. Real await-chain tracking lights up when Phase 6.3's network event loop ships and registers WaitTargets at I/O-effect-boundary operations. Sequencing: depends on slice 3 for `KARAC_SPAWN_SITES` (the SpawnSiteId table that frame metadata indexes into); independent of slices 1, 2, 6.

### Auto-Concurrency Codegen ŌĆö Parallax-lite Workload

First demo-shaped consumer of slices 1 + 2. A real K─üra program with hand-coded providers, distinct effect resources, and three independent fan-out statements that auto-par lowering parallelizes in compiled output. Validates `karac query cost-summary` against the Cumulative Cost Surface table from `design.md ┬¦ Performance Diagnostics > Cumulative Cost Surface`. Sets up the framework for v1.x cost-model tuning + the `par struct` single-task overhead measurement; both follow-on analyses are explicitly v1.x territory per `roadmap.md ┬¦ Phase 8 ┬¦ Parallax-lite ŌĆö first ground-truth measurement workload`.

**Demo-shape gap, surfaced upfront.** The canonical Parallax demo (`dogfooding.md ┬¦ Parallax`) is *fan-out + join* ŌĆö four parallel reads, results fed into `build_dashboard(profile, orders, notif, recommended)`. Slice 2's `group_defines_binding_used_outside` gate blocks this exact pattern today: bindings defined inside a parallel group that are read by stmts outside the group don't auto-parallelize, because `karac_par_run`'s branch fns capture *into* their env struct but don't propagate let-bindings *out*. Lifting the gate requires the still-open `phase-7-codegen.md:182` entry **"Par codegen: return values"**, which extends the runtime ABI with per-branch return slots. Slice 6 ships the **measurement workload** (effect-only fan-out ŌĆö three independent `writes(R_i)` calls on distinct resources, no joined return) which IS auto-par-eligible today. The demo workload (canonical fan-out + join) lights up when "Par codegen: return values" lands.

- [x] **Debugger Contract slice 6 ŌĆö Parallax-lite microbenchmark workload.** Hand-coded effect-only-fan-out workload exercising slices 1 + 2 on a real program. Three deliverables: (a) a `examples/parallax_lite/` K─üra project with three trait-bound effect resources + `InMemoryMetrics` provider impl + a `process_request` driver function whose three top-level call statements auto-parallelize; (b) `karac query cost-summary` validation against the workload, pinning the output for the Cumulative Cost Surface table from `design.md ┬¦ Performance Diagnostics > Cumulative Cost Surface`; (c) a `--sequential` codegen flag (or env-var equivalent) that disables auto-par dispatch in `compile_function_body`, enabling side-by-side wall-clock benchmarking. Sequencing: depends on slice 2 (auto-par codegen MVP ŌĆö already landed at `8bc3bab`). Independent of slices 3, 4, 5.

- [ ] **Parallax-lite multicore scaling ŌĆö v1.x cost-model ground-truth data (collected 2026-05-08).** Not a tracker entry awaiting implementation ŌĆö a data filing for the v1.x cost-model tuning track that the roadmap.md ┬¦ Phase 8 ┬¦ Parallax-lite "Cost-model tuning (v1.x)" bullet calls for. Slice 6 shipped a 3-branch wall-clock measurement; this entry extends to a scaling curve (N=3..500) on an 18-core machine. Ground-truth observations:

  - **Near-linear scaling holds through `branch_count Ōēż available_parallelism()`** ŌĆö measured 88% scaling efficiency at N=18 on an 18-core machine (15.88x speedup). The runtime's per-branch overhead is below the wall-clock noise floor up to the core-count ceiling.

  - **Slice 4's `Mutex<Vec<FramePtr>>` active-frames registry doesn't bottleneck at 18 concurrent par-block branches.** The push/retain cost (~1┬Ąs each per spawn) is dwarfed by 80ms of busy-compute. Validates the slice-4 design choice (Mutex<Vec> over RwLock<HashMap<ThreadId,_>>) empirically ŌĆö RwLock+HashMap would have been over-engineered for the actual contention profile.

  - **Sharp efficiency dip at medium N (50ŌĆō100), recovers at high N (200ŌĆō500).** N=50 efficiency is 43% (7.18x of 16.67x ideal); N=500 efficiency rises back to 83% (14.80x of 17.86x ideal). Initial stdout-contention hypothesis was *ruled out* by a 10x larger busy-compute test (efficiency stayed low). Real cause: **thermal throttling on sustained all-cores load** plus L3 cache / memory bandwidth contention. At small N (Ōēż18) workers run ~one branch and finish before throttling fully engages; at medium N busy-compute doesn't dwarf the per-branch dispatch cost; at high N busy-compute dominates again. **Laptop-class hardware artifact, not runtime design.** Server-class hardware with proper cooling would push the curve closer to ideal across all N.

  - **Linear compile time scaling: ~0.5ms per branch.** N=500 compiles in 0.26s (auto-par) / 0.15s (sequential). **No quadratic-time analyzer pass** ŌĆö load-bearing finding for v1.x compiler perf; the conflict-matrix construction in `concurrency.rs` and effect-set unification in `effectchecker.rs` both stay near-linear at 500-element scale.

  **Actionable for the v1.x cost-model spec work** (per `design.md ┬¦ 8779` "v1.x specification work"):

  - **Fork threshold heuristic.** Today `is_trivial` is the only granularity gate. Empirical sweet spot is `branch_count Ōēż available_parallelism()`. v1.x spec should add a `branch_count Ōēż N_hw_cores` check in the analyzer or the codegen. v1 ship posture: do nothing and document the cliff (the data shows the cliff is mild ŌĆö N=500 still gets 14.80x speedup).

  - **Per-branch dispatch overhead is hardware-thermal-dependent, not constant.** ~5ms on cold-start (N=18); ~100ms on sustained all-cores load (N=50ŌĆō100). The cost-model spec should NOT bake in a hardcoded per-branch overhead constant; defer threshold tuning to post-Parallax-lite measurement on server-class hardware. Document the laptop number as "expected upper-bound ceiling on thermally-constrained hardware."

  - **The `is_trivial` boolean granularity gate is the right v1 abstraction** but loses signal at the cost-model level. v1.x cost-model spec should likely refine to per-branch cost estimate (`branch_cost: Option<Duration>` based on inferred-effect classification) rather than the binary `is_trivial`.

  - **Stdout contention is *not* a meaningful auto-par overhead source** at typical busy-compute / println balances. Initial hypothesis ruled out by the 500M-iter test (efficiency *dropped* rather than improved). The v1.x cost-model spec should ignore stdout-write effects in granularity heuristics unless the busy-compute kernel is unusually small relative to expected per-write overhead.

  Reproducible setup at `examples/parallax_lite/README.md` ┬¦ Multicore scaling. Raw scripts not committed; reproducible from the README's setup section.

### Auto-Concurrency Codegen ŌĆö `std.runtime` Introspection APIs

Slice 5 of the auto-concurrency slate. Closes out the four-piece Debugger Contract by exposing slice 3's `KARAC_SPAWN_SITES` metadata table + slice 4's `KaracFrame` active-frames registry as K─üra-callable APIs. Drafted last (after slices 1ŌĆō4 + 6) per demo-driven sequencing ŌĆö slice 6's Parallax-lite workload provides a concrete consumer to design against.

- [x] **Debugger Contract slice 5 ŌĆö `std.runtime::list_par_blocks()` / `list_tasks()` / `has_debug_metadata()`. DONE ŌĆö verified 2026-07-11 (reconciliation sweep).** All three introspection functions ship end-to-end: stdlib surface in runtime/stdlib/runtime.kara (+ `ParBlockInfo`/`TaskInfo` in src/prelude.rs); runtime externs `karac_runtime_has_debug_metadata` / `karac_runtime_list_par_blocks_into` (runtime/src/lib.rs, reading `KARAC_SPAWN_SITES_ENABLED` + the spawn-site table from slice 3); codegen `assoc_call` wiring + interpreter arms; tests at every layer (typechecker signatures, interpreter behavior, codegen E2E incl. gate-on/off + observing self inside a `par` block, runtime unit tests). `list_tasks()` returns empty at v1 by design. Item (4) of the four-piece contract per `design.md ┬¦ Debugger Contract`. Three K─üra-callable functions that materialize the runtime introspection surface for tooling and crash-report consumption. `has_debug_metadata()` returns a `bool` reading `KARAC_SPAWN_SITES_ENABLED`. `list_par_blocks() -> Vec[ParBlockInfo]` enumerates the *currently-active* par blocks across all OS threads (joins slice 4's `karac_runtime_for_each_active_frame` against slice 3's `KARAC_SPAWN_SITES` table to enrich each frame's `spawn_site_id` with its `(file, line, col, worker_count)`). `list_tasks() -> Vec[TaskInfo]` enumerates suspended tasks ŌĆö **always returns empty in v1** because v1's blocking runtime has no real suspension to track (`Receiver.recv()` returns `Unit` on empty rather than blocking; no event loop). Phase 6.3's network event loop is the predecessor that lights this up. Sequencing: depends on slices 3 + 4 (both landed at `c6d8b44` / `22fa27a`); independent of slices 1, 2, 6 once those have landed.

### Provider Implementations

The `with_provider[R]` mechanism is spec'd in `design.md` and parsed today, but several pieces of the runtime/codegen wiring are gappy. Items here track those gaps. The full provider surface is referenced from `roadmap.md ┬¦ Phase 8 ┬¦ Provider Implementations`.

- [x] **`with_provider[R]` trait-method dispatch wiring (GAP-N follow-up).** Inside a `with_provider[R](inst, || { ... })` scope, calls of the shape `R.method(args)` should dispatch to `inst`'s `R: Trait` impl per `design.md ┬¦ Provider-Rooted Resources` ("Resource call desugaring" + "Runtime mechanics" + "with_provider and parameterized resources" paragraphs). In v1 codegen the dispatch is currently a **no-op at runtime**: the `with_provider` block compiles + links, but `R.method(...)` calls inside the closure body never invoke the bound provider's impl method. Empirically validated by slice 6 (Parallax-lite workload, 2026-05-08): a `with_provider[MetricsA](inst, || { MetricsA.record(50_000_000); })` shape that should run a 50M-iteration busy-compute kernel returns in <5ms ŌĆö the kernel never executed. Slice 6 fell back to a no-providers entry point (calling `process_request` directly) and inlined the busy-compute kernel into the `record_*` driver functions to keep the wall-clock benchmark meaningful; the canonical `R.method(...)` shape is documented in `examples/parallax_lite/src/main.kara` comments + slice 6's "Deviations" close-out. **Demo readiness load-bearing**: the canonical Parallax demo (`dogfooding.md ┬¦ Parallax`) is `let profile = fetch_profile(user_id);` etc., where `fetch_profile` typically dispatches through the active `UserDB: DatabaseProvider`. When `phase-7-codegen.md:229` "Par codegen: return values" lands and unblocks the canonical fan-out + join shape, this GAP-N wiring also needs to ship for the demo's `fetch_*` calls to do anything observable. The two are paired demo-readiness items.

  **Spec status ŌĆö locked.** `design.md ┬¦ Provider-Rooted Resources` already pins the rule (clarified during slice 6 follow-up reframing 2026-05-08): `R.method(args)` desugars to `Arc<dyn R::Provider>` lookup in the per-task provider stack followed by a vtable call; `with_provider[R](p, ||...)` pushes/pops a frame; parameterized instances `R[k]` always route through the base-resource binding. The interpreter implements this at `src/interpreter.rs::eval_resource_method` (line 7146). The remaining work is **codegen-only** ŌĆö the implementation, not the spec. The earlier "needs design discussion" framing in this entry referred to the spec gap that is no longer open; what remains is **implementation-design choice** on the codegen ABI, scoped in the slice plan below.

  **Codegen ABI design choices** (all decidable from existing constraints; no further spec discussion needed before slice plan execution):
  - **(a) Per-task provider stack representation.** Two natural shapes ŌĆö (i) thread-local `Vec<HashMap<ResourceId, Arc<dyn Any>>>` mirroring the interpreter, accessed through a runtime helper; (ii) frame-allocated linked list of `(resource_id, provider_arc)` cells, with the head pointer carried in `KaracFrame` (slice 4) so the existing per-thread frame plumbing extends naturally. **Recommend (ii)**: avoids `thread_local!` bookkeeping on Apple/Linux platforms with cheap-but-not-free TLS, and reuses the slice 4 KaracFrame infrastructure already wired into `karac_par_run`. Lookup is O(stack-depth ├Ś resource-count); typical depths are 1-3, so linear scan is fine.
  - **(b) Vtable layout.** Trait-object support is *new* ŌĆö K─üra v1 has no other trait-object lowering site. Two options ŌĆö (i) per-trait single-dispatch vtable (data ptr + fn ptrs), classic Rust shape; (ii) per-method-call lookup table keyed by `(resource_id, method_name) ŌåÆ fn_ptr`, sidestepping vtable construction entirely. **Recommend (i)**: the v1 cost model already names "thin Arc deref + one vtable indirection" at `design.md ┬¦ Resource call desugaring`; option (ii) adds a hash lookup per call which is observably slower and not what the spec promises. Vtable construction at `with_provider` call site is a one-time cost; subsequent calls are pointer-chases.
  - **(c) Arc-sharing on spawn.** `karac_par_run` (slice 2 + 4) already passes branch closures captured environments into worker threads. The provider stack head pointer needs to flow through that capture so spawned tasks see the parent's bindings. Implementation: add a `provider_stack_head: *const ProviderFrame` field to the env-struct emitted by `compile_par_block` / `emit_par_run`, populated from the calling thread's KaracFrame at par-block entry; each worker thread initializes its KaracFrame with this head when entering the branch fn. Arc clones happen lazily at first use, not eagerly at spawn (matches the cost note at `design.md:7078`).
  - **(d) Parameterized-resource binding.** `design.md ┬¦ with_provider and parameterized resources` (line 7101) locks the rule: `Db["users"]`, `Db["orders"]` all key on the base resource `Db`. Codegen already has access to the resource's base name via `effectchecker.rs` resource-ID interning. The lookup uses base name only; the parameter is passed through to the provider's method as a normal argument. No new design.
  - **(e) Vtable storage on `with_provider` call.** When `with_provider[R](provider, ||body)` runs, we need the provider's vtable for trait `R::Provider` to be addressable. Option (i): emit a per-`(provider_type, trait)` static vtable global at codegen time, referenced by `with_provider`'s frame push. Option (ii): build the vtable on the fly at the `with_provider` call site. **Recommend (i)** ŌĆö vtables are statically known per impl; static globals avoid per-call construction overhead and match the standard Rust trait-object model.
  - **(f) Resource ID assignment.** `effectchecker.rs` already interns resource names to stable IDs for conflict analysis. Codegen reuses these IDs as the provider-stack lookup key ŌĆö no new ID space.

  **Slice plan (autonomous-friendly bar, drafted 2026-05-08).**

  *Goal.* Codegen `R.method(args)` calls inside `with_provider[R](inst, ||body)` scopes to dispatch through the bound provider's trait impl, matching the interpreter's `eval_resource_method` semantics and the design.md spec.

- [x] **Typed effect resources + in-memory providers + canonical `get_dashboard` workload (full Parallax demo, Slice C).** The demo's load-bearing source artifact: four typed effect resources (`UserDB / OrderDB / NotifDB / RecommendDB`), four single-method provider traits returning typed result data (`fetch_profile -> Profile`, `fetch_recent_orders -> Vec[Order]`, `fetch_notifications -> Vec[Notification]`, `fetch_recommendations -> Vec[Recommendation]`), four in-memory provider impls (`InMemoryUserDB / InMemoryOrderDB / InMemoryNotifDB / InMemoryRecommendDB`), and the canonical `get_dashboard(user_id)` workload ŌĆö four `let` bindings into typed return values, joined into a `Dashboard { profile, orders, notif, recommended }` result struct. Lives at `examples/parallax/` (sibling to `examples/parallax_lite/`). The combined workload exercises the integration of two recently-landed mechanisms in one place: Theme 6's `with_provider[R]` trait-method dispatch for the per-call routing, and Slice A's per-branch return slots for the four-way fan-out+join. Each was test-covered independently at landing time; this slice is the first source artifact that puts them together end-to-end. **Demo readiness:** pairs with Slice B (HTTP server FFI) for the `serve_http` entry point and Slice E (benchmark harness) for the side-by-side compare; the workload itself ships standalone and can be benchmarked directly via `cargo run --release` before B/E land.

> **Moved (2026-06-06):** the numerical type-system forcing functions (Q1ŌĆōQ4: shape generic-parameter kind, shape literal grammar, `Tensor[T, Shape]`, tensor arithmetic traits, explicit broadcasting, and the shipped Q4 literal-promotion entry) and the Arrow data-type commitments (Q5ŌĆōQ6: `Column[T]`, `DataFrame`, Arrow IPC / Parquet / CSV) now live in [`phase-11-stdlib-longtail.md ┬¦ Numerical and data-science stdlib`](phase-11-stdlib-longtail.md#numerical-and-data-science-stdlib).

**Script mode (Q7).**

- [ ] **Script mode ŌĆö files without `fn main`.** Parser change: when `src/parser.rs` encounters a top-level statement (`let`, expression, assignment) *before* any `fn main` declaration, switch to script mode and synthesize `fn main() -> Result[Unit, Error]` wrapping all top-level statements in file order. Items (fn, struct, enum, trait, impl, use) remain at module scope and hoist as today. Mix of top-level statements and an explicit `fn main` is a parse error with a diagnostic pointing at both. Resolver / typechecker treat the synthesized main exactly as they would a user-written `fn main()` with `Result[Unit, Error]` return type ŌĆö effect inference applies, `?` works, existing entry-point rules apply.

- [x] **`main()` entry-point contract enforcement (typechecker) + `ExitCode` stdlib type.** Ō£ō DONE 2026-06-13 ŌĆö Slices A (payload-enum Display), B (`ExitCode`), C (enforcement + derives + migration) all landed. Per design.md ┬¦ Entry Point (lines 6267ŌĆō6293), `main()` must return exactly one of `()`, `Result[(), E: Display]`, or `ExitCode`; any other return type is a compile error, and the `Result` form additionally requires `E: Display` (checked at the entry-point boundary with an `impl Display` fix-it). **Current state (probed 2026-06-13): NOT enforced** ŌĆö `karac check` passes on `fn main() -> Result[(), NoDisp]` with a non-`Display` `NoDisp`, and never rejects disallowed return types. Surfaced while fixing the codegen entry-point adaptation (B-2026-06-12-9, `e5be4553`): that fix makes a valid `main() -> Result` exit correctly (`Ok`ŌåÆ0, `Err(e)`ŌåÆ`Error: {e}\n` stderr + exit 1, via E's Display), but with no `E: Display` check the *codegen* Err path silently degrades to a bare `Error: \n` for any error type the Display path can't render ŌĆö which today is only reachable via an ill-typed `main` (a payload-bearing enum error type: such enums can't be `Display` in v1, since user `impl Display` is resolver-rejected and `#[derive(Display)]` on a payload enum is typecheck-rejected). Enforcing this bound closes that hole at the signature instead of at the exit. **Agreed scope (2026-06-13): FULL enforcement, payload-enum Display built FIRST as prerequisite.** Recon found `E: Display` (the leg that closes the bare-`Error:` hole) is transitively blocked: `type_supports_display` (`src/typechecker/derives.rs:285`) requires user enums/structs to derive/impl Display, and the canonical `IoError` is a *payload-bearing* enum (`Other(String)`) with NO Display ŌĆö so enforcing `E: Display` rejects `Result[(), IoError]` (and the all-unit `MyErr` in the B-12-9 codegen test) until payload enums can be Display. `#[derive(Display)]` on a non-all-unit enum is itself rejected today (`derives.rs:797 validate_derive_display_on_enums`). So the work sequences as three shippable slices:

**Slice A ŌĆö payload-enum Display (PREREQUISITE, = the long-deferred Display-floor "subtask 5").** Make arbitrary user enums (tuple + struct variants) render via Display, matching the interpreter format (interp already does this ŌĆö `Value::EnumVariant` Display in `src/interpreter/value.rs`: `variant` / `variant(v0, v1)` / `variant { f: v }`). (A1) Lift the all-unit restriction in `validate_derive_display_on_enums` (`derives.rs:797`) so `#[derive(Display)]` is accepted on payload enums. (A2) Codegen: a value-driven `void karac_display_<enum>(ptr val, ptr acc)` fn ŌĆö load tag (field 0), switch per variant, append the variant name, and for payload variants reconstruct each field from the unified payload words via `EnumLayout.field_word_offsets` (`src/codegen/state.rs:169`, same extraction `bind_pattern_values`'s `TupleVariant` arm uses, `control_flow_match.rs:1156`) + recurse through `emit_display_fn_for_type_expr` with the buffer-append helpers (`disp_append_lit`, model on `emit_vec_display_body` `synth_display.rs:314`). Route the `Named` user-enum arm of `emit_display_fn_for_type_expr` (which currently panics, `synth_display.rs:288`) here, and extend the f-string/println/to_string enum dispatch beyond all-unit (today `expr_user_enum_name` only returns Some for all-unit; payload enums need the alloca + `render_via_display_fn` path). (A3) interp parity check + tests. This also lets the B-2026-06-12-9 main Err exit render payload-enum errors (removing its bare-`Error:` fallback for that class) and lets `IoError` derive Display.

  **Core LANDED 2026-06-13.** `emit_enum_display_fn` (value-driven, read-only payload extraction ŌĆö heap-payload-safe, no move/free, the `IoError.Other(String)` shape works), routed from `emit_display_fn_for_type_expr`'s `Named` arm; f-string + `println` dispatch extended to payload enums (`expr_user_enum_name_any` + `render_user_enum_display`); A1 derive restriction lifted (`validate_derive_display_on_enums` now a no-op); interp `display_render` gained an `EnumVariant` arm rendering struct-variant fields in DECLARATION order (was hash order ŌĆö a latent interp/codegen parity bug, now fixed). Tests: `tests/codegen.rs::test_e2e_enum_display_payload_variants`, `tests/typechecker.rs::test_derive_display_payload_variant_accepted`. **Slice-A follow-ons (deferred, do before Slice C leans on them):** (i) **unannotated struct-variant-enum let** (`let b = E.S { .. }` with no `: E` annotation) doesn't register `var_type_names` ŌåÆ `println(b)` / `f"{b}"` fail codegen with the struct-arg "bind to a let first" error; the `StructLiteral`-RHS let arm classifies the variant name (not in `struct_types`) and the enum-name fallback added at `stmts.rs` ~1999 isn't on the path this RHS actually takes ŌĆö needs the real registration site. Workaround: annotate, OR a tuple variant (those work unannotated). (ii) **`to_string()` on payload enums** ŌĆö the typechecker still gates `to_string` typing to all-unit enums; extend it + route codegen through `render_user_enum_display`.

**Slice B ŌĆö `ExitCode` stdlib type.** Represent as `distinct type ExitCode = i32` (transparent zero-cost, `distinct_bases` in codegen ŌåÆ lowers to i32; constructor `ExitCode(code)` is a zero-cost wrap). `ExitCode.from(code: i32) -> ExitCode` = a real K─üra body `{ ExitCode(code) }` (no builtin needed). `ExitCode.SUCCESS` / `FAILURE` are paren-free associated CONSTANTS ŌåÆ add a dedicated arm to the `i64.MAX`-style intercepts (typechecker `fields.rs:19` / `const_eval.rs:624`, interp `eval_expr.rs:193`, codegen `expr_ops.rs:329`) that yields an *ExitCode*-typed `0`/`1` (NOT `primitive_const_type`ŌåÆi32, or the `main() -> ExitCode { ExitCode.SUCCESS }` body mistypes). New `runtime/stdlib/exitcode.kara` + register in `prelude.rs` (`PRELUDE_TYPES`, `STDLIB_SOURCES`). Codegen: a third `main` return arm in `src/codegen/functions.rs` (~line 1134) ŌĆö `main() -> ExitCode` extracts the i32 and `ret i32 <code>` (ExitCode is transparently i32). Interp: `Interpreter::run`/`cmd_run` map a returned `ExitCode` to `process::exit(code)`.

  **LANDED 2026-06-13.** `runtime/stdlib/exitcode.kara` (`distinct type ExitCode = i32;` + `impl ExitCode { fn from(code: i32) -> ExitCode { ExitCode(code) } }`); registered in `PRELUDE_TYPES` + `STDLIB_SOURCES`; `lookup_exitcode_const` (`prelude.rs`) maps `SUCCESS`ŌåÆ0 / `FAILURE`ŌåÆ1. **Reality vs the plan:** `ExitCode.SUCCESS` parses as a 2-segment **`Path`**, not a `FieldAccess` (the leading segment is a known type name), so the intercepts live at the Path sites ŌĆö typechecker `resolve_path_type` (`expr_ops.rs`), interp `eval_expr.rs` Path arm, codegen `compile_path_expr` (`exprs.rs`) ŌĆö each returning the `ExitCode`-typed value/`i32` const (the `fields.rs`/`eval_expr.rs` FieldAccess arms were added too as a defensive mirror). `main_returns_exitcode` flag (`codegen.rs`) drives the third `main` tail arm; `cmd_run` consults `main_return_is_exitcode(program)` on the AST and maps a returned `Value::Int` to `process::exit(code)`. `ExitCode.from` is a codegen call-site intercept (`call_dispatch.rs`, mirroring the distinct constructor + `try_from`), not a compiled baked body. Baked-stdlib distinct types are now registered into codegen `distinct_bases` and interp `stdlib_distinct_types` so `ExitCode(code)` resolves. **`coerce_to_distinct_base`** (`expr_ops.rs`) narrows a default-`i64` literal arg to the distinct base width at the constructor + `from` ŌĆö without it a `match` mixing `ExitCode.SUCCESS` (`i32`) with `ExitCode.from(3)` (`i64`-literal) produced incompatible phi inputs. Tests: `tests/codegen.rs::test_e2e_main_exitcode_*` (5), `tests/interpreter.rs::test_exitcode_*` (2), `tests/typechecker.rs::test_exitcode_constants_type_as_exitcode`.

  **Surfaced + fixed mid-slice ŌĆö `Ok(())` / unit-payload + generic-payload pattern exhaustiveness (general, pre-existing).** The canonical design.md ┬¦ Entry Point demo shape ŌĆö `match run() { Ok(()) => ExitCode.SUCCESS, Err(e) => ŌĆ” }` ŌĆö was wrongly flagged non-exhaustive (`Ok(_)` not covered) AND miscompiled (the `Err` value fell through to a placeholder; AOT exited 1). Root cause in `src/exhaustive.rs`, in two spots, both unrelated to ExitCode: (1) `variant_payload_types` / `ctor_field_types`'s `Variant` arm returned the enum's **raw generic param** (`Ok`'s `T`) instead of substituting the instantiated arg (`()`), so the payload column was an open `TypeParam` domain ŌĆö fixed by substituting `info.generic_params` Ōå” the `Type::Named` args (new `subst_type_params` helper), and routing `ctor_field_types`'s `Variant` arm through `variant_payload_types`; (2) `enumerate_ctors` lacked a `Type::Unit` arm (Unit's sole constructor is the empty tuple) ŌĆö added. Net: generic-payload matches now resolve to their concrete payload domain, so finite payloads (`Option[bool]`) are exhaustively checkable without a wildcard and `Ok(())` covers `Ok(_)`. Regression tests: `tests/typechecker.rs::test_match_ok_unit_payload_exhaustive` / `test_match_generic_finite_payload_*`; `tests/codegen.rs::test_e2e_match_ok_unit_payload_*`; `tests/interpreter.rs::test_match_ok_unit_payload_selects_correct_arm`.

**Slice C ŌĆö entry-point enforcement + IoError Display + test migration.** (C1) Typechecker: at `main()` registration reject any return type outside `()` / `Result[(), E]` / `ExitCode` (`E_MAIN_RETURN_TYPE`), and discharge `E: Display` via `type_supports_display` (`E_MAIN_ERR_NOT_DISPLAY`, with the `impl Display for E` fix-it). Note `Unit` spelled `Unit` must count as `()`. (C2) Add `#[derive(Display)]` to `IoError` (now possible after Slice A) and to any other prelude error enum used as a `main` error (`VarError`, etc.). (C3) Migrate the ~40 non-conforming inline test `main`s found in recon ŌĆö mostly `tests/typechecker.rs` GAT/`?`-tests + `tests/codegen.rs` IR tests + `lowering.rs`/`rc_predicate_parity.rs`/`cfg.rs`: rename `fn main()` ŌåÆ a non-entry name (`fn f()`) for the typecheck/lowering scaffolds, real migration for the codegen run/IR tests; add `#[derive(Display)]` to test error enums; confirm `Result[Unit, String]` (mcjit) is treated as conforming. **Negative tests** for both new diagnostics.

  **Slice C LANDED 2026-06-13.** (C1) `check_main_entry_return_type` in `src/typechecker/items.rs` (called from `check_function`, gated on a free fn named `main` ŌĆö `self_type`/`self_param` exclude methods) rejects any return type outside `()` / `Unit` / `Result[(), E]` / `ExitCode` with `E_MAIN_RETURN_TYPE` (`E0266`), and discharges `E: Display` via `type_supports_display` with `E_MAIN_ERR_NOT_DISPLAY` (`E0267`, help text suggests `#[derive(Display)]`). New `TypeErrorKind::{MainReturnType, MainErrNotDisplay}` + cli.rs code mapping. `is_entry_unit` accepts both `()` (`Type::Unit`) and the bare `Unit` identifier spelling (`Type::Named{"Unit"}`); a `Type::Error` return is skipped (no double-report). (C2) `#[derive(Display)]` added to `runtime/stdlib/io_error.kara` (payload enum ŌĆö possible post-Slice-A) + `var_error.kara`. (C3) ~33 non-conforming test `main`s migrated: typecheck/lowering/IR scaffolds renamed `main` ŌåÆ `app_main` (28 in `tests/typechecker.rs`, 4 i32 IR tests + 1 i64 IR test in `tests/codegen.rs`, `lowering.rs`, `rc_predicate_parity.rs` ŌĆö paired `extract_fn_ir`/`fn_body_final`/`predicate_uam` assertions updated); the codegen E2E main-`Err` tests got `#[derive(Display)]` on their `MyErr` / `IoError` error types. Negative + positive tests in `tests/typechecker.rs::test_main_entry_*` / `test_main_return_contract_does_not_bind_non_entry_functions`. Full `--features llvm` suite green (66 binaries, 0 failed). `examples/word_count.kara`'s `main() -> Result[(), IoError]` now passes the entry-point check (its pre-existing `undefined name 'read_file'` is a separate, unrelated example gap).

- [x] **Codegen Display for baked-stdlib enums (surfaced by entry-point Slice C, 2026-06-13; LANDED 2026-06-14, B-2026-06-14-16).** `#[derive(Display)]` on a baked-stdlib enum (`IoError`, `VarError`, ŌĆ”) is type-correct and renders correctly in the **interpreter** (`Error: Other(disk full)` / `Error: NotPresent`), but the **codegen** Display path could not render baked enums: `emit_enum_display_fn` (`src/codegen/synth_display.rs`) sourced variant defs only from `program_snapshot` (the user AST, which excludes baked stdlib), and `expr_user_enum_name_any` explicitly excluded `seeded_enum_names`. Net: a compiled `fn main() -> Result[(), IoError]` returning `Err` printed `Error: 0` (multi-word) / `Error: ` (all-unit) instead of the variant rendering, and a bare `f"{io_err}"` / `println(io_err)` rendered the same placeholder. Pre-existing and broader than `main` ŌĆö it was *latent* because baked error enums weren't `Display`-eligible until Slice C's C2 derives; now reachable. **Exit codes are correct (0/1); only the rendered message degrades in AOT.** Companion gap observed in the same recon: an `IoError.Other(_)` payload-variant **match** misfired in AOT (selected the wrong arm).

  **Root cause was deeper than the original sketch.** Recon assumed `IoError` was a *seeded* layout with imprecise tags; it was in fact **never seeded at all** (not in `seed_builtin_enum_layouts`, not in the user program). So a user-written `IoError.Other("ŌĆ”")` had no layout, construction fell to the `i64 0` placeholder, a payload `match` couldn't bind (`Undefined variable 'm'`), and Display had no variant set ŌĆö *all three symptoms shared one cause*. **Fix as landed:** (1) **seed the `IoError` layout** in `src/codegen/declarations.rs::seed_builtin_enum_layouts` (mirrors the `Utf8Error` `Other(String)` template ŌĆö 4-word struct, tags `NotFound=0 ŌĆ” Other=6`, `Other` drops `VecOrString`); (2) **`emit_enum_display_fn` falls back to `crate::prelude::STDLIB_PROGRAMS`** for variant names+kinds when the enum isn't in `program_snapshot` (`src/codegen/synth_display.rs`); (3) **`expr_user_enum_name_any` re-admits Display-deriving baked enums** via a new `baked_display_enum_names` set (populated once from `STDLIB_PROGRAMS` via `extract_derived_traits`) so the f-string/`println` dispatch reaches the generic Display path despite the seeded status; (4) **qualified `Enum.Variant` resolution** in both construction (`try_compile_enum_variant` gains an `enum_name_override`; the qualified `compile_assoc_call` path passes the known enum) and match (`compile_pattern_condition`'s Binding/TupleVariant/Struct arms prefer `variant_pattern_enum_and_tag`) so the `Other`/`PermissionDenied` collisions across `IoError`/`Utf8Error`/`TcpError`/`TlsError` resolve deterministically instead of by HashMap order. E2E regression `tests/codegen.rs::e2e_baked_stdlib_enum_display_and_qualified_match` covers f-string/println Display, qualified unit+payload+collision match, and the `main`-Err exit; interpreter and AOT now agree (`Other(disk full)` / `NotFound` / `NotPresent`). The Slice-A follow-on (i) `var_type_names` registration for unannotated enum lets was already adequate in practice (an unannotated `let e = IoError.Other(ŌĆ”)` displays correctly post-fix).

Phase target: Slice A = Phase 7 codegen + Phase 3 typechecker; Slice B = Phase 8 (`ExitCode`) + Phase 7; Slice C = typechecker + migration. Cross-ref: design.md ┬¦ Entry Point; the B-2026-06-12-9 codegen adaptation (`src/codegen/functions.rs` `emit_main_result_return` / `emit_main_result_err_exit`); the Script-mode entry directly above (its synthesized `main() -> Result[Unit, Error]` must satisfy the same contract once enforcement lands); `phase-7-codegen.md:468/473` (the struct + all-unit-enum + collection Display already shipped, which Slice A extends to payload enums).

- [ ] **`std.regex`.** Compile regex patterns to an NFA/DFA state machine; `Regex.compile(pattern) -> Result[Regex, RegexError]`, `rx.is_match(s)`, `rx.find(s) -> Option[Match]`, `rx.find_all(s) -> Vec[Match]`, `rx.captures(s)`, `rx.replace_all(s, replacement)`. Use a tested regex crate as the initial backend; eventually replace with a K─üra-native implementation. Pure (no effects).

- [ ] **`std.http` (client only).** `Client.new()`, `client.get(url)`, `client.post(url, body)`, chained builders for headers / body / timeout. `Request.send() -> Result[Response, HttpError] with sends(Network), receives(Network)`. Response exposes `status_code`, `headers`, `text()`, `bytes()`. TLS via stdlib-adjacent crate. **Superseded framing ŌĆö "Server is v1.5+" is stale:** the v64 backend-first reshape (┬¦ Backend Platform) lifted both server *and* client into the Phase-8 floor, so this entry is now the client-surface spec for the `Client.get` / `Client.post` sub-item under the [┬¦ Backend Platform `std.http`](#backend-platform-v64-lifted) parent (currently a stub `get` + interpreter-only `post`). Implement against this spec there.

- [x] **`std.http` server ŌĆö minimal surface (pulled forward from v1.5 for Parallax demo).** Ō£ō Landed 2026-05-09 (commit `3c3d87b`). One-line summary: hyper-backed FFI surface in karac-runtime (`karac_runtime_serve_http_static` + `karac_runtime_serve_http` + `KaracHttpRequest` / `KaracHttpResponse` C-ABI structs); B3 fallback (b) taken ŌĆö non-polymorphic `Server.serve_static(addr, body)` that erases effects at the FFI boundary, since free-fn fn-pointer-as-arg + effect-set parameterization isn't typechecker-supported yet (Theme 6 settled the trait-method shape but free-fn shape is the open delta); B5 smoke test in `tests/http_server.rs` passes ŌĆö compiles a K─üra binary, binds `127.0.0.1:0`, GET `/dashboard/1` returns 200 + the demo-shaped JSON body.

- [x] **`std.json`.** Ō£ō Landed 2026-05-09 (commit `91768f2`). Interpreter dispatch `Json.parse` + `j.stringify()` over a `Json` enum baked at `runtime/stdlib/json.kara`; runtime crate exposes the same surface through `karac_runtime_json_*` C-ABI exports for codegen-side wiring (deferred). Six tests in `tests/json.rs` cover round-trip + insertion-order + error-line/col + manual `ToJson` impl. Variant-payload-struct shape chosen for `KaracJsonValue` per the slice plan's recommendation; `serde_json` carries `preserve_order` in both crates so `Json.Object` iterates in insertion order. Inline-fix in `typechecker::resolve_identifier_type` skips enum-variant fallback when the bare name matches a primitive / prelude type ŌĆö needed because `Json.String(String)` would otherwise shadow `String.from(...)` calls (predecessor test surface didn't exercise the collision).

- [x] **`std.json` codegen-side wiring ŌĆö `Json.parse` / `j.stringify()` from compiled binaries.** Ō£ō Landed 2026-05-21 across two commits (`5562309` for stringify side, follow-up for parse). Compiled-binary `Json.parse(s)` and `j.stringify()` work end-to-end across the full variant surface. Stringify side: a single synthesized LLVM helper `__karac_json_kara_to_ffi(tag, w0, w1, w2) -> *mut KaracJsonValue` dispatches on the variant tag and emits per-variant calls into eight new runtime constructors (`karac_runtime_json_make_null` / `_make_bool` / `_make_number` / `_make_string` / `_make_array` / `_make_object`, plus `_alloc_items_buf` / `_alloc_keys_buf` / `_alloc_key` for the Array/Object buffer transfer). Array (32-byte Json stride) and Object (56-byte (String, Json) tuple stride) arms walk their underlying `Vec[T]` payload and recurse via direct LLVM self-call. All three receiver shapes work: identifier (`let j = Json.Number(3.14); j.stringify()`), Call-shaped non-identifier (`Json.Object(pairs).stringify()`), and 3-segment-Path unit (`Json.Null.stringify()`). Parse side: the inverse synthesized helper `__karac_json_ffi_to_kara(*const KaracJsonValue) -> {i64,i64,i64,i64}` walks the FFI tree, copies String payloads into K─üra-owned buffers, mallocs Vec[Json] / Vec[(String, Json)] backing storage at exact size (cap = len), and recurses on children. The parse-dispatch entry in `src/codegen/call_dispatch.rs` allocates a null-terminated cstr copy of the input, calls `karac_runtime_json_parse`, branches on null return, and merges Ok/Err arms via phi. Result's enum layout in `seed_builtin_enum_layouts` was widened from `{i64, i64}` to `{i64, i64, i64, i64, i64}` (tag + 4 payload words) so the Ok arm can carry the 4-word Json enum value verbatim; existing Result consumers are backwards-compatible by construction (the `?` operator pulls `enum_ty` dynamically from the function return type, par-block surfaces read the slot type from a layout descriptor, single-word constructions write only field 1 with trailing slots staying undef). The Err arm of `Result[Json, JsonError]` truncates JsonError's String `cap` (5-word payload trimmed to 4) ŌĆö acceptable v1 trade-off since the kata's `/echo` arm only discriminates on the tag; a future Result-width sweep can extend further. Two new cross-cutting fixes shipped alongside slice 2: (a) `pattern_payload_word_count` / `pattern_payload_llvm_type` (`src/codegen/control_flow_match.rs`) now look up `enum_layouts` after `struct_types` so enum-typed bindings (`Ok(j)` where j: Json) reconstitute as the full tagged-union struct instead of falling to the i64-default ŌĆö this also unblocks any future `Result[E, E]`-style multi-word Ok payloads; (b) `reconstruct_payload_value`'s multi-word target-type pick was symmetrically extended to consult `enum_layouts`. Layout invariants pinned in runtime: `test_karac_json_value_layout_pinned` locks the 10-field 72-byte `KaracJsonValue` shape and `test_karac_json_error_layout_pinned` locks the 16-byte `KaracJsonError` shape ŌĆö both feed hand-coded byte-stride GEPs in `src/codegen/json.rs`. Tests: 12 codegen E2E tests in `tests/codegen.rs::test_e2e_json_parse_*` covering every variant (null, bool both polarities, number, string + empty-string, array + empty-array, object, deeply-nested, parse-error) plus `test_ir_json_parse_emits_lift_helper_once` pinning the single-walker-definition invariant. Existing `tests/par_codegen.rs::test_ir_par_branch_result_typed_let_emits_slot_and_cancel_store` was updated to reflect the new Result struct shape. Closes the deferral noted in the std.json shipped entry above ("runtime crate exposes the same surface through `karac_runtime_json_*` C-ABI exports for codegen-side wiring (deferred)"). Original detailed slice plan retained below for reference. Closes the deferral noted in the std.json shipped entry directly above ("runtime crate exposes the same surface through `karac_runtime_json_*` C-ABI exports for codegen-side wiring (deferred)"). Surfaced 2026-05-21 by `kara-katas/backend/todo-api/main.kara` build: `error: codegen failed: codegen: no handler for method 'stringify' on variable 'j'` (and `... on non-identifier receiver` for unbound expressions like `Json.Object(p).stringify()`). The interpreter dispatch is shipped and exercised by `tests/json.rs`; this entry adds the compiled-binary path. **Why P0 v1:** every backend kata + flagship demo that emits JSON over a real HTTP server needs `Json.stringify()` to work in compiled mode (the interpreter has no `Server.serve` arm ŌĆö confirmed via probe 2026-05-21 that `karac run` on a `Server.serve` program panics with `internal error: ... path 'Server.serve' not found ... should be caught by resolver`). Slices: (1) **Lowering ŌĆö `Json` enum Ōåö `KaracJsonValue`.** The K─üra-side `pub enum Json { Null, Bool(bool), Number(f64), String(String), Array(Vec[Json]), Object(Vec[(String, Json)]) }` (`runtime/stdlib/json.kara:30-39`) and the runtime-side `KaracJsonValue` C struct (`runtime/src/lib.rs:1805-1822`, variant-tagged struct per locked design at line 1786) need a bidirectional lowering: a K─üra `Json` value lowered into a `*mut KaracJsonValue` to pass to runtime externs, and a returned `*mut KaracJsonValue` translated back into a K─üra `Json` value for the user. The variant-tag enum layout already exists at the LLVM IR level for ordinary K─üra enums; this slice adds the FFI-translation pair (likely a runtime-side `karac_runtime_json_from_native(...)` taking the K─üra variant tag + payload-pointer triple, and a `..._to_native(value)` for the inverse). Memory ownership per the runtime's locked rule: both `karac_runtime_json_parse` and `karac_runtime_json_stringify` allocate Boxed trees / `CString`s and the caller frees via `karac_runtime_json_free_value` / `..._free_string` (see `runtime/src/lib.rs:1769-1772`). (2) **`Json.parse(s)` codegen.** New compile-time dispatch: when a free fn call resolves to the path `Json.parse`, lower to `karac_runtime_json_parse(s.data, s.len) -> KaracJsonResult { tag, value_ptr, error_line, error_column, error_msg_ptr, error_msg_len }`. Translate `KaracJsonResult` into the K─üra-side `Result[Json, JsonError]` via the lowering from slice (1). Free the runtime allocation after translation. (3) **`j.stringify()` codegen.** New method-call dispatch: when the receiver type resolves to `Json` (whether the receiver is an identifier `j`, a let-bound variable, or a non-identifier expression like `Json.Object(pairs).stringify()`), lower to `karac_runtime_json_stringify(value_ptr) -> *mut c_char` after lowering the receiver into a `*mut KaracJsonValue` via slice (1)'s `..._from_native` helper. The returned C string is owned by the runtime; copy bytes into a fresh K─üra `String { data, len, cap }` (mirroring `compile_request_string_method` in `src/codegen/http.rs`) and call `karac_runtime_json_free_string` to release the runtime's allocation. (4) **Non-identifier-receiver path.** `Json.Object(p).stringify()` currently fires `error: codegen failed: codegen: no handler for method 'stringify' on non-identifier receiver` because the method-call dispatch falls through before any Json-typed handling is reached. Plumb the non-identifier path through the same `compile_method_call` arm as the identifier path ŌĆö both lower to the same `..._from_native + extern call + String-copy` sequence; the only difference is whether the receiver value is read from a slot (identifier case) or assembled into a temp (non-identifier case). (5) **Tests in `tests/codegen.rs`.** New section `Phase 8 line 431 follow-up ŌĆö std.json codegen`: positive ŌĆö `let j = Json.Number(3.14); println(j.stringify());` produces `3.14`; `Json.Object([(\"a\", Json.Number(1.0))]).stringify()` produces `{"a":1.0}` (non-identifier-receiver path); `Json.parse("[1,2,3]")` round-trips via `match` + `Json.Array` destructure. Negative ŌĆö `Json.parse("not json")` emits `JsonError` with non-zero line/col. The existing `tests/json.rs` (interpreter) tests stay green unchanged ŌĆö this entry's tests live in `codegen.rs` and run under `--features llvm`. (6) **Reused infrastructure.** The same `..._from_native` / `..._to_native` helpers will be reused by future `#[derive(ToJson)]` codegen (v1.5 per the original `std.json` ship note's locked design (v)). Doc those helpers as the stable internal surface for that follow-up. Phase target: Phase 7 (codegen) for slices (2)-(4); Phase 8 (stdlib) for the runtime-side translation helpers in slice (1). Cross-reference: `runtime/src/lib.rs:1765-1830` (`KaracJsonValue` + ownership rules); `runtime/stdlib/json.kara` (`Json` enum decl); `src/codegen/http.rs::compile_request_string_method` (the `String`-copy pattern this slice mirrors); `tests/json.rs` (existing interpreter coverage ŌĆö the v1 contract this slice extends to compiled mode); `kara-katas/backend/todo-api/main.kara` (first consumer to surface the gap); `wip-todo-api-kata.md ┬¦ Decisions log 2026-05-21 (later)` (write-up of the kata's workaround pattern).

> **Moved (2026-06-06):** `std.stats`, the GPU call-site backend deferral, the lazy-evaluation (Q8) v1.5 deferral, and the Phase-11 fallback-plan note now live in [`phase-11-stdlib-longtail.md ┬¦ Numerical and data-science stdlib`](phase-11-stdlib-longtail.md#numerical-and-data-science-stdlib). The `std.regex` / `std.http` / `std.json` entries above stay ŌĆö they are Phase 8 floor (v64 lift).

- [ ] **G23 ŌĆö Trait coherence / orphan rules**. Decide and enforce: can you implement a foreign trait for a foreign type? Recommendation: Rust's orphan rule (must own either the trait or the type). Document the newtype workaround. Not relevant until multi-package support exists ŌĆö moved from Phase 3.

> **Self-hosting prerequisites (2026-06-10).** This note marks the FFI **call-out** items immediately below (`#[repr(C)]` / `#[repr(transparent)]`, callback passing, String marshaling, error-code mapping) as **self-hosting blockers** ŌĆö the compiler-in-K─üra's codegen binds LLVM-C through them. The other prereqs live elsewhere in this file, each tagged `[self-hosting prereq ŌåÆ phase-12]` at its own location: `CString` + raw-pointer deref (further below), `From` / `TryFrom` + `Error` trait, `Iterator.next()`, and `Map.new()` / `Set.new()` + plain `insert` / `get` / `contains`. **NOT prereqs:** the *fallible* `Map.try_insert` / `Set.try_insert` (compiler aborts on OOM); K─üra-to-C *exports* and C-header generation (the compiler calls *into* LLVM, never *from* C). See [`phase-12-self-hosting.md` ┬¦ Pre-pivot blockers](phase-12-self-hosting.md#pre-pivot-blockers-fix-before) and the [LLVM-C FFI spike](../spikes/self-hosting-llvm-c-ffi.md).

- [ ] **G14 ŌĆö FFI effect annotation completeness**. Create comprehensive syscall-to-effect mapping table. Review POSIX/Linux syscall man pages for composite effects (e.g., `sendfile()` needs both `reads(FileSystem)` and `sends(Network)`). Build integration tests that validate effect annotations against actual syscall behavior.

- [x] **FFI ŌĆö K─üra-to-C exports. Ō£ō SUBSTANTIALLY DONE** (reconciled 2026-07-11 ŌĆö audit found it implemented, not open). `pub extern "C" fn` parses; codegen emits C-ABI symbols (`functions.rs`: `#[unsafe(no_mangle)]`, external linkage, C-callability for non-`pub` too); `cheader::validate_exports` / `export_symbols` enforce C-representable param/return types. **Residual:** opaque-handle ownership mechanics ("additive-interop Slice 4 `forget`" ŌĆö the boxing/handoff behind a `KaraHandle`). Original text: Enable K─üra functions to be callable from C. Requires: `#[export]` or `pub extern "C"` annotation, compiler generates C-compatible calling convention, restrictions on parameter/return types (must be C-representable). Needed for shared libraries, plugins, and embedding K─üra in C/C++ applications.

- [x] **FFI ŌĆö C header generation. Ō£ō DONE** (reconciled 2026-07-11 ŌĆö audit found it implemented). Full `src/cheader.rs` cbindgen-analogue (`emit_c_header` / `validate_exports` / `export_symbols`), CLI-wired on staticlib/cdylib builds, with the honest v1 type mapping (primitives + raw pointers + `#[repr(C)]` cross transparently; everything else ŌåÆ opaque `KaraHandle` void*). Original text: Tooling to auto-generate `.h` header files from `extern "C"` K─üra exports (like Rust's `cbindgen`). Maps K─üra types to C equivalents. Needed for C consumers of K─üra libraries.

- [x] **FFI ŌĆö `#[repr(C)]` struct layout. Ō£ō SUBSTANTIALLY DONE** (reconciled 2026-07-11 ŌĆö audit found it implemented). Codegen has the full `#[repr(C)]` struct-by-value ABI (per-target AArch64 + SysV classifiers in `driver.rs`/`functions.rs`/`call_dispatch.rs`), `#[repr(C)]` unions, and the C-boundary ABI for exports; the parser + `has_repr_c` detect it. Original text: Attribute to guarantee C-compatible memory layout for structs passed across FFI boundaries. Without this, K─üra's compiler is free to reorder/pad fields (especially with layout blocks). `#[repr(C)]` pins layout to match C's rules.

- [x] **FFI ŌĆö `#[repr(transparent)]` for distinct-type FFI. Ō£ō DONE (2026-07-11).** Landed across three layers: (1) **Parser** ŌĆö the "already lexes" claim below was WRONG (`transparent` is a reserved keyword ŌĆö it also introduces `transparent effect` ŌĆö so `#[repr(transparent)]` was a parse error); fixed with a targeted keyword-accept in `parser/attributes.rs`. (2) **Typechecker** ŌĆö `items.rs` `check_repr_transparent_*` carrier-shape validation with all six focused codes wired; one `TypeErrorKind::ReprTransparentInvalid` (E0803), symbolic code in the message. (3) **Codegen** ŌĆö no new work needed (distinct types are already zero-cost, single-field structs already lay out as their field); `.raw()`/field-access unwrap at `extern "C"` lowers with no conversion, verified E2E through libc `abs` with `size_of[Wrapper] == size_of[Inner]`. Tests: parser ├Ś2, typechecker ├Ś12, codegen-E2E ├Ś1. **Residuals:** `PhantomData` isn't yet a prelude type (recognized by name for when it lands; `()` covers the companion allowance today); `_REQUIRES_SIZED` approximates "no `T: Sized` bound" as "bare-type-param carrier" (K─üra has no `Sized`-bound surface). Obsolete original sub-step note follows: Spec lives at design.md ┬¦ `#[repr(transparent)]` for distinct-type FFI (v60 item 23). Sub-steps: (1) Parser ŌĆö `#[repr(transparent)]` already lexes per the existing `#[repr]` infrastructure; the typechecker is the new work. (2) Typechecker carrier-shape validation at item-decl time: accept on `distinct type`, single-field `struct` (single non-zero-sized field; zero-sized companion fields are permitted iff every companion has size zero AND alignment one ŌĆö `PhantomData[T]`, `()`, `[T; 0]`, an empty unit struct), and single-variant single-field `enum`. Reject multi-field struct (`error[E_REPR_TRANSPARENT_REQUIRES_SINGLE_FIELD]`); zero-field struct (`error[E_REPR_TRANSPARENT_REQUIRES_FIELD]`); enum with !=1 variant or with payload-less variant (`error[E_REPR_TRANSPARENT_ENUM_NOT_SINGLE_VARIANT]`); union (`error[E_REPR_TRANSPARENT_UNION_FORBIDDEN]`); generic carrier whose inner is a type parameter `T` without a `T: Sized` bound (`error[E_REPR_TRANSPARENT_REQUIRES_SIZED]`). Combination with any other repr (`#[repr(C)]`, `#[repr(packed)]`, `#[repr(align(N))]`, `#[repr(intN)]`) is rejected (`error[E_REPR_TRANSPARENT_EXCLUSIVE]`). (3) Layout ŌĆö codegen records the wrapper as a layout-pass-through to the inner field (no separate type registered in the LLVM type table; the wrapper's LLVM type *is* the inner type). The inner type's repr passes through unchanged: a `transparent` wrapper around a `#[repr(C)]` inner has the same layout as the inner. (4) FFI ABI integration ŌĆö at `extern "C"` call sites, an argument of the wrapper type whose declared `extern` parameter type is the inner type is permitted with an explicit unwrap (`.raw()` for `distinct type`, named-field access for single-field struct carriers); the type system enforces the unwrap, but codegen lowers without conversion (the bit-pattern is identical). (5) Auto-derive integration ŌĆö `#[derive(...)]` walks the carrier's fields normally for `Eq`/`PartialEq`/`Hash`/`Clone`/`Copy`/`Debug`; the existing distinct-type derive rules continue to govern `distinct type` carriers. (6) Orphan-rule integration ŌĆö no special handling; `transparent` is a layout claim that doesn't change the orphan-rule arithmetic (the wrapper is still a local type for orphan purposes). Test plan: positive ŌĆö `#[repr(transparent)] distinct type Fd = i32` round-trips through an `extern "C" fn close(fd: i32)` signature with `.raw()`; `#[repr(transparent)] struct Tagged[T] { inner: i32, _marker: PhantomData[T] }` accepts the zero-sized companion; layout-pass-through verified via `size_of` and `align_of` on wrapper equals same on inner. Negative ŌĆö multi-field `struct Wrapper { a: i32, b: i32 }` rejected; zero-field `struct Empty {}` rejected; multi-variant `enum E { A(i32), B(i32) }` rejected; `union U` rejected; `#[repr(transparent, C)]` rejected; `#[repr(transparent)] struct Tagged[T] { inner: T }` without `T: Sized` rejected. (Phase 5.2 ŌĆö typechecker work; depends on `#[repr]` parsing infrastructure being stable.)

- [ ] **FFI ŌĆö Callback passing.** Define how K─üra closures (or function values, G51) are passed as C function pointers. Non-capturing functions can map directly to `fn` pointers. Capturing closures need a `void* context` + function pointer pair (standard C callback pattern). Document the effect implications ŌĆö C callbacks are unverified effect boundaries.

- [x] **FFI ŌĆö String marshaling. DONE (verified + round-trip test 2026-07-11).** Realized via the explicit, safer `CStr`/`CString` surface (design.md ┬¦ C-String Literals) rather than the originally-sketched `from_c`/`as_c_str` method names. **Inbound** (C `char*` ŌåÆ K─üra `String`, copies + validates UTF-8): `CStr.from_ptr(p: *const u8) -> ref CStr` (unsafe; libc `strlen` recomputes the length) then `CStr.to_string() -> Result[String, Utf8Error]`. **Outbound** (K─üra `String` ŌåÆ C `char*`, appends NUL): `String.to_cstring() -> Result[CString, NulError]` then `CString.as_ptr() -> *const u8`. Introspection on both (`len`/`is_empty`/`as_bytes`), plus a zero-copy `CStr.to_string_slice() -> Result[StringSlice, Utf8Error]`. **Ownership answered:** the owning `CString` holds its heap buffer and frees it on drop (the shape for handing a runtime-built string to C); `CStr.from_ptr` *borrows* the caller's memory (caller owns; the borrow is tied to the `ref self` receiver). `CStr.from_ptr` is `karac build`-only ŌĆö the tree-walk interpreter has no raw-pointer model and rejects it loudly (real values flow through codegen / `karac run`'s JIT). Wired across typechecker (`infer_cstr_method` / `infer_cstring_method` / `String.to_cstring` / `CStr.from_ptr` assoc-call), interpreter, codegen (`karac_runtime_string_to_cstring` / `karac_runtime_cstr_to_string` + the `{ptr, strlen}` from_ptr aggregate), and the `Value::CString`/`Value::CStr` runtime. Tests: extensive per-piece coverage (`test_e2e_cstr_*`, `test_e2e_string_to_cstring_*`, `test_e2e_cstr_from_ptr_round_trips_*`, memory_sanitizer + unsafe_lint) plus a new `test_e2e_string_marshaling_round_trips_through_cstring` locking the full StringŌåÆCStringŌåÆ`*const u8`ŌåÆCStrŌåÆString identity through the owning-CString path.

- [ ] **FFI ŌĆö Error code mapping.** Define stdlib pattern for converting C-style error codes (`i32` return, `errno`) to K─üra `Result[T, E]`. Provide a `CError` type or trait-based conversion. Stdlib wrappers should use this consistently for all POSIX wrappers.

- [ ] **Dynamic dispatch / trait objects.** Implement trait object support. All design decisions are settled: (1) syntax is `dyn Trait` ŌĆö the explicit keyword is required, and a bare trait name in a type position is a compile error; (2) unbound `dyn T` (no trait constraint) is not allowed ŌĆö erasure without interface knowledge is useless; (3) multiple bounds allowed: `dyn Shape + Display`; (4) object safety: traits with generic methods cannot be used as trait objects ŌĆö compiler emits a clear diagnostic; (5) owned `dyn Trait` requires heap allocation and produces `allocates(Heap)`; `ref dyn Trait` borrows an already-allocated value and does not; (6) effect semantics use an open-world model (design.md): the programmer declares the effect bound at the trait definition (`trait Handler with reads(UserDB), sends(AuditLog) { ... }`), all impls must have effects ŌŖå that bound, and call sites use the declared trait bound as the effect set ŌĆö no whole-program analysis needed; (7) trait objects cannot use `layout` blocks ŌĆö concrete type is unknown at compile time. Implementation tasks: vtable layout and codegen (Phase 7 prerequisite), object safety checker in the type checker, `allocates(Heap)` inference for owned `dyn Trait` positions. Depends on Phase 3 trait system and Phase 7 LLVM codegen being stable.

- [ ] **G10 ŌĆö Cycle detection with generic containers and trait objects.** Document the `dyn Trait` limitation in the ownership section. The compiler can't see through `dyn Trait` to detect cycles. Recommend `shared struct` with `weak` or `Arena` for patterns where trait objects create cycles. Consider whether the compiler should warn when `dyn Trait` appears in a position that could form a cycle.

- [ ] **G24 ŌĆö Compile time strategy**. Validate that `pub` boundaries as inference firewalls effectively bound compilation cost. Benchmark full compilation on non-trivial programs. Ensure architecture supports incremental compilation, cached analysis, and parallel module compilation.

- [ ] **G25 ŌĆö Standard Error trait**. Define `trait Error` with `message()` and `source()` chaining. Define `trait From[T]` for error conversion via `?` operator. Implement for all stdlib error types. **[self-hosting prereq ŌåÆ [phase-12](phase-12-self-hosting.md#pre-pivot-blockers-fix-before)]** ŌĆö the compiler uses `?` across error types everywhere.

- [ ] **String interpolation format specifiers.** Design and implement `{expr:spec}` syntax in `f"..."` strings. Open questions: syntax form (Rust-style `{x:.2}`, Python-style `{x:.2f}`, or K─üra-specific); whether format specifiers desugar to a `Format` trait separate from `Display`; interaction with `#[derive(Display)]`; width, precision, fill, alignment, sign, radix. The syntax space is reserved ŌĆö `{expr:spec}` is a compile error until this is implemented.

- [ ] **Conversion traits (`From`/`Into`/`TryFrom`/`TryInto`).** Implement the four conversion traits and the blanket impl (`impl From[T]` ŌåÆ automatic `Into`). Enforce: implementing `Into` directly is a compile error. Wire `?` operator to desugar cross-error-type propagation to `From.from()`. Refinement types auto-generate `TryFrom` impls. See design.md ŌĆö "Conversion Traits". **[self-hosting prereq ŌåÆ [phase-12](phase-12-self-hosting.md#pre-pivot-blockers-fix-before)]** ŌĆö `?`-operator cross-error-type propagation in the compiler.
  - **Slice 1 shipped** (commit `deff0e3`): `From` dispatch via `T.from(x)` with source-type disambiguation; 19 built-in numeric widening impls; user `impl From[E1] for E2` resolves; `?` typechecker validates cross-error `From` and records conversion target in `TypeCheckResult.question_conversions`; interpreter consults that side-table and calls `<Target>.from(e)` before propagating Err.
  - **Slice 3a shipped:** `.into()` with expected-type threading. `TypeChecker` gained `check_expr(expr, expected)` that recognizes a zero-arg `.into()` method call against a Named / primitive expected type and records the target in `TypeCheckResult.into_conversions` (span ŌåÆ target-type name). Expected-type threading is wired at four positions: (1) `let x: T = ...`, (2) `let x: T = ...` in `let-else`, (3) `Assign { target, value }` (target-type-driven), (4) function call argument slot against the parameter type, (5) explicit `return expr;` against the current function's return type, (6) function body final expression against the declared return type (via `check_block_against`). Lowering then rewrites `x.into()` to `Target.from(x)` ŌĆö the `Into` blanket impl is purely a lowering rewrite, no impl entries materialized at typecheck time. Codegen falls through naturally: numeric widening is a passthrough in `compile_assoc_call`, user-type `T.from(x)` routes to the impl-block-compiled `T.from` LLVM function. Missing `impl From[S] for T` emits a targeted diagnostic with the source and target type names. `let` codegen now uses the type annotation as a fallback type hint when the RHS shape isn't classifiable (fixes user-struct `var_type_names` registration for `let c: Cm = i.into();`).
  - **Slice 3b shipped:** user `impl Into for T` and `impl TryInto for T` rejected at the resolver. Distinct from the operator-trait restriction (those only fire on ArithOps / Index / Display); Into/TryInto use their own `ResolveErrorKind::IntoTraitImplNotAllowed` (code `E0109`) with a suggestion to implement `From` / `TryFrom` instead.
  - **Follow-ups not in slice 3:**
    - `TryFrom` / `TryInto` with associated `Error` type; numeric narrowing impls.
    - `From[T] for Option[T]` and `From[T] for Result[T, E]` wrapping.
    - `From[StringLit] for String` / from char literals.
    - `.into()` expected-type threading at more positions (match arm bodies, struct-literal field values, if/match final expressions).
    - Codegen `?` operator ŌĆö **RESOLVED (verified 2026-07-09); this gate is stale.** It was gated on `Result`/`Option` as built-in enum layouts in codegen, which are now registered by `Codegen::seed_builtin_enum_layouts` (`src/codegen/declarations.rs:3473`; the layouts are also asserted `[x]` at the standalone "`?` operator codegen" item below, Step 1). The full `compile_question` path shipped in that item (all steps `[x]`), so the feared `_ => const 0` fallback no longer applies ŌĆö `try_compile_enum_variant` finds the seeded built-in enums via the same path as user enums.

- [x] **Extend operator lowering to comparison, equality, bitwise (slice 2 of Phase 8).** `src/lowering.rs` now rewrites arithmetic (`+ - * / %`), equality (`== !=`), comparison (`< <= > >=`), bitwise (`& | ^ << >> ~`), and both unary forms of `not` (`!` on bool ŌåÆ `bool.not`, `~` on int ŌåÆ `T.not`). Short-circuit `&&`/`||` and range `..`/`..=` stay as `Binary` deliberately. Interpreter `dispatch_lowered_op` and codegen `compile_assoc_call` gained method-name maps for the new ops. `infer_closure_return_type` returns bool for `eq`/`ne`/`lt`/`le`/`gt`/`ge` and Self for bitwise/arithmetic/`not`. v1 comparison shortcut: `<`/`<=`/`>`/`>=` lower directly to `T.lt`/`T.le`/`T.gt`/`T.ge` (bool-returning), sidestepping the `Ordering` enum detour until `Ord.cmp`'s own callable path is fleshed out. Eq/Ord impls now register `ne`/`lt`/`le`/`gt`/`ge` as user-callable methods alongside `eq`/`cmp`, and type-receiver dispatch in both interpreter (`eval_method_call`) and codegen (`compile_method_call`) handles every operator method name by delegating to the shared lowered-op fast-path. User-defined `impl Eq for MyStruct` and `impl Ord for MyStruct` are now carved out of the resolver's operator-trait restriction ŌĆö the lowering pass emits `Call(Path([TypeName, method]))` for Named operand types with a registered impl, and `TypeCheckResult.trait_impls` exposes the (trait, target) set so lowering can check without re-querying `env`. `!=` on user types desugars to `!T.eq(a, b)` (mirroring Rust's PartialEq default) so user impls only need to provide `eq`. Remaining follow-ups:
  - `?` codegen (task #9) remains the orthogonal blocker for full Phase 8 close-out ŌĆö see the standalone entry below.

[x] **`error_return_trace` push at each `?` site.** Ō£ō DONE (2026-04-28) ŌĆö runtime extern `karac_error_trace_push(file_ptr, file_len, line, col)` + `karac_error_trace_clear()` backed by a global `Mutex<ErrorTraceState>` ring buffer (depth 64); atexit handler prints to stderr at process exit in the same format as the interpreter's text mode. Note: switched from `thread_local!` to a global mutex because Rust's TLS is torn down before C atexit handlers run. - [x] **`?` codegen follow-up: `error_return_trace` push from compiled binaries.** Shipped 2026-04-28. Runtime side (`runtime/src/lib.rs`): two new externs `karac_error_trace_push(file_ptr, file_len, line, col)` and `karac_error_trace_clear()`, backed by a global `Mutex<ErrorTraceState>` (depth-64 ring buffer). Storage is mutex-protected, *not* `thread_local!` ŌĆö TLS gets torn down before C `atexit` handlers run, which manifests as a "cannot access a Thread Local Storage value during or after destruction" panic; the global mutex stays valid throughout `atexit`. The first `push` lazily registers a printer via libc's `atexit`; the printer emits to stderr in the interpreter's text format (`Error return trace:\n  <file>:<line>:<col>\n...`). Codegen side (`src/codegen.rs`): `compile_question` emits a `karac_error_trace_push` at the failure block before `emit_scope_cleanup`, and a `karac_error_trace_clear` at the OK block. CLI needs no change ŌĆö the binary's stderr passes through. 3 codegen E2E tests in `tests/codegen.rs`. **Filename threading follow-up shipped 2026-04-28** (round 2 ŌĆö see git history `ba2dc9a`): added `compile_to_object_with_options` / `compile_to_ir_with_options` taking `Option<&str>` source filename (existing two-arg APIs delegate, so all 20+ in-tree callers keep working unchanged). `Codegen` carries the filename and a memoized `(PointerValue, len)` for a deduped global string materialized lazily on the first `?` site (`ensure_source_filename_global`). `emit_error_trace_push` consults that helper instead of always passing `(null, 0)`. CLI: `cmd_build` passes the source filename it already has on hand. 1 new E2E test (`test_e2e_question_trace_includes_source_filename_when_threaded`). **JSON / JSONL trace output mode shipped 2026-05-08** (close-out below). All planned follow-ups closed; entry flipped `[~]` ŌåÆ `[x]`.

- [x] **Codegen for user impl-block methods.** Added passes over `Item::ImplBlock` in `CodegenCtx::compile` that declare and compile each method as an LLVM function named `Type.method`; `self`-taking methods get `self` prepended as an owned `Type` parameter (synthetic `Function` built by `make_impl_method_function`). `compile_assoc_call` and `compile_method_call` now fall through to `get_function("Type.method")` and call it, routing both the operator-lowered `Call(Path([T, m]))` shape and source-form receiver calls `obj.method(args)`. `compile_expr` gained an `ExprKind::SelfValue` arm that loads from the `self` local; `field_index_for` maps `self.field` via `var_type_names["self"]`. `ref self` / `mut ref self` deferred ŌĆö all current call sites (Eq/Ord, constructors) take owned receivers, and wiring reference passing needs synthesizing `TypeKind::Ref` around the target type plus coupling with the existing `fn_param_ref` call-site logic. Generic methods on impl blocks also deferred (matches the existing generic-fn monomorphization gap).

- [x] **Associated types in traits.** `type Item` declarations in trait bodies, `type Item = T` bindings in impl blocks, `where C.Item = i64` equality constraints, and bounds on associated type declarations (`type Output: Display`) ŌĆö all parsed and validated. **New in this CR:** `Type::AssocProjection { param, assoc }` added to the `Type` enum; `lower_path_type` recognises `I.Item` where `I` is a generic type parameter; `TypeEnv::impl_assoc_types` stores `(type_name, assoc_name) ŌåÆ Type` from impl blocks; `TypeChecker::resolve_assoc_projections` post-resolves after `substitute_type_params` at generic call sites; `contains_type_param` and `types_compatible` treat `AssocProjection` permissively (like `TypeParam`). 12 typechecker tests added. Open: `Iterator` / `IntoIterator` trait definitions (Step 2); `for` loop desugaring through `IntoIterator`; method dispatch on `T: Trait` via associated type return types.

- [ ] **Effect-polymorphic `Iterator.next()` + stdlib `io.lines()` / `fs.read_lines()`.** **PARTIAL ŌĆö base `io.lines()` shipped 2026-07-11 (as `stdin.lines()`).** The streaming stdin line iterator ships end-to-end for direct `for line in stdin.lines()` iteration under BOTH `karac run` (interpreter drain) and `karac build` (codegen loop over a new `karac_runtime_stdin_next_line` extern ŌĆö strips the trailing newline, 3-state-signals EOF/line/error), yielding `Result[String, IoError]` per line (the `LinesIter` family's Item shape; the design's `Item = String` reconciled to `Result` so per-line read errors aren't dropped). Realized as `stdin.lines()` / `Stdin.lines()` ŌĆö the design's `io.` prefix is not a wired module alias for any stdin method (same realization as `Stdin.read_line`). The `reads(Stdin), blocks` effect is a new static effect-checker seed attributed at the `lines()` call (the per-line reads have no call site of their own), routed for the lowercase `stdin` receiver via `effectchecker/inference.rs` ŌĆö so a pub fn iterating it must declare the effect. Run==build verified over empty / no-trailing-newline / blank-line inputs; valgrind + ASAN/LSan clean (per-iteration owned `Result[String]` dropped). Tests: 1 typechecker (binds `Result[String, IoError]`), 2 effectchecker (must-declare / accepts), 1 CLI E2E (run==build with piped input). **Still OPEN in this rollup:** `fs.read_lines()`; adaptor chaining over `stdin.lines()` (`for x in stdin.lines().filter(p)` ŌĆö the intercept handles the bare `.lines()` receiver only; the chained form now REJECTS loudly at typecheck per **B-2026-07-11-34** (fixed ŌĆö also closed the `BufReader.lines()`/`LinesIter` silent-no-op twin), pointing users to iterate directly + filter/map in the loop body; full adaptor *support* over line iterators remains a follow-on); and the general effect-polymorphic `Iterator.next()` source-effect threading through adaptors. `Iterator.next()` carries a `with _` ceiling (design.md ┬¦ Iterator Traits), so one trait covers pure, blocking, suspending, and remote sources ŌĆö no separate `Stream` type. Implementation touches (1) typechecker: source effects on `next()` thread through `self` into adaptor result types, unioned with any closure effects per design.md ┬¦ Iterator Adaptors; adaptor signatures stay as currently written (no new `E_src` slot). (2) stdlib: `io.lines() -> impl Iterator[Item = String] with reads(Stdin), blocks`, `fs.read_lines(path) -> Result[impl Iterator[Item = String] with reads(Fs), blocks, IoError]` (outer `Result` for open-time failure, per-line errors surface via `Item = Result[String, IoError]` on a fallible variant). EOF/termination keeps `Option[Item]` (S3c) ŌĆö per-item errors live in the `Item` type. Error-strategy combinators (`retry_on`, `skip_errors`, `take_until_error`) deferred until a concrete use case lands. Book note added to ch10. **[self-hosting prereq ŌåÆ [phase-12](phase-12-self-hosting.md#pre-pivot-blockers-fix-before)]** ŌĆö the compiler iterates over tokens / items / source lines.

- [ ] **`core`/`alloc`/`std` standard library split.** Implement three-layer stdlib: `core` (always available, no OS/allocator), `alloc` (requires heap allocator), `std` (requires OS). Profile mapping: `kernel` ŌåÆ core only, `embedded` ŌåÆ core + optional alloc, default ŌåÆ all three. `no_alloc` context: `f"..."` interpolation unavailable, provide `format_into!` for fixed-size buffer formatting.
