- [x] **Try block grammar ŌĆö `try { ... }` (parser/AST only; typechecker pipeline is P1).** Spec at `design.md ┬¦ Error Handling > Try Blocks (try { ... })` (v60 item 42). v1 work is parser-only. Slices: (1) Lexer ŌĆö no change; the `try` keyword is already reserved per ┬¦1.1 of syntax.md (item 9 of v60). (2) Parser ŌĆö extend `parse_prefix` (or wherever block-shaped prefix expressions are dispatched) so a `try` token in expression position consumes the `try` keyword and parses the following `BLOCK` per syntax.md ┬¦5.3 `TRY_EXPR`. The body is parsed with the existing `parse_block` function ŌĆö try blocks share BLOCK semantics for statements and tail expression. AST: new `ExprKind::Try { body: Block, span: Span }` variant. (3) Resolver ŌĆö walk the body normally (try blocks introduce no new name-resolution scope beyond what the inner `BLOCK` already does); record the construct on the AST for downstream typechecker consumption. (4) v1 typechecker stub ŌĆö when the typechecker visits an `ExprKind::Try`, emit `error[E_TRY_BLOCK_NOT_IMPLEMENTED_YET]: try block syntax is recognized but the typechecker pipeline lands in P1 ŌĆö extract the body into a helper function returning Result for now`. The diagnostic includes the block's source span and the help line; the typechecker still walks the body to type-check inner expressions (so unrelated errors inside the body still surface), but the block's overall type is recorded as the error sentinel and downstream uses propagate the same diagnostic. (5) Effect-checker ŌĆö `try { ... }` contributes no effects of its own; effects from the body flow to the enclosing function as they would in any block. (6) Formatter ŌĆö emit `try ` followed by the formatted block body. Test coverage: positive ŌĆö `let r: Result[i32, MyError] = try { 42 };` parses and registers; nested try blocks parse; try block with internal `?` parses (the inner `?` is parsed by ordinary expression machinery); try block as the right-hand side of an assignment, function call argument, return expression all parse. Negative ŌĆö the v1 stub diagnostic fires at every typechecker-visit of a try block; bare `try ;` (missing block) is rejected at parse. Phase target: 5.2 (Language Features) for parser/AST/resolver/v1-stub diagnostics. Cross-reference: `deferred.md ┬¦ P1 ┬¦ Try Blocks ŌĆö ?-Retargeting and Error-Type Unification` for the P1 implementation slice (the actual `?`-target stack, error-type unification, From-chain coercion, T/E inference, defer/errdefer integration).

- [ŌåÆ P1] **Try blocks ŌĆö `?`-retargeting and error-type unification.** Full design in [`docs/deferred.md` ┬¦ P1 ┬¦ Try Blocks ŌĆö `?`-Retargeting and Error-Type Unification](deferred.md#try-blocks--retargeting-and-error-type-unification). The v1 grammar entry above lands the parser, AST, resolver, and use-site stub diagnostic; this P1 entry covers the implementation: (1) `?`-target stack (innermost-`try`-frame resolution); (2) per-block error-type unification with From-chain coercion; (3) block-level `T`/`E` inference flowing into the enclosing context; (4) empty / diverging-tail special cases; (5) `defer` / `errdefer` per-block scope integration; (6) closure-boundary rule (a `?` inside a closure body inside a `try` block does not target the outer `try`); (7) diagnostic enrichment naming the return target at `?` sites that fail unification. Replaces the v1 stub diagnostic with the real typechecker pipeline.

- [x] **Trait alias grammar ŌĆö `trait NAME = bounds;` (parser/AST only; expansion is P1).** Spec at `design.md ┬¦ Trait Aliases` (v60 item 40). v1 work is parser-only. Slices: (1) Lexer ŌĆö no change (uses existing `trait`, `=`, `+`, `;`, identifier tokens). (2) Parser ŌĆö extend `parse_trait_def` to peek for `=` after the optional `[GENERIC_PARAMS]`. If `=` is present, parse a `+`-separated `TRAIT_BOUND` list followed by an optional `WHERE_CLAUSE` and a terminating `;` per syntax.md ┬¦3.4 `TRAIT_ALIAS_DEF`. The alias's bound-list parser reuses the existing `parse_trait_bound` function used by supertrait parsing. (3) AST ŌĆö new `Item::TraitAlias { name: String, generic_params: Vec<GenericParam>, bounds: Vec<TraitBound>, where_clause: Option<WhereClause>, vis: Visibility, attributes: Vec<Attribute>, span: Span }` variant. The shape is deliberately parallel to `Item::Trait` (same generic-params, same where-clause shape) so resolver reuse is mechanical. (4) Resolver ŌĆö register the trait alias in the trait namespace alongside ordinary traits. The resolver records the alias's bound list verbatim ŌĆö no expansion at v1. (5) v1 typechecker stub ŌĆö when a use site (a bound, a `where`-clause predicate, or a `dyn` type) resolves to a trait alias, emit `error[E_TRAIT_ALIAS_NOT_IMPLEMENTED_YET]: trait alias 'NAME' is recognized but not yet expanded; the implementation lands in P1 ŌĆö write the bound list explicitly for now`. The diagnostic includes the alias declaration's source span and the alias's bound list copy-pasted into the error so users see the workaround inline. (6) `impl TraitAlias for T { ... }` rejection ŌĆö already at v1 since it would otherwise fall into the typechecker; emit `error[E_IMPL_TRAIT_ALIAS]: cannot implement trait alias 'NAME'; implement each component trait separately` with the bound-list enumeration. (7) Effect-bound-in-body rejection ŌĆö at parse time, scan the alias's bound list for any effect predicate (`reads(R)`, `writes(R)`, etc.) and emit `error[E_EFFECT_IN_TRAIT_ALIAS]: effect predicates do not belong in a trait alias body; use an effect group declaration`. (8) Formatter ŌĆö emit the alias declaration as `trait NAME[generic_params] = bound1 + bound2 + ... [where ...];`. Test coverage: positive ŌĆö `trait Numeric = Copy + Add + Sub + Mul + Div;` parses and registers; generic alias `trait IteratorOver[T] = Iterator[Item = T];` parses; alias with where-clause `trait OrderedFloat[T] = Ord where T: Numeric + Bounded;` parses; visibility `pub trait Foo = Bar;` parses; multiple aliases in one module register independently. Negative ŌĆö empty bound list `trait Foo = ;` rejected at parse; effect predicate in body rejected with named diagnostic; `impl Foo for T { ... }` against an alias rejected with named diagnostic + bound-list enumeration; use-site of declared alias produces the v1-stub diagnostic. Phase target: 5.2 (Language Features) for parser/AST/resolver/v1-stub diagnostics. Cross-reference: `deferred.md ┬¦ P1 ┬¦ Trait Aliases ŌĆö Expansion` for the P1 implementation slice (the actual bound-substitution machinery, cycle detection, where-clause propagation, `dyn` handling, cross-package re-exports).

- [ŌåÆ P1] **Trait aliases ŌĆö expansion (substitution, cycle detection, dyn handling).** Full design in [`docs/deferred.md` ┬¦ P1 ┬¦ Trait Aliases ŌĆö Expansion](deferred.md#trait-aliases--expansion-trait-numeric--copy--add--sub--). The v1 grammar entry above lands the parser, AST, resolver registration, and use-site stub diagnostic; this P1 entry covers the implementation of bound expansion at every use site, transitive flattening across nested aliases, generic-argument propagation, alias-`where`-clause gating, impl-of-alias rejection with bound enumeration, cycle detection (Tarjan SCC over the alias-mentions-alias graph), `dyn`-of-alias acceptance for single-method-trait expansions, effect-bound-in-body rejection, and cross-package re-export resolution. Replaces the v1 stub diagnostic with the real expansion machinery.

- [x] **Explicit discriminants on payload variants ŌĆö `enum Op { Connect { addr: u32 } = 0x05, ... }`. DONE 2026-07-11.** Full front-end feature (codegen is a documented no-op). `Variant` gained an `Option<Expr>` `discriminant` field; the parser accepts `= CONST_EXPR` after all three variant forms (unit / struct / tuple); the formatter emits `= VALUE` with one space either side and round-trips idempotently. The typechecker (`check_enum_discriminants`, E0804 / `DiscriminantInvalid`, symbolic codes in-message) folds each discriminant to `i64` (`fold_int_const`: integer literals, unary negation, and `+`/`-`/`*`/`/`/`%` + bitwise/shift arithmetic over them) and runs all four checks ŌĆö (a) `E_PARTIAL_EXPLICIT_DISCRIMINANTS` all-or-nothing, (b) `E_DISCRIMINANT_OUT_OF_RANGE` per `#[repr(intN)]` / `c_int`-under-`#[repr(C)]`, (c) `E_DUPLICATE_DISCRIMINANT` over resolved values, (d) `E_PAYLOAD_DISCRIMINANT_REQUIRES_REPR` (rejects `#[repr(transparent)]`/`packed`/`align` as non-committing). Codegen unchanged (interpreter run == build parity verified). **Const-ref folding CLOSED (follow-up same day):** `fold_int_const` now resolves a discriminant that references a module-level integer constant ŌĆö an immutable `let` binding or a `const` decl (`= SOME_CONST`, incl. chains like `let B = A + 1; enum E { X = B }`) ŌĆö through a nameŌåÆvalue map built from the program's module items, with a cycle guard. The resolved value flows into the range + duplicate checks. `let mut` bindings (reassignable), non-integer / unknown names, and reference cycles remain non-constant ŌåÆ `E_NON_CONSTANT_DISCRIMINANT`. Tests: 20 typechecker total (added const-ref accept / chain / `const`-decl / range-participation / duplicate-participation / `let mut`-rejected / unknown-name), 1 parser, 1 formatter, 1 codegen E2E. The entire spec const surface (literals, arithmetic, module-const references) is now covered. Spec at `design.md ┬¦ Explicit Discriminants on Payload Variants` (v60 item 43). Full v1 implementation (no P1 carve-out ŌĆö there is no companion runtime-surface lift; the explicit values are declarations only). Slices: (1) Parser ŌĆö extend the `VARIANT` rule per syntax.md ┬¦3.3 so each of the three variant forms (unit, struct, tuple) optionally accepts `"=" CONST_EXPR` after the payload portion. The const-expression parser is the existing `parse_const_expr` already used by module-level bindings ŌĆö literals, arithmetic on literals, and references to other module-level integer constants. AST: extend the existing variant node (likely `EnumVariant { name, kind: VariantKind, discriminant: Option<ConstExpr>, span }`) with a `discriminant` field; the field is `Option<ConstExpr>` so the field-less-no-explicit-value case (`Audio,`) round-trips the same way it does today. The formatter emits `= LITERAL` after the variant body (struct `{ ... }` or tuple `(...)`) when present, with one space on either side of `=` for parity with the existing field-less formatting (`Audio = 0x01`). (2) Resolver ŌĆö const-expression evaluation runs at item-resolution time so per-enum duplicate-value detection happens before downstream phases. (3) Typechecker ŌĆö three new checks, all at the enum-decl site after const-eval has folded each `discriminant` to an integer literal: (a) **All-or-nothing rule.** Walk the variant list; if some variants have `discriminant.is_some()` and some don't, emit `error[E_PARTIAL_EXPLICIT_DISCRIMINANTS]: enum 'NAME' mixes explicit and implicit discriminants; declare a value on every variant or remove the explicit values and rely on declaration order` with the first explicit + first implicit variant spans labeled. (b) **Range check per `#[repr(intN)]`.** When `#[repr(intN)]` is present, every explicit value must fit the repr type's range ŌĆö otherwise `error[E_DISCRIMINANT_OUT_OF_RANGE]: discriminant 'N' on variant 'V' does not fit in 'intN' (range '[MIN, MAX]')` with the offending value's span. Under `#[repr(C)]` without an `#[repr(intN)]` companion, the range is the platform's `c_int` (signed `i32` on every supported target at v1; the diagnostic should name `c_int` rather than `i32` to make the C-ABI-driven choice explicit to the reader). (c) **Duplicate-value rejection.** Build a `HashMap<i64, Span>` over the resolved values; on any insert that collides, emit `error[E_DUPLICATE_DISCRIMINANT]: variant 'V2' has the same discriminant value 'N' as variant 'V1'` with both spans labeled. The diagnostic uses the *resolved* integer value so const-expression aliasing (e.g., two variants pointing at the same module-level constant) is caught. (d) **`#[repr]` requirement on payload variants.** If the enum has at least one variant with both a payload (`VariantKind::Struct` or `VariantKind::Tuple`) and a `discriminant`, and the enum's `#[repr]` set does not contain `#[repr(intN)]` or `#[repr(C)]`, emit `error[E_PAYLOAD_DISCRIMINANT_REQUIRES_REPR]: explicit discriminants on payload variants require '#[repr(intN)]' or '#[repr(C)]'; without one, the discriminant location is unspecified and the value commitment is unreachable` at the first offending payload-variant's discriminant span. The check rejects `#[repr(transparent)]`, `#[repr(packed)]`, `#[repr(align(N))]` as repr forms that satisfy the requirement (none commits to a discriminant position). Field-less variants with `= N` under a `#[repr]`-less enum continue to be legal per the existing C-like-enum rule. (4) Runtime-surface preservation. The existing payload-enum exclusion from `.discriminant()` / `TryFrom[intN]` / `.values()` continues to apply unchanged ŌĆö explicit discriminants on payload variants do not lift the exclusion. Calls to `.discriminant()` on a payload enum (with or without explicit discriminants) continue to fail with the existing diagnostic that points at the manual-`tag` workaround; the design.md cross-reference now mentions the explicit-discriminant declaration form as the source of the literal values the manual `tag` method's match arms reference. (5) Effect-checker / ownership-checker integration ŌĆö none. The discriminant declarations are pure data attached to variant decls and contribute no effects, no consume tracking, no reference flow. (6) Codegen ŌĆö the explicit values on payload variants are *declarations*, not layout commitments. At v1 the LLVM lowering of payload enums is unchanged: the compiler may still elide tags via niche optimization, store the discriminant non-contiguously, and otherwise treat the variant set as it does today. The declarations exist for documentation, semver-lock, and as the literal values a hand-written `tag` method's arms reference. Field-less explicit-discriminant enums under `#[repr(intN)]` continue to lower with the declared integer at the runtime-surface position, exactly as today. Test coverage: positive ŌĆö `#[repr(u8)] enum Op { Reset = 0x01, Connect { addr: u32 } = 0x05, Send(Bytes) = 0x06, Disconnect = 0xFF }` parses, resolves, type-checks, formats; `#[repr(C)] enum E { A = 1, B { x: i32 } = 2 }` accepted; signed-repr negative values `#[repr(i8)] enum E { A = -1, B(u32) = 5 }` accepted; a manual `fn tag(ref self) -> u8` calling `match self { Op.Connect { .. } => 0x05, ... }` type-checks normally and is the documented consumption pattern. Negative ŌĆö partial-explicit (`enum E { A = 1, B(u32) }`) rejected with `E_PARTIAL_EXPLICIT_DISCRIMINANTS`; out-of-range `#[repr(u8)] enum E { A = 256 }` rejected with `E_DISCRIMINANT_OUT_OF_RANGE`; duplicate values `#[repr(u8)] enum E { A = 1, B(u32) = 1 }` rejected with `E_DUPLICATE_DISCRIMINANT` naming both variants; payload variant with explicit discriminant on a `#[repr]`-less enum rejected with `E_PAYLOAD_DISCRIMINANT_REQUIRES_REPR`; same on `#[repr(transparent)]` rejected; `.discriminant()` call on a payload enum (regardless of explicit discriminants) continues to be rejected with the existing payload-exclusion diagnostic. Phase target: 5.2 (parser/AST/resolver/typechecker). No P1 companion ŌĆö option (b) of v60 item 43 deliberately scopes the v1 work to declarations only; a future `#[derive(Discriminant)]` synthesizing `tag` from the declared values is additive-later and is not on the v1 critical path.

- [x] **`#[derive(Default)]` and `#[default]` on enum variants.** **DONE (2026-06-19)** ŌĆö `#[default]` enum-variant marker implemented for non-generic types. (1) Attribute recognition: `default` registered in `attribute_validator::RECOGNIZED_BARE_ATTRIBUTES`. (2) Position/shape checks (resolver pass 1.7, `validate_default_attribute`): `E_DEFAULT_ATTRIBUTE_INVALID_POSITION` (`#[default]` anywhere but a variant ŌĆö struct/field/fn/etc.), `E_DEFAULT_ATTRIBUTE_WITHOUT_DERIVE` (variant marker without `#[derive(Default)]` on the enum), `E_MALFORMED_ATTRIBUTE_ARGS` (`#[default(...)]` / `#[default = ...]`). (3) Derive semantics (typechecker `validate_derive_default`, split out of the generic `validate_derived_trait` since Default's enum rule is marker-based, not a field-walk): `E_DEFAULT_NO_VARIANT_MARKED`, `E_DEFAULT_MULTIPLE_VARIANTS` (names both), `E_DEFAULT_VARIANT_HAS_PAYLOAD` (marked variant must be field-less); struct field-default check now emits `E_DERIVE_DEFAULT_MISSING_FIELD_DEFAULT`. (4) Synthesis (`desugar::enum_default_body`) lowers the unique `#[default]` unit variant to `Enum.Variant` (was: first declared variant). Composes with `#[non_exhaustive]`. Tests: resolver 6, typechecker 7 (4 new), interpreter 6 (2 reworked + 1 new), codegen 3. **DEFERRED (additive-later):** generic struct bound-propagation (`impl[T: Default] Default for Pair[T]`) and generic-enum default ŌĆö both need `T.default()` trait-bound associated-fn dispatch, a separate enabling feature; non-generic types are the shipped scope (matches the prior derive-Default slice's primitives+user-types boundary). Original spec follows. Spec at `design.md ┬¦ #[derive(Default)] and #[default] on enum variants` (v60 item 44). Full v1 implementation (no P1 carve-out ŌĆö option (a) is fully achievable at v1; payload-bearing default variants are deliberately deferred indefinitely as additive-later). Slices: (1) Parser ŌĆö extend the `VARIANT` rule per syntax.md ┬¦3.3 so each of the three variant forms accepts a leading `[ ATTRIBUTES ]` (the existing attribute parser handles every form already; the rule extension just records the parsed attributes on the variant AST node). AST: extend the existing `EnumVariant` node with `attributes: Vec<Attribute>` if not already present; the field defaults to empty so the no-attributes case round-trips today. (2) Attribute recognition ŌĆö the parser-side attribute table (syntax.md ┬¦8) gains `#[default]`. The attribute carries no arguments; `#[default(...)]` and `#[default = ...]` are rejected at the attribute parser as malformed (existing `E_MALFORMED_ATTRIBUTE_ARGS` machinery, with the diagnostic naming `#[default]` and saying it accepts no arguments). (3) Position checker (resolver / pre-typechecker pass) ŌĆö `#[default]` is legal **only** on an enum-variant decl. Applying it to a struct, struct field, function, type alias, distinct type, trait, trait method, impl block, const, or extern declaration emits `error[E_DEFAULT_ATTRIBUTE_INVALID_POSITION]: '#[default]' is only valid on a unit enum variant under '#[derive(Default)]'` with the offending item's span. The check runs before the per-derive validators so the diagnostic is location-focused rather than coming out of the derive machinery. (4) Derive registration ŌĆö `Default` joins the existing derivable-traits table (the same machinery that handles `Eq` / `Clone` / `Debug`). The derive is keyed off `#[derive(Default)]` literal text; it has no derive dependencies (i.e., does not auto-derive any other trait, and is not auto-derived from any other derive). (5) **Struct derive body** ŌĆö `#[derive(Default)]` on a struct generates `impl[GENERIC_BOUNDS_PROPAGATED] Default for StructName { fn default() -> Self { StructName { f1: F1.default(), f2: F2.default(), ... } } }`. Each field's `default()` resolves through the existing trait-associated-function dispatch. The bound-propagation rule mirrors `#[derive(Eq)]` ŌĆö the compiler infers the minimal set of generic-param bounds (`T: Default` for every type-param `T` used in any field type) and emits them on the impl block. If any field's type does not implement `Default` (and is not a type-param with a propagatable bound), emit `error[E_DERIVE_DEFAULT_MISSING_FIELD_DEFAULT]: cannot #[derive(Default)] for 'StructName' ŌĆö field 'name' of type 'T' does not implement 'Default'` with the offending field's span. (6) **Enum derive body** ŌĆö `#[derive(Default)]` on an enum scans variant attributes for `#[default]` and emits four checks before generating the body: (a) **No marker**: zero variants carry `#[default]` ŌåÆ `error[E_DEFAULT_NO_VARIANT_MARKED]: #[derive(Default)] on enum 'StatusName' requires exactly one variant to be marked with #[default]; consider adding it to the variant that represents the starting state` with the enum-decl span labeled. (b) **Multiple markers**: Ōēź2 variants carry `#[default]` ŌåÆ `error[E_DEFAULT_MULTIPLE_VARIANTS]: #[derive(Default)] on enum 'EnumName' requires exactly one variant marked with #[default]; found markers on 'V1' and 'V2'` with both attribute spans labeled. (c) **Marked variant has fields**: the marked variant is `VariantKind::Struct` or `VariantKind::Tuple` (not unit) ŌåÆ `error[E_DEFAULT_VARIANT_HAS_PAYLOAD]: #[default] on enum variant 'V' requires a field-less variant; either declare the marked variant as 'V,' (no fields) or write a manual 'impl Default for E' that constructs the desired starting state` with the marked variant's payload span labeled, and the manual-impl skeleton inlined into the help line so the user sees the exact replacement. (d) **All checks pass**: emit `impl Default for EnumName { fn default() -> Self { EnumName.MarkedVariant } }` ŌĆö a constant-expression body, no field walk, no generic bound propagation needed (the marked variant is field-less). Generic enums are still generic on the impl (`impl[T] Default for Box[T]` if the marker is on a unit variant ŌĆö no `T: Default` bound, since the marked variant doesn't reference `T`). (7) **`#[default]` requires `#[derive(Default)]` on the enclosing enum** ŌĆö an enum that does not carry `#[derive(Default)]` but has at least one variant with `#[default]` is rejected with `error[E_DEFAULT_ATTRIBUTE_WITHOUT_DERIVE]: '#[default]' on variant 'V' requires the enclosing enum 'E' to carry '#[derive(Default)]'` with both the variant attribute span and the enum-decl span labeled, and a fix-it suggesting `add #[derive(Default)] to enum E`. The check runs at type-decl time after resolver-side derive registration so dead annotations don't accumulate silently. (8) Effect-checker / ownership-checker integration ŌĆö none. The derived `default` is a constructor with no effects on user-defined resources beyond what the field types' own `default()` methods carry (struct case) or zero (enum unit-variant case). (9) Composition ŌĆö verify orthogonality with `#[non_exhaustive]` (the variant set may grow without changing the default), explicit discriminants from item 43 (a marked variant may also carry `= N`; the two are independent), and `#[deprecated]` on the same variant (legal ŌĆö emits the existing deprecation warning at every reference site, including the synthesized `default()` body, which surfaces the marker's attribution to the user). Test coverage: positive ŌĆö `#[derive(Default)] struct Point { x: i64, y: i64 }` generates `Point { x: 0, y: 0 }`; `#[derive(Default)] struct Pair[T] { a: T, b: T }` generates `impl[T: Default] Default for Pair[T]`; `#[derive(Default)] enum Status { #[default] Pending, Active, Closed }` generates `Status.default() == Status.Pending`; `#[derive(Default)] enum Mode[T] { #[default] Idle, Custom(T) }` generates `Mode[T].default() == Mode.Idle` with no `T: Default` bound; `#[non_exhaustive] #[derive(Default)] enum M { #[default] A, B }` accepted; `#[repr(u8)] #[derive(Default)] enum Op { #[default] Reset = 0x01, Send = 0x02 }` accepted with `Op.default() == Op.Reset`. Negative ŌĆö `#[derive(Default)] enum E { A, B }` (no marker) rejected with `E_DEFAULT_NO_VARIANT_MARKED`; `#[derive(Default)] enum E { #[default] A, #[default] B }` rejected with `E_DEFAULT_MULTIPLE_VARIANTS` naming both; `#[derive(Default)] enum E { #[default] A(i32), B }` rejected with `E_DEFAULT_VARIANT_HAS_PAYLOAD` plus the manual-impl-skeleton help line; `#[derive(Default)] struct S { v: NonDefault }` (where `NonDefault` does not impl Default) rejected with `E_DERIVE_DEFAULT_MISSING_FIELD_DEFAULT` naming the offending field; `#[default] struct S { ... }` rejected with `E_DEFAULT_ATTRIBUTE_INVALID_POSITION`; `#[default]` on a struct field rejected with the same diagnostic; `enum E { #[default] A, B }` (no derive) rejected with `E_DEFAULT_ATTRIBUTE_WITHOUT_DERIVE`; `#[derive(Default)]` plus a manual `impl Default for T` rejected with the existing duplicate-impl diagnostic; `#[default(some)]` and `#[default = "x"]` rejected as malformed-args. Phase target: 5.2 (parser/AST/attribute-position-checker/derive). Cross-reference: design.md ┬¦ `#[derive(Default)]` and `#[default]` on enum variants; syntax.md ┬¦8 attribute table row for `#[default]`.

- [x] **Codegen hint attributes ŌĆö `#[inline]`, `#[inline(always)]`, `#[inline(never)]`, `#[cold]`.** **DONE (2026-06-19).** (1) Parser scan `scan_codegen_hint_attrs` (`parser/items.rs`) resolves the four attributes from arg-shape and runs in both `parse_function` and the trait-method constructor; bad shapes emit `E_MALFORMED_ATTRIBUTE_ARGS`. (2) AST: `Function`/`TraitMethod` gained `inline_hint: Option<InlineHint { Default | Always | Never }>` + `is_cold: bool` (`ast/items.rs`); `Attribute::codegen_hint_name` (`ast/types.rs`) classifies a hint for the placement gates. (3) Conflicts diagnosed in the parser scan ŌĆö `E_INLINE_HINT_CONFLICT` (two different inline-axis attrs, naming both) and `E_COLD_INLINE_ALWAYS_CONFLICT` (`#[cold]`+`#[inline(always)]`); `#[cold]`+`#[inline]`/`#[inline(never)]` accepted. The old reserved `cold`Ōåö`inline` entry in `attribute_validator::QUERY_RESOLUTION_CONFLICT_PAIRS` was removed (it contradicted the now-authoritative design.md rule) and its resolver test repurposed. (4) Position gate `reject_codegen_hint_attrs` / `reject_codegen_hint_on_extern` (`resolver/collect.rs`) ŌĆö `E_CODEGEN_HINT_INVALID_POSITION` on non-fn items + whole impl blocks, `E_CODEGEN_HINT_ON_EXTERN_DECL` on foreign-fn decls (new `ResolveErrorKind::{CodegenHintInvalidTarget,CodegenHintOnExternDecl}`, mapped in `cli.rs`); closures rejected at parse with `E_CODEGEN_HINT_ON_CLOSURE` in `parse_prefix`. Allowed: free `fn`, inherent/trait-impl methods, trait method decls, `extern "C" fn` definitions, `Drop` destructors. (2-cont) TraitŌåÆimpl propagation: `desugar::propagate_codegen_hints` copies a trait method's hint to non-overriding impl methods (per-axis, last-writer-wins). (5) Codegen `emit_codegen_hint_attrs` (`codegen/functions.rs`) attaches `inlinehint`/`alwaysinline`/`noinline`/`cold` at declare time. Tests: parser 14, resolver 9 (incl. propagation + override), codegen IR 7 (each attr in IR, recursive `#[inline(always)]` compiles, cold+inline(never) coexist, traitŌåÆimpl propagation visible). **Note:** the checklist's "used through a function pointer still compiles" IR test is deferred ŌĆö K─üra `fn(T)->R` value/pointer types don't parse in the current compiler (separate language feature); the attribute is emitted regardless of call shape, so direct-call + recursive cases cover the lowering. Original spec follows. Spec at `design.md ┬¦ Codegen Hint Attributes` (v60 item 38). Slices: (1) Attribute parser (Phase 5.2) ŌĆö recognise the four attributes per syntax.md ┬¦8. `#[inline]` parses with no args; `#[inline(always)]` and `#[inline(never)]` parse with a single keyword arg (`always` / `never`); `#[cold]` parses with no args. (2) AST ŌĆö capture inlining axis as `Option<InlineHint { Default | Always | Never }>` and a separate `is_cold: bool` on the existing `Function` node and the trait-method declaration node. Trait-decl propagation parallels `#[track_caller]`: the hint applies to every impl unless that impl carries its own override (last-writer-wins). (3) Conflict checker (Phase 5.2) ŌĆö reject `#[inline]` + `#[inline(always)]`, `#[inline]` + `#[inline(never)]`, `#[inline(always)]` + `#[inline(never)]` with `error[E_INLINE_HINT_CONFLICT]` naming both attribute spans; reject `#[cold]` + `#[inline(always)]` with `error[E_COLD_INLINE_ALWAYS_CONFLICT]`. `#[cold]` + `#[inline]` and `#[cold]` + `#[inline(never)]` are accepted. Duplicate same-attribute on one fn falls through to the existing `E_DUPLICATE_ATTRIBUTE` diagnostic. (4) Position checker (Phase 5.2) ŌĆö reject on closure expressions (`error[E_CODEGEN_HINT_ON_CLOSURE]`), on foreign-function declarations inside `unsafe extern { }` (`error[E_CODEGEN_HINT_ON_EXTERN_DECL]`), and on entire `impl` blocks (per-method only at v1). Allowed positions: free `fn`, methods inside inherent and trait `impl`, trait method declarations, `extern "C" fn` definitions (K─üra-side body), `impl Drop for T` destructors. (5) Codegen (Phase 7) ŌĆö at LLVM IR emission time, attach the corresponding LLVM function attribute: `#[inline]` ŌåÆ `inlinehint`, `#[inline(always)]` ŌåÆ `alwaysinline`, `#[inline(never)]` ŌåÆ `noinline`, `#[cold]` ŌåÆ `cold`. The attributes are advisory at the LLVM level; LLVM honors them faithfully under all standard optimization levels but the K─üra-side compiler does not depend on them being honored ŌĆö they are reported behavior, not guaranteed semantics. (6) Effect-system orthogonality ŌĆö codegen hints contribute no effects to the enclosing function and do not alter the inferred set; an inlined body's effects have already been folded into the caller's inferred effects via normal effect inference. (7) `#[track_caller]` interaction ŌĆö orthogonal; both attributes coexist without diagnostic. When a `#[track_caller] #[inline]` function is inlined at a call site, the hidden caller-location parameter folds into the receiver function's site (LLVM-side; no K─üra-pass change). (8) Silent-leave-out-of-line policy ŌĆö when `#[inline(always)]` cannot inline (recursive call site, function-pointer call, cross-package without LTO IR available, or function body containing inlining-blocking constructs like large `asm` blocks or `#[interrupt]` ISR handlers), no diagnostic is emitted at v1. Future tooling (`karac build --perf-report`) will surface "had no inlining sites" as a hint, but the build never fails on it. Test coverage (parser/checker ŌĆö Phase 5.2): each attribute parses; each conflict pair rejects with the named diagnostic; closure-expression rejection; extern-decl rejection; entire-impl-block rejection; trait-decl propagation honored by impls that don't override. Test coverage (codegen ŌĆö Phase 7): emitted LLVM IR carries the expected `alwaysinline` / `noinline` / `inlinehint` / `cold` attribute; a recursive `#[inline(always)]` function still compiles cleanly; a `#[inline(always)]` function used through a function pointer still compiles cleanly; `#[cold]` placement bias visible in IR via the `cold` attribute on the function. Phase target: 5.2 (parser, AST, conflict/position checks); 7 (LLVM attribute emission). Cross-reference: design.md ┬¦ Codegen Hint Attributes; syntax.md ┬¦8 attribute table rows.

> **Moved (2026-06-06):** Critical sections (`CriticalSectionGuard`) ŌåÆ [`phase-11-stdlib-longtail.md ┬¦ Embedded / Hardware Primitives`](phase-11-stdlib-longtail.md#embedded--hardware-primitives); the `std.secret` module entry (full 9-step stdlib + compiler split) ŌåÆ [`phase-11-stdlib-longtail.md ┬¦ Security (std.secret)`](phase-11-stdlib-longtail.md#security-stdsecret).

- [x] **Parser/AST: thread `#[attr]` and `pub` through `LayoutDef`, `ExternFunction`, `StructField`.** Preparatory scaffolding shared across several later items. Added `attributes: Vec<Attribute>` + `is_pub: bool` to `LayoutDef` and `ExternFunction`, and `attributes: Vec<Attribute>` to `StructField`. Parser (`parse_layout_def`, `parse_extern_function`, struct-field loops) now captures the `#[...]` and `pub` tokens it previously dropped on the floor. No behavior change yet ŌĆö each downstream consumer reads these slots: `#[link_name]` / `#[no_mangle]` / `#[used]` / `#[link_section]` on extern (see "Linker control attributes" below), `#[interrupt]` on extern, field-level `#[must_use]` / `#[allow]`, `#[no_rc]` / `@no_rc` on layout, and `pub extern` / `pub layout` for cross-module visibility. Covered by three parser tests in `tests/parser.rs`.

- [x] **Linker control attributes.** Ō£ō DONE (2026-04-28) ŌĆö `Codegen::apply_linker_attrs` consumes `#[link_section("name")]`, `#[no_mangle]`, and `#[used]` on `Function` / `ExternFunction` declarations: section directive set on the LLVM symbol; `#[no_mangle]` is a no-op (codegen already uses source names); `#[used]` queues into `Codegen::used_symbols` and `emit_llvm_used` produces the standard `@llvm.used` appending-linkage global in section `llvm.metadata` after all functions are declared. All permitted outside `unsafe`. `#[no_mangle]` controls symbol name only ŌĆö does not imply `extern "C"` ABI. 5 IR-level tests in `tests/codegen.rs`.

- [ ] **G32 ŌĆö Serialization / deserialization**. Design `Serialize` / `Deserialize` traits. Depends on G27 ŌĆö Derive / compiler-synthesized traits. Support JSON at minimum, TOML for config. Attribute syntax for field customization (`#[serialize(rename: "...")]`).

- [x] **`String.sorted()` method.** Ō£ō DONE (2026-04-27) ŌĆö `infer_str_method` dispatch in typechecker (`Type::Str` branch before generic fallthrough); `sorted`/`sorted_by` arms in interpreter `eval_method_call` (char-level sort for strings, `value_compare` fallback for arrays). 3 typechecker tests + 4 interpreter tests added.

- [x] **Typechecker accepts `+` between `String` operands.** Both backends already handled it ŌĆö interpreter via the `(BinOp::Add, Value::String(a), Value::String(b)) => Value::String(a + &b)` arm in `eval_ops`, codegen via `compile_string_binop`'s `BinOp::Add` (fresh malloc + copy both ŌåÆ owned `{data, len, cap}`). The typechecker's `+` operand-type rule listed only numerics, so `a + b` (both `String`) errored `arithmetic operator requires numeric type, found 'String'`. Fixed by adding a String-concat case to `infer_binary`'s `Add` arm: `is_string_concat_operand(left) && is_string_concat_operand(right) -> Str`, where the helper strips `ref` / `mut ref` so all three forms (`String + String`, `String + ref String`, `ref String + String`, incl. `ref + ref`) admit ŌĆö verified codegen auto-loads the borrowed pointee before the concat (`test_e2e_string_concat_ref_operands`). `String + <non-String>` and `String - String` stay rejected. Surfaced 2026-05-20 (kata-katas/leetcode/71-simplify-path sidestepped via f-strings) and again 2026-05-29 while writing the `Request.query()`/`headers()` E2E handlers. Tests: `tests/typechecker.rs` (`test_string_concat_ok`, `_with_literal_ok`, `_chained_ok`, `_ref_operand_ok`, plus `test_string_subtraction_rejected` and the existing `_no_int_promo` reject) + `tests/codegen.rs::test_e2e_string_concat_ref_operands`.

- [x] **`String.push(char)` end-to-end + `push_str` interpreter dispatch.** Ō£ō DONE (2026-05-25) ŌĆö added `"push"` arm in `infer_str_method` accepting a `Char` argument and returning `Unit`; codegen arm in `compile_vec_method` gated on `string_vars` membership that calls `emit_codepoint_to_utf8` (1ŌĆō4 UTF-8 bytes via `karac_string_encode_char`) and shares `push_str`'s power-of-two growth + heap-free geometry; interpreter dispatch arm in `method_call_seq.rs` rebinds the receiver via `env.set`. The same commit closed a `push_str` interpreter gap that surfaced as a side observation ŌĆö `push_str` typechecked + codegened cleanly since 2026-05-23 but `karac run` panicked on the unreachable arm. Both gaps surfaced as the kata-71 follow-up after the bench showed the `out = f"{out}{c}"` self-append shape was O(n┬▓): kata-katas/leetcode/71-simplify-path's auto-par lane went from 28.5 ms ŌåÆ see ┬¦ Benchmarks for the post-fix delta once it's measured. 8 regression tests added (3 codegen e2e + 2 interpreter + 3 typechecker).

- [x] **`CStr` borrowed surface ŌĆö `as_ptr` / `len` / `is_empty` / `as_bytes` (the first pointer-producer surface).** *(2026-06-06)* The full borrowed-`CStr` method set from design.md ┬¦ C-String Literals, end-to-end across all four layers. `as_ptr() -> *const u8` is the language's **first safe pointer-producer** ŌĆö it unblocked the phase-10 "`(ptr, len)` string-passing E2E" entry (now shipped: browser-WASM guest string through `kara_host`, plus the native `puts` E2E). Landed pieces:
  - **Scope-0 registration:** `"CStr"` joined `PRELUDE_TYPES` (`src/prelude.rs`) so the design's annotated form `let msg: ref CStr = c"..."` resolves (the bare-let form never needed it; the resolver rejected the annotation with `undefined type 'CStr'` before this).
  - **Typechecker:** `infer_cstr_method` (`stdlib_seq.rs`) + a `CStr` named-receiver arm in `infer_method_call` that also records `method_callee_types["CStr.<method>"]` (the HTTP-arm pattern) ŌĆö codegen keys its routing off that. `as_ptr -> *const u8`, `len -> i64`, `is_empty -> bool`, `as_bytes -> Slice[u8]`; unknown methods get the `require_known_method` candidates diagnostic.
  - **Interpreter:** new `Value::CStr(Arc<Vec<u8>>)` (bytes exclude the NUL); `len`/`is_empty`/`as_bytes` dispatch in `method_call_seq.rs` (`as_bytes` materializes type-erased `Value::Int` bytes, the `String.bytes()` pattern). `as_ptr` is **rejected at eval time** with a compile-with-`karac build` pointer ŌĆö the tree-walk has no raw-pointer representation and nothing interpreted can consume one (extern/host bodies are link-time constructs).
  - **Codegen:** `CStringLit` lowers to a NUL-terminated internal rodata global (`context.const_string` ŌĆö raw bytes, `\xHH` escapes need not be UTF-8) carried as a `{ptr, i64}` slice-struct value (len stored alongside the pointer = the design's O(1) `len`). `compile_cstr_method` (method_call.rs) extracts/compares on the aggregate; `as_bytes` returns the aggregate unchanged (`Slice[u8]` shares the layout); LLVM const-folds literal-receiver `as_ptr` to the global itself at the call site. `cstr_vars` side-table + `is_cstr_type_expr` for binding-registration heuristics; `as_bytes` joined `infer_slice_elem_from_rhs` so the result binding gets `Slice[u8]` dispatch.
  - **Load-bearing fix (pre-existing, surfaced by the producer):** `llvm_type_for_type_expr` had **no `TypeKind::Pointer` arm** ŌĆö every pointer-typed extern/host-fn param silently declared as `i64`, a module-verifier error the moment a real `ptr` argument reached a call. Pointer types now lower to genuine LLVM `ptr`; the `ptr.*` strict-provenance module migrated off its i64-pointer ABI to real `ptrtoint`/`inttoptr`/`const_null` (this is the "raw-pointer slots i64 ŌåÆ `ptr`" uplift phase-5-diagnostics line 511's slice 3 deferred ŌĆö its `!provenance` metadata refinement remains open there).
  - **Tests:** typechecker ├Ś7 (incl. the `(ptr, len)` host-fn shape + WrongNumberOfArgs + NoMethodFound), interpreter ├Ś4 (UTF-8 byte-count, NUL exclusion, as_bytes values, annotated form), codegen ├Ś4 (NUL-terminated-global IR pin, rodata-pointer-direct call-site pin incl. the `declare ŌĆ”(ptrŌĆ”)` param pin, len/is_empty/as_bytes E2E with interpreter-parity outputs, libc-`puts` E2E), plus the phase-10 browser E2E extension. Full suite green.

- [x] **`CString` owning type + `CStr`Ōåö`String` conversions. Ō£ō COMPLETE (2026-07-11).** The remainder of design.md ┬¦ C-String Literals after the borrowed surface above: owning `CString` (heap `String`-shaped buffer with guaranteed trailing NUL, drops normally, `.as_ptr()`), `String.to_cstring(ref self) -> Result[CString, NulError]` (copy + NUL-append + interior-NUL rejection, `NulError` type), `c_str.to_string() / .to_string_slice() -> Result[_, Utf8Error]` (UTF-8 validation), and the `unsafe` `CStr`-from-raw-pointer constructor (the O(N) strlen-walk `len` case the design describes). **Progress (2026-06-11):** the `unsafe` raw-pointer constructor landed as **`CStr.from_ptr(*const u8) -> ref CStr`** ŌĆö libc-`strlen` length walk + `{ptr, len}` aggregate, `unsafe`-gated, interpreter-rejected, tested across all three layers. **UNBLOCKED (verified 2026-07-09) ŌĆö the codegen UTF-8 validator landed, so `CStr.to_string()` is already wired end-to-end (the "still open" listing below was stale for it).** `build_utf8_validated_result` (`src/codegen/method_call.rs:7594`) backs both `compile_cstr_to_string` (`method_call.rs:7541`, dispatched at `method_call.rs:668` for `CStr.to_string`) and `compile_string_from_utf8` (`method_call.rs:7567`, dispatched at `src/codegen/assoc_call.rs:1868`); `Utf8Error` is seeded into `seed_builtin_enum_layouts` (`src/codegen/declarations.rs:3784`) and the runtime extern is `karac_runtime_cstr_to_string` (`runtime/src/lib.rs:4499`, declared at `:294`). So the earlier "blocked on a codegen UTF-8 validator, since `String.from_utf8` is interpreter-only" framing no longer holds ŌĆö `String.from_utf8` codegens too. **DONE (2026-07-11) ŌĆö CString bundle landed across all four layers.** `CStr.to_string_slice() -> Result[StringSlice, Utf8Error]` (the earlier "genuinely absent" note was stale ŌĆö it had already shipped by 2026-07-09: `infer_cstr_method` arm + `compile_cstr_to_string_slice` + `karac_runtime_utf8_validate`, with codegen-E2E + asan tests). This slice added the rest: (a) owning **`CString`** ŌĆö a `String`-shaped `{ptr, len, cap = len + 1}` heap buffer with a guaranteed trailing NUL, scope-0 in `PRELUDE_TYPES`, lowered to `vec_struct_type` and dropped via the same `string_vars` buffer-free (let-bound AND match-payload-bound ŌĆö `pattern_binding.rs` treats `CString` like `String`); its introspection surface (`as_ptr`/`len`/`is_empty`/`as_bytes`) dispatches through the typechecker-recorded `CString.<method>` key (`infer_cstring_method` + `compile_cstring_method`; `as_ptr` interpreter-rejected like `CStr`). (b) **`String.to_cstring(ref self) -> Result[CString, NulError]`** ŌĆö copy + trailing-NUL append + interior-NUL reject, via the `karac_runtime_string_to_cstring` extern (`compile_string_to_cstring`); interpreter scans for an interior NUL and yields `Value::CString`. (c) **`NulError`** ŌĆö `runtime/stdlib/nul_error.kara` enum (`InteriorNul` / `Other(String)`, mirroring `Utf8Error`'s minimalism), prelude + `seed_builtin_enum_layouts`. Tests: runtime unit ├Ś4, typechecker ├Ś5, interpreter ├Ś4, codegen-E2E ├Ś3 (incl. a runtime-built String ŌåÆ `to_cstring` ŌåÆ `as_ptr` ŌåÆ libc `puts`), memory-sanitizer ├Ś1 (owning buffer freed exactly once, interior-NUL `Err` leak-clean). **Residual (minor, deferred):** the design's passing mention of constructing a `CString` from a `Slice[u8]` ŌĆö no `Slice[u8].to_cstring()` yet; pick it up when a workload needs it (katas-are-bug-finders loop). `CStr.to_string()` was the Phase-12 self-hosting critical-path item (the proof's `char*` read needs it to compile ŌĆö [phase-12 Cluster 2](phase-12-self-hosting.md#pre-pivot-blockers-fix-before)); that read now compiles. Owning `CString` remains the self-hosting-relevant remainder (codegen builds runtime names it may need to hand to C). None of the rest blocks FFI handoff (the borrowed surface covers the literal-driven use cases); becomes load-bearing when a workload needs to pass a *runtime-constructed* string to C ŌĆö pick it up then, per the katas-are-bug-finders loop. **[self-hosting prereq ŌåÆ [phase-12](phase-12-self-hosting.md#pre-pivot-blockers-fix-before)]** ŌĆö self-hosting IS that workload: codegen passes runtime-built names (fn/type/global) to LLVM-C.

- [x] **Raw-pointer deref/method surface ŌĆö `p.read()` / `p.write(v)` / `p.offset(n)` / `read_unaligned` / `write_volatile` / method-form `is_null`, plus `*p` deref. Ō£ō FUNCTIONALLY COMPLETE (2026-07-11).** Spec at `design.md ┬¦ Raw Pointer Construction: ptr.const / ptr.mut` ("Construction is safe; dereference is unsafe") and `design.md ┬¦ Method Resolution > Method dispatch on raw pointers requires a known pointee` (which writes the method-call form for all of these). **DONE across three landings:** (1) B-2026-07-08-4 shipped the codegen lowering (`compile_pointer_instance_method`: typed load/store/GEP for `read`/`write`/`offset`/`add` + `_unaligned`/`_volatile` variants) and `*p` deref ŌĆö the 2026-06-07 "nothing past construction exists" audit is obsolete. (2) 2026-07-11 closed the correctness gap that made it usable: the typechecker's `Type::Pointer` method arm had NO return-type inference, so `p.offset(..)` fell through to `Type::Error` ŌĆö an un-annotated `let p1 = p.offset(1)` lost its pointer type and every downstream `p1.read()` failed codegen. Added proper return types (`offset`/`add` ŌåÆ `*_ T` same mutability, `read*` ŌåÆ `T`, `write*` ŌåÆ `Unit` with the value checked against `T`, `is_null` ŌåÆ `bool`), so un-annotated chains, `mut`-pointer reassignment loops (the `char*` buffer-walk shape), and derived pointers now dispatch. (3) Same slice added the `p.is_null()` method-form (safe, codegen `build_is_null`) and wired the `unsafe { }` requirement for the through-pointer method forms in `unsafe_lint` (`read`/`write`/`offset`/`add`/`_unaligned`/`_volatile` require `unsafe`, mirroring the existing `*p` deref rule; `is_null` stays safe). Tests: typechecker ├Ś6, unsafe-lint ├Ś5, codegen-E2E ├Ś4 (un-annotated offset chain, `char*` buffer-walk loop, is_null, plus the existing round-trip). **Residual (deferred, "or immediately after" per this item): the focused `E_RAW_POINTER_UNRESOLVED_POINTEE` diagnostic** ŌĆö an unresolved pointee is already REJECTED today (generic "cannot infer type parameter 'T'; add a type annotation" at the construction + read sites), but the design's focused variant (naming the pointee, offering the turbofish fix-it, suppressing the redundant binding-level error) needs inference-ordering surgery and is tracked as a follow-up. The `E_RAW_POINTER_UNRESOLVED_POINTEE` roadmap entry (v60 item 54) remains open on that refinement only. Original audit note (2026-06-07, now obsolete) follows for history: Current state (audited 2026-06-07): nothing past construction exists. The `ptr.*` module is constructors + strict-provenance ops only (`null(_mut)` / `dangling(_mut)` / `addr` / `with_addr(_mut)` / `expose(_mut)` / `from_exposed(_mut)` / `container_of(_mut)` / free-fn `is_null` ŌĆö `src/typechecker/env_build.rs:756ŌĆō945`); `infer_method_call` has **no `Type::Pointer` receiver arm** (no method of any name dispatches on a pointer), there is no `*p` deref lowering, and method-call turbofish is hardcoded `None` at `src/parser/exprs.rs:129` (free-function turbofish parses fine). `CStr.as_ptr` (the first safe pointer-producer, entry above) is currently produce-only ŌĆö nothing in the language can read through what it returns, so the surface becomes load-bearing the first time a workload consumes an FFI pointer (strlen-walk `CStr`-from-raw constructor in the `CString` entry above is one known consumer-in-waiting) ŌĆö per the katas-are-bug-finders loop. Shape decision to make at implementation time: inherent methods on `*const T` / `*mut T` (the design's written form ŌĆö needs the `Type::Pointer` dispatch arm and, for `p.read[T]()`-style pinning, method-call turbofish) vs `ptr.read(p)` free functions matching the shipped module's style; design.md's method-form text is the default unless implementation surfaces a reason to amend. Codegen side is small once `T` is known (typed load/store/GEP off the existing LLVM `ptr` lowering). **Dependency (bidirectional): the `E_RAW_POINTER_UNRESOLVED_POINTEE` entry above (v60 item 54, ┬¦ near the variance entry) is blocked on this surface** ŌĆö implement that check in the same slice (or immediately after); its hook point follows from this slice's shape decision. Phase target: 5.2 (Language Features) for typechecker dispatch + Phase 7 (codegen) for the load/store lowering. **[self-hosting prereq ŌåÆ [phase-12](phase-12-self-hosting.md#pre-pivot-blockers-fix-before)]** ŌĆö codegen reads through FFI pointers returned by LLVM-C.

- [x] **`String` substring / slicing surface. Ō£ō Interpreter MVP + codegen both shipped 2026-06-06.** No way to extract a sub-range of a String before this. Existing String method surface enumerated in `src/typechecker/stdlib_seq.rs:172` is `bytes`, `chars`, `sorted`, `sorted_by` ŌĆö none return a `String`. Surfaced 2026-05-20 by kata-katas/leetcode/71-simplify-path, which had to rebuild each path component character-by-character via f-string append. **Shape resolved:** `s[a..b]` range-indexing (lines up with design.md range syntax + Rust's `&s[a..b]`), NOT a named `substring` method. All range forms work: `a..b` / `a..` / `..b` / `..` / `a..=b` (inclusive includes byte `b`). Returns a **fresh `String`** (no borrowed-substring zero-copy view at v1 ŌĆö `ref str` lifetime extension is its own design slice). UTF-8-aware: byte offsets validated against char boundaries; a non-boundary index is a runtime panic carrying `E_STRING_SLICE_NOT_AT_CHAR_BOUNDARY` (mirrors Rust), and an out-of-range bound is a `string slice bounds ŌĆ” out of range` runtime error. **Implementation (interpreter):** typechecker `ExprKind::Index` range arm returns `Type::Str` for a `String` object (before the `Slice[T]` element-type path) in `src/typechecker/exprs.rs`; interpreter adds a `Value::String` arm to the range-index match in `src/interpreter/eval_expr.rs` (byte-range copy + `is_char_boundary` checks). **Tests:** 3 typechecker (`test_string_slice_returns_string`, `..._open_and_inclusive_forms_return_string`, `..._result_concatenates_as_string`) + 7 interpreter (half-open / open-ended / inclusive+empty / result-is-String-concats / multibyte-on-boundary / non-boundary-panics / out-of-range) + 1 codegen lowering test + 3 codegen E2E (below). fmt + clippy (`--all-targets --features llvm`) clean; full `cargo test` + `cargo test --features llvm` green. **Codegen ŌĆö shipped:**
  - [x] **`String` slicing codegen lowering. Ō£ō Shipped 2026-06-06.** `s[a..b]` lowers in `src/codegen/collections.rs::compile_string_slice` (dispatched from `compile_index`'s range branch when `string_typed_exprs` flags the object as a String ŌĆö before the array/slice element path, which can't handle a String): extract the `{ptr,len,cap}` aggregate, resolve byte bounds (`a..` ŌåÆ end = len; `..b` ŌåÆ start = 0; `a..=b` includes byte `b`; indices coerced to i64), then delegate validation + alloc + copy to a new **`karac_string_slice(data, len, start, end) -> *mut u8`** runtime helper (`runtime/src/clone.rs`). The helper validates bounds + UTF-8 char boundaries and `exit(1)`s with `E_STRING_SLICE_NOT_AT_CHAR_BOUNDARY` / a bounds message on a bad index (matching `emit_panic`'s shape, the interpreter, and Rust's `&s[a..b]`); returns the new NUL-terminated buffer (null for an empty slice, matching `karac_string_clone`'s empty convention). Codegen builds the result `{ptr, len, cap}` with `len = cap = end - start`; the result is a normal owned String, so the let/temp machinery frees it at scope exit exactly like a concat result (helper uses Rust `alloc`, same as `karac_string_clone`). Earlier this path **silently miscompiled** (the range branch fell through to integer-indexing ŌåÆ empty output); the lowering replaces the interim fail-loud guard per [[prefer-failloud-over-silent-miscompile]]. **Tests:** 5 runtime unit (`slice_*` in `runtime/src/clone.rs` ŌĆö subrange / full / emptyŌåÆnull / multibyte-on-boundary) + 1 codegen IR (`string_slice_lowers_to_runtime_helper`) + 3 codegen E2E (`e2e_string_slice_basic_forms` matches interpreter output exactly; `e2e_string_slice_result_is_string_and_concatenates`; `e2e_string_slice_non_char_boundary_panics` asserts the runtime panic). Runtime archives rebuilt (lean + full). End-to-end `karac build` + run verified: compiled output matches the interpreter, and a mid-char-boundary slice panics with exit 1. **kata-71 integration:** `kara-katas/leetcode/1-100/71-simplify-path/simplify.kara` was rewritten to use `s[a..b]` for output reconstruction (replacing the per-char `out.push(cs[p])` loop) ŌĆö verified correct on all 24 cases, interpreter == compiled. (Note: kata-71 was never *blocked* ŌĆö it had a working char-push impl since 2026-05-25; slicing is a cleaner shape and the natural integration test, not an unblock. The `bench/` variant still uses the char-push shape; re-benching it against slicing is a separate task.)

- [x] **Built-in `Display` for collections.** Already in place ŌĆö `type_supports_display` in `typechecker.rs:1596` recursively recognises `Vec[T]`, `Set[T]`, `SortedSet[T]`, `Option[T]`, `Map[K, V]`, `Result[T, E]`, `Tuple[..]`, `Array[T, N]`, `Slice[T]`, `Ref[T]`, `MutRef[T]` when their element types support Display; the `Value::Display` impl in `interpreter.rs:411` mirrors the recursion for runtime formatting. Codegen path lands separately under [phase-7-codegen.md ┬¦ Phase 7.2 ┬¦ Display for collections](phase-7-codegen.md). Regression tests in `tests/typechecker.rs` (`fstring_accepts_*`) cover Vec, nested Vec, Map, Set, Option, Result.

### Book Documentation

- [x] **Book appendix: Keywords (P1).** Add `docs/book/src/appendix-a-keywords.md` (mirrors Rust book Appendix A). Enumerate every reserved word in K─üra ŌĆö `fn`, `let`, `mut`, `ref`, `own`, `pub`, `struct`, `enum`, `shared`, `trait`, `impl`, `where`, `match`, `if`, `else`, `while`, `for`, `loop`, `break`, `continue`, `return`, `yield` (reserved per design.md:6032), `defer`, `errdefer`, `par`, `seq`, `spawn`, `collect_all`, `with`, `reads`, `writes`, `sends`, `receives`, `allocates`, `panics`, `layout`, `distinct`, `type`, `as`, `use`, `mod`, `unsafe`, `extern`, `asm`, `global_asm`, `self`, `Self`, `true`, `false`. Cross-reference each to its introducing design.md section. Mirror the Rust book's split into "currently used" vs "reserved for future." Generate from a single source if possible so drift is caught at build time.

- [x] **Book appendix: Operators and Symbols (P1).** Add `docs/book/src/appendix-b-operators.md` (mirrors Rust book Appendix B). Catalog every operator and punctuation symbol ŌĆö `+ - * / %` (arithmetic), `== != < <= > >=` (comparison), `&& || !` (logical), `& | ^ ~ << >>` (bitwise), `= += -= *= /= %= &= |= ^= <<= >>=` (assignment), `? ?.` (error propagation), `|>` (pipe, design.md:2479), `..` `..=` (range), `[T]` (generics), `f"..."` (interpolation), `#[...]` (attribute), `//` `///` `/* */` (comments), `->` `=>` `.` `:` `;` `,` `.` ŌĆö and every K─üra-specific symbol. One row per symbol with name, example, and cross-reference.

List every trait that works under `#[derive(...)]` in K─üra ŌĆö `Debug`, `Display` (design.md:603), `Eq`, `PartialEq`, `Ord`, `PartialOrd`, `Hash`, `Clone`, `Copy`, `Default`, `Serialize`, `Deserialize` (deferred, design.md:911), plus any K─üra-specific additions. - [x] **Compiler queries channel ŌĆö P0 architectural commit.** Ō£ō Landed 2026-05-18. Spec at [`design.md ┬¦ Specification Layers > Compiler Queries`](../design.md#compiler-queries) (graduated from brainstorm v63, 2026-05-08). Ships the channel infrastructure even with zero query catalogue entries; subsequent P1 entries are non-breaking additions that ride on this floor. Five sub-items, all P0 ŌĆö all landed:

  1. [x] **Stable item identity ŌĆö path-based DefId + structural-hash sub-item slots.** Ō£ō Landed 2026-05-18. New `src/def_path.rs` with `DefPath`, `SubItemHash`, `QueryId`. `collect_item_def_paths` walks every top-level Item kind and builds the index; `ResolveResult.def_paths: HashMap<String, DefPath>` carries it. Resolver-side map keeps the storage burden at item-level only (no per-AST-node field churn); sub-item slots compute their hash on demand. `SubItemHash::of_expr` is intentionally a stub returning `ROOT` for v1 ŌĆö the real hashing lands with the first sub-item-addressing catalogue entry (phase-7-codegen.md line 25). Four regression tests in `tests/resolver.rs::def_paths_*` confirm the motivating property: stability under unrelated source insertions and unrelated item renames.

  2. [x] **Per-phase `queries: Vec<CompilerQuery>` field.** Ō£ō Landed 2026-05-18. New `src/queries.rs` with `CompilerQuery` struct + `QueryKind` (`non_exhaustive`, ships with one `Stub` placeholder for v1) + `QueryOption` / `Confidence` / `ResolutionSurface` / `Phase`. Empty `queries: Vec<CompilerQuery>` field added to `ResolveResult`, `TypeCheckResult`, `EffectCheckResult`, `OwnershipCheckResult`, `ConcurrencyAnalysis`. Surface lock ŌĆö adding new `QueryKind` variants or populating queries from any phase is non-breaking; the `non_exhaustive` attribute forces match exhaustiveness handling for unknown variants in tools.

  3. [x] **`karac query queries` CLI surface.** Ō£ō Landed 2026-05-18. New `QueryKind::Queries` variant on the CLI enum + dispatch in `cmd_query`. Runs the full pipeline (typecheck ŌåÆ lower ŌåÆ effectcheck ŌåÆ ownershipcheck ŌåÆ concurrencycheck), collates `queries` across every phase result, and emits the JSON envelope on stdout. v1 output is `{"queries":[]}` because no phase populates yet; the empty-only emitter notes if a phase has unexpectedly pushed values so the serializer extension doesn't get skipped. `tests/cli.rs::test_query_queries_empty_envelope` locks the surface; help text lists the new kind. Streaming-mode `phase_queries` event integration deferred to the first P1.x entry that actually populates.

  4. [x] **Attribute extension surface verification.** Ō£ō Landed 2026-05-18. Future query-resolving attribute names (`prefer_rc`, `specialize`, `fork_at` ŌĆö companion to existing `no_rc`) registered in `RECOGNIZED_BARE_ATTRIBUTES`. Reserved at v1; semantic enforcement lands with their P1.x catalogue entries. Regression test `tests/resolver.rs::query_resolving_attribute_propagates_through_pipeline_without_diagnostic` confirms `#[specialize(T = i64, mode: "x")]` carrying nested named args parses, attaches to the item, and survives resolve + typecheck + ownership without any diagnostic ŌĆö verifying the AST shape supports query-resolving attributes without parser changes.

  5. [x] **Multi-resolution conflict diagnostic.** Ō£ō Landed 2026-05-18. New `ResolveErrorKind::QueryResolutionConflict` variant; new error code `E_QUERY_RESOLUTION_CONFLICT` in the CLI mapper. Conflict-pair registry `QUERY_RESOLUTION_CONFLICT_PAIRS` in `attribute_validator.rs` lists `(cold, inline)` (P1.3 inlining query) and `(no_rc, prefer_rc)` (P1.1 RC-fallback query); both `inline` / `cold` / `likely` / `unlikely` / `inline(never)` added as reserved attribute names. The validator walks each item's attributes, detects conflict pairs, emits one error per (pair ├Ś item), anchored at the second attribute's span. Three tests in `tests/resolver.rs::query_resolution_conflict_*` cover both pairs + the negative (single attribute of a pair must not fire).

  *Out of scope for the P0 commit.* Specific query catalogue entries (P1.1ŌĆōP1.6) are tracked as separate items below and in [`phase-7-codegen.md`](phase-7-codegen.md). Verifier-backed resolution (Alive2-class checks against author claims), runtime feedback into the queries report, and cross-phase deduplication are deferred to post-v1 (see `deferred.md`).

  *Cross-references.* design.md ┬¦ Specification Layers > Compiler Queries (the spec); design.md ┬¦ AI-First Compiler Interface > Structured Compiler Output (the JSON output discipline this joins); `src/ownership.rs:360` (P1.1 first decision site); brainstorm archive `brainstorming/archive/v63_llm_compiler_query_channel.md` (full design rationale and prior-art map).

- [x] **Compiler queries ŌĆö P1.1: RC fallback at use site.** Ō£ō Landed 2026-06-16. New `src/rc_fallback_queries.rs` plain-data analyzer walks the ownership pass's `OwnershipCheckResult.rc_values` (one `RcEntry` per RC-promoted binding ŌĆö trigger + both spans + optional `type_name`) and emits one `QueryKind::RcFallbackDecision` per RC-fallback binding, keyed on the enclosing function's def-path (`SubItemHash` = the later use-site offset, so multiple fallbacks in one function get distinct ids). Each query enumerates `{ keep_rc (default) | prefer_rc | no_rc }` with per-option rationale (the `keep_rc` note names the binding + the trigger label, e.g. "closure capture with outer use", and whether it's Rc- or Arc-shared); `default_confidence` is `Medium` (the fallback is a deterministic dataflow result, but carries a real perf cost worth surfacing). Resolution surface `["no_rc", "prefer_rc"]` ŌĆö both already reserved in `RECOGNIZED_BARE_ATTRIBUTES` and registered as a `QUERY_RESOLUTION_CONFLICT_PAIRS` entry; no parser change. **Why standalone, not in-pass:** the tracker framing ("push a CompilerQuery onto the ownership result") and the standalone-analyzer route produce the same end result ŌĆö a query per RC fallback flowing through `query_queries` ŌĆö but reading the finished `rc_values` (already fully exposed) keeps the complex ownership pass untouched and matches the P1.2/P1.3 analyzer shape. `cli.rs::query_queries` calls `rc_fallback_queries::analyze(&program, ownership)` and folds the result into the `{"queries":[ŌĆ”]}` envelope (new `rc_fallback_decision` JSON kind). **Suppression (already-resolved sites):** function carries `#[no_rc]`/`#[prefer_rc]` (`collect_resolved_fns`, mirroring `enforce_no_rc_attrs`'s keying); function carries `#[allow(rc_fallback)]` (reads the existing `suppressed_rc_fn_keys` set); value's type is a `#[no_rc]` struct (via `RcEntry.type_name`). **v1 limitation:** the type-level `#[no_rc]` check keys on `RcEntry.type_name`, which the pass populates for parameter/`self` bindings but not local `let`s ŌĆö an RC-promoted local of a `#[no_rc]` type is already a hard `NoRcViolation` error, so the redundant query it may surface is harmless (documented in the module frontmatter). Tests: 6 unit in `tests/rc_fallback_queries.rs` (fires for a closure-capture RC promotion; suppressed by `#[prefer_rc]`/`#[no_rc]`/`#[allow(rc_fallback)]` on the function and by a `#[no_rc]` parameter type; clean program ŌåÆ empty) + `tests/cli.rs::test_query_queries_populated_envelope_has_rc_fallback_query` (end-to-end envelope lock).

- [x] **Compiler queries ŌĆö P1.2: Generic specialization on monomorphization tuple.** Ō£ō Landed 2026-06-16. New `src/specialization_queries.rs` plain-data analyzer reads the monomorphization counter (`monomorphization::analyze`, the same table behind `karac query monomorphization` ŌĆö now effect-aware after the effects-slot work shipped the same day) and emits one `QueryKind::SpecializationDecision` per user-defined generic free function instantiated at Ōēź `SPECIALIZATION_QUERY_MIN_TUPLES` (4) distinct concrete *type* tuples, unless the definition already carries `#[specialize]`. **Fan-out shape (the entry's stated stress test):** one query per generic *definition* ŌĆö `QueryId` keyed on the generic's def-path with `SubItemHash::ROOT` ŌĆö with every concrete tuple folded into `options` (one `specialize_<types>` option per tuple, each note reconstructing the `{T = i64}` binding by zipping the alphabetically-sorted type-param names against the resolved tuple, capped at 8 with the full count surfaced in the trailing `no_specialize` default's note). This validates that the P0 identity scheme produces one stable id for a multi-instance item. Lives outside the typechecker pass for the same reason P1.3 lives outside codegen ŌĆö the monomorphization counter is produced *after* typecheck, so `query_queries` in `cli.rs` calls `specialization_queries::analyze(&program, tc, effects)` when a typecheck result is available and folds the result into the `{"queries":[ŌĆ”]}` envelope (new `specialization_decision` JSON kind). Resolution surface `#[specialize]` was already reserved in `RECOGNIZED_BARE_ATTRIBUTES` (sub-item 4) ŌĆö no parser/resolver change. **v1 scope (documented in the module frontmatter):** free functions only (impl/type-param generics and stdlib collection methods have no annotatable definition keyed to the method's own params); counts distinct *type* tuples, not (type, effect) tuples, since `#[specialize(T = i64)]` is type-keyed; path-form callees (`Module::process`) are not attributed (under-report, matching `codegen_queries`). Tests: 6 unit tests in `tests/specialization_queries.rs` (fires for 4 tuples; folds all tuples into options + carries the count + binding; suppressed by `#[specialize]`; no-fire below threshold; no-fire for monomorphic fn; dedups repeated instantiations) + `tests/cli.rs::test_query_queries_populated_envelope_has_specialization_query` (end-to-end envelope lock).

- [ ] **Compiler queries ŌĆö P1.4: Effect-set narrowing. ŌĆö BLOCKED at v1 (architecture), do not re-attempt as a result-reader.** Effect inference at function exit would emit a query when the inferred effect set could be narrower if a specific branch were proven unreachable: "inferred effect set is `{reads(file), allocates}` but I could narrow to `{reads(file)}` if the allocation is gated by an unreachable branch ŌĆö confirm reachable?" Resolution: existing effect declaration on the function. **Why blocked (verified 2026-06-16):** the effect model *trusts declarations* ŌĆö for any function with a `with` clause the checker *seeds* `inferred_effects` from the declared set and never narrows it (a declared body "may contain effectful calls we can't trace ŌĆö FFI, stdlib"; `effectchecker.rs` ~line 1294). Empirically, a `pub fn f() with reads(Db) writes(Log)` whose body only does `reads(Db)` reports `inferred == declared == {reads(Db), writes(Log)}` and compiles clean. So `declared ŌŖŗ inferred` is structurally impossible by default and there is **no slack to narrow** from a standalone `EffectCheckResult` reader (the route P1.1/P1.2/P1.3/P1.6 used). A faithful P1.4 needs (a) a body-retrace that *ignores* the declaration ŌĆö which is unsound, it would drop the untraceable FFI/stdlib effects the trust model exists to preserve ŌĆö plus (b) per-branch reachability analysis to attribute an inferred effect to a possibly-dead branch. That is the phase-11 work the catalogue table already tags P1.4 with (phase 11). Unblock only when branch-reachability lands; this is not a quick analyzer. Cleanest demonstrator of the channel's novel value ŌĆö pure intent question PGO cannot answer ŌĆö but it requires the reachability substrate first.

- [x] **Compiler queries ŌĆö P1.5: Layout choice.** Ō£ō Landed 2026-06-16. New `src/layout_queries.rs` plain-data analyzer detects a `for <name> in <collection>` loop that reads a **strict subset** of the iterated struct's fields and emits one `QueryKind::LayoutChoice` proposing a struct-of-arrays `layout` block. It types the iterated expression via `TypeCheckResult.expr_types` (recovering the element struct of `Vec[S]` / `Array[S]` / `Slice[S]`), reads the struct's fields from `TypeCheckResult.struct_info`, and walks the loop body for `<name>.<field>` reads; it fires when the accessed set is a non-empty strict subset and the struct has Ōēź 2 fields. Keyed on the enclosing function's def-path (`SubItemHash` = the loop's offset). Options `{ keep_aos (default) | group_hot_fields }`; the `keep_aos` note reports "reads N of M fields (ŌĆ”)". `default_confidence` is `Low` (access-pattern heuristic). **Resolution surface is empty** ŌĆö the resolution is the existing `layout` block *syntax* (design.md ┬¦ Feature 1), not an attribute; the query self-resolves once a `layout` block names the struct (suppression reads every `layout` block's collection type). Standalone analyzer like P1.1/P1.2/P1.3/P1.6, run from `cli.rs::query_queries` (new `layout_choice` JSON kind). **This implements the loop-field-access analysis `design.md ┬¦ Feature 1` attributes to `karac explain` ("statically analyzes field access patterns ŌĆ” emits a concrete `layout` block") ŌĆö that analysis did not previously exist (the `explain` command only renders static concept/error-class pages); P1.5 delivers it through the query channel.** **v1 scope (documented in the module frontmatter):** access-pattern heuristic, NOT a SoA-vs-AoS cost model (the catalogue's "field grouping alternatives the cost model considered" framing presumes a layout cost model that is still unspecified at v1 ŌĆö this fires on the clear-cut strict-subset signal and proposes the SoA direction); direct `for name in collection` over a `Vec`/`Array`/`Slice`-typed expression only (iterator adaptors, destructuring loop patterns, `Map`/`Set` out of scope). Tests: 5 unit in `tests/layout_queries.rs` (fires for strict subset; no-fire when all fields read / single-field struct / non-struct collection; suppressed by an existing layout block) + `tests/cli.rs::test_query_queries_populated_envelope_has_layout_query` (end-to-end envelope lock).

- [x] **Compiler queries ŌĆö P1.6: Auto-concurrency fork threshold.** Ō£ō Landed 2026-06-16. New `src/fork_threshold_queries.rs` plain-data analyzer walks the concurrency analysis's `ConcurrencyAnalysis.function_decisions` (per function, a list of `ParallelGroup`s each tagged `is_trivial`) and emits one `QueryKind::ForkThresholdDecision` per **non-trivial** parallel group (i.e. one the auto-parallelizer forks onto the par runtime), keyed on the enclosing function's def-path (`SubItemHash` = the group's first-statement offset, mapped from the group's statement indices via the function body). Each query enumerates `{ keep_auto (default) | pin_fork | keep_sequential }`; `default_confidence` is `Low` (the v1 fork gate is the crude `non_constant_count <= 1` `is_trivial` heuristic ŌĆö the real numeric cost model is "unspecified for v1"). Resolution surface `["fork_at"]`, already reserved in `RECOGNIZED_BARE_ATTRIBUTES` ŌĆö no parser change. Standalone analyzer (not in-pass) like P1.1/P1.2/P1.3: reads the finished result, runs from `cli.rs::query_queries` (new `fork_threshold_decision` JSON kind), folds into the `{"queries":[ŌĆ”]}` envelope. **Suppression:** the enclosing function carries `#[fork_at]`. **v1 limitation (documented in the module frontmatter):** the only fork signal exposed is the binary `is_trivial` gate, so the analyzer surfaces *every* auto-fork rather than only near-threshold ("marginal") ones ŌĆö when the numeric cost model graduates from "unspecified for v1" (per design.md ┬¦ Reported behavior > Auto-concurrency cost-model decisions), the same query can filter to forks whose estimate sits within a band of the threshold. The original framing ŌĆö "I would fork this group at N=64 estimated cost; raise/lower?" ŌĆö is the post-cost-model target; v1 ships the fork-decision surface that exists today. Tests: 4 unit in `tests/fork_threshold_queries.rs` (fires for a 2-call forked group; suppressed by `#[fork_at]`; no-fire for a trivial/inlined group; no-fire for a serialized body) + `tests/cli.rs::test_query_queries_populated_envelope_has_fork_threshold_query` (end-to-end envelope lock).

- [ ] **Comptime ŌĆö ASTŌåÆAST `comptime fn` (post-v1).** Spec lives at [`deferred.md ┬¦ Comptime ŌĆö ASTŌåÆAST comptime fn`](deferred.md#comptime--asttoast-comptime-fn) (v60 item 31, decided 2026-05-02). Four discrete implementation substrates, all post-v1: (1) **Comptime evaluator** ŌĆö treewalk interpreter over the typed AST, retargeted from the existing Phase 4 interpreter to compile-time invocation; covers value-level computation in `comptime fn` bodies excluding AST/type-as-value work. (2) **`Type` as first-class value + reflection API** ŌĆö expose the compiler's existing type registry as immutable `Type` values; field/variant/method iteration; size/align queries; the `Type` pseudotype is comptime-only (runtime references emit `E_TYPE_VALUE_AT_RUNTIME`). (3) **AST builder + emission** ŌĆö stdlib `compiler.ast` module with typed builder API (`ast.expr`, `ast.method`, `ast.impl_block`, etc.) plus quasi-quote shim (`ast.parse_expr(string)`); module-level splicing rules for items returned from comptime fns. (4) **Derive desugaring** ŌĆö `#[derive(Trait)]` resolves to a `derive_<Trait>` `comptime fn` lookup; built-in derives (`Eq`, `Hash`, `Display`, `Debug`, `Clone`, `Copy`, `PartialEq`, `PartialOrd`, `Ord`, `Arithmetic`, `Serialize`, `Deserialize`) are stdlib `comptime fn`s with no special compiler treatment beyond the lookup convention; user-defined derives use the same mechanism. Each substrate is internally complete on its own ŌĆö partial deployment never leaks a half-built feature into the v1 language. Effect-system wiring (already pinned in v1 ŌĆö design.md ┬¦ Comptime Effect Defaults): `reads(CompileTimeEnv)` / `writes(CompileTimeEnv)` / `allocates(CompileTimeHeap)` permitted; `panics` becomes a build-time diagnostic; runtime resource verbs forbidden via `E_RUNTIME_EFFECT_AT_COMPTIME`. Resource limits (configurable via CLI flags): 2^24 instructions, 512 MiB CompileTimeHeap, 1024 frames recursion. Tooling integration: `karac doc` documents comptime fns with a "comptime" badge; `karac explain --expand <span>` prints post-expansion AST; `karac` debugger sees comptime frames as a dedicated stack; `karac query monomorphization` tracks comptime invocations alongside type/effect tuples. (Post-v1.)
